It likewise states,<sup class="footnote-marker">20</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 126:6</i> “He who goes weeping on his way, [bearing a bag of seed, shall come back with a joyful shout, carrying his sheaves].”
However, in the coming future there will be laughter, as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">21</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 126:2</i> “Then shall our mouths be filled with laughter,” and as explained elsewhere regarding the matter of the joust [<i>kenigya</i>].<sup class="footnote-marker">22</sup><i class="footnote">See Vayikra Rabba 13, 3. It is stated that in the future there will be a “joust” between the <i>Shor Ha’bar</i> – the Giant Ox, and the Leviathan, and that this joust will bring the righteous much pleasure. The <i>Shor Ha’bar</i> will gore the Leviathon with his horns, while the leviathan will slaughter the <i>Shor Ha’bar</i> with its fins. It is explained that this refers to the “battle” which will take place between the animal soul and the Divine soul, i.e. the physical and the spiritual. The two will “slaughter” each other. The Hebrew word for slaughter can also mean to “uplift.” That is, the two will cause each other to be uplifted to a higher level than they are at the moment.</i>
This is likewise the explanation of the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">23</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 63:16</i> “You are our father,” that<sup class="footnote-marker">24</sup><i class="footnote">See tractate Shabbat 89b</i> “this refers to <i>Yitzchak</i>,” that this <i>Tzchok</i> (laughter) will come about in the future.<sup class="footnote-marker">25</sup><i class="footnote">The word <i>Yitzchak</i> (the name of the second forefather) means, “I will laugh” in the future tense. This refers to the laughter in the time of revelation which follows the tears of the time of concealment during exile. Specifically at that time, we will address <i>Yitzchak</i> as “our father.”</i> That is, it will come out from its opposite, which is the weeping that there was during the time of exile, as known.
Based on all this we may understand the true reason why the midnight prayers of <i>Tikkun Chatzot</i> are specifically done through tears.
This is advantageous for the soul, allowing one to pray [the morning service] with a revelation of an essential pleasure [in <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה], as in the verse, “We shall rejoice in You” etc.
and although the weeping during the midnight prayer of <i>Tikkun Chatzot</i> are simple tears shed over “the sins of one’s youth” and the like, nonetheless, about this it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">26</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 42:4</i> “My tears were my bread day and night.”
[“Day and night”] refers to the recital of the <i>Shema</i> and the [<i>Amidah</i>] prayers of the morning and evening.
This is because his tears over his distance, which are caused by his sins and transgressions, rectify the aspect of the source of the sin [itself]. This [source of sin] is specifically the casting off of the yoke of Heaven, and the aspect of the exile of the Indwelling Presence of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, which comes in a particular manner in each Godly spark.
These tears rectify and remove the blemish completely, and awaken above the aspect of the weeping that opposes and comes out of its opposite power, which is the essential joy, mentioned above.
This [joy] will radiate within his Godly soul during the <i>Shema</i> recital and the prayers etc. and will, literally, become as bread for his soul.
[On the other hand] the casting off of the yoke of Heaven is its opposite, which is the opposite of tears. This is like the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">27</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 29:18</i> “He blesses himself in his heart, saying, I shall have peace, though I walk in the stubbornness of my heart.”
This is like a servant who rebels. His rebelliousness and [the fact] that he has cast off the yoke [of his Master] is the main problem and is the source of anything that he will do contrary the will of his master.
About this it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">28</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 107:17</i> “The foolish afflict themselves on account of their sinful ways and their iniquities.” “[Now, the iniquitous are those who are rebellious,” <sup class="footnote-marker">29</sup><i class="footnote">See Talmud Bavli, Yomah 36b</i> who cast off the yoke of Heaven. Although they afflict themselves for their sins, and the sins of their youth, how will it help, because,<sup class="footnote-marker">30</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 107:14</i> “Their soul abhors all manner of food” [which refers to the bread] of <i>Chochmah,</i> as mentioned above.
[This is] the opposite of the pleasure which surely enlivens one’s soul.
The verse then continues,<sup class="footnote-marker">31</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms, 107:18</i> “They reached the gates of death,” as in the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">32</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 30:15</i> “[See I have set before you this day] life and good” which is the joy and good heartedness, from the aforementioned essential pleasure. Its opposite is “the death and evil” through casting off the heavenly yoke.
Now, it is specifically the tears during the midnight prayer of <i>Tikkun Chatzot</i> which is the foremost preparation for one’s soul to stand in prayer with all of the aforementioned matters of the three of levels of “weeping from this side…etc.”
[However] if not, he will delude himself in one of these ways. Either he will have weeping alone, or joy alone, or [he will have both but] they will not be true, to their depth.
This is a sign that the Godly light has not touched his soul except from a great distance. This is like the secret of the exile of the Divine Presence in the collective souls of the Jewish people.
(This then, is the main source and general reason for those who constantly fall from their levels of Divine pleasure and joy, without it being established whatsoever.
With the slightest resistance and opposition, the “Ropes that bind” him to <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה become completely uprooted from his heart. This is as mentioned above regarding the verses, “The foolish afflict themselves…Their soul abhorred all manner of food…etc.”
Therefore, whoever truly desires closeness to God should constantly make a great preparation within his soul during the midnight prayer of <i>Tikkun Chatzot,</i> and with the aforementioned matter of “weeping is affixed in my heart on this side and joy on that side.”
He should not delude himself, thus literally freely destroying his soul. This will suffice those of understanding.)
(From all of the above we may also understand the reason for the great principle, [which was said] in the name of the <i>Maggid</i> of <i>Mezritch</i> of blessed memory. [That to] naturally [have a dominance of the] “black gall”<sup class="footnote-marker">33</sup><i class="footnote">A serious nature.</i> is a preparatory receptacle to the attainment of true pleasure through self-sacrifice in “One-<i>Echad</i>-אחד,”<sup class="footnote-marker">34</sup><i class="footnote">This refers to the recitation of the <i>Shema.</i> When one says the words <i>HaShem</i> is One-<i>HaShem Echad-</i>יהו״ה אחד he gives his entire life over to <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, with true and absolute dedication, even to the point of death for the sake of the sanctification of the Name of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה.</i> and for the reception of all the secrets [of Torah]. All this is explained in <i>Kuntras</i> [<i>HaHitpa’alut</i>] at length. This will suffice those of understanding.)

Chapter 7

Now, before we proceed to [explain] the detailed knowledge of the Chaining Down of the worlds (<i>Seder Hishtalshelut</i>), we must preface with a matter that was previously mentioned (in chapter four).
This specifically refers to the connection of the particulars to the general principle.
As known to those who delve into the <i>Zohar</i> and other authentic texts of Kabbalah, in the [study of the] <i>Hishtalshelut</i> and the investment of the statures (<i>Partzufim</i>)<i>,</i> it is necessary for each person to know the [explanation of the <i>Seder Hishtalshelut</i>] in short form.
Beginning with the Simple Unity at the beginning of all things, until the end of all things, which is at the end of our lowly world, it all is literally bound with one “knot.” This is similar to a chain that goes from beginning to end and chains down from cause to cause etc.
The first light of the simple unity of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, who is called, “The Cause of all causes”<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar Bereshit 22b</i> is also called “First” or “Preceding,” as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 44:6</i> “I am first and I am last.”
“I am first” refers to <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Ein Sof</i> (The Unlimited One) after the first <i>Tzimtzum</i>, which is known as “the empty place.”<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">See Etz Chayim (<i>Drush Igullim V’Yosher</i>) Shaar 1, Anaf 2</i>
“I am last” at the end of everything, is the aspect of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Asiyah</i>, which is the source of the existence of this lowly world.
“Their beginning is bound to their end and their end to their beginning.”<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">See <i>Sefer Yetzirah</i>, Chapter 1, Mishnah 7</i> They are literally as one, like a chain whose lowest link is bound to its highest link.
This is the meaning of the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 32:39</i> “See now that I, I am He,” without any change at all from beginning to end.
Now, although it is known that there are a multitude of details in the chaining down from beginning to end, the entire purpose of man is the contemplation of all the particular details from beginning to end, to bind them all into one general unity with the Simple Unity of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, Who is called “first.”
This is as stated, “See now that I, I am He,” literally, and as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">Malachi 3:6</i> “I <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה have not changed.”
This is the pivotal point upon which the contemplation of the particulars must be founded, so that all [the particulars] are drawn to this general principle, as previously explained.
Now, the explanation of this matter for beginners [is as follows]: The order of the multitude of [details] of the chaining down of the line and thread (<i>Kav V’Chut</i>) which is drawn out after the first <i>Tzimtzum</i>, is known briefly as follows:
At first, before the first <i>Tzimtzum</i>, there was “Him and His Name alone.”<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">Pirke D’Rabbi Elazar, Chapter 3</i>
This refers to the Essential Self of the Unlimited One, blessed is He (<i>Atzmoot Ein Sof</i>), and His light and ray, which is called “His Name.”
It was all in the aspect of His essence, literally in an aspect of limitlessness, and He filled all “empty space.”
Afterwards, He made a <i>Tzimtzum</i> within Himself, and there remained an aspect of an Impression (<i>Reshimu</i>) of what was withdrawn, within this “empty space.”
From this impression (<i>Reshimu</i>) He drew out the line and thread (<i>Kav V’Chut</i>), in an aspect of encompassing and inner [lights].
The Unlimited Light before the withdrawal (<i>Tzimtzum</i>) is called “The upper purity,”<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Tihiru Ila’ah</i> – The Upper Purity</i> whereas the general encompassing light of this line (<i>Kav</i>), at its beginning, is called “The lower purity,”<sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Tihiru Tata’a</i> – The Lower Purity</i> as known.
Afterwards, through a <i>Tzimtzum</i> (withdrawal), <i>Malchut</i> of the Unlimited was drawn down to become <i>Keter</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon.</i>
[Then,] from <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i> there became <i>Keter</i> of <i>Atik Yomin</i> and <i>Arich Anpin</i>.
From <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Arich Anpin</i> there came <i>Keter</i> of <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i>. From <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i> there came <i>Keter</i> of <i>Zeir Anpin</i>, and [likewise] from <i>Zeir Anpin</i> to <i>Nukvah</i>, until from <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Atzilut</i> there came <i>Keter</i> of <i>Briyah</i>.
In this manner [there chained down] from <i>Briyah</i> to <i>Yetzirah</i>, and from <i>Yetzirah</i> to <i>Asiyah</i>, until the aspect of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Asiyah</i>, which is the end of everything.
We find that the “end of everything,” which is <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Malchut</i> of the world of Action-<i>Asiyah</i> is bound to the “beginning of everything,” which is the aspect of <i>Malchut</i> of the Unlimited One (<i>Ein Sof</i>) which contracted to become <i>Keter</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>.
This is as stated in the beginning of <i>Etz Chayim</i>, in <i>Shaar HaKlallim</i>, and is the meaning of “I am first and I am last,” as previously explained.
(In contrast, the aspect of the Essential Self of the Unlimited Light before the <i>Tzimtzum</i> cannot yet be called by the terms “beginning” or “end” since it is still an aspect of the light of His Essence, as it is before being drawn down to influence below.
This is as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote">In the liturgy of the <i>Amidah</i> prayer.</i> “You are holy and Your Name is holy,” as known.)
Now, after [one contemplates the particulars] is the unification.
Through the thorough contemplation (<i>Hitbonenut</i>) of all the particulars of the chaining down (<i>Hishtalshelut</i>), from the beginning of all things, which is <i>Malchut</i> of the Unlimited One until <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Asiyah</i> specifically, they should then all be drawn to the First Source, which is the aspect of the Essential Self of the Limitless Light of the Unlimited One before the <i>Tzimtzum</i>.
This is the general intention of the first verse of the <i>Shema</i><sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 6:4</i> recital, [which is] the “Upper Unity.”<sup class="footnote-marker">12</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar Bereshit 18b. The first verse of the <i>Shema</i> is the “Upper Unity,” while the second statement of the prayer is the “Lower Unity.”</i>
[In other words, Listen Israel, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה our God] <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה is One” refers to His simple unity before the first <i>Tzimtzum</i>. About this it states in <i>Sefer Yetzirah</i>,<sup class="footnote-marker">13</sup><i class="footnote">See Sefer Yetzirah, Chapter 1, Mishnah 7</i> “Before One, what do you count?”
[This is to say, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He is] higher than the ten <i>sefirot.</i> This is as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">14</sup><i class="footnote">See Introduction to Tikkunei Zohar 17a</i> “You are One, but not in enumeration” of the ten <i>sefirot</i>, as known.
However, the general intent of “Blessed is the Name of His glorious kingship forever and ever,”<sup class="footnote-marker">15</sup><i class="footnote">In the daily <i>Shema</i> prayer, the statement which immediately follows the first verse of “Listen Israel,” is the “<i>Baruch Shem Kevod Malchuto LeOlam Va’ed.</i>”</i> which is the “lower unity,”<sup class="footnote-marker">16</sup><i class="footnote">See tractate Psachim 56a, and Zohar Bereshit 18b</i> is the aspect of <i>Malchut</i> of the Unlimited One after the <i>Tzimtzum</i>.
About this it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">17</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 145:13, “<i>Malchutcha Malchut Kol Olamim</i>.” The literal translation is “Your kingdom is an everlasting kingdom.” However, it can also be translated as, “Your kingdom is the kingdom of all the worlds.” (<i>Malchut</i> is Kingdom). This signifies how <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, not only brings all worlds into existence, but that He is the ruler of them all.</i> “Your kingdom is the kingdom of all worlds,” until <i>Malchut</i> (Kingdom) of <i>Asiyah</i>. This is the aforementioned matter of “I am first and I am last.”
Now, this entire unification (<i>Yichud</i>) and “binding” from the beginning to the end, which follows the contemplation of the multitude of intermediary particulars, is only like a single detail in comparison to the general principle which includes them all.
This general principle is the aspect of the general encompassing of the Circle (<i>Igul</i>) which encompasses the Line (<i>Kav</i>).
[Moreover,] it too is considered to only be a detail in comparison to the Essential Self of the Unlimited Light before the <i>Tzimtzum,</i> which is called the “Upper Purity.”
[This “Upper Purity”] is even higher than being an aspect of a “general principle” for “particular details,” since we have already stated that “He is Holy” and removed in the aspect of His Essential Self.
This is the meaning of the words,<sup class="footnote-marker">18</sup><i class="footnote">See the <i>Baruch She’amar</i> and <i>Yishtabach</i> prayers of the morning prayers, “<i>Yachid Chay HaOlamim</i>”</i> “The Singular One, Life of the worlds.”
From this aspect of “<i>Yachid –</i> Singular,” [influence] is drawn down by means of the aforementioned first <i>Tzimtzum,</i> to become what is called “the life of the worlds” of <i>ABY”A,</i><sup class="footnote-marker">19</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Atzilut, Briyah, Yetzirah</i> and <i>Asiyah.</i></i> which are within the line-<i>Kav</i> in an encompassing and inner manner, as known. This will suffice those of understanding.
It is necessary for a person to know and implant in his soul all the explanations of the chaining down of the worlds. After the explanations of all the particular details in the order of the chaining down (<i>Seder Hishtalshelut</i>) have been explained to a person,
then he should constantly accustom himself, throughout his life, [to contemplate them] in his mind and heart, so that he will be proficient in all the details, specifically.
[Through this,] he will [be capable of] making a summation of the entire length, including [the entirety of it] from beginning to end as one.
This [should be done] to such a degree that in a single moment of contemplation within his soul, [when he contemplates] “the end of everything,” which is the comprehension of physical coming into being of “something out of nothing,” [that is, the creation] of the physical planets and the four physical foundations, and all the other particulars of this lowly world, [he will see that there rests upon them the aspect of <i>Malchut</i> of the Unlimited One, literally].
This is as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">20</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 40:26</i> “Lift up your eyes on high, and behold Who has created these.” “Lift up your eyes on high” with an actual physical sight, “and behold Who has created these” into a completely physical something, through the most final <i>Tzimtzum</i>-concealment.
It is literally in this [“end of everything”] where <i>Malchut</i> of the Unlimited One, which is the “beginning of everything” and is even higher than the source of <i>Atzilut</i>, rests, in a limitless aspect, specifically.
This is why the book of Psalms only mentions the greatness of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, in a simple manner, [as it pertains to] the greatness and wondrousness of the acts of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה in the [physical] heavens and the earth, and its physical hosts, specifically.
It makes no mention or praise of His greatness [as it pertains to] the upper spiritual worlds and the highest heights which even precede the world of <i>Atzilut</i>.
This is because, as previously mentioned, “the beginning is specifically bound to the end.” This is [also] as stated, “See now that I, I am He,” and that the Essential Self of the Unlimited Light is what encompasses [all of existence]. This will suffice for those of understanding.
This then, is the true intent in the contemplation of the particulars, as previously explained.
(Even though according to the calculation of the [multitude of] details in the chaining down of the worlds, there is a very vast distance between the beginning and the end, nonetheless, in truth, it is very close, without any interruption and concealment in between.
This is as stated, “See now that I, I am He” and,<sup class="footnote-marker">21</sup><i class="footnote">See Tikkunei Zohar 120a</i> “There is no other besides Me, as an intermediary.” This will suffice for those of understanding.)
(This is as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">22</sup><i class="footnote">Kohelet 7:29</i> “[Lo, this only I have found,] that God has made man upright; but they have sought out many calculations.” “That God has made man upright” [refers to] Primordial Man (<i>Adam Kadmon</i>), from the beginning of the line (<i>Kav</i>) until the “heel” of Primordial Man (<i>Adam Kadmon</i>), which concludes at the end of the world of <i>Asiyah</i>.
It is all one complete [matter] from beginning to end. [However,] “They have sought out many calculations” [referring to] the aspect of Circles (<i>Igullim</i>), with separations and divisions, one above the other.)
All the above may be understood, in a very brief way, from the aspect of the <i>Ketarim</i><sup class="footnote-marker">23</sup><i class="footnote">This word is the plural of <i>Keter</i> (crown). The <i>sefirah</i> of <i>Keter</i> corresponds to the faculty of “pleasure” and “desire,” as will be explained at great length later.</i> of each world.
In the aspect of the <i>Ketarim</i> there is no aspect of “chaining down” from cause to effect in a way of distance of levels, at all.
For example, the aspect of the simple desire in the Essential Self of the Unlimited Light, as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">24</sup><i class="footnote">See introduction of Etz Chayim, and Shaar 1, Anaf 2</i> “When it arose in His simple desire,” that is, the aspect of <i>Malchut</i> of the Unlimited One itself is what arose in His simple thought, [as in the statement] “I shall rule,”<sup class="footnote-marker">25</sup><i class="footnote">As stated in the Zohar on “<i>VaYimloch</i>.” These words, “I will rule – <i>Ana Emloch</i>” is the original simple desire which arose in His simple thought.</i> which is much higher than the desire to Emanate (<i>Atzilut</i>) or to Create (<i>Briyah</i>) etc.
Those [desires] are still only in the aspect of a <i>Heyulie</i>.
From this first [simple desire], there is a <i>Tzimtzum</i> – lessening to the “Primal Desire,” which is called <i>Keter</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>.
Afterwards, [there came] the desire to Emanate which in general is the aspect of <i>Keter</i> of <i>Atzilut</i>.
Afterwards was the desire to Create, which is <i>Keter</i> of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Briyah</i>, following which [there came] <i>Keter</i> of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Yetzirah,</i> until the aspect of <i>Keter Malchut</i> of <i>Asiyah</i>, which is the desire to actualize.
This is as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">26</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 135:6</i> “Whatever <i>HaShem-</i>יהו״ה desired He did…”
[Similarly,] below in man, what difference is there between the aspect of his desire and essential <i>heyulie</i> in which there were included four desires.
For example, the desire for his essential self and his most final desire to actualize, all came from and are rooted in one source.
Likewise, there is no difference between <i>HaShem</i>’s-יהו״ה simple desire that was drawn down to become the desire for emanation, and His simple desire that was drawn down to become [the aspect of] “Whatever <i>HaShem-</i>יהו״ה desired He did,” at the end of our world of action. This will suffice for those of understanding.

Chapter 8

Now, just as in the aspect of <i>Keter,</i> there is a unification of all the particulars to the general principle, reaching, literally all the way to the aspect of the simple desire [as it is] in the Essential Self of the Unlimited Light, in this same way, a person may contemplate the aspect of the <i>Chochmah</i> of each world, from beginning to end.
This then is the meaning of what is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 1:1</i> “<i>Bereshit Barah</i> – In the beginning God created etc.”
“<i>Bereshit-</i>בראשית” is translated by Targum Yerushalmi<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">See Targum Yerushalmi to Genesis 1:1</i> as “<i>B’Chochmeta -</i> with Wisdom.” Onkelos translates it as “<i>BeKadmin</i> – Primordially.”
This is the aspect of <i>Keter,</i> which is called <i>Kadmon</i> – Preceding, since it is the aspect of the essence as it precedes <i>Chochmah</i>.
This is because,<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">Job 28:12</i> “Wisdom is found <b>from</b> “nothing” but it is not an actual “nothing” itself, which is not so of desire.
However, just as desire is [brought about] from the Essential Self by means of <i>Tzimtzum</i>, until it [finally] becomes invested in action, thus fulfilling the above-mentioned verse, “Whatever <i>HaShem-</i>יהו״ה desires He did,” so is it with the aspect of <i>Chochmah</i>.
[In other words, <i>Chochmah</i> too is brought about] by means of <i>Tzimtzum</i> from His Essential Self.
[The Essential <i>Chochmah</i>] is what is called “the Primal <i>Chochmah</i>” or “the Simple <i>Chochmah</i>” as it exists within the Simple Unity of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה.
From there it is drawn down into each particular world of <i>ABY”A</i>, until [it reaches] the aspect of <i>Chochmah</i> of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Malchut</i> of the world of <i>Asiyah</i>.
About this [last level] it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 104:24</i> “You have made them all with wisdom.”
For, just as it states “<i>Bereshit-</i>בראשית,” that “He created” with wisdom, in the same way, he likewise “formed” and “actualized” with wisdom.
This is similar to how it is that the desire to create, form, and actualize are all [rooted] in a single [primary] desire.
However, it chained down from the world of Creation to the world of Formation, and from the world of formation to the world of Actualization, with a lowering of levels from cause to effect.
For example, from <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Keter</i> of the world of <i>Briyah</i> there came <i>Keter</i> of the world of <i>Yetzirah</i>.
Likewise, He created, formed and actualized [everything] with a single wisdom.
However, [here too, in regard to <i>Chochmah</i>] it chained down from <i>Briyah</i> to <i>Yetzirah</i> etc.
In other words, from the aspect of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Chochmah</i> of <i>Briyah</i> [influence] is drawn down to <i>Chochmah</i> of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Yetzirah</i>.
Likewise, in this manner [influence chains down] from <i>Yetzirah</i> to <i>Asiyah</i>, until [it reaches] the aspect of <i>Chochmah</i> of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Asiyah</i> about which it states, “You have made them all with wisdom.” Similarly, it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 3:19</i> “<i>HaShem-</i>יהו״ה founded the earth with wisdom,” and other such verses.
(More particularly the chaining down is that <i>Keter</i> of <i>Yetzirah</i> comes from the aspect of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Briyah</i>, and <i>Chochmah</i> of <i>Yetzirah</i> comes from <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Keter</i> of <i>Yetzirah</i>. Nevertheless, generally, all aspects of cause and effect from one world to the next are drawn one from the other without being diminished by the multitude of intermediaries that are between them.
For example, it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">Kings I, 5:26</i> “And <i>HaShem-</i>יהו״ה gave Shlomo wisdom.” [Now, Shlomo] was in the world of <i>Asiyah</i>.
This influence was drawn down from <i>Chochmah</i> [as it exists] in the Essential Self of the Unlimited Light (<i>Ohr Ein Sof</i>), to <i>Chochmah</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>.
From <i>Chochmah</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i> [it was drawn down] to the Concealed <i>Chochmah</i> of <i>Atik Yomin</i> and <i>Arich Anpin</i>.
From there [it descended] to become the light of <i>Abba</i> of <i>Atzilut</i>. [From there it descended] until [it reached] the aspect of <i>Chochmah</i> of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Atzilut</i>.
From there [it descended further] to <i>Chochmah</i> of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Briyah</i>.
In this manner it [descended] from <i>Briyah</i> to <i>Yetzirah</i>, and from <i>Yetzirah</i> to <i>Asiyah</i>, until from <i>Chochmah</i> of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Asiyah</i> this light and influence of Godly wisdom entered the soul of <i>Shlomo</i>.
[This was] likewise [the case], in the chamber of the Holy of Holies in the Temple. There radiated from <i>Keter</i> and <i>Chochmah</i> of the Essence [of the Unlimited Light] until [it reached] the aspect of <i>Keter</i> and <i>Chochmah</i> of the chamber of the Holy of Holies in the world of <i>Asiyah</i> – Actualization. [This is to say that] the spiritual [light] of <i>Keter and Chochmah</i> of <i>Asiyah</i> rested upon the physical Tablets and the Holy Ark, which stood in the chamber of the Holy of Holies in the physical Temple below.
(Similarly, [in our daily prayers] we request,<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">See the beginning of the Amida prayer.</i> “You grace man with knowledge” and, “Grace us from You,” specifically. This will suffice for those of understanding.)
(By way of example, this may be understood from human beings below. For instance, a person’s essential <i>Heyulie</i> wisdom includes [within itself] all that spreads forth and branches out of the light of his wisdom, even completely outside of his essence,
That is, even [to the point of] intellect that is invested in a physical act, which is separate [from his essential self].
For him, there is no difference between the spreading of his essential insight (<i>Chochmah</i>) within the essence of his intellect, in which he conceptualizes [in a way of] intellectual analysis, and the spreading forth [of the intellect] into a [physical] act, which is separate [and apart from his essence].
It is all considered to be a single insight, except that this [level] is more spiritual and essential to him, while in action it [the wisdom] becomes [invested] into a separate thing.
This is so much so, that in relation to the aspect of his actual essential self it is but a single wisdom, except that it spreads forth from his intellectual analysis into his emotions and thoughts, until, ultimately, he actually puts this insight into action.
An example is [when someone has] an [innovative] insight in business matters etc. (
Similarly, [this may be understood] in regard to the speech [of God], as in the verse, “And God said, let there be light” which then came into action, as in the verse, “And there was light.”
Of course, this originated from the aspect of His Essential Wisdom as it is in the Essential Self of the Emanator.
[This is to say,] that He emanated (<i>Atzilut</i>) the light, and afterwards he created (<i>Briyah</i>), formed (<i>Yetzirah</i>) and made (<i>Asiyah</i>).
This is likewise the case in regard to all the specifics of the coming into being of the emanated, created, formed and actualized, from the Essential Self of the Unlimited One (<i>Ein Sof</i>).
All the particulars of these [worlds] are unified and bound with the Essential Self of the Unlimited Light (<i>Atzmoot Ohr Ein Sof</i>), which is [vested] in <i>ABY”A</i>.
Moreover, from [the perspective of] His Essential Self, there is absolutely no difference between the first and the last.
This being the case, the statement, “I am first and I am last” likewise applies to the aspect of <i>Chochmah</i> at the beginning of the emanation – <i>Atzilut,</i> until <i>Chochmah</i> at the end of the Actualization – <i>Asiyah</i>.
Furthermore, in this way, the aspect of the general unification of the emotions, thought, speech and action of each of the four worlds of <i>ABY”A</i>, may also be understood in a manner of particulars.
[This is to say] that the emotions of <i>Atzilut</i> become invested within the emotions of <i>Briyah</i>, and the emotions of <i>Briyah</i> become invested within the emotions of <i>Yetzirah</i>. The emotions of <i>Yetzirah</i> [then] become invested within the emotions of <i>Asiyah,</i> so that ultimately, the six directions of <i>Asiyah</i> are bound up with the beginning of everything, that is, with His Essential emotions, which precede the world of <i>Atzilut.</i>
About these [emotions] it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote">See the morning prayers, blessing of <i>Yotzer</i>.</i> “[The King who is exalted and alone,] who is exalted above the days of the world.”
This refers to the aspect of the seven lower <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Atik Yomin</i>, [which receive] from the seven lower <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>, [which receive] from the emotions of the Unlimited Light itself, which are concealed within His Essential Self, literally.
An example [of the above] is the aspect of <i>Chessed –</i> Kindness of the Unlimited Light. About this [Kindness] it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote">Lamentations 3:22</i> “<i>HaShem</i>’s-יהו״ה kindnesses have not ceased,” since it, literally, is in an aspect of Limitlessness.
[Regarding this Kindness] we say,<sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 33:22, and Shabbat Prayers</i> “Let Your Kindness…be upon us,” literally.
[This is to say that it should radiate] within the kindness of the diminished emotions of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Asiyah</i>, which radiates in this world.
Likewise, from the aspect of His essential thought, [influence] is drawn down until [it reaches] the aspect of the thoughts of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Asiyah</i>, in that He thinks to do it, in actuality.
The same [principle] applies to speech and action, because just as “everything that <i>HaShem-</i>יהו״ה desires” in His Essential desire, “He does,” so too, “everything that <i>HaShem-</i>יהו״ה desires” [to think], He thinks.
[The] only [difference between this and the desire as it exists in His Essential Self is] that it descends and is drawn into the [order of the] chaining down [of the worlds from cause to effect] until His desire, intellect and thought is to actually do.
However, [the entire chaining down process] of the desire, intellect, emotions, thought and action are all considered to literally be one [thing] relative to the aspect of His actual Essential Self. This is understood from all the above, and will suffice for those of understanding.
Now, after [contemplating] all this, a person should conceptualize and contemplate “Who created these,” physically, how it is that even the last particular is not separate from the first general source.
[He should contemplate this in regard to] each particular of Creation, such as the creation of the heavens and the earth, or all the particulars in the categories of Inanimate, Vegetation, Animal, and Speaking Beings.
[He should contemplate] how their spiritual source in <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Asiyah</i> is bound up and connected to the highest heights, like a chain.
This is so, just as the aspects of <i>Keter</i> and <i>Chochmah</i> of <i>ABY”A</i> are unified [with their source], as stated, “In the beginning He created” [which was translated as] “Primordially – <i>Keter</i>,” and, “With Wisdom – <i>Chochmah</i>.”
So too, with the particulars which branch out from them, These being the emotions, thought, speech and action of each world.
(Which are the ten general <i>sefirot</i> of each world. That is, <i>Atik Yomin</i> and <i>Arich Anpin, Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i>, <i>Zeir Anpin</i> and <i>Nukvah</i> of [each of] the four worlds of <i>ABY”A</i>.)
[This continues] until the aspect of Action – <i>Asiyah</i> of <i>Malchut</i> of the world of <i>Asiyah.</i> The end [of everything] is bound with the beginning of everything.
For, just as He emanated with <i>Kadmon</i> (Desire), so too, with this very same <i>Kadmon</i> (Desire) He created, formed and did, as is written, “Everything that <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה desired, He did etc.”
Likewise, the emotions (the six directions) are nullified to <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, as in the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote">Exodus 33:21</i> “Behold, the place is with Me.”
[For example,]<sup class="footnote-marker">12</sup><i class="footnote">Chronicles I 29:11</i> “Yours, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, is the greatness” [represents the nullification of <i>Chessed</i> to <i>HaShem-</i>יהו"ה] in each world, according to what it is.
[This continues upward] until the aspect of His Essential Space. This is called “His Place,” as in the dictum of our sages, of blessed memory,<sup class="footnote-marker">13</sup><i class="footnote">Bereshit Rabba 68:9</i> “He is the place (<i>Makom</i>-מקום) of the world, but the world is not His place.”
This is similar to the well-known adage,<sup class="footnote-marker">14</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar (Raya Mehemnah) Pinchas 225a</i> “He grasps all worlds, but there are none who grasp Him.” Even the Primal Thought and Desire [cannot grasp Him].
From all this, the matter of the unification and connection of the particulars to the general principle by way of the totality of everything in the essence of the Unlimited light [as it is drawn down] into ABY’’A, may be understood.
This is besides the aspect of the unity [as it relates to] each world, in a way of particulars, in regard to the ten <i>Sefirot</i> [of each world]<i>.</i>
Now, although a person may know the explanations for the entire chaining down of <i>ABY”A</i> [with all its] particulars, he should [nonetheless] draw his soul to [contemplate and] unify the particulars to the general totality, in the aforementioned manner, until [they are] literally [one] with the Essential Self of the Unlimited Light (<i>Ohr Ein Sof</i>).
This is aside from [his contemplation in] unifying and nullifying each particular world to the Essential Self of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He.
[He should do this] until his vast contemplation in the particulars of this matter, become encapsulated in a wondrously brief summary.
An example of this [can be understood from the verse],<sup class="footnote-marker">15</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 145:13</i> “Your kingdom is the kingdom of all worlds.”
This is the aspect of <i>Malchut</i> of the Unlimited One (<i>Ein Sof</i>) [as it is invested] within <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Asiyah</i>, as previously explained regarding Desire, Wisdom and Emotions.
This is in accordance with the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">16</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 32:39</i> “See now that I, I am He,” literally.
Similarly, [regarding the verse,]<sup class="footnote-marker">17</sup><i class="footnote">Malachi 3:6</i> “I <i>HaShem-</i>יהו״ה have not changed.”
“I-<i>Ani-</i>אני,” which is the aspect of <i>Malchut</i>, is the [same] “nothingness-<i>Ein</i>-אין” as <i>Keter</i>, since “the beginning is bound up with the end.”
[This is true] both particularly in each particular world, and in the general totality of everything.
It thus states, “I <i>HaShem-</i>יהו״ה have not changed.” [That is, there is no difference] whatsoever between <i>Malchut</i> of the Unlimited One and <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Asiyah</i>.
This then, is the meaning of, “Your kingdom is the kingdom of all worlds,” that is, even until <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Asiyah</i>. [It all is] because of the reason explained above. This will suffice for those of understanding.

Chapter 9

At first glance, the verse, “I HaShem have not changed,” is not understood.
Now, [this verse] is speaking in regard to <i>Malchut</i> of the Unlimited One (<i>Ein Sof</i>) Himself.
However, if in <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Asiyah</i> (Actualization) there is a change between judgment and kindness, which is [only] an aspect of a reaction, then it must be that in <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Ein</i> Sof (The Unlimited One) this change also takes place.
After all, it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 32:39</i> “See now that I, I am He.”
It likewise states,<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 145:13</i> “Your kingdom is the kingdom of all worlds,” literally equally, as explained previously.
In other words, when the desire for kindness arises in His simple essential desire, this very same essential desire for kindness descends until the very end, to the desire for kindness of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Asiyah</i>, literally.
According to all the above mentioned, it is likewise understood that the opposite is true as well.
Furthermore, we recite [daily],<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">See the blessings before the <i>Shema</i> recital.</i> “He renews every day…the act of creation” here below [in our physical world].
In other words, [“he renews”] in “<i>Kadmin</i> – Desire” and “<i>Chochmeta –</i> Wisdom,” [which are the translations]<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">See Targum Onkelus and Targum Yerushalmi to Genesis 1:1</i> of “In the beginning He created.”
[These are “renewed”] all the way until the highest heights, literally in His Essential Self.
This being the case, [it seems] that there is a renewal even in the Essence of the Limitless Light of the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He. (<i>Atzmoot Ohr Ein Sof)</i>.
How then can it state,<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">Malachi 3:6</i> “I <i>HaShem-</i>יהו״ה have not changed,” [implying that there is no change] whatsoever?
Similarly, we say,<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">See the morning prayers.</i> “You are He before the creation of the world; You are He after the creation of the world.” This [principle] likewise applies “before He emanated,” as known.<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">See Avodat HaKodesh (R’ Meir ben Gabay) Chelek HaYichud, Ch. 2.</i>
Moreover, in the analogy of man below, there is change from a desire for judgment to a desire for kindness, even in the essential desire, as known.
Likewise, how can we [pray and] request, “May it be desirable before You,” [requesting of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה to have] a new desire; that a desire for judgment should be overturned into a desire for kindness?
[This question is further strengthened by the fact that] we see multitudes of changes every day and every hour, in “everything that <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה desires”<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 135:6</i> and constantly does in the heavens and the earth.
Now, the resolution for all this is the matter of <i>Tzimtzum</i>, as known.
For, if the influence was in a manner of cause and effect, then the matter of change and reaction would fall upon it.
However, since the aspect of the drawing down [of influence] is only in an aspect of a light and ray, and this too is by means of <i>Tzimtzum</i>, there is therefore no change at all in the Essential Self of <i>HaShem</i>’s-יהו״ה Godliness, even in <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Asiyah</i>.
Such is the case, all the way to the highest level.
After <i>Tzimtzum</i> [however] there is an aspect of change, but only from the perspective of the recipients, as known.
The explanation of the difference between “<i>Ohr</i> (Light) and <i>Shefa</i> (Influence) is known to all.
However, even in the aspect of the light it was necessary for [its revelation] to be by means of <i>Tzimtzum</i>.
It therefore is incumbent upon every individual to know the matter of <i>Tzimtzum</i> and to contemplate it [relative] to each world according its value.
This is because it is the main principle in the general matter of the unity of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, and [in understanding] how there is no change relative to the Essential Self of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He.
[This is to say] that before Him, “the darkness and the light are equal,”<sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 139:12</i> the spiritual and the physical are equivalent, so much so, that the world of <i>Atzilut</i> and the world of <i>Asiyah</i> are equal [before Him], as known.
Now, the [above] is only in relation to the encompassing light of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, which is called <i>Sovev Kol Almin</i> (The light that encompasses or transcends all worlds) both generally and particularly.
This [light] is higher than the level of light that is in an aspect of <i>Memale Kol Almin</i> (the light of <i>HaShem-</i>יהו״ה, blessed is He, that fills all worlds), as known.
However, even in the aspect of the inner light of <i>Memaleh</i>, both generally and particularly, there is no change.
[Here too] its upper and lower [levels] are equivalent.
This is as stated, “I <i>HaShem-</i>יהו״ה have not changed,” and “I-<i>Ani-</i>אני” refers to the aspect of <i>Memaleh</i> [the inner pervading light], as known.
Likewise, it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote">Jeremiah 23:24</i> “Do I not fill the heavens and the earth? – says <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה.” He, specifically, fills them equally.
This too [refers to] the aspect of the inner pervading light, as in the dictum,<sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote">See Tikkunei Zohar, 457 (91b) and 470 (122b) and other sources.</i> “There is no place void of Him,” as known.
The reason is because even in the aspect of [the inner light of] <i>Memaleh</i>, the light and influence descend specifically by means of <i>Tzimtzumim.</i><sup class="footnote-marker">12</sup><i class="footnote">This is the plural of <i>Tzimtzum</i>.</i>
As known, even the aspect of the line and thread (<i>Kav V’Chut</i>) which is drawn from the Essential Self of the Limitless Light of the Unlimited One and is generally called the inner light<sup class="footnote-marker">13</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Memale Kol Almin</i>.</i> of the worlds of <i>ABY”A</i>,<sup class="footnote-marker">14</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Atzilut, Briyah</i>, <i>Yetzirah</i> and <i>Asiyah</i>.</i> is, likewise, initially drawn by means of <i>Tzimtzum</i> in the Essence.
This is the first <i>Tzimtzum</i>, which is called the “empty place” (<i>Makom Panuy</i>) and the “empty void” (<i>Challal Reikan</i>), as stated in <i>Etz Chayim</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">15</sup><i class="footnote">See <i>Etz Chayim</i>, Shaar 1, Anaf 2 (<i>Drush Igullim V’Yosher</i>)</i>
This is likewise the case in the descent of the <i>Kav-</i>line down, into the aspects of <i>Igullim</i> and <i>Yosher</i>, until it becomes the aspect of <i>Keter</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>, [this too] is by means of <i>Tzimtzum</i>.
The same [principle] applies [in the descent] from <i>Adam Kadmon</i> to <i>Atik Yomin</i> and <i>Arich Anpin.</i> [It too is by way of <i>Tzimtzum</i>].
Even within the world of <i>Atzilut</i> itself, generally, there is a screen (<i>Masach</i>) between <i>Keter</i> and <i>Chochmah</i>.
This is the meaning of the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">16</sup><i class="footnote">Terumah 26:33</i> “The curtain shall be for you as a division between the holy and the holy of holies,” as explained in <i>Zohar</i>.
Similarly, [there is a screen (<i>Masach</i>)] between <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i> to <i>Zeir Anpin</i>, and between <i>Zeir Anpin</i> and <i>Nukva</i>, as known.
[Furthermore], between <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Atzilut</i> and <i>Briyah</i>, there is a <i>Masach</i> (screen) and <i>Malchut</i> penetrates the screen and becomes <i>Keter</i> of <i>Briyah</i>.
In this manner, there is a <i>Masach</i> (screen) between <i>Briyah</i> and <i>Yetzirah</i>, and <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Briyah</i> penetrates the screen and becomes <i>Keter</i> of <i>Yetzirah</i>.
Similarly, <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Yetzirah</i> penetrates the screen and becomes <i>Keter</i> of <i>Asiyah</i>.
[This continues] until <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Asiyah</i>, which is called “The King who is exalted and alone.”
This is also like the statement of the Sages,<sup class="footnote-marker">17</sup><i class="footnote">See Talmud Bavli, Shabbat 77b</i> “Like the creation of the world: At first there was darkness, and then the light returned.”
Similarly, the Sages stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">18</sup><i class="footnote">See Rashi on Bereshit 1:1 and the citations there.</i> “Initially it arose in His thought to create with the quality of Judgment.” This [quality of Judgment] is the aspect of <i>Tzimtzum</i>, [which is] the title God-<i>Elohi”m-</i>אלהי״ם of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Asiyah</i>.
This is as stated, “In the beginning God-<i>Elohi”m</i>-אלהי״ם created etc.” [“<i>Bereshit</i> – In the beginning” is translated as] “<i>Bechochmeta –</i> With Wisdom,” and “<i>BeKadmin</i> – With Desire,” which is the desire and wisdom of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Asiyah</i>. This will suffice for those of understanding.
According [to all of the above] everything is resolved [in regard to] the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">19</sup><i class="footnote">Malachi 3:6</i> “I <i>HaShem-</i>יהו״ה have not changed.”
[This is to say that there is no change] between a desire for kindness or for judgment in all of the worlds of <i>ABY”A</i>.
In other words, [this refers to] how He is before the <i>Tzimtzum</i> or <i>Masach</i> (screen) through which [the light] penetrates and becomes the <i>Keter</i> of the lower world.
It is, specifically, to this aspect, [that is, the Essential Self of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, that we pray and] say, “May it be desirable, specifically, before You.”
[Relative to the Essential Self of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He,] all aspects of “higher” and “lower” in the world, are literally equivalent.
However, after the <i>Tzimtzum</i>, the desire is drawn into the intellect and emotions with changes, until the aspect of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Asiyah</i> [about which] we say, “May it be desirable before You,” [meaning that <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, should cause] a change in actual action, from judgment to kindness and the like. This will suffice those of understanding.

Chapter 10

We must now understand all the particulars of the four worlds of <i>ABY”A</i><sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Atzilut, Briyah, Yetzirah</i> and <i>Asiyah</i>.</i> in a manner of specifics. In other words, we must understand all the specifics in the matter of the ten <i>sefirot</i> of <i>ABY”A</i>, their lights and vessels, and their vestments, one within the other.
Moreover, we must understand all their particulars, even how each <i>sefirah</i> divides into its particular specifics.
For example, we even [must understand] the aspect of <i>Chessed</i> of <i>Malchut</i> that is in <i>Chochmah</i>, that is in <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Chessed</i>, and the like.
[Furthermore, we must understand] the matter of the unifications and inclusions [of the <i>sefirot</i>] in the aspect of the <i>Keter</i> of each world. [<i>Keter</i>] is the aspect of the intermediary between the upper world and the world that is below it.
Briefly, this general principle is known, that from the aspect of <i>Malchut</i> of the upper [world], there comes about the <i>Keter</i> of the lower [world]. This [principle] applies even to the highest levels.
However, all those who contemplate should first contemplate upon the Primal Source, Who is called,<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar Bereshit 33a. (<i>Mekora D’Koola</i>)</i> “The Source of everything” (<i>Mekora D’Koola</i>).
That is, [he should contemplate] the aspect of the Essential Self of the Unlimited Light (<i>Atzmoot Ohr Ein Sof</i>), [even] before the aforementioned first <i>Tzimtzum</i> which is called “the empty place” (<i>Makom Panooy</i>).
There too [he should contemplate] specifically in a manner of particulars.
This [contemplation] is known as the “elongation of the One-<i>Echad</i>-אחד,”<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Brachot 13b</i> [signifying that one is to contemplate] specifically upon the Simple Unity of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה.
In general, this [Simple Unity] is divided into three levels, each of which includes ten <i>sefirot</i>.
These [three levels are called] <i>Yachid-</i>Singular<i>, Echad-</i> One, and <i>Kadmon-</i>Preceding. All this is still within the aspect of the Essential Self of the Unlimited Light (<i>Atzmoot Ohr Ein Sof</i>) before the aforementioned first <i>Tzimtzum</i>.
The aspect of <i>Yachid</i>-Singular, connotes that He is literally alone.
This is higher than the unity of parts, which is called <i>Echad</i>-One, as known.
Accordingly, in the aspect of the actual Essential Self of the Unlimited Light, it is not yet fitting to discuss the matter of the ten <i>sefirot</i> at all.
For example, [to say] “<i>Malchut</i> of the Unlimited One (<i>Ein Sof</i>)” would automatically imply an understanding that it was preceded by the aspect of <i>Keter</i> and <i>Chochmah</i> etc.
Now, in truth, even the aspect of the Essential Self of the Unlimited Light, which is called “Alone,” includes ten <i>sefirot</i> within itself.
However, they are called,<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">See Introduction to Tikkunei Zohar 17a-b</i> “He is wise, but not with a knowable wisdom etc.,” to the point that we say, “He is not of any of these qualities at all,” as known.
The explanation of the matter is that, in truth, just as the Essential Self of the Unlimited One (<i>Atzmoot Ein Sof</i>) is an absolutely simple light, so is this [the case] with His light and ray, which is called the Unlimited Light (<i>Ohr Ein Sof</i>).
As mentioned previously, this is the meaning of “Before the creation of the world there was Him and His Name alone.”<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">Pirkei d’Rabbi Eliezer, Ch 3.</i>
This [level] is called the “upper purity.”<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Tehiroo Ila’a</i></i>
This is the matter of the revelation of the light of His Essential Self, specifically as it is.
This [level] is called <i>Yachid-</i>Singular. That is, there is nothing besides Him that the terminology of “unity” or “singularity” may be applied to.
This is the meaning of,<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">Introduction to Tikkunei Zohar 17a</i> “You are one, but not in enumeration” of ten.
However, from the fact that they stated, “He is wise, but not with a knowable wisdom etc.,” it is, nonetheless, [apparent] that there are various categories and levels [such as] wise, understanding, merciful etc.
[Nevertheless,] all this is not [stated] in regard to His Essential Self, but only in regard to what He estimated within Himself in potential, of what is destined to be in actuality, after the aforementioned first <i>Tzimtzum</i>
(As written in <i>Mikdash Melech</i>,<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote">See Mikdash Melech to Zohar I 15a.</i> quoting the <i>Arizal</i> himself, and as explained elsewhere at length.)
This is also the meaning of the first general teaching of the <i>Zohar</i>,<sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar I 15a</i> “In the beginning of the rule of the King, He engraved an engraving in the Upper Purity.”
The explanation of this is that in the aforementioned Essence of the revelation of His simple light, which is called the Upper Purity, “He engraved an engraving,” which is the matter of engraving letters.
“The beginning of the rule [of the King],” refers to when it arose in His simple desire. This is the aspect of <i>Keter</i>, whereas the aspect of the letters which He engraved is the aspect of <i>Malchut</i> of the Limitless Light of the Unlimited One.
If this is the case, then there is a beginning and end, a <i>Keter</i> and <i>Malchut</i>, even in the aspect of the Essence of the Limitless Light of the Unlimited One.
The explanation of this is that it arose in His simple thought and desire, “<i>Ana Emloch –</i> I shall rule.”<sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote">See Magid Dvarav l’Yaakov of the Maggid of Mezhritch, Ch. 83 and elsewhere.</i>
All this is still totally within His Essential Self. [That is, it] still precedes the matter of the estimation within Himself, in potentiality, of what His revealed desire for Kingship will be, after the first <i>Tzimtzum,</i> which is called the “empty place” (<i>Makom Panuy</i>).
The analogy for this, as known, is from the powers of the [human] soul, as they come into revelation from desire until action.
All these [powers] and their specifics exist in the concealed light of the essence of the soul, which is called the aspect of <i>Yechidah</i>.
For example, when a person [who] desires kindness and goodness, [wants] to do a particular act of goodness, this comes about because he possesses this quality of kindness and goodness in the aspect of the essence of his soul, which is called <i>Yechidah</i>.
It is because of this that this desire for kindness comes into revelation from its concealment.
Now, we must say, with certainty, that in the essence of his soul, this desire for kindness exists in a way of an essential <i>Heyulie</i> power.
[That is to say,] it includes within itself everything that he may come to desire of kindness and goodness, in every particular specific that may be asked of him.
If this is the case, we must say that prior to his revealed arousal of desire and will to express his kindness in this particular deed, it was included in the essential <i>Heyulie</i> desire for kindness.
It then came out of the <i>Heyulie</i> state to become revealed in this particular act.
Furthermore, we observe that in the [revealed] desire for kindness, there is intellect, wisdom, emotions, thought, speech and action.
It therefore is certain that in the source of this desire for kindness, while it was concealed in the essential <i>Heyulie</i> desire for kindness, there too, it included these divisions of intellect, emotions, thought, speech and action, which it possesses.
However, in the aspect of the essential <i>Heyulie</i> desire for kindness, as it exists prior to being expressed into a particular thing, even though, there too, there are divisions of intellect and emotions etc., nevertheless, they are included and unified in an ultimate state [of unity].
This likewise applies to any other particular essential qualities, such as the quality of <i>Gevurah</i>-Judgment<i>, Tiferet</i>-Beauty (or Mercy)<i>,</i> or <i>Netzach-</i>Conquest<i>,</i> and the like. [This is so,] until the quality of <i>Malchut-</i>Kingship<i>,</i> which is the quality of leadership.
Certainly, it too includes ten [qualities, such as] the desire and will for kingship, the wisdom [for kingship], emotions, thoughts, [speech and action] etc.
However, before it comes to an aspect of revelation in a particular thing, such as ruling over a specific country etc., they were absolutely included and unified in the aspect of the essential <i>Heyulie</i> desire for kingship.
[This is] similar to [what was explained] regarding the aforementioned essential <i>Heyulie</i> desire for kindness.
If so, it is automatically understood [in regard to] the essential <i>Heyulie</i> qualities of <i>Keter, Chochmah, Binah, Chessed, Gevurah, Tiferet, Netzach, Hod, Yesod</i> and <i>Malchut</i>, [all of] which are in the essence of the soul, that it is not fitting to speak of them using a terminology of “unification” or “inclusion,” [stating that they are “unified”] in the essence of the soul, which is called <i>Yechidah</i>.
This is because they are not at all separate from the essence.
For example, with the aforementioned quality of the <i>Heyulie</i> desire for kindness that is embedded in the essential nature [of a kind person, it cannot be spoken of as being separate from his essential self].
The essence of the soul itself is even higher than being [called] an “essential desire for kindness,” since this [kindness] is only a particular of the actual essential being, which is the ultimate of simplicity.
However, [although this desire for kindness is only a single particular that is drawn from the essence,] it nonetheless is impossible to say about it, that it “unifies” with the <i>Heyulie</i> quality of <i>Netzach</i> – Conquest, which is [also] embedded in the essence of the soul. This is because the two are both absolutely unified with the essence, and are not at all separate from the self.
By way of analogy, the power of movement, that actually is included in the essence of an animal, even before it moves at all, is not at all separate from the essential self of the animal.
Now, even though in the revelation of this [<i>Heyulie</i>] power of movement, [that is, when the animal] makes a particular movement, it divides into many particular ways [of moving], it [nonetheless] is impossible to state that all the particular movements were “included” and “unified” while the power of movement was still included in the essence of the animal.
This is because, at that point, it was not within the category or definition of “movement” at all, not generally and not particularly.
This is likewise [the case] with the aspect of the revelation and spreading forth of the life force to enliven the entire body, while it still is completely included in the essential spirit of life.
Even though [this life force] divides into [various powers, such as] sight to the eye and hearing to the ear etc.
Certainly, even before it came forth to materialize in the eye and ear in actuality, there was included [in this life force] a spiritual power and life force of sight [destined] to the eye, in and of itself, and a spiritual power and life force of hearing [destined] for the ear, in and of itself etc.
Nonetheless, before the essence of the soul came to the aspect of spreading forth life force, even though it was included in it, nonetheless, it is in the same way that the aforementioned power of movement is included in the essential self of an animal.
It is only applicable to [use a terminology of] inclusion and unification of “sight” and “hearing” when [these powers] are <b>destined</b> and <b>prepared</b> to come into revelation in actuality, to enliven [the body].
However, while they were still completely included in the essence of the soul, it was as if this [aspect of] “spreading forth of life force” was completely nonexistent.
This is because the essential self of the soul is much higher than the aspect of “spreading forth,” except that it includes within itself this [<b>ability</b>] to spread forth [and enliven] as well, just as the essential self of an animal includes the power of movement within itself, as explained above.
If so, then how is it fitting or proper [to use terms] such as the aspects of “unification” and “inclusion” of the particular light and life force?
[Rather,] it is only fitting in regard to the particular divisions of life force that are <b>destined</b> and <b>prepared</b> to spread forth into revelation.
From this we are forced to say that all these particulars that spread forth [into revelation], [exist] completely included within the essence, for if this was not so, from where did these particulars in the spreading forth of revelation come?
This is similar to the light and rays that are included in the self of the sun. [In other words,] concealed within [the sun] are all the particular ways of the spreading forth of its rays etc. This will suffice for those of understanding.
We thus find that there are three levels, one following the other, that are drawn from the actual essence of the soul, which is called the <i>Yechidah</i>.
The first [level] is the ten essential <i>Heyulie</i> powers, such as the essential <i>Heyulie</i> desire for kindness, and the like.
They are absolutely and totally included in [the essence]. [This is] like the inclusion of the power of movement in the essential self of an animal, or like the inclusion of the [power] to “spread forth life force,” which is included in the essential self [of the soul], as explained above.
In regard to these [<i>Heyulie</i> powers,] it is not fitting to use a terminology of “unification of separate parts together.”
This is because they are completely included in the essential self, and it is as if they have no existence at all, as explained above.
The second [level] is the aspect of the spreading forth of the ten powers, as they are prepared to come into revelation.
This is like the essential <i>Heyulie</i> desire for kindness, as it comes to do a particular act of kindness.
[However, this is] still before it is drawn out into actuality. Rather, it is only <b>destined</b> and <b>prepared</b> to come out to this particular [act of kindness].
Here, [on this level,] the matter of “unification” of the many particulars which are within it, is applicable.
For example, [included within this are] the intellect and emotions of this desire for kindness, which are drawn from their concealment in the general <i>Heyulie</i>.
The third [level] is when it is drawn to that particular [act of kindness], only that it has not yet come into [actuality] due to some lacking or obstacle.
However, the preparation itself is already complete. The only thing that is missing is for it to come out and be revealed in actuality.
In other words, he already estimated within himself, in a manner of particulars, [everything that is necessary to bring] this thing into actuality.
This is to say that he estimated within himself, in potential, what is necessary [for him] to bring it into actuality.
In the aforementioned allegory of the power of movement, [this can be seen] when it is prepared and destined to come into revelation in a particular [movement].
In the example of the spreading forth of life force to enliven the body, [this can be seen] when it is prepared to come out [of the essence].
At this point, all the particular life forces [like sight and hearing] are completely included in a general unity.
After this, he estimates within himself and prepares within his power of movement, how to move in a particular way.
Similarly, [regarding the example of the influx of life force], there is the estimation of the revelation and spreading forth of the spirit of life, as he prepares within himself to enliven [the body] in actuality.
Another example is the power of growth, as it is prepared to grow in actuality. Here too, there are these three levels.
Furthermore, [all three of these levels] are before anything came out into actuality.
For example, in the [power of] movement, [this entire estimation] is before any actual physical movement. Or, in the spiritual life force, [this preparation] is before it actually comes into a physical body.
Then, there is a change from a spiritual existence to a physical existence, such as a physical movement and physical life force.
The same is true in the example of physical growth.
For this [change of existence] to be, it is necessary for there to be an initial <i>Tzimtzum</i> - contraction and restraint in the revelation of this spiritual [<i>Heyulie</i>]. This is so that there may be [a transition] from spiritual to physical (as will be explained in chapter 12).

Chapter 11

Now, the analogue for all that was mentioned above about the [human] soul, may be understood by [a person] who conceptualizes [how it is] above in the Essential Self of the Limitless Light of the Unlimited One before the <i>Tzimtzum</i>, which is called <i>Yachid-</i>Singular.
Included [in the level of <i>Yachid</i>] there also are ten <i>sefirot</i>. These are called “the ten hidden <i>sefirot</i>”<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">In Hebrew this is “<i>Eser Sefirot Hagnoozot BeHelem Ha’Atzmoot</i>.”</i> that are hidden in the Essential Self, literally.
For example, the simple desire for the entire chaining down, which is a specific [line of revelation], arose because of the desire for kindness included in the aspect of the Essential Self of the Limitless Light of the Unlimited One.
This is as stated in the introduction of <i>Etz Chayim</i>,<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">See Etz Chayim, Shaar 1, Anaf 2. Also see, Etz Chayim Shaar HaKlallim, Chapter 1. There it states, “When it arose in His desire to create the world, blessed be His name, in order to bestow goodness unto His creatures…” This indicates that the desire for creation comes from a desire to bestow kindness and goodness.</i> “When it arose in His simple desire.”
Certainly, the reason for this arousal of the simple desire of His Essential Self is only because in His Essential Self, “He desires kindness.”<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">Micah 7:18</i>
It therefore arose in His desire to bestow His goodness and kindness, to be a source for the source of the chaining down of the line and thread (<i>Kav V’Chut</i>).
This is like the aforementioned analogy, that because of the essential [<i>Heyulie</i>] desire for kindness that is included in the aspect of the <i>Yechidah</i> [of one’s soul], it arises in the desire of [a person] to do goodness and kindness through a specific act, as explained previously.
[That is,] it becomes revealed from its concealment in the <i>Heyulie</i> for the desire of kindness, to include every particular that will ever arise in his desire to bestow goodness.
Everything [that becomes revealed] comes because of [this <i>Heyulie</i>], and because of its strength.
Furthermore, the revelation of the desire which comes because of this [<i>Heyulie</i>] desire for kindness includes ten [<i>sefirot</i>]; <i>ChaBa”D</i>,<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">This is an acronym for the three intellectual <i>sefirot</i>, <i>Chochmah</i>, <i>Binah</i> and <i>Da’at</i>.</i> emotions (<i>Midot</i>) etc.
From this we must conclude that also the aspect of the <i>Heyulie</i> desire for kindness, which is literally included in the Essential Self of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, likewise includes ten [<i>sefirot</i>]; intellect and emotions etc.
However, it is not fitting to speak of them using terms of “inclusion” or “unification,” since they still are included in His Essential Self in the way of a <i>Heyulie</i>.
This is likewise so in regard to the other qualities, such as the qualities of <i>Gevurah</i>, <i>Netzach</i> or <i>Tiferet</i> etc.
They all are included in the Essential Self of the Limitless Light of the Unlimited One, which is called the “Upper Purity.”
It is this [level] that is called <i>Yachid</i> – Singular, and is higher than <i>Echad Pashut</i> – Simple Oneness [or Unity].
This [inclusion] is so, until the quality of Kingship in the Essential Self of the Unlimited Light, which is called <i>Malchut</i> of the Unlimited One.
It too is included in the aspect of the essential <i>Heyulie</i> of the Essential Self of the Limitless Light of the Unlimited One.
[Furthermore,] it is literally Unlimited.
Just as the desire for kindness of the Essential Self is completely Unlimited, and [just as] there is no limit to His wisdom, likewise, the quality of “ruling over” (<i>Malchut</i>) which is included in the Essential Self of the Limitless Light, is Unlimited.
Moreover, in the concealment of the Essential Self, it [too] includes ten [<i>sefirot</i>]. These are the desire, pleasure, wisdom and emotions of the quality of Kingship – <i>Malchut</i>.
However, the matter of “I shall rule” which arose in His simple desire and thought, represents [the essential <i>Heyulie</i> desire for kingship] as it comes out of the concealment of the <i>Heyulie</i>, to be revealed in a particular thing; [namely,] the entire chaining down of the worlds.
This is similar to what was explained above in regard to the quality of the desire for kindness in a human being below, and as explained in the analogy of the ten powers that are included in the aspect of the <i>Yechidah</i> [of the soul], [that they are there] in a way of an essential <i>Heyulie</i>.
[That is,] they are not at all separate from the essential self.
Similarly, [analogies were given of] the power of movement, which is included in the essential self of an animal, and the <i>Heyulie</i> ability to spread forth life force [and enliven], which is included in the essential self of the soul, literally, as previously explained.
Lower than this [level] is the aspect of the Unlimited Light that radiates and spreads forth.
However, this all is still in the aspect of His Essential Self, before the <i>Tzimtzum</i>.
This [level] is what is called “<i>Achdut HaPshuta</i> – Simple Oneness [or Unity].”
Here it is possible [to speak of the] “inclusion” and “unification” of the ten <i>sefirot</i>, [however,] they too are called<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">See Sefer Yetzirah Chapter 1, Mishnah 2 – “<i>Eser Sefirot Blimah</i>”</i> “ten <i>sefirot</i> without ‘whatness,’” because they nonetheless are still beyond the aspect of preparing to influence below, in [actual] revelation.
However, it is already prepared to come out of the <i>Heyulie</i> state [into revelation] into a particular matter.
For example, in the aforementioned analogy of the <i>Heyulie</i> desire for kindness, [this is] when it comes to the realm of will and desire [to be expressed in actuality] in the chaining down of a line [of action].
Although, even within Himself, this has not yet come out into complete revelation, nonetheless, here the aspects of “unity” and “inclusion” are applicable.
However, it is called a “Simple Unity” because it still is within the light of the His Essential Self, which is the ultimate simplicity.
For example, in the [<i>Heyulie</i>] desire for kindness there are the aspects of division of intellect and emotions etc., even before it comes into any [actual] revelation whatsoever. [It is] because of [these concealed qualities] that it arose in His [revealed] desire and wisdom to bestow goodness, as was previously explained in regard to the second level in the human soul.
Now, the third [level] is when from the aspect of this desire for kindness, it already arose in the desire and intellect etc.
An entire estimation is ready in “letters,” which He estimates within Himself of how the influence will actually be drawn outside of His Essential Self.
For example, in the analogy of the power of movement, [this is when he] prepares how to move.
[This may also be compared] to the power of the life force of the soul, as it is prepared to enliven.
[This is to say that] they already are prepared and estimated in a limited way, as previously explained in regard to the third level in the [human] soul.
Similarly, [in regard to <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, Above, this [level] is what He estimated within the Essential Self of the Limitless Light, which is called the “Upper Purity.”
[That is, He makes] an estimation of how everything that He desires in the entire chaining down [will be revealed], as an actual line of revelation, all the way until the end of world of <i>Asiyah</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">The world of Actualization.</i>
This then, is [the meaning of] the statement,<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar I 15a</i> “He engraved an engraving in the Upper Purity,” as mentioned previously.
This level is called <i>Kadmon</i>-Preceding. In other words, this is the desire for the manner of the influence, which precedes any actual revealed influence.
[All] this is still prior to the first <i>Tzimtzum</i>, which is called the “Void” or “Empty Place,”<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote">The first <i>Tzimtzum</i> is called the Void-<i>Challal-</i>חלל, and Empty Space-<i>Makom Panooy</i>-מקום פנוי.</i> as mentioned previously. This will suffice for those of understanding.
Now, the fourth level is how after the <i>Tzimtzum</i> (withdrawal), there remained an aspect of an impression (<i>Reshimu</i>), from which the line [of limited revelation] was drawn.
This is generally [called] the “Lower Purity,”<sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote">Tihiru Tata’ah</i> which is the general encompassing [light] for the entire chaining down of the line.
[The line] comes as an aspect of influence lower than the Essential Self, as in the analogy of the life force which spreads forth in revelation, to enliven [the body].
It is also similar to the power of movement, which spreads forth to actually move [the body] in a revealed way.
[Here], there is a change from spiritual existence to physical existence, as previously mentioned.
This is [also] similar to the physical growth [of a plant, which comes] from the spiritual [power] of growth.
Likewise, this is the difference between the light which follows <i>Tzimtzum</i>, compared to the Essential Light of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, that precedes <i>Tzimtzum</i>.
Because of this [infinite difference], the matter of <i>Tzimtzum</i> was necessary. It was specifically so that there could be a [limited] ray and line of light, the purpose of which is to be the source of the worlds of <i>ABY”A</i>,<sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Atzilut, Briyah, Yetzirah</i> and <i>Asiyah</i>.</i> as known.
Nevertheless, all the particular specifics of the ten <i>sefirot</i> of <i>ABY”A</i> were originally included in the Essential Self of the Limitless Light of the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, in the aspect of an Essential <i>Heyulie</i>.
Afterwards, by means of the <i>Tzimtzum</i>, it changes [to be revealed] in a limited fashion, according to the general influence of the line, which is the aspect of the [general] encompassing [light].
This is similar to the spiritual life force of the soul when it comes to enliven the body.
Included in the spiritual [life force] are all the particular specifics of the physical life force, such as physical sight and hearing etc., as explained previously.
(The matter of the Restraint-<i>Tzimtzum</i> and the Impression-<i>Reshimu</i> which remained, will be explained in the next chapter.)
(This then, is the general explanation for that which is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote">See the beginning of the daily prayers, “<i>Baruch She’amar</i>.”</i> “Blessed is He who said and the world came into being.”
The explanation is that “He said” in concealment, in His simple desire within <i>Malchut</i> of the Unlimited One (<i>Ein Sof</i>), as it still is included within the aforementioned essential [<i>Heyulie</i>] desire for kindness.
Afterwards, “[and the world] came into being,” [refers to] the revelation of light which spreads forth for a specific matter to chain down, to become the source of all the worlds.
The explanation of “the world came to be,” is [that it came to be] specifically from that which He estimated within Himself in potential etc.
For, this is the source for what comes into existence afterwards, that is, the general world which is drawn from the <i>Kav-</i>Line, as mentioned above. This will suffice for those of understanding.
[The prayer then continues,] “Blessed is He.” [The word “He-<i>Hoo</i>-הוא”] is in the third person. This refers to the aspect of the Predecessor of the world – <i>Kadmono Shel Olam</i>.
In other words, this is the aspect of [<i>Kadmon-</i>Preceding<i>,</i> which is] the estimation within Himself in potential.
This is as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">12</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 46:10</i> “He declares the end from the beginning,” that is, from the “beginning” of the <i>Kav-</i>Line, to its end.
The verse then continues, “<i>Umikedem Asher Lo Na’aseh –</i> And from before, [He declares] that which has yet to been done.”
This [too] means, from the Predecessor of the world – <i>Kadmono Shel Olam</i>.
