[This] is also called,<sup class="footnote-marker">13</sup><i class="footnote">Micha 7:20</i> “<i>Yemei Kedem</i> – The preceding days.” That is, it precedes that which is drawn in the <i>Kav</i> [the limited line of revelation].
This refers to the fact that He preceded [and prepared] within Himself in potential, that which is destined to come out in actuality. This will suffice for those of understanding.
[The prayer] then continues, “Blessed is He who says and does.” This refers to what is actually drawn into the <i>Kav</i>.
[The prayer continues,] “Blessed is He who makes the Beginning.” This refers to the entire measure of the stature of <i>Adam Kadmon</i> (Primordial Man) etc.
[The prayer continues,] “Blessed is He who decrees and fulfills” – in the beginning. This refers to the aspect of the <i>Kav HaMidah</i> (The Measuring Line), that precedes <i>Adam Kadmon</i>.
This is the aspect of the <i>Tzimtzum</i> of the <i>Reshimu</i>-Impression, from which the <i>Kav-</i>line is drawn, as known, and as will soon be explained with the help of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He.)

Chapter 12

We must now understand the explanation of the aforementioned matter of the first <i>Tzimtzum</i>, and the aspect of the <i>Reshimu</i>-Impression which remained.
Although it is known to those who are familiar [with these matters], nonetheless, there are many particular details in it.
One must delve very deeply into this [matter], for it is pivotal to true union with the Essential Self of the Limitless Light of the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He.
[That is, the understanding of this is pivotal to the realization of] how everything, even the entire chaining down of the <i>Kav</i>, is literally as nothing before Him.
[This should be contemplated] to the point that a person is capable of focusing his desire, with self-sacrifice, upon the Essential Self of the Limitless Light of the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-<i>יהו״ה</i>, blessed is He, alone.
This is as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">Nechemia 9:6</i> “You are He, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה alone etc.”
This is [also] the meaning of,<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">The blessings of the <i>Shema</i> recital.</i> “The King who is exalted, alone,” [which refers to] the aspect of <i>Malchut</i> of the Unlimited One (<i>Ein Sof</i>) before the <i>Tzimtzum</i>.
That is, “He is exalted” even “over the days of the world” of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>, which are called “the preceding days (<i>Yemei Kedem</i>),” as previously mentioned.
This is [also the explanation of the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">Kings I, 8:27</i> “The heavens, and the heavens of the heavens, cannot contain You”]. “The heavens” refers to the aspect of the general encompassing [light] which follows the <i>Tzimtzum</i>.
“The heavens of the heavens” refers to [the Limitless Light of the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He,] before the <i>Tzimtzum</i>. “They cannot contain You” even in the way of a “vessel for a vessel,” as in “He engraved an engraving in the upper purity.”<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar I 15a</i> This will suffice for those of understanding.
This [matter] is further [emphasized by] the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 73:25</i> “Who have I in the heavens but You? And there is none upon earth that I desire beside You.” “Who have I in the heavens” refers to the general encompassing [light] (<i>Sovev</i>) before the <i>Tzimtzum</i>, which is called “the heavens of the heavens.”
“There is none upon earth that I desire beside You,” refers to the aspect of the <i>Kav V’Chut</i> (Line and Thread), which is the aspect of the general inner, pervading [light] (<i>Memaleh</i>).
Now, as known to those who have done the analysis, there are various different analogies and ways to explain the matter of the <i>Tzimtzum</i>, which is called “the empty place.”
[However,] they all arrive at one general point; that in order for the Limitless Light of the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, to be expressed in a limited way, in the aspect of a [thin] line [of revelation], He necessarily restrained His essential light, so that it would remain concealed in His Essential Self.
[This is necessary, so that] not all of it would shine forth, but only an infinitesimal amount.
This is in order that the light could afterwards be drawn down [into revelation] in [a way of] a qualitative leap of [diminished] value.
This is analogous to the brilliance of a deep and broad concept [as it exists in the] self of the teacher.
In order for him to draw [this concept] to the student, who is not [intellectually] comparable to him, the teacher must conceal the entire depth of his comprehension within himself, so that all that is left is but an aspect of an impression, which is like a single point from all the depth and breadth.
This is not to say that [his understanding] was completely withdrawn and concealed.
Rather, it is like one who relates a teaching in a brief way. He himself has the entire depth and breadth of the logical arguments in his intellect, only that during the time that he states his ruling briefly, they are temporarily included and concealed within himself.
However, as soon as he is questioned [about it], he can expand on the subject.
Only that in order for the student to understand, through this short [ruling], he temporarily conceals [the depth and breadth of it] within himself, as explained elsewhere at length.<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">See Likutei Torah, Vayikra (in the additions) 52c and on; Also see Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Vayikra, Vol. 2, pg. 921 and on.</i>
Now, the impression, which remains like a point, is not a complete and true <i>Tzimtzum</i> (withdrawal).
[A true and complete <i>Tzimtzum</i>] would be like one who completely withdraws [revelation] and completely conceals, [in which case] the student lacks all [revelation].
Rather, [the explanation of] the matter is that included in this short [ruling] is the entire length. Not a single thing is missing, not even half a thing.
This is similar to how the short rulings of the <i>Mishnah</i> include the entire length of the logical debate of the <i>Talmud</i>.
This is [likewise] similar to how the entire logical debate is not concealed from one who knows it, even when he reviews it to himself briefly.
We find that his knowledge of the length encompasses the entire revelation of the brief [teaching], in a concealed way.
[However,] it is not completely withdrawn, as [in the case of] forgetfulness or the like, as explained elsewhere at length.<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">See Likutei Torah, Vayikra (in the additions) 53c; Also see Sefer HaMa’amarim 5647, pg. 48.</i>
The second type of analogy, which is the life of the soul [as it is invested] in the body, also brings out the same point as above.
This is that in order for there to be a change from the essential spiritual life of the soul, to a [physical] life of flesh, it is necessary for there to be an initial concealment and contraction of the light of the soul.
This is because there is no comparison between them.
Nonetheless, the soul is affected by the occurrences of the body.
Therefore, even the light of the physical life [force] is connected and bound with the spiritual light of the essence.
This is similar to [how the aforementioned] physical growth is bound to the spiritual power of growth.
However, when one’s [physical] limb becomes severed, God forbid, this does not cause a loss to the spiritual light and life force of that limb.
Proof of this is [the fact that] a blind person can give birth to a whole person, as known.
This [shows that] the spiritual [life force] is merely concealed, but still exists, hovering over the physical life force of the body.
This is called “<i>Tzelem Ish</i> – The form of man.”
This is similar to how the aforementioned [breadth and length of] knowledge, which is concealed, [encompasses the brief teaching] etc. (This is all explained elsewhere at length.)
Likewise, when the spiritual power of movement comes into an [actual] physical movement, it becomes constrained within itself.
Nonetheless, the physical movement is connected and bound to the spiritual [power of] movement.
There are many other examples of this as well, such as the matter of having insight into a particular concept, which comes from the power of conceptualization [of his soul], which rests upon him in a concealed [fashion].
However, [we must now] understand the aspect of the <i>Reshimu</i> – Impression, which indicates the withdrawal of everything into concealment, so that only an impression of everything remains.
This is better understood through other analogies and matters. For example, it is like the blueprint<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote">The word for “Impression” is “<i>Reshimu,</i>” and it is worthy to note that this shares the same root as “Blueprint – <i>Roshem</i>.”</i> that the architect drafts.
He is capable of constructing the [entire] building from the small lines of the blueprint. The entire length of the construction is included briefly in the blueprint.
Another example [of a <i>Reshimu-</i>impression] is like someone who makes a sign [for himself] as a memory aide.
The sign [or mnemonic] has no [actual] relation to the essence of the matter, but is merely a memory aide, as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote">Jeremiah 31:20</i> “Make signs for yourself.”
This is a much greater concealment than the [aforementioned analogy of someone who] teaches the summary of the law, which includes the entire [logic] within it.
[For, in that example] there at least is some relationship between the short summary and the lengthy [explanations].
There is another analogy for this <i>Reshimu</i>-Impression, which implies an even greater <i>Tzimtzum</i>-Restraint and concealment.
It is like a person who throws a stone. The power that propels it is separate from the self [of the thrower].
Nonetheless, the entire power of movement is invested within [the stone] in a concealed fashion.
However, there is a great distance of separation from the essential power [of movement] in his hand.
In contrast, this is not the case with the power of movement itself, when he physically moves himself.
[In this case] it is vested within the physical in a more revealed [manner], as mentioned previously.
There is an [analogy of] even greater concealment than this [example of the thrown object], which is similar to the concept of the impression that [one makes] only as a reminder.
This is like when one hints with his hand to a very deep concept or idea.
The physical movement is totally separate from the spiritual thought, but nonetheless, the concept is understood through [the movement].
An even greater concealment is how the light of an intellectual [concept] is [invested] within the [physical] movements of one’s fingers when he writes it down, as explained elsewhere at length.
Now, all the above bring out the same point, as mentioned above.
This is that the aspect of the essence remains concealed and included within this impression and point. This will suffice for those of understanding.

Chapter 13

Now, from all that was said above, we can understand the analogue, as it is above in <i>HaShem</i>’s-יהו״ה Godliness. This is the general matter of the <i>Tzimtzum</i> which is called the “empty place” and is the aspect of the withdrawal and concealment [of His revelation] within Himself, so that afterwards there could be the aspect of an influence of light [in a limited fashion], as mentioned previously.
Now, [this revelation] was not completely removed or concealed.
Rather, it is like the aforementioned analogy [that when a teacher] conveys [a teaching] in a brief manner, his knowledge of all the depth and length becomes concealed within himself.
If so, according to this, even after the entire chaining down of the worlds of <i>ABY”A</i><sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Atzilut, Briyah, Yetzirah</i> and <i>Asiyah</i>.</i> which occupy this “empty place,” the aspect of the concealed light of His Essential Self encompasses and surrounds the entire chaining down of the <i>Kav</i>-line.
Furthermore, just as before the <i>Tzimtzum</i> the light of His Essential Self filled this entire void and empty space, as stated in <i>Etz Chayim</i>, so too, after the <i>Tzimtzum</i> the light of His Essential Self is present, as it is, in an unlimited aspect, literally, except that it is not revealed below, relative to the influence [that reaches] the recipients.
However, in regard to His Essential Self, there is no change here, whatsoever.
This is like the analogy of a person who knows the entire length [of a concept], [so that] even while he is teaching his student in a brief way, if questioned, he can immediately respond [at length].
However, the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 18:12</i> “He sets darkness as His hiding place,” and the statement of our Sages, of blessed memory,<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">See (Rashi) to Talmud Bavli, Shabbat 77b.</i> “At first there was darkness [and then the light returned],” is only speaking in regard to [Creation] below.
This is because [Creation] is only drawn from the aspect of the <i>Reshimu</i>-Impression that remained after the aforementioned concealment.
This then, is the meaning of [the words],<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">In the <i>Amidah</i> prayer.</i> “You are holy, and Your Name,” that is, the Light of <i>HaShem</i>’s-יהו״ה Essential Self, “is Holy” and removed [from Creation].
Similarly, [it states,]<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">In the liturgy of the morning prayers.</i> “You are He before [the creation of the world, and You are He after the creation of the world],” and as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">Malchi 3:6</i> “I <i>HaShem-</i>יהו״ה have not changed.”
This is because, that which He afterwards “reveals deep things out of [the] darkness”<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">Job 12:22</i> and concealment, through the radiance of the <i>Kav-</i>line<i>,</i> specifically [comes] from the same light of <i>HaShem</i>’s-יהו״ה Essential Self that precedes the <i>Tzimtzum.</i>
This is the meaning of “You are He,” as known.
However, the light of <i>HaShem</i>’s-יהו״ה Essential Self is not considered to be encompassing the chaining down [of the worlds] that occupies the “empty place,” as an encompassing [light encompasses] an inner [light], such as the general encompassing [light] of the <i>Kav</i> that encompasses [all the worlds of] <i>ABY”A</i> equally.
This is because it is not yet within the definition or category of an influencing light altogether, so much so, that it cannot even be [considered to be] an aspect of “encompassing [light].”
Rather, it is the light of the Essential Self of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, which is the aspect of His revelation, as He essentially is.
This is why we say,<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote">See the liturgy of the <i>Emet VeYatziv</i> blessing following the <i>Shema</i> in the morning prayers.</i> “He endures and His Name endures.”
Likewise, [the statement,] “Blessed is He and Blessed is His name,” and the like, only refer to the “letters” that He “engraved” in the “upper purity,” which is what He estimated within Himself in potential.<sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote">The Hebrew word “Blessed-<i>Baruch</i>-ברוך” also means “to draw down,” as indicated by the words of Mishnah (Kilayim 7:1), “One who draws down the vine to the ground-<i>Hamavreech et HaGefen</i>-המבריך את הגפן.”</i>
Moreover, [after <i>Tzimtzum</i>] this [impression] too, remains somewhat concealment and withdrawal.
In other words, it is only according to what is necessary for the chaining down (<i>Hishtalshelut</i>) that follows this <i>Tzimtzum.</i> This will suffice for those of understanding.
Likewise, [this may be understood] according to the second analogy mentioned above, of the life force of the soul in the body, in that it changes from spiritual existence to physical existence.
Here too, there is no change at all, since, just as there is a connection and bond between the physical life force and the spiritual life force, in that we see that the soul is affected by the circumstances of the life of the body, but nonetheless, there is no change in the spiritual essence as a result of a lack of spreading forth of life force to a physical limb, as explained previously, so too, there is no change in the light of <i>HaShem</i>’s-יהו״ה Essential Self, even as it radiates after the <i>Tzimtzum</i>.
[This is true] even though [after <i>Tzimtzum</i>] it is [revealed] only according to the capacity of the chaining down [of the worlds].
For, [although] there is a connection and bond between them, nonetheless, according to this analogy, the <i>Tzimtzum</i> of the light into a [limited] line [of revelation] does not cause any change at all in the light of <i>HaShem</i>’s-יהו״ה Essential Self.
This is, likewise, the case according to the third analogy of the physical [movement] that comes from the [spiritual] power of movement (<i>Koach HaTnoo’ah</i>), or [similarly], according to the aforementioned analogy of the insight (<i>Chochmah</i>) that comes from the power to conceptualize (<i>Koach HaMaskil</i>).
All these [analogies] arrive at the same point, as explained before at length. This will suffice for those of understanding.
Now, it was explained above that the aspect of the Impression (<i>Reshimu</i>) is like a summary that includes the entire length within it.
From this it is understood that above, in <i>HaShem</i>’s-יהו״ה Godliness, this is the “Power to Limit” (<i>Koach HaHagbalah</i>) which exists in the Limitless Light, which is essentially utterly unlimited.<sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote">See Avodat HaKodesh (R’ Meir ben Gabay) 1:2</i>
In other words, [He has the ability] to bring the entire radiance of His Essential Unlimited Light, into an aspect of limitation.
This is the matter of the Impression (<i>Reshimu</i>), within which the entirety of the Limitless Light of the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, is included in a limited fashion, similar to the analogy of the brief summary that includes the whole [concept] within it.
This is possible because <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, is all capable, and [therefore] also includes the power to limit (<i>Koach HaMagbil</i>).<sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote">See Avodat HaKodesh (R’ Meir ben Gabay) 1:2 ibid.</i>
[He can therefore] limit and include the entire Light of His Essential Self in a single impression, as explained elsewhere at length.
However, actually, [the above] is not an accurate analogy for the aspect of the Impression (<i>Reshimu</i>) that remained in the aforementioned “void” (<i>Challal</i>) and “empty place” (<i>Makom Panuy</i>).
This is because this [impression] indicates that everything was withdrawn from there.
[It does not indicate] that some light remained, albeit, in a brief and limited fashion. Rather, [in truth], only an impression remained.
This being the case, a truer analogy [for the <i>Reshimu</i> – Impression] is [the analogy] of the short lines and signs of the blueprint that architects draft, which includes the entire length of the construction of the building.
An even greater [example of concealment], is [the analogy of a person who makes] a sign for remembrance, as previously explained.
Similarly, [regarding how it is] above [in regard to <i>HaShem</i>’s-יהו״ה Godliness], it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">12</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 145:7</i> “The remembrance of Your abundant kindness” and the like, [in reference to] the essential kindness of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה.
An even greater [example of] concealment and withdrawal is like the aforementioned analogy of a person who throws a stone.
Similarly, it states in <i>Sefer HaBahir</i>,<sup class="footnote-marker">13</sup><i class="footnote">Also see Midrash Shemot Rabba, Ch. 13.</i> “It is as if it was thrown” etc.
This is because the aspect of the <i>Reshimu</i>-Impression remains separate and distant from the essence of the light.
This power that is concealed within the impression-<i>Reshimu</i> is called the aspect of the “concealed light,” which is separate from the concealed Essential Light of the Unlimited One, blessed is He.
This is similar to the separate force concealed in a thrown stone.
[The force that propels the stone] comes from the power [of movement] of the hand, which already becomes concealed within the self [once the stone leaves his hand].
(This is comparable to all the stars and planets whose orbit is [caused] by the hidden Godly power of movement that comes about in an aspect of a “throw” from the light and Godly force of the nine external vessels of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Asiyah</i>.
This [Godly force that propels them] is a “separate force,” and is called the aspect of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Malchut</i>, which comes out as separate and distant [from its source].
This is unlike [the force vested in] the fingers when [a person] writes or the power of the hand as it [applies] itself [directly] upon an object.
These are [examples of] a revelation of the essential power in [a way of] closeness and is called the aspect of <i>Malchut</i>, as explained elsewhere at length.)
An analogy that is even closer to this [aspect of Impression-<i>Reshimu</i>] is like how an intellectual concept is concealed and hinted at through a physical motion [of the hand].
This is called the aspect of “investment” or “containment” within a separate matter.
This is, likewise, the case when a person writes, [so that] the intellect and wisdom [are invested in] the movements of his fingers, as mentioned previously.
Likewise, above in <i>HaShem</i>’s-יהו״ה Godliness, the aspect of the <i>Reshimu</i> is like something relatively separate, within which the entire Light of His Essential Self is invested in a concealed manner. This will suffice for those of understanding.
Now, through all the above [analogies], we have, at least, understood the general matter of the <i>Reshimu</i>-Impression.
That is, though it comes in an aspect of complete withdrawal, so that all that remains in it is [just] an aspect of total brevity and “hinting” or [something] like a separate power, in a way of great brevity, nonetheless, all the particulars in the [entire] chaining down of the <i>Kav-</i>line [of limited revelation] come out of, and are drawn from this <i>Reshimu</i>-Impression itself.
This is because of [the fact] that this <i>Reshimu</i> – Impression includes everything within it, albeit in a concealed manner. It is for this reason that [afterwards] everything can come into revelation, through the aspect of the <i>Kav</i>-Line, until the end of <i>Asiyah</i> (the world of Actualization).
This is like the statement,<sup class="footnote-marker">14</sup><i class="footnote">See <i>Zichronot</i> blessing of the <i>Rosh HaShanah Musaf</i> prayer.</i> “All of creation is not concealed from You.”
It specifically says “from You.” This is [to indicate] that everything is done [by] and drawn into revelation according to how it arose in His simple desire, in the essential light which preceded the <i>Tzimtzum</i>.
[That is, according to] how He estimated within Himself.
For, with this primal thought that He estimates within Himself, “He sees and gazes at everything in one glance.”<sup class="footnote-marker">15</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Rosh Hashanah 18a.</i>
That is, [He sees] that which is hidden and concealed in the brevity and “hint” of the <i>Reshimu</i>.
This is analogous to the architect’s blueprint. It is specifically from this [blueprint], that he will know [how] to make all the particular details of the entire length of the actual construction, from beginning to end.
However, in order that he will not forget his [original] reasoning and considerations due to the lengthiness of the subject, he drafts a blueprint as a reminder.
In this way he will not veer from [his original intent] and he will not have to rethink [the matter] within himself, anew.
This is likewise the case in the matter of making mnemonics for a deep study within himself.
These are beneficial to him, in [the fact] that through them, he [is reminded and] knows the entire length of the analysis of the depth within himself, so that he will not stray from [his reasoning] etc.
Likewise, this aspect of the <i>Reshimu</i>-Impression, within which the entire light of the Essential Self of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, is concealed and included in the way of a “summary” or “hint,” is itself the source for the drawing down of the line and thread-<i>Kav V’Chut</i>.
[It is the source both] of the aspects of the encompassing [lights] and the inner, pervading [lights, of the entire Creation,] from beginning to end.
This is so that everything should be [created exactly] as it arose in His simple desire and wisdom, in the Essence of the Unlimited Light, literally.
This is the meaning of what is stated elsewhere, that a point contains two opposites, concealment and revelation.
It is concealment relative to everything above it, [but, on the other hand] all revelation to the recipients comes about specifically from it.
This [revelation] is the aspect of the <i>Kav</i>-Line, that is drawn from the <i>Reshimu</i>-Impression.
[The <i>Kav-</i>Line] is in the shape of [the letter] <i>Vav</i> (ו), which begins as a <i>Yod</i> (י) and is drawn down, as explained elsewhere at length.
Through all the above, the general matter of the <i>Tzimtzum</i> [which is called] the “empty place,” and the aspects of the <i>Reshimu</i> and the <i>Kav,</i> may be understood.
[It is understood] that this is a self-limitation only in order that everything will be drawn into revelation.
This then is the meaning of [the verse],<sup class="footnote-marker">16</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 36:10</i> “With You is the source of life, [in Your light is seen light.” That is,] from Your essential light there is seen a [secondary] “offspring” light, which is the aspect of the line-<i>Kav</i>, as will be explained with the help of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He.
Now, the entire purpose of man is the deep contemplation of this matter, and the like.
It is specifically through this, that he will come to the true unity of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, binding his soul to the Supernal Life of all lives, which is the Essential Self of the Limitless Light of the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, literally, for the above-mentioned reason. This will suffice for those of understanding.

Chapter 14

We must now understand the aspect of the Line and Thread (<i>Kav V’Chut</i>), that is drawn from the aspect of the aforementioned <i>Reshimu</i>, in a manner of particulars.
Firstly, we must understand the general matter of [the <i>Kav-</i>Line]; that it is the literal opposite of the aspect of the aforementioned <i>Reshimu-</i>Impression.
This is because a point indicates the concealment and withdrawal of everything, so that only a single point remains.
Moreover, this point or impression specifically indicates the aspect of the absence of spreading forth below.
In other words, the matter [of a point] is the absence of extension and revelation to a length and width.
This is like the form of the letter <i>Yod</i> (י) which has no inner space, as known.
Now, regarding the matter of the <i>Tzimtzum</i> of [the <i>Reshimu</i>] from above, in other words, that [everything] remains in the aspect of a point alone, it is possible that its opposite can come from this.
This is because, the result of the [<i>Tzimtzim</i>] is that everything becomes included in the [<i>Reshimu</i>] in a brief and “hinted” manner, and the like.
On the contrary, this is the main cause of all revelation of influence [from the <i>Reshimu</i>], as mentioned previously.
However, at first glance, the fact that this point indicates a complete absence of spreading forth below, certainly could be considered to be a complete and true <i>Tzimtzum</i>.
[That is,] it completely hides and conceals, making it impossible for light to come and [be revealed] below.
This being the case, how is it possible that the opposite [of this point], which is the drawing down and spreading forth of the <i>Kav</i> – line, can be drawn from it?
Rather, as known, the [explanation of the] matter is that, in truth, a point and a line are not two opposites, for a line is drawn from a point, and by the joining of many points, a line is made.
Rather, the [explanation of the] matter, as known, is that a point is like a <i>Heyulie</i> relative to a line (<i>Kav</i>).
It [therefore] is similar to every [type] of <i>Heyulie</i> or simple substance.
[This is to say that] though [a Heyulie] is specifically in a state of the absence of spreading forth, nonetheless, this is not at all by necessity, but only because of what a <i>Heyulie</i> essentially is, in that as of yet, it is higher than the aspect of spreading forth.
It thus has not [yet] descended from its essential state.
[For example,] this is like the <i>Heyulie</i> of the life-force of an animal to enliven [the body] in a revealed fashion, as it still is included in its essential self, in that it has yet to spread forth to enliven [the body].
Similarly, it is like the <i>Heyulie</i>-ability of movement as it is in the essential self, before it spreads forth to move.
And is likewise like the power of growth before it spreads forth to cause growth
And like the power of intellect before it spreads forth to conceptualize, and there are many other similar examples.
It therefore is understood that, in and of itself, this absence of spreading forth cannot be called a true <i>Tzimtzum</i>.
On the contrary, it is the essential <i>Heyulie</i> power, from which everything is revealed and spreads forth.
In a similar manner we may understand the aspect of a point relative to a line.
[That is], its lack of spreading forth is only because, as of yet, it is an essential aspect, and is above the aspect of “spreading forth.”
Now, although [the <i>Reshimu</i>] comes about through the <i>Tzimtzum</i> of everything, so that nothing remains except for a single point, as mentioned above, however, this itself indicates that the entire aspect of the Essential Self is included in it.
Since this is the case, it therefore does not spread forth downward.
This is analogous to a <i>Talmid</i> (student) in the presence of his <i>Rebbe</i>.
As long as he is preoccupied with absorbing [the teachings] and is [focused], similar to a point, with a concentration (<i>Tzimtzum</i>) of his whole essence, he cannot “give out” by influencing his fellow [with explanations of the teachings].
However, after he has received [the teachings], the opposite [is true].
For it is from this very <i>Tzimtzum,</i> in that he was [focused] like a point, that all the influence spreads forth and is drawn out to his fellow, as explained elsewhere.
From all this we understand that the line which extends from the point, is just like the aspect of spreading forth from an essential <i>Heyulie</i>.
However, [in regard to] the fact that it is drawn out in an aspect of a “short line,” it is explained elsewhere that just as a point is the aspect of a <i>Heyulie</i> relative to a line, likewise, a line is the aspect of a <i>Heyulie</i> relative to the aspects of the length and breadth of a plane.
For as known, although the line-<i>Kav</i> comes in an aspect of being drawn down and spreading from above to below, nonetheless, it is not [yet] a specific manner of drawing down [or revelation] at all.
Rather, it only is that the light has been drawn from above to below.
It is through this that the aspects of “above” and “below,” from influencer to recipient, comes about.
This is not the case in regard to the <i>Heyulie</i> of a point, in which there is no up or down, beginning, middle, or end, as known.
(This is the [meaning] of the statement in <i>Etz Chayim,</i><sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">Etz Cha<i>yim</i>, Drush Igullim V’Yosher, Shaar 1, Anaf 2</i> that the whole essential [purpose of the] radiance of the line-<i>Kav</i> is solely to bring about the aspects of “up” and “down,” as will be explained.)
This [<i>Kav</i>] is analogous to a “Builder’s Rod,” which is not [counted] into the measurements of the length and width of the area of the building itself.
Nonetheless, with [the builder’s rod, the builder] measures all the measurements of the length and width [of the building].
[However, the builder’s rod] itself is only like a short line which includes all possible measurements of length and width.
Thus, the form of the <i>Kav</i>-Line is an aspect of a <i>Heyulie</i> relative to the plane of the letters and gives them their length and width, such as the lines of the letter <i>Beit</i>-ב, as stated elsewhere.
According to this, even the beginning of the extension of the line from the point, although it comes in an aspect of spreading forth and drawing down, nonetheless, it still is in an aspect of a <i>Heyulie</i>, in that it includes many ways that length and width may be drawn out within measure.
This is why it is called the <i>Kav HaMidah –</i> The Measuring Line, as is known.
This is indicated by its form, which in essence is short, and merely issues from above to below.
Nonetheless, included within this issuance is everything that was concealed in the <i>Heyulie</i> of the point, except that it [now] comes in a way of being drawn down.
This [ability] comes from the power of the essential light that is concealed in the Essential Self of the Influencer, before being concentrated (<i>Tzimtzum</i>) into a single point.
However, now it comes [into revelation] solely by way of a line, and not as it [originally] was in the Essence of the Influencer, where it was with the great expanse of His actual Essential Self.
In this <i>Kav-</i>line, the light of the Essential Self only comes according to the capacity of the recipients.
However, it nonetheless possesses a likeness to the light of the Essential Self that is concealed in the point, except that it [now] comes [into revelation] in a manner of being drawn down.
It therefore comes in the form of a <i>Kav</i>-line.
This [<i>Kav-</i>line] is the aspect of a <i>Heyulie</i> for all the light and influence [given] to the recipients. This will suffice for those of understanding.

Chapter 15

Now, the analogue of all of the above may be understood regarding the aspect of the impression-<i>Reshimu</i> which remained in the aforementioned “void” and “empty space.”
(This is the <i>Yod-</i>י of <i>Sa”G-</i>ס״ג (יו״ד ה״י וא״ו ה״י) of the Upper Purity, as stated in the book <i>Emek HaMelech</i>.)<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">See <i>Emek HaMelech</i> – Shaar “<i>Yod</i> of the name of <i>Sa”G-</i>ס״ג.”</i>
This is the aspect of the <i>Heyulie</i>, which includes everything that will [afterwards] branch out from it [into revelation] by means of the <i>Kav V’Chut</i> – Line and Thread.
Now, although all the Light of the Essential Self of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, was concealed until only the aspect of an impression remained, nonetheless, as mentioned above, specifically through this <i>Tzimtzum</i>, everything is certainly included in it in short form.
Furthermore, although [the point of the <i>Reshimu</i>] indicates the absence of spreading down, [nonetheless] this is not an aspect of total <i>Tzimtzum.</i>
It is only because it is an [essential] <i>Heyulie</i> power [that it does not spread down], as explained above.
Rather, since it is a power that restrains the entire original light, therefore it does not spread forth except by way of a line, according to the manner [necessary] for influence, as mention before.
Nevertheless, from the above it is understood that this line-<i>Kav</i> possesses the power of the original [Limitless] Light that preceded the <i>Tzimtzum.</i>
[Furthermore, this light] is [still] literally in an aspect of Limitlessness, except that it comes by way of a line, according to the manner [in which] the recipients [are capable of receiving].
Through this we may understand the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 186:2, “With You is the source of life, in Your light is seen light.”</i> “In Your light is light seen.”
[This is a secondary light,] a radiance of a radiance, which is called an “offspring light.”
For, [although] after the <i>Tzimtzum</i> the light breaks through by way of a mere line, it nevertheless comes from “Your” essential light, since everything is included within the <i>Reshimu</i>, and it is from [the <i>Reshimu</i>] that the <i>Kav</i>-Line is drawn.
[The <i>Kav-</i>line] is an aspect of a <i>Heyulie</i> for all the influence [of the chaining down of the worlds], and [it] brings about the dimensions of “up” and “down,” as stated in <i>Etz Chayim.</i><sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">Etz Chayim, Drush Igullim V’Yosher, Shaar 1, Anaf 2.</i>
For this reason, we may [now] understand the answer to two [seemingly paradoxical] opposites that are found in this <i>Kav-</i>Line.
The first [aspect of the <i>Kav-</i>line] is that it has the power to “include the left in the right etc.”<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar<i>,</i> beginning of Parshat Korach.</i>
This is the aspect of the inter-inclusions and unifications of all the lights which branch out, from <i>Keter</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i> until <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Atzilut.</i>
It is specifically through [the <i>Kav-</i>line] that [it is possible for] a light to be exchanged into a vessel which is not its own, such as the light of <i>Chessed</i>-Kindness [being invested in] the vessel of <i>Gevurah</i>-Sternness.
This is in accordance to what is explained elsewhere at length in regard to the matter of the letter <i>Vav</i> (ו) of the word “The Awesome One-<i>VeHanora</i>-<b>ו</b>הנורא.”
The second [aspect of the <i>Kav</i>] is that it is specifically called the “Measuring Line,” in that it gives measure to all lights and vessels.
This is as we previously explained regarding the matter of the <i>Kav-</i>line, that it is called the “Builders Rod.”
[Now], at first glance, this seems to be the opposite of inter-inclusion [and unification] etc.
However, [the explanation of] the matter is that both [these aspects of the <i>Kav-</i>line] are true.
Quite the contrary, the [two] are interdependent.
This is because the <b>root</b> of this <i>Kav</i> comes from the original power of the Essential Self of the Limitless Light of the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, which preceded the <i>Tzimzum</i>.
This is as explained above regarding the matter that “In Your light,” specifically, “light is seen,” [referring to the light] of this <i>Kav-</i>line.
Certainly, <b>it is within the power</b> of the essential light of the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, to make inter-inclusions and unifications of all opposites throughout the entire chaining down [of the worlds], from the “top” of <i>Adam Kadmon,</i> until <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Atzilut</i>.
This is in accordance with the statement,<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">Introduction to Tikkunei Zohar, 17a.</i> “You are He who unifies them and binds them… You are He, inside and out.”
This is also the [explanation of the] matter of “the name of <i>Ma”H-</i>מ״ה-45 (יו״ד ה״א וא״ו ה״א) within, which is the path of the entire Emanation-<i>Atzilut</i>,” and there are other such statements.
All this [inter-inclusion and unification] is [possible] because of the radiance of the limitless light of The Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, which is within this <i>Kav</i> and goes and extends down until <i>Malchut,</i> the end of all the levels [of the world of <i>Atzilut</i>].
It is for this very same reason that it is within the power [of the <i>Kav</i>] to measure every measurement and limitation. [That is, it measures] all lights and vessels, and all unifications of “influencer and recipient,” [determining exactly] how much the “masculine waters” and “feminine waters” will be.
This [aspect of measurement comes] from the aspect of the <i>Reshimu-</i>impression, which limits all the light of the Essential Self in various manners, according to His estimation within the Essential Self of the limitless light of the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, before the <i>Tzimtzum</i>.
We find that from the angle of the Light of the Essential Self in the <i>Kav</i>-Line, it is considered to be an aspect of a <i>Heyulie</i> [the function of which is] to inter-include and unify everything, [whereas] from the angle of the limiting power of the <i>Reshimu</i> in it, it limits and gives measure to everything, according to the aspect of the first assessment [and estimation] which was included in this <i>Reshimu</i>.
By way of analogy, this is similar to an architect who drafts a blueprint, which defines the manner in which the [building will be] built, so that everything should be precisely according to how he decided within himself of how the measurements [should be].
[This is done] so that he should neither stray to the left nor to the right [from his original plan].
Now, although at times it is possible for there to be additional radiance in the emanated [<i>sefirot</i>], more so than the dictates of the “measuring line” (<i>Kav HaMidah</i>), this specifically comes about from the power of the Light of the Essential Self of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He.
At times it will radiate in one way, and at times it will radiate in another way.
For this reason, any aspect of <b>new</b> light [found] within <i>ABY”A</i><sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Atzilut, Briyah, Yetzirah</i> and <i>Asiyah</i>.</i> comes specifically from the Essential Self of the limitless light of the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, which precedes the <i>Tzimtzum</i>.
This is because it is from His essential light, that light is seen within this <i>Kav-</i>line.
At times there is additional [radiance] and at times there is diminished [radiance].
This also [accounts] for the changes [that take place] in the unifications of all the <i>Partzufim</i> (Statures), from [the top of] <i>Adam Kadmon</i> to the “heel” of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>, at the end of [the world of] <i>Asiyah.</i>
An example is the change between the time of the Holy Temple to the time of the exile, and the like.
Moreover, we generally [pray and] say, “May it be desirable before You.”
[This to say,] literally before Your Essential Self, which is even higher than the ten essential <i>sefirot</i>.
[We request that <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He] should change “The simple essential desire” that has already been drawn forth within the Essential Self of the limitless light of the Unlimited One.
[That is, we request that it should be drawn forth] and come into the estimation which He estimated within Himself [for the entire chaining down of the worlds] until the end of the <i>Kav-</i>line, in an entirely different way, such as from Judgment (<i>Din</i>) to Kindness (<i>Chessed</i>), and the like.
This is as previously explained (at the end of chapter nine) regarding the matter of “I <i>HaShem-</i>יהו״ה have not changed.”
[That is,] in the original light that precedes the <i>Tzimtzum</i> there is no change between a desire for kindness or [a desire for] judgment.
[This is] because of the reason mentioned above (in chapter ten), regarding the matter of the essential <i>Heyulie</i> desire for kindness, which is completely included in the Essential Self of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He.
[It was previously explained] that there are three levels until it comes to a particular matter, (as explained at length in chapter eleven).
When the Sages stated, “[Pray] to Him and not to His qualities” this even refers to His <b>essential</b> qualities, which are [one] with the light of His Essential Self.
This is because the Essential Self of the light of the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, “is not of any of these qualities altogether.” This will suffice for those of understanding.
This then, is the meaning of, “You are He who unifies them etc.” It specifically states, “You [are He],” referring to “He” who “is One, but not in [a way of] enumeration”<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">Introduction to Tikkunei Zohar 17a.</i> of ten <i>sefirot.</i>
Similarly, the power of the <i>Reshimu</i> and the <i>Kav</i> to limit and measure, (which is why it is called “The Measuring Line” (<i>Kav HaMidah</i>)), comes specifically from the Essential Self of the Limitless Light of the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He.
Moreover, [these two powers] are interdependent.
(This is in accordance with what is stated elsewhere<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote">See Shaarei Teshuva 87a.</i> regarding the general matter of <i>Chessed</i> (Kindness) and <i>Gevurah</i> (Might) within the Essential Self of the limitless light of the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He.
[It explains there] that [the <i>Gevurah</i> of His Essential Self] is the power of limitation, to limit and conceal, [thus withdrawing into] Himself [in a way of] elevation after elevation, endlessly and without measurement.
This is the meaning of the statement,<sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar Chadash, Yitro 34c. See also Tikkunei Zohar, 40b. See also Torat Chayim, Noach 69b, and footnote 11 there. The entire statement is, “The light of the Unlimited One is above without end, and below without conclusion.”</i> “The light of the Unlimited One is above without end.” [In contrast, <i>Chessed</i> of His Essential Self] is the aspect of the spreading down of the light, “down below without conclusion,” by means of the <i>Kav</i> which extends from the <i>Reshimu</i>.
These are two equally balanced lines, and [are both] completely in a state of being unlimited.
Therefore, even in the lowering of the Light of the Unlimited One within this line-<i>Kav</i>, these two powers, these being the power to restrain and limit and the power to bind and unify, are equal.
Likewise, regarding the matter of changes in the light and its expression, whether [it will be] with additional or diminished [revelation], such as [the difference] between the weekdays and Shabbat and Holidays, or the [difference between the] time of the Holy Temple and the time of exile, it all comes from one power. [This one power] divides into the two lines of <i>Chessed</i> and <i>Gevurah</i>, which are equally balanced.
This comes from the power of the original light, that is, the Light of the Essential Self of the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, from the aspects of <i>Chessed</i> and <i>Gevurah,</i> as He is, in and of Himself. This will suffice for those of understanding.)
This is in accordance with what was explained above (in chapter fourteen), that a line is a <i>Heyulie</i> relative to a plane.
[This is to say,] it includes the essential power and light of the Essence of the Influencer, except that in the Essential Self it is [revealed] with great expanse, whereas in this line, the very same power comes [revealed] in an aspect of restricted influence and expression [according to the capacities] of the recipients.
This being the case, even the aspect of the restraint and expression of [the <i>Kav-</i>line], comes specifically from the Essential Self of the limitless light of the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He. This will suffice for those of understanding.

Chapter 16

We now must understand the specifics of the matter of this Line and Thread (<i>Kav V’Chut</i>), [and] how it has [both] the aspects of encompassing [lights] and inner [lights].<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">Encompassing lights are called <i>Makifim</i>, and inner lights are called <i>Pnimim</i>.</i>
This is as stated in <i>Etz Chayim</i>,<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">Etz Chayim, Drush Igullim V’Yosher, Shaar 1, Anaf 2.</i> “It circles and returns and re-encircles,” (as explained elsewhere at length).
[It is] this aspect of the first encompassing circle that is called “the Lower Purity.”<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Tihiroo Tata’a –</i> The Lower Purity</i> This is the aspect of the general encompassing [light], which encompasses the four worlds of <i>ABY”A</i><sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Atzilut, Briyah, Yetzirah</i> and <i>Asiyah</i>.</i> equally, as stated in [the beginning of] <i>Etz Chayim</i>.
However, let us first preface with [an explanation] of the general matter of the Line (<i>Kav</i>), [to understand] how it is the aspect of a general <i>Heyulie</i> for all the many particular influences that “branch out” from it, until the end of the [world of] <i>Asiyah</i>, as mentioned previously.
This may be understood by way of the well-known analogy regarding the matter of a general thought.
With this general thought, “He gazes and sees to the end of all generations…with one glance.”<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Rosh HaShanah 18a</i> (As Maimonides<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">Mishneh Torah, Hilchot Yesodot HaTorah 8:9-10; Also see Tanya, Ch. 42 and 48.</i> expresses it, this is the [meaning of his] statement, “With the knowledge of Himself, He knows all creatures,” as explained elsewhere at length.)
As known, the explanation of these things is that there are two types of desire.
The first is the simple [essential] desire of the Essential Self of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, which is literally included in His Essential Being. This cannot yet be called a “general thought or desire,” since it still is totally one with His Essential Self, literally.
For example, even if this desire has already been determined within Himself, [that is,] how to do a particular act of kindness, or how to speak or think it, or how to conceptualize a particular concept, or how to have desire or pleasure in a particular thing.
Nonetheless even though this [essential] determined desire is connected to the extension of the desire for a particular matter, however, it [itself] remains included in His hidden essence.
It, therefore, does not yet have aspects of “general” and “particular.”
It is only afterwards, when the desire which He determined [within Himself] arises to come [out] into actuality, that it becomes revealed out of its hiddenness.
[Only] then does this desire come to an aspect of “general” and “particular.” In other words, [now it may be defined as a] general thought that includes the entire [concept of] the act, from beginning to end, in one glance.
Afterwards, it divides into particular desires, each of which possess intellect and emotions etc.
[Each of these desires] come in succession to one another in a chaining down, in which the upper [desire] encompasses the lower [desire], “like a circle within a circle.”
This [type of desire] is called a “composite” desire, for it [is made up of] a general [desire] and particular [desires].
This may be understood through the well-known analogy of a person who wants to build a large building, according to his predetermined desire that it should specifically be [built] in a special manner.
Now, even though this predetermined desire comes in a way of a measured, specific pleasure, that it should [specifically] be thus, and it obviously [follows that] the intellect and emotions [of this desire] come with [certain defined] proportions and measurements, nevertheless, all this is the estimation and predetermination as it still [exists] within himself. [As of yet] it is [totally] included within himself and is as if it is nonexistent.
Only with the passage of time, when this thought comes to be acted upon, do the actual divisions of all these predetermined particulars and various specifications become recognized.
However, at first, this desire comes in a general manner, that is, that he should have a building with a particular form.
Afterwards, it divides into particular desires for each particular detail.
It [thus] descends with order and levels, [beginning with the first general [desire] that includes everything in one glance, to a particular of this desire. [Now, the particular desire] is [also] called a general [desire] relative to the [particular] desires that branch out from it.
[This process continues] until the very final desire and concept, which is the final action, at the conclusion of everything. This will suffice for those of understanding.
The analogue of all this, may be understood [in regard to how it is] above in <i>HaShem</i>’s-יהו״ה Godliness, in regard to the difference between the aspects of the Upper Purity and the Lower Purity that follows the <i>Tzimtzum</i>.
That which He estimated within Himself in potential within the Upper Purity, is similar to the aforementioned determination as it is within the simple desire of the self.
As of yet, it has not come to an aspect of spreading forth from the Self altogether.
Moreover, even though this essential determined desire connects to the extended desire that follows it, nonetheless, it remains included in a hidden manner in the Essential Self of the Limitless Light of the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He.
It is therefore above [and beyond] the aspect of a general [desire], to be considered as “[a general desire] that foresees and gazes [at everything] in a single glance.”
However, the second desire that follows the aforementioned <i>Tzimtzum</i>, is when the simple determined desire of His Essential Self comes to the aspect of spreading forth.
This is the aspect of the <i>Heyulie</i> Line and Thread (<i>Kav V’Chut</i>), which includes every particular issuance from the beginning [of the chaining down] to its end, as previously mentioned.
The first encompassing [light of this <i>Kav</i>-line] is called “the Lower Purity.” This is analogous to the general desire for a large building. [This general desire] includes all its particulars from beginning to end, at once.
Afterwards it divides with order and levels [descending] from the general to the particular, as in the aforementioned analogy.
In other words, as it arose in His simple <i>Heyulie</i> desire, to specifically come out into revelation, it included all the particular desires.
This is the desire that includes [and encompasses] them all, and is called, “The Primal Desire” (<i>Ratzon HaKadoom</i>) [relative] to everything that follows it.
Afterwards, this desire comes by way of particulars, such as the desire to emanate (<i>Atzilut</i>), within which is included [the desire for the] ten <i>sefirot</i> [of the world of <i>Atzilut</i>] in all their particulars.
However, all this is still concealed, until it comes into an aspect of revelation, when the light is emanated in an aspect of [actual] emanation (<i>Atzilut</i>).
Following this is the desire to create (<i>Briyah</i>) something from nothing etc. This [desire] includes [the ten <i>sefirot</i> of] intellect and emotions etc.
[This descent of desires continues] until the final desire, which is, “Everything that <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה desired, He did” [and brought out into actuality]. [This is] the final conclusion of everything.
Now, all these particulars were included in the Primal Desire (<i>Ratzon HaKadoom</i>), which comes in an aspect of influence <b>after</b> the [original] <i>Tzimtzum</i>.
This then, is the aspect of the beginning of the Line (<i>Kav</i>). That is, it is the first “circle” that follows the drawing down of the beginning of the aforementioned <i>Heyulie</i> Line (<i>The Kav HaMidah</i>).
[This first “circle”] is called the general encompassing [light] of the four worlds of <i>ABY”A,</i><sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Atzilut, Briyah, Yetzirah</i> and <i>Asiyah</i>.</i> and encompasses them [all] equally.
It is [also] called the “general thought” that foresees and “gazes” upon [all of Creation], from beginning to end, in a single glance.
This then, is the explanation of the general matter of the whole of this Line-<i>Kav</i>.
All the particular ways that it, “circles and returns and re-encircles…” may be understood according to the aforementioned analogy, as will be explained in the following chapter, with the help of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He. This will suffice for those of understanding.

Chapter 17

We must now understand the particulars of the matter of the <i>Kav-</i>Line, as it is in an aspect of “<i>Igullim-</i>Circles” [and “<i>Yosher-</i>Upright”] etc.
However, we must preface with [an explanation] of the aspect of the beginning of this <i>Kav-</i>Line, which comes in an aspect of an inner light (<i>Ohr Pnimi</i>), and then encircles and [once again] is drawn down as an inner light. Then it once again encircles etc.
It is explained in <i>Etz Chayim</i><sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">See Etz Chayim (Drush Igullim V’Yosher), Shaar 1, Anaf 2-3.</i> that in the aspect of the ten <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Igullim</i> – The circles of desire, the uppermost is the most superior, while the innermost is the [most] inferior, whereas in the aspect of the ten <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Yosher –</i> The upright <i>sefirot</i>, the opposite is true. [This is to say that] the uppermost is the [most] inferior, while the innermost is the [most] superior.
Now, the explanation of these matters is as follows: It is known that although in relation to the aspect of the simple determined desire of the Essential Self of the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, the aspect of this Primal Desire (<i>Ratzon HaKadoom</i>) is called a spreading forth of the desire. However, it too is still concealed, and not at all revealed.
This is because [the <i>Ratzon HaKadoom-</i>the Primal Desire] is only the influence and expression of the Simple Desire for kindness, which has already been determined in the Essential Self of the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, that it should come into actuality in a particular way.
Immediately, when it arises in thought how everything should be, it is called the “Primal Thought and Desire” (<i>Machshava V’Ratzon Kadoom</i>). [This thought] includes within itself every particular desire [of the entire chaining down of the worlds], as explained previously in the analogy of a building.
If this is the case, this entire Primal Desire is still within Himself, without being revealed outside [of Himself]. Nonetheless, afterwards, everything is actualized from this [Primal Desire].
This then, is the meaning of [the verse],<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 33:9</i> “For He said,” within the Primal Thought, “and it was.”
This [Primal Thought] is called “The life of all the worlds,” from the “head” of <i>Adam Kadmon</i> to the “heel” of <i>Adam Kadmon</i> [which is] at the end of the world of <i>Asiyah</i> (Actualization). This is the meaning of [the statement], “All of creation is not concealed from You.”
[This means that] there is [not a single particular detail], even the most final of details, that did not originally exist within this [Primal] Desire and Thought.
On the contrary, [as it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">See <i>Lecha Dodee</i> prayer of Friday night.</i> “The end action arose first in thought”]. [This is to say that] “The end action,” such as the end of the seventh millennium, “arose” within this Primal Thought “first,” as explained elsewhere at length.
(In the terminology of the <i>Zohar</i> this [Primal Thought] is called “<i>Ateeka D’Ateekin</i>-The Ancient of the Ancients”<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar II 165b; Zohar III (<i>Idra Rabba</i>) 128a-b, and elsewhere.</i> or<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar III (<i>Idra Rabba</i>) 129a, 132a, and elsewhere.</i> “<i>Ateeka Stima’ah</i>-The Concealed Ancient One.” This is the aspect of, “The Supernal Desire of all Desires, which is revealed in the forehead of the Holy Ancient One (<i>Atika Kadisha</i>).”<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar III (<i>Idra Rabba</i>) 129a, 136b - “<i>Rayva D’Kol Rayvin Ila’een, D’Itgalyn B’Metzcha D’Atika Kadisha.</i>”</i>
This is because pleasure is invested within desire, so that they are literally as one.
Likewise, the simple [essential] <i>heyulie</i> desire of the <i>heyulie</i> desire for kindness (which was mentioned previously in chapters 10 and 11), included the simple pleasure of the Essential Self of the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He. This is called, “the delight of the King in Himself (<i>Sha’ashoo’aiy HaMelech B’Atzmooto</i>).”
This is also [the case] in regard to the three levels of [<i>Yachid, Echad</i> and <i>Kadmon</i>], until [the Essential desire] came to the particular matter of “<i>Ana Emloch-</i>I shall rule,” which is the aspect of <i>Malchut</i> (Kingdom) of The Unlimited One (<i>Ein Sof</i>), that preceded the <i>Tzimtzum</i>, as explained there.<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">That is, as explained in chapters 10 and 11.</i>
All [these levels] are the aspect of “The delight of the King in Himself, within the Upper Purity.
However, “<i>Ateeka D’Ateekin</i> – The Ancient of the Ancients,” which is the source of all pleasures, and [is also known as] “The Supernal Desire of all Desires,” refers to the aspect of the Line-<i>Kav</i> that follows the <i>Tzimtzum</i>. It includes [all] the various desires and pleasures that are destined to be revealed.
“<i>Atika Stima’ah</i>-The Concealed Ancient One” is the aspect of <i>Keter</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i> [and] is the concealed desire and pleasure, as it still relates to Himself, except that [now, after the <i>Tzimtzum,</i>] He thinks to bring this [desire] into actual revelation.
[For example,] this is like [the desire] that there should be a revelation of the desire and pleasure to emanate the ten <i>sefirot</i> [of the world of <i>Atzilut-</i>Emanation], (It is for this reason that “<i>Atika Stima’ah</i> – The Concealed Ancient One” is considered to be an aspect of “concealment which is at least subject to revelation.” This is not the case with the beginning of the <i>Kav,</i> which is called “The Concealment of all Concealments – <i>Steema D’Kol Steemeen</i>,” for even the thought of <i>Adam Kadmon</i> cannot grasp Him.) or that there should be the desire and pleasure to create [the world of <i>Briyah</i>] etc.
[The aspect of] “<i>Atika Kadisha-</i>The Holy Ancient One” is the pleasure that [becomes invested] within <i>Chochmah</i> (Insight).
This is the aspect of <i>Atik Yomin</i> (“The Ancient of Days”) and <i>Arich Anpin</i> (“The Long Face”) [which are the <i>Keter</i> (pleasure and desire)] of [the world of] <i>Atzilut</i> (Emanation). [This is when] the pleasure and desire become revealed, all of which will be explained in a manner of specifics.)
Now, the [explanation of the] aspect of the ten <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Igullim</i>-Circles of desire, one within the other, is as known, that every cause encompasses its effect, “like a circle within a circle,”<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote">Ezekiel 1:16, 10:10</i> and that the effect can never grasp its cause, except in a way of distance from it.
This may be understood from a desire that becomes completely revealed.
Although this [revealed desire] includes ten [<i>sefirot</i> within itself, such as] intellect and emotions etc., nonetheless, it initially comes about as a single decision, without any apparent divisions [into ten <i>sefirot</i>].
This is called, “The General Circle of Desire” which encompasses [and] contains all [the particulars that will become revealed], within it. [Every subsequent “circle of desire”] comes about specifically from its power. However, [it encompasses these “circles of desire”] from a distance.
An example is the reasoning and intellect for this desire, which is called its effect.
It is impossible for it to be close [in a way of] comparison, to its cause, which is the desire, because, as known, “desire is altogether beyond reason,”<sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote">See Shnei Luchot HaBrit, Beit HaShem 4b, (See footnote in the name of Rabbi Yosef Al Kastilia); Yonat Elem (of Rabbi Menachem Azaria de Fano) Ch. 2; Also see Torat Chayim 63a, note 7.</i> [and, therefore] it can never be comprehended [through reasoning].
Nevertheless, it is from the power of desire that the “circle” of <i>Chochmah-</i>Insight comes about, though it too has no recognizable divisions into ten [<i>sefirot</i>].
This is similar to the analogy of [a judge] who, [because he] has been bribed, will find a rationalization for the desire.
Although this [desire for] reasoning also includes ten [<i>sefirot</i>], that is, desire, intellect, and emotions, nonetheless, it is comes about in a general fashion etc.
Likewise, the “circle” of <i>Binah</i>-Comprehension, which comes about from the power [of the “circle” of <i>Chochmah</i>], can never grasp [<b>its</b> cause]. In this manner, the [“circles of the desire” for the] emotions [are also drawn forth,] one within the other. [This continues] until the [“circle of the desire” for the] end action, which is the final circle [of desire].
All this is included in the desire for Himself, until the end action which is the innermost [circle of desire] etc.
Likewise, this is how it is in the aforementioned concealed desire, which is called the Primal Desire (<i>Ratzon HaKadoom</i>), the source of all the desires [for the entire chaining down of the worlds].
It includes ten <i>sefirot</i>, one circle [of desire] within the other circle [of desire], until the circle [of the desire] for the end action. This is the desire for the end action, since “everything that He desires, He does” in actuality.
The aforementioned Primal Desire (<i>Ratzon HaKadoom</i>) is the uppermost circle [of desire], that includes [and encompasses] everything [that is desired in the entire chaining down of the worlds.]
[Now, all this is in the aspect of desire], however, when this desire in Himself comes to be <b>actualized</b>, it is the other way around.
[This is to say that] the desire becomes concealed and invested in the intellect, and the intellect encompasses it.
Then the intellect becomes concealed and invested in the emotions, one within the other, until the end action, which is the uppermost.
In other words, invested within the actual power of the action are the thoughts. Invested within the thoughts are the emotions. Invested within the emotions are <i>Chochmah</i>-Insight and <i>Binah-</i>Comprehension, and invested within <i>Chochmah</i> is the desire (<i>Arich</i>) and pleasure (<i>Atik</i>).
[Here] we find that the innermost of them all is the desire and pleasure, while the most external of them all is the action [which is the most] inferior one.
This is the aspect of <i>Yosher-</i>Upright, which comes in an aspect of the upper being invested in the lower.
However, in the aspect of the aforementioned Primal Desire (<i>Ratzon Kadoom</i>), since it is still within Himself, it therefore is drawn forth in an aspect of <i>Igullim-</i>Circles, in which the uppermost is this concealed all-encompassing desire.
The first circle [in the scheme of <i>Igullim</i> – Circles] is the desire and pleasure for the whole chaining down [of the worlds], which is within it. This circle is the general encompassing [light] of the [four worlds of] <i>ABY”A</i>, as mentioned previously.
The beginning of the <i>Kav-</i>Line is the aspect of a <i>Heyulie</i> drawing down [of influence], like a short line that diminishes (by way of <i>Tzimtzum</i>) from cause to affect, such as from <i>Ratzon-</i>Desire to <i>Chochmah</i>-Insight, and the like.
Likewise, from the aspect of the aforementioned <i>Reshimu-</i>Impression, a <i>Kav</i>-Line is drawn with very great diminishment.
For, although the <i>Reshimu-</i>Impression comes about in [a way of] limitation [of the Unlimited Light], as explained previously, nonetheless, it is still from the aspect of the World of the Unlimited One (<i>Ein Sof</i>), except that it is the last aspect [of the Unlimited], which comes about with brevity.
This is not the case with the Primal Desire (<i>Ratzon HaKadoom</i>) which comes into the category of [expressing] influence <b>outside</b> of the World of the Unlimited.
However, [because] it [still] is an all-encompassing <i>Heyulie</i> [for the entire chaining down of the worlds], therefore it is drawn out by way of a short line. This will suffice for those of understanding.
(This is [in accordance with] the statement in <i>Etz Chayim</i>; that the essential purpose of the radiance of the <i>Kav</i>-Line, is solely to bring about the aspects of “above” and “below” such as the ten <i>Igullim-</i>Circles, [which follow in progression from higher and lower] until the end action.
In contrast, in the World of the Unlimited One (<i>Ein Sof</i>), even the aspects of “above” or “below” do not exist. Rather, there is only His absolutely simple singularity, as previously explained.
Furthermore, even though [in potential] He estimated within Himself that which is destined to be, it all is actually still within Himself and is literally in an aspect of being limitless (<i>Ein Sof</i>).
Because of this it states in <i>Etz Chayim</i><sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote">See Etz Chayim, (Drush Igullim V’Yosher) Shaar 1, Anaf 5, and the end of Anaf 2, and Shaar 42 (Shaar Drushei ABY”A) Ch. 1.</i> that it is forbidden to speak even in regard to the aspect of <i>Malchut</i> of the Unlimited One (<i>Malchut D’Ein Sof</i>).
Rather, we are permitted to speak only in regard to the aspect of the <i>Kav-</i>Line and the aspect of <i>Adam Kadmon</i> (Primordial Man). [Since] this is the aspect of the first source of the entire chaining down [of the worlds], it may, therefore, be comprehended in [relation to] the many descents [that take place] until [the comprehension of how] the ten <i>sefirot</i> of [the world of] <i>Atzilut</i> become [invested] within <i>BY”A.</i><sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Briyah, Yetzirah</i> and <i>Asiyah</i>.</i>
This is because they [the <i>Kav</i> and particularly <i>Adam Kadmon</i>] are called by the name, “the Cause of all causes” (<i>Eelot Kol HaEelot</i>)<sup class="footnote-marker">12</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar I 22b; Pardes Rimonim, Shaar 3, Chapter 1.</i> and<sup class="footnote-marker">13</sup><i class="footnote">Tikkunei Zohar, Tikkun 19 (42a).</i> “the Primordial of all the Primordials” (<i>Kadmon L’Kol HaKedoomin</i>).
However, [in regard to] the Essential Self of the light of the Unlimited One (<i>Atzmoot Ohr Ein Sof</i>) [it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">14</sup><i class="footnote">Introduction to Tikkunei Zohar, 17a.</i>] “No thought can grasp Him,” [which includes] even the aforementioned Primal Thought (<i>Machshava HaKedooma</i>).
This is because the World of the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, is qualitatively beyond and is called “Totally Holy” [and transcendent], as a result of the aforementioned <i>Tzimtzum</i>.
[In contrast], the aforementioned aspect of the Primal Desire (<i>Ratzon Kadoom</i>) is called “His Great Name.” “His Name-<i>Shmo</i>-שמו-346” is the same numerical value as “Desire-<i>Ratzon</i>-רצון-346.”<sup class="footnote-marker">15</sup><i class="footnote">See Pri Etz Chayim (Shaar Kriyat Shma), Shaar 8, and end of chapter 28.</i> This is the [explanation] of the matter of [the words of the <i>Kaddish</i> prayer,] “May His Great Name be blessed etc.”<sup class="footnote-marker">16</sup><i class="footnote">As mentioned previously, the word “Blessed-<i>Baruch-</i>ברוך” also means to “draw down.”</i>)
(Furthermore, as known, the aspect of <i>Adam Kadmon</i> is called “<i>Adam D’Briyah</i>-Man of Creation,” as will be explained [in the following chapter].
This is in contradistinction to the Essential Self of the light of the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, [about Whom] it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">17</sup><i class="footnote">Samuel I 15:29</i> “For He is not a man.”
As known, this is also [in accordance] with the intentions of the prayer, “<i>Nishmat Kol Chai</i> – The Soul of all living beings,” which is the aspect of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>. This will suffice for those of understanding.)

Chapter 18

Now, [regarding] the aspect of the Primal Desire to Himself, of everything that will be in the [whole] chaining down [of the worlds] (<i>Hishtalshelut</i>), it includes ten [<i>sefirot,</i> or “circles”] until the “end action” that arose in this Primal Desire, which is the last aspect within it.
Now, the <i>Keter</i> of the lower [world] comes about from the aspect of <i>Malchut</i> of the upper [world].
This is the aspect of <i>Keter</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i> (Primordial Man). Moreover, as known, in [regard to] the general manner [of the chaining down of the worlds], the aspect of <i>Adam Kadmon</i> (Primordial Man) is called “<i>Adam D’Briyah</i>-Man of Creation,” which is the aspect of Thought (<i>Machshavah</i>).
<i>Atik Yomin</i> and <i>Arich Anpin</i> of [the world of] <i>Atzilut</i> (Emanation) are called “<i>Adam D’Yetzirah-</i>Man of Formation.” <i>Zeir Anpin</i> and <i>Nukvah</i> [of the world of <i>Atzilut</i>] are called “<i>Adam D’Asiyah</i>-Man of Action.”
Just as the [particular] world of <i>Briyah-</i>Creation is, literally, a creation of “something from nothing,” as known, so too, the aspect of <i>Keter</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i> is considered to be a creation of something from nothing. [This is to say that it is created] from the <b>true</b> “<i>Ein-</i>Nothing” of the Light of the Unlimited One Himself, which is in the aforementioned <i>Kav-</i>Line, which is called the Primal Desire to Himself (<i>Ratzon Kadoom L’Atzmo</i>).
Now, as known, the explanation for this is [as follows]: It was explained above that the aforementioned Primal Desire (<i>Ratzon Kadoom</i>) is called “the source of all desires.”
It is the aspect of the <i>Heyulie</i> desire, which is the source from which all “desires for desires” find [their existence].
This can be understood by way of analogy from the aspect of the <i>Yechidah</i> of the human soul. The essential <i>Heyulie</i> desire for kindness, which is included in it in an aspect of a <i>Heyulie,</i> includes every particular desire for kindness that he is destined to desire.
When [this <i>Heulie</i> desire for kindness] comes to be drawn forth in a particular manner for a specific matter, it comes out of the aspect of the essence [of his soul] so that he will have an essential and concealed desire, which is the aspect of the aforementioned Primal Desire (<i>Ratzon Kadoom</i>).
However, [this Primal Desire] has not yet become invested within that thing [which he desires at all], but is rather still [completely] to himself, as mentioned previously.
However, when [the Primal Desire] becomes invested [within] and affects a “desire for a desire” for this particular matter, such as becoming invested within the intellect and thought, to cause a “desire for a desire” for this particular thing, the existence of this desire for this thing within the intellect and thought is like an entirely new creation from its source.
This is because the aforementioned aspect of the Primal Desire is the source for the creation of this “desire for the desire” of the intellect, and this “desire for the desire” is called a [new] creation.
For, we observe that it is not at all times that a person has a desire for a specific desire, such as the desire for business or for study.
It is [therefore] necessary [to state] that there is a source that creates this specific desire.
[This source] is called “the desire for this [specific] desire.” It automatically [follows] and is understood, that since the desire for this [specific] desire is not drawn forth at all times, and furthermore, at times it will radiate with great strength and light, while at other times it will radiate in a diminished and weak [fashion], therefore, it must be said that even the source which makes and brings about this [specific] desire, which is called the “<b>desire</b> for the desire,” also comes about in an aspect of “something” coming into being from “nothing.”
This is comparable to a bribe, which brings about a constant “desire for a desire” to merit [the briber].
This is because the bribe touches the essence of his soul. Because of this, it is constantly drawn out, bringing into being a “desire for a desire” of kindness and merit [towards the briber].
The opposite [is true] in regard to his enemy. A constant “desire for a desire” of judgment will be brought about [towards him], and the like. This will suffice for those of understanding.
Now, as known, every revealed desire includes ten [<i>sefirot</i>]. This being the case, this “desire for the desire” also includes ten [<i>sefirot</i> within it].
Moreover, [being that] there are ten powers, it automatically follows that there are ten types of “desire for desire,” all of which come into being in an aspect of “something” from “nothing.”
All this is an example, in order to understand the aspect of the ten <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i> (Primordial Man), which is entirely just the matter of “a desire for a desire.”
This is because they are the aspect of the concealment of the ten <i>sefirot</i> of [the world of] <i>Atzilut</i> (Emanation) [whereas the ten <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Atzilut</i>] are revealed [desires], as known.
For example, <i>Keter</i> (desire) of <i>Chochmah</i> (insight) of <i>Atzilut</i> is the desire for intellect.
Its source is in <i>Keter</i> (desire) of <i>Chochmah</i> (wisdom) of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>, which is called “the [hidden] desire for this [revealed] desire.”
Likewise, [the revealed] <i>Keter</i> (desire) of <i>Chessed</i> (kindness) of <i>Atzilut</i> comes from [the concealed] <i>Keter</i> (desire) of <i>Chessed</i> (kindness) of <i>Adam Kadmon</i> etc.
However, the coming into being of the ten <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i> itself, is all drawn from the aspect of the <i>Kav-</i>Line, which is called “The Source of the Coming into being of all Desires for Desires.”
This is because it is the essential simple desire, which originated within Himself that it should be thus, as mentioned previously.
It therefore causes and makes the “desire for desire” [to be] in a particular way.
[This principle applies] from the aspect of <i>Keter</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i> until the aspect of <i>Malchut</i> [of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>], which is the aspect of the “desire for the desire” for Kingship.
However, the aspect of <i>Keter</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i> only comes about from the last level of the aforementioned <i>Heyulie</i> Primal Desire (<i>Ratzon HaKadoom HaHeyulie</i>).
[<i>Keter</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>] is the “desire for the concealed desire” which is higher than the aspect of <i>Chochmah-</i>Wisdom of the “desire for the concealed desire.”
In this manner, all the ten <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i> are in an aspect of concealment.
