[The <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>] are all the [hidden] “desires for the desires” for all the ten <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Atzilut</i>, which [themselves] come in an aspect of revelation, as will be explained. This will suffice for those of understanding.
This then, is the [reason why] the aspect of <i>Adam Kadmon</i> is called “<i>Adam D’Briyah</i>-Man of Creation,” [for] it [comes into being] similar to the aspect of the coming into being of “something” from “nothing.”
We clearly observe that a “desire for desire” comes into being at specific times, similar to how all other created entities come into being.
This is similar to the coming into being of thought, which is a creation of “something” from “nothing” in comparison to the essential desire in [a person’s] soul.
We [also] clearly observe that [in regard to] the “desire for the desire” which comes into an aspect of being, the beginning of its coming into being is specifically in thought.
This is because thought is an aspect of a vessel for the desire, since the desire becomes invested in the thought, as in the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">Jeremiah 26:3, 36:3</i> “As I have thought to do.”
Similarly, the first existence of the “desire for the desire” is [also] within thought, and is called “the desire which is within thought.”
This is the general [explanation] for the matter of <i>Keter</i> (Desire)<i>, Chochmah</i> (Insight) and <i>Binah</i> (Comprehension) of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>. That is, this is the aspect of the coming into being and actualization of the light of the “desire for the desire” in a specific manner, as it comes in the “hidden thought” [of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>].
In contrast, the aspect of the <i>Kav-</i>Line is higher than the actualization of the existence of a “desire for desire” for a particular thing, even in the “hidden thought.”
Rather, the thought of everything that will be, is still entirely to Himself.
This is to say that it still includes [everything] in the thought for Himself, and is not an existence of a desire within a thought for anything outside of Himself whatsoever. This will suffice for those of understanding.
(In the words of Maimonides,<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">Mishneh Torah, Hilchot Yesodei HaTorah, 2:9-10.</i> this is “the knowledge of Himself, rather than a knowledge which is outside of Himself etc.,” as explained elsewhere.)

Chapter 19

We must now understand the source of the ten emanated <i>sefirot</i> [of the world of <i>Atzilut</i> – Emanation]. Their source is from the aspect of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>.
This is as stated in <i>Etz Chayim Shaar HaKlallim,</i><sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">See Etz Chayim, (Shaar Seder Atzilut) Shaar 3, Chapter 1.</i> that <i>Keter</i> of <i>Atik Yomin</i> comes about from the aspect of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon.</i>
Now, we must first preface with [an explanation of] the matter of how the ten hidden <i>sefirot</i>, which are concealed, come out into revelation.
This is the meaning of the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 41:4</i> “He calls out the generations from the beginning (<i>Rosh</i>-ראש),” that is, from the “head (<i>Rosh</i>-ראש)” of <i>Adam Kadmon</i> etc.
<i>Sefer Yetzirah</i> states<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">Sefer Yetzirah 1:7</i> that [the revelation of the concealed] is like “the flame that is bound in the coal,” and there are many similar analogies to this.
However, this [matter] may be better understood from the [revelation] of the ten powers of the soul.
As known, the matter of “concealment and revelation” is unlike the spreading forth of a power from its essence, such as the “power of action” that spreads forth in the action, since [in such a case] it is the power of the essence itself [that spreads forth] and is called, “cause and effect.”
Rather, it is similar to the aspect of the ray and light of the essence.
This is like the radiance of the rays of light of the sun, or like the life and light of the soul as it is within the vessel of the body, or like a flash of insight [as it comes] from the “power of conceptualization,” and the like.
However, a truer analogy for the matter of “the revelation of the concealed” is like the revelation of movement from a living animal, or like the letters of thought and the letters of speech, and the like.
All the above are better [analogies] than the analogy of the flame that is bound, in a hidden fashion, with the coal.
For although the flame was indeed hidden in the coal, nonetheless, the flame came out of the essential heat of the coal, and thus, this is not a true comparison to the matter of “revelation.”
[This is because, “the revelation of the hidden”] is merely like the aspect of an appearance or a color, such as the color of an apple, which is not essential to the apple, as known.
This is likewise the case with the revelation of the concealed essential powers of the soul, such as the power of the quality of <i>Chessed-</i>Kindness, as it is in the essence.
Its revelation is when a desire and intellect for kindness and goodness is constantly brought into being because of this essential quality of the essence of the soul.
The opposite is true of someone whose essential quality is cruelty. [In such a person] a desire and intellect for judgment and punishment is brought into being.
Now, the coming into being of the source of this desire for [either] kindness or judgment is still considered to be [part and parcel] of the essential quality, and is altogether not separate from it.
However, the revealed desires for judgment or its opposite, which are born [of the “desire for the desire”], are merely like a revealed indication of the essence.
This may be compared to the revealed movement [which comes] from the [power of movement in the] essence of the animal, or to the revealed life force [of the soul as it exists] in a separate thing, that is, the [physical] body.
This is to say that because he is essentially alive, he reveals his life force in [physical] movement.
Moreover, because he essentially is a living being, he [therefore] also enlivens the inanimate body. [The physical life] is called “<i>Chayei Bassar-</i>the life of the flesh” etc.
[Similarly,] the revelation of desire comes into a separate thing, which is this [above mentioned] matter of [either] kindness or judgment.
However, the source that gives rise to this desire comes from the power of the essential quality alone.
[We] automatically understand [from this] that since there are many different types of things, a specific desire will be born for each of them from a single source, which at all times is dependent upon the essential quality.
Similarly, [when one’s] intellect constantly leans towards a desire [for] kindness, this is only because of [his] essential quality of kindness, which constantly gives rise to a desire and intellect for kindness, specifically.
Because there are many different separate things [through which this kindness may be expressed, therefore,] an individual desire and intellect is born [from the same essential source] for each one [in and of] itself. This will suffice for those of understanding.
We [therefore] find that the general “desire for the desire” for kindness can bring forth many different particular desires for kindness, in many very different matters and ways.
[Nonetheless,] they all are from one source, this being the concealed desire, which is called, “The essential desire for kindness,” [which comes about] because of the essential <i>Heyulie</i> quality [of kindness in the essence of the soul].
However, [this essential <i>Heyulie</i> quality] comes [to be expressed] in a specific way, to be this [specific] “desire for the desire” for this specific thing. This will suffice for those of understanding.
However, it is nevertheless understood that there is a great difference between [the concealed desire of <i>Adam Kadmon</i> and] the revelation of the desire for kindness [of <i>Atzilut</i>] which is merely the aspect of a “revelation of the concealment” of the essential desire, which arouses this [specific] desire.
[In contrast, the concealed desire of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>] comes from the power of the essential quality [of the Self], and is not an aspect of a “separate thing.” This will suffice for those of understanding.
Now, the matter of “He calls out the generations from the head of <i>Adam Kadmon</i> etc.,” may be understood according to the above analogies.
This is analogous to a person who calls out to something to come out from its concealment and be revealed outside.
Likewise, the main matter of the aspect of the ten <i>sefirot</i> of [the world of] <i>Atzilut-</i>Emanation, is only that they come out from being concealed to being revealed.
This is why they are called by the terms, “Lights-<i>Orot</i>” or “Emanations-<i>Sefirot</i>,” [in that they are] similar to a ray and a light.
This is similar to any aspect of the “revelation of the concealed,” in that it is only an aspect of light, or only like the aspect of an indication [of the Essence], [such as the] color [of an apple]. [In other words,] it is like the movement of an animal [which is merely an indication that, in essence, it is alive] etc.
Moreover, this is the meaning [of the word <i>Atzilut</i>-Emanation,] as in [the verse],<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Beha’alotcha</i> 11:25.</i> “And He emanated from the spirit,” which was not the [actual] spirit of Moshe [itself].
Rather, it was only an aspect of a revelation of his light and ray, which spread forth and emanated, similar to a flame [that emanates] from a coal, and the like.
All this may be understood according to the aforementioned analogy regarding the matter of [how] the desire becomes revealed in a separate thing.
That is, it emerges from the concealment of the essential desire, according to [his] essence, as mentioned previously.
Likewise, the aspect of the <i>Ketarim</i> (Crowns) of [the world of] <i>Atzilut</i>-Emanation, is only the aspect of the <b>revelation </b>of the desire, in comparison to the concealed essential desire [itself], which is called “the desire for the desire,” this being the aspect of <i>Adam Kadmon,</i> as previously explained.
For example, the revealed desire for kindness of <i>Atzilut</i> which is called <i>Keter</i> of <i>Chessed</i>, is drawn from the aspect of the concealed desire for kindness of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>.
Likewise, [the revealed desire for wisdom (<i>Chochmah</i>) of <i>Atzilut</i> is drawn] from the aspect of the concealed desire of <i>Chochmah</i> [of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>].
However, just as it is understood from the aforementioned analogy that the existence of what is called “the desire for the desire” comes as an aspect of a “general [desire],” which “gives birth” to many different [particular] desires and many different matters and ways, likewise, many different types of revealed desires for kindness of [the world of] <i>Atzilut</i> are “born” from the aspect of the “desire for the desire of kindness” of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>.
The [explanation of the] matter is that from the aspect of the <i>Malchut</i> of a [particular] quality of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>, comes about the aspect of the <i>Keter</i> of that quality of <i>Atzilut</i>.
However, [when speaking] of the ten <i>sefirot</i> generally, it is only from the [general] aspect of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i> that the [general] <i>Keter</i> of [the world of] <i>Atzilut</i> is made.
This is to say that it is only from the “letters” and revelation of the <b>concealed</b> essential desire that the essential light of the <b>revealed</b> desire is made.
(This bears a similarity to what was explained in chapter eighteen, that the “desire for the desire,” that is, the <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>, is only made from the aspect of the “end action” of the “Essential [Primal] Desire”- [<i>Ratzon HaKadoom</i>].)
(By way of analogy, [this is like] the revelation of the desire in the speech of the influencer, which becomes the essential desire of the recipient.
Similarly, it is like how the letters that reveal the intellect in the speech of the influencer, become the essential intellectual light of the recipient.
Likewise, the light of the desire for kindness in the recipient, only comes about from the letters and revelation of kindness in the speech of the influencer.
As known regarding every [type of] cause and effect, that the root and beginning of the effect is made from the last level of the cause.
Similarly, <i>Keter</i> of <i>Atik Yomin</i> [of <i>Atzilut</i>] is made from the aspect of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>.
In other words, the source of revelation of the desire which results from pleasure, which is called <i>Atik Yomin,</i> as will be explained, is made only from the revelation of the “desire for the desire” in “speech.”)
This is the general [explanation] of the matter of the ten <i>sefirot</i> of [the world of] <i>Atzilut</i>, which came out of the concealment of the ten <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>, as stated, “He calls out the generations from the head” [of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>] etc.

Chapter 20

Now, before the details of the ten <i>sefirot</i> of [the world of] <i>Atzilut</i> can be explained, we must preface [by explaining] the matter of <i>Nekudah</i>-Point, <i>Sefirah-</i>Emanation, and <i>Partzuf-</i>Stature.
As known, the general difference between the aspect of <i>Tohu</i> (Chaos) and the aspect of <i>Tikkun</i> (Rectification) is that the ten <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Tohu</i> (Chaos) are only in an aspect of “points,” which are the aspects of the <i>Ketarim</i> (Desires).
[In contrast,] in the world of <i>Tikkun-</i>Rectification, the [<i>sefirot</i>] come in an aspect of division in which each <i>sefirah</i> [is divided] into ten, and therefore, the aspect of “Rectification” automatically comes about.
This is the aspect of the inter-inclusion [of the <i>sefirot</i>] by means of the Name of <i>Ma”H-</i>מ״ה-45 (יו״ד ה״א וא״ו ה״א).
Now, the explanation of these matters is known, that the aspect of <i>Nekudot</i>-Points is the aspect of an essence before it spreads forth. This is similar to a point, which does not spread forth.
An example [of this] is the light of the quality of <i>Chessed-</i>Kindness. The aspect of the essential quality of kindness is the aspect of its <i>Keter</i> (Desire).
However, what is meant here is not the aspect of the essential quality of <i>Chessed-</i>Kindness as it is embedded and rooted within the essence of the soul, which is called the <i>Yechidah</i> (Singular), as mentioned previously, since [the way it exists embedded in the essence of the soul] is [still] totally in an aspect of a <i>Heyulie,</i> (as mentioned previously in chapters 10 and 11).
Rather, what is meant here is in regard to the aspect of the revelation of the desire for a <b>particular</b> [act of] kindness, [as it becomes revealed] from its concealment in the essential <i>Heyulie</i> of kindness.
[Now], even this [revealed] desire has not yet spread forth [from its essential state].
Rather, it [exists] as it is, beyond reason whatsoever for this desire, [such as the reason for] why he desires to reveal kindness etc.
Certainly, [as of yet], there are no divisions into the various different ways [that this kindness may be expressed].
Even if his intellect leans specifically to <i>Chessed-</i>kindness, [nonetheless] it is not divided into various ways [of how the kindness will come out].
[This is because] although the [aspect] of intellect that essentially leans toward kindness and merit, is the aspect of the <i>Chochmah</i> (Insight) of the essential <i>Chessed</i> (Kindness), nonetheless, it too, is only in an aspect of a <i>Nekudah</i>-Point.
Likewise, [the aspect of] the <i>Netzach</i> (Conquest) of this <i>Chessed</i> (Kindness) [also] comes in the way of a <i>Nekudah</i>-Point.
We [therefore] find that although the aspect of the essential kindness which comes into revelation, includes ten [<i>sefirot</i> within it, that is, desire, intellect and emotions, nonetheless, there are no recognizable divisions within them.
Rather, they are all [included] in an aspect of a single point. This is the aspect of <i>Akudim</i>-Bound, wherein [the <i>sefirot</i>] were all bound up in a single vessel.
It is because of this that the aspect of the ten <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Tohu</i>-Chaos cannot unite or become inter-included one with the other.
Rather, they are [disjointed points,] one beneath the other, as stated, “He reigned and he died etc.”
An example of this is an essential desire for kindness that comes into revelation.
Although it includes intellect etc., nonetheless, it cannot join with an essential desire that is its opposite, [such as an essential desire] that comes in an aspect of judgment.
[This is the case] even though it too includes intellect, [albeit, one] which essentially leans towards judgment.
This is because they do not have a vessel within which two [essential] opposites, such as these, can become inter-included.
We can observe this tangibly, that a person whose intellect essentially leans towards kindness cannot, in any way, tolerate his opponent, who is a person whose intellect essentially leans towards judgment.
(This is analogous to the debates between the academies of Shammai and Hillel, and the like. Even if his opponent poses difficult questions [on his views], which he is unable to logically answer, he will remain silent, but will [find it] impossible to acknowledge [the correctness of his opponent’s opinion]. [Neither will he be able] to retract [his opinion] and align himself with the opposite view, whatsoever.)
However, the aspect of <i>Tikkun-</i>Rectification is when a quality comes to spread forth from its [essential] point (<i>Nekudah</i>), outside of its essential desire and intellect.
In other words, this is like when the quality of <i>Chessed-</i>Kindness gives rise to a desire and intellect to have a kind disposition toward his fellow, [specifically] because he did him a favor.
[This is to say that] it is not because his [own] essential goodness and kindness becomes revealed, as a necessary consequence of the natural goodness in the essence of his soul.
On the contrary, he may be cruel by nature. However, he will desire to do [acts of] goodness to someone who was gracious to him and who saved him from death, or the like. [Moreover,] his intellectual disposition towards him will always lean towards [thoughts of] kindness and merit, and the like.
This is called <b>composite</b> kindness and goodness. It is not at all the simple essential kindness that stems from his [essential] nature.
The same [principle] is true of the opposite [quality], which is the composite quality of judgment. Towards his enemy, who has done him much harm, his desire and intellect will lean towards [judging him as being] guilty, even though he [himself] may be a kind and merciful person in his essential nature.
Accordingly, it is understood that there are many different ways in which the composition [of one’s desires] are formed, according to the composition of his emotions towards [any given] thing.
This is like love or hate that are dependent upon something, as mentioned above.
It is therefore possible to find something that, from one angle, he loves, and his desire and intellect are entirely for goodness and kindness [towards that thing], while from another angle of the very same thing itself, he hates it. [This is to say that] his desire and intellect is turned towards harming and punishing [the very same thing].
[Because of this,] it is possible for there to be an intermediary [composite] aspect, which includes <i>Chessed</i>-Kindness and <i>Gevurah</i>-Judgment together as one.
This is in accordance with the teaching,<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">See Talmud Bavli, Yevamot 78b, and Rashi there; Also see Zephaniah 2:3</i> “[In the same matter] where His judgment is, [there He enumerates good deeds],” in regard King Saul who killed the Gibeonites. [Simultaneously, King David was reprimanded] for not properly eulogizing [King Saul]. [This is an example of] two opposites at once.
Similarly, regarding King Solomon’s marriage to the daughter of Pharaoh it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">Jeremiah 32:31; Talmud Bavli Nidah 70b</i> “My anger has been aroused etc.”
However, the Song of Songs was said in reference to <i>HaShem</i>’s-יהו״ה joy over the building of the Holy Temple, as stated, <sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">Song of Songs 3:11; Zohar II 143a.</i> “On the day of the joy of His heart.”
[This is an example of] joy and anger, one thing and its opposite, as one.
Similarly, [regarding the flood] it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 8:21</i> “[I will not again curse the ground any more for man’s sake;] for the impulse of man’s heart is evil from his youth.”
However, previously it was stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 6:5-6</i> “And <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה saw that the wickedness of man was great in the earth, [and that all the impulse of the thoughts of his heart was only evil continually.] And <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה repented [for having made man on earth] etc.”
As explained elsewhere, all this comes about from the aspect of the qualities of <i>Tikkun-</i>Rectification, which are composite aspects.
In other words, they spread forth [outside of their essence] and do not result from the essential [nature] alone.
Therefore, it is possible for there to be an inter-inclusion of one thing with its opposite.
In contrast, [regarding] the <i>Nekudah</i>-Point of <i>Tohu</i>-Chaos; even when it is made into a division of ten [<i>sefirot</i>], [nonetheless] it is only [in the aspect of] a <i>Sefirah</i>-Emanation.
[However,] it is not a <i>Partzuf Adam</i>-Stature of Man, wherein there is the aspect of the inter-inclusion of all opposites.
Rather, it is specifically in the aspect of <i>Tikkun</i>-Rectification, in which each point spreads forth out of its essence, that they can become inter-included through the abundance of many different vessels, within which they are composed. This will suffice for those of understanding.
This then, is [the meaning of] the statement in <i>Sefer Yetzirah</i>, “He took fire and water and mixed them one with the other.”<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">See Talmud Bavli, Chagigah 12a</i>
In other words, [this is] the aspect of the composition of fire and water [together], specifically <b>not</b> [as they are] in their essential state, as explained elsewhere at length.

Chapter 21

With all the above [in mind], the general matter of the inter-inclusions of the three emanated lines may be understood. [The <i>sefirot</i> of] <i>Chochmah, Chessed</i> and <i>Netzach</i> are to the right, <i>Binah, Gevurah</i> and <i>Hod</i> are to the left, and <i>Da’at, Tiferet</i> and <i>Yesod</i> are in the middle.<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">These three lines are known in Kabbalah and Chassidut by their abbreviations. <i>Chochmah, Chessed</i> and <i>Netzach</i> are called <i>ChaCha”N</i>. <i>Binah, Gevurah</i> and <i>Hod</i> are called <i>BoGa”H</i>. <i>Da’at, Tiferet</i> and <i>Yesod</i> are known as <i>DaTi”Y</i>. (It is this configuration of the <i>sefirot</i> into three lines, right, left and middle, which is usually depicted as “The Tree of Life.” This configuration of the three lines of the <i>sefirot</i> as they are inter-included, is generally called the ten <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Yosher</i>.)</i>
[Now,] it is stated in <i>Pardes</i><sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">See Pardes Rimonim of Rabbi Moshe Cordovero, Shaar HaTzinorot.</i> that the inner aspect of <i>Keter</i>, which is called <i>Keter</i> of <i>Keter</i>, is not divided into three lines.
[It is only from] the external aspect of [<i>Keter</i>] that the three lines separate.
[In other words, it is] from the aspect of <i>Chochmah</i> of <i>Keter</i> [that a distinction of three lines begins], as known regarding the [Kabbalistic] intentions of [the words] “The Great, The Mighty and The Awesome”<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">See the beginning of <i>Amidah</i> prayer. As mentioned previously, “The Great – <i>HaGadol</i>” represents <i>Chessed</i> (Kindness) to the right, “The Mighty – <i>HaGibor</i>” represents <i>Gevurah</i> (Might/Judgment) to the left, and “The Awesome” represents the median conduct, the middle line which synthesizes the right and the left, which is <i>Tiferet</i> (Beauty/Mercy).</i> etc.
The explanation of these matters is that the aspect of the inter-inclusions of the right and left lines [one with the other] is specifically by means of the middle line.
The [explanation of the] matter is that in the right line of <i>ChaCha”N,</i><sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Chochmah, Chessed</i> and <i>Netzach</i></i> <i>Chessed</i> – Kindness is an offshoot of <i>Chochmah</i> – Insight, but is [nonetheless] separate from it.
This may be [understood by] the fact that <i>Chessed</i> – Kindness, branches from [<i>Chochmah</i>, which is] the intellect and reasoning that in the composition of something separate, leans toward kindness.
Similarly, <i>Netzach</i> – Conquest is an offshoot of <i>Chessed</i>, but is [nonetheless] separate from it. This is to say that the quality of kindness necessitates the aspect of triumph, in order to bring the kindness into actualization etc.
[On the other hand] the left line [of <i>BoGa”H</i><sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Binah, Gevurah</i> and <i>Hod</i>.</i>] is the opposite [of the above]. For example, the [emotional] quality of judgment, branches out from an intellect that leans towards judgment.
In the same manner <i>Binah</i> [gives rise to] <i>Gevurah</i>, as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 8:14</i> “I am <i>Binah</i>, <i>Gevurah</i> is mine.”
[For, as known,] <i>Chochmah</i> leans towards kindness, while judgments are aroused from <i>Binah</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar VaYikra 10b-11a</i>
(This accords with the statement in <i>Etz Chayim</i> that <i>Abba</i> (Father-<i>Chochmah</i>) is the source of the kindnesses and <i>Imma</i> (Mother-<i>Binah</i>) is the source of the judgments, as known.)
Now, the aspect of the inter-inclusion of these two [opposite] lines, so that they come to be connected [and synthesized] as one, is by means of the middle line of <i>DaTi”Y</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Da’at, Tiferet</i> and <i>Yesod</i></i>
For example, <i>Da’at</i> is the aspect of the median [conduct] that tips [the mind] from intellectual kindness to intellectual sternness, and is [therefore] called “The Leaning <i>Da’at</i>.”
(For example, [the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 8:21</i> “I will not continue to curse the earth because of mankind,] because the inclination of man’s heart is evil from his youth, [I will, therefore, not continue to punish any living thing, as I had done etc.”] becomes an intellectual reasoning for merit, though at first, this very same intellectual [reasoning] leaned toward judgment, as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 6:5,6</i> “And <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה saw that the wickedness of man was great [in the earth, and that all the impulse of the thoughts of his heart was only evil continually. And <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה repented that he had made man on earth] etc.” There are [many] other cases similar to this, as explained elsewhere.)
We find that [specifically] in <i>Da’at</i>, the two conceptual opposites of <i>Chessed</i> (Kindness) and <i>Gevurah</i> (Judgment) become connected. That is, it may lean toward kindness in one way and toward judgment in another way, and the like, even in [regard to] the same case.
Similarly, the quality of <i>Tiferet</i> mediates between [the heartfelt emotion of] <i>Chessed</i> and [the heartfelt emotion of] <i>Gevurah</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote">See Pardes Rimonim of Rabbi Moshe Cordovero, (<i>Shaar HaMachri’in</i>) Shaar 9; Chapter 3.</i>
An example of this is the [quality of] mercy, which can only take place after the quality of judgment. [This is to say that] although [he is found guilty], mercy releases him. This is the quality of <i>Yaakov</i>, as known.<sup class="footnote-marker">12</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar I 87b</i>
Likewise, the aspect of <i>Yesod</i> is the mediator to inter-includes the two opposites [gut emotions] of <i>Netzach</i> and <i>Hod</i>.
This is the matter of, “The kidneys which counsel” [either] yes or no,” before the [actual] influence of the influencer [is expressed]. [This takes place] whenever it is necessary to express the essential [heartfelt emotional] qualities of <i>Chessed</i> and <i>Gevurah</i>.
For example, in every deliberation of <i>Da’at</i>, [the final decision] comes about through the tipping of the [intellectual] balance.
Then, after the verdict [has been reached], it is weighed upon “The Righteous Scales,” which are <i>Netzach</i> and <i>Hod</i>, [to determine exactly] how to bring the influence out to the recipient.
This then, is the general matter of the middle line of <i>DaTi”Y,</i><sup class="footnote-marker">13</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Da’at, Tiferet, Yesod</i></i> which connects the two lines to its right and to its left.
[Now,] as known, the particulars of how [the <i>sefirot</i>] are inter-included are called,<sup class="footnote-marker">14</sup><i class="footnote">Sefer Yetzirah 5:1</i> “The Twelve Diagonal Lines – <i>Yood Beit G’voolei Alachson</i>,” whereas the middle line is called,<sup class="footnote-marker">15</sup><i class="footnote">Exodus 26:28; Zohar II 175b.</i> “The Inner Beam,” for runs through from end to end.
In other words, it reaches up to the inner aspect of <i>Keter</i>, which itself is higher than division into lines.
Because of this [the middle line] has the power to unify and synthesize the two [opposite] lines [to its right and left].
Now [for] the explanation of the matter of the inner <i>Keter</i> of the Emanated (<i>Atzilut</i>), which is called the <i>Keter</i> of <i>Keter,</i> (and is the aspect of <i>Keter</i> of <i>Atik Yomin</i> and <i>Arich Anpin</i> etc.).
This is the aspect of the desire and pleasure that comes into revelation, which is called “The Light of <i>Keter</i>.” It too includes ten <i>sefirot</i> within it.
[However] the aspect of <i>Chochmah</i> of <i>Keter</i>, is the reasoning for the desire and is called “The Hidden Reason of the Desire.”<sup class="footnote-marker">16</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Ta’am HaKamoos LaRatzon</i></i>
Similarly, [<i>Keter</i>] contains a <i>Chessed</i> and a <i>Netzach</i> etc, [until the aspect of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Keter</i>.]
All this is within the aspect of desire, which [still] is unlimited, even when it comes into revelation from the “Hidden Essential Desire” [of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>], as previously explained.
It is for this reason that the emotional [<i>sefirot</i>] of the desire and pleasure (that is <i>Keter itself</i>) are called “the preceding days” in comparison to the emotional [<i>sefirot</i>] of [the levels of] <i>Chochmah</i> and <i>Binah</i> (Insight and Comprehension) [themselves], which come about in a limited fashion, [that is], only according to the limitations of revealed intellect, as will be explained.
It is [only] from the external aspect of <i>Keter</i> that there comes about a division into three lines.
This is because in the “Hidden Reason for the Desire,” the desire is [already] regarded as being divided into <i>Chessed</i>, <i>Gevurah</i> and the intermediary [quality of <i>Tiferet</i>].
However, in <i>Keter</i> of <i>Keter</i>, which is beyond the “Hidden Reason for the Desire,” it is still only a simple essential desire, altogether beyond reason.
This is because a desire is altogether beyond reason, even a hidden reason.
This is similar to the matter of,<sup class="footnote-marker">17</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Menachot 29b</i> “Be silent! It thus arose in thought etc.,” as explained elsewhere.
Therefore, although [the level of <i>Keter</i> of <i>Keter</i>] comes into revelation from the lowest aspect of the concealed desire of the aspect of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>, (as explained at the end of chapter 19), it [nonetheless] is above divisions of right and left.
About this it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">18</sup><i class="footnote">Exodus 26:33</i> “And the curtain shall be for you as a separation between the Holy and the Holy of Holies.”
[This refers to] the aspect of the space (<i>Parsa</i>) separating <i>Keter</i> of <i>Keter</i> from <i>Chochmah</i> [of <i>Keter</i>].
This is the aspect of the <i>Krooma D’Aveera</i><sup class="footnote-marker">19</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar III (<i>Idra Rabba</i>) 128b.</i> (“Airy Membrane”), as explained elsewhere at length.
For this reason, we say [in our prayers],<sup class="footnote-marker">20</sup><i class="footnote">See the morning blessings and other places.</i> “May it be desirable <b>before</b> you,” [that is,] before the <i>Parsa</i>-Space.
[Since <i>Keter</i> of <i>Keter</i> is above division, it can therefore] change from a desire of judgment to a desire of kindness, and the like. This will suffice for those of understanding.

Chapter 22

We must now understand the particular inter-inclusions of the ten <i>sefirot</i> of [the world of] <i>Atzilut</i> (Emanation).
However, we must first explain the specifics of the matter of the sub-division of the <i>sefirot</i> into ten, and ten into ten etc.
For example, <i>Chessed</i> of <i>Chochmah</i> (Kindness of Insight) also divides into ten, and likewise, <i>Gevurah</i> of <i>Chochmah</i> (Sternness of Insight) divides into ten etc.
For, [as known], <i>Chochmah</i> (Insight) includes ten [<i>sefirot</i>] in it.
An example is <i>Chessed</i> and <i>Gevurah</i> of <i>Chochmah</i> (Kindness and Sternness of Insight), which are the [intellectual] leanings, either toward merit or toward judgment.
Now, <i>Chessed</i> of <i>Chochmah</i>, which is the intellectual leaning towards merit, also includes ten [<i>sefirot</i>] within it.
This is like <i>Chessed</i> and <i>Gevurah</i> as they are within [<i>Chessed</i> of <i>Chochmah</i>, so that there is an intellectual] leaning toward merit in a specific manner, and also an [intellectual] imperative toward judgment in a specific manner.
(For, although merit will be overturned to culpability within [the quality of] Judgment of <i>Chochmah</i>, and culpability will be overturned to merit within Kindness of <i>Chochmah</i>, this is [only so] as the quality is in its essence, [wherein] there are no sub-divisions.
However, [as it is in a state of] sub-divisions, [of the ten sub-dividing into ten etc.], it is possible for the aspect of Judgment to even be within Kindness of Insight (<i>Chessed</i> of <i>Chochmah</i>), and for the aspect of Kindness to be within the Judgement of Insight (<i>Din</i> of <i>Chochmah</i>), as known.)
Similarly, the [actual] emotional [<i>sefirot</i>] of <i>Chessed</i> and <i>Gevurah</i> themselves, are also divided into the ten [<i>sefirot</i>], <i>Keter, Chochmah, Binah</i>, and the emotional characteristics-<i>Midot</i> etc.
For, although [it was stated],<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Ketubot 84a</i> “We do not [exercise] mercifulness during judgment,” this was [said in regard to] the essential [quality] Judgment.
Similarly, there is no Judgment in the essential [quality] of Kindness.
However, as they spread forth from the essence [to become composites], there <b>is</b> Kindness in Judgment and Judgment in Kindness, as mentioned above.
Now, there is a [type of] inter-inclusion called, “The nullification of a thing to its opposite, that opposes it,” in which it becomes just like its opposite.
This is like the [matter of] “sweetening” of the Judgments (<i>Gevurot</i>) within the Kindnesses (<i>Chassadim</i>).
For example, this is like when the prosecutor transforms to become a defender, or the opposite, when the defender transforms to become a prosecutor.
Similarly, it is like the sweetening of bitter waters in sweet [waters], or the opposite.
Likewise, [it is like] the nullification of an intellectual [reasoning] for merit, into an intellectual [reasoning] for culpability, or the like.
These are [all examples of] true inter-inclusion, which is only possible because the opposition itself [latently] possesses its [opposite] power.
If this was not so, it would be impossible for it to become nullified to it.
For example, sweetness possesses [latent] bitterness and bitterness possesses [latent] sweetness.
By way of analogy, an example of this is a [dish called] <i>Merkachat</i>, [which is made] from honey cooked with radishes. This creates a delightful taste, which includes sharpness and sweetness as one, as known.
Similarly, there is [something of] the nature of fire in water, and [something of the] nature of water in fire.
Because of this, there can be an inter-inclusion of fire with water, or water with fire, as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">See Talmud Bavli, Chagigah 12a</i> “He took water from fire and fire from water etc.”
This [principle] likewise [applies to] the emotions of <i>Chessed</i> (Kindness) and <i>Gevurah</i> (Judgment). Because there is Judgment in Kindness and Kindness in Judgment, as mentioned above, therefore, Judgment may be nullified within Kindness, or vice versa, Kindness [may be nullified] within Judgment.
If this was not so, there could never be an inter-inclusion of one thing with its opposite.
However, there is [another type of] inter-inclusion of Judgment with Kindness [which comes about specifically] because it is essentially similar to it, rather than being negated by it.
On the contrary, [in such a case], it [actually] gives [additional] strength and force [to its opposite].
Nonetheless, it is called <i>Gevurah</i> of <i>Chessed</i> (Sternness of Kindness) or the reverse, <i>Chessed</i> of <i>Gevurah</i> (Kindness of Judgment) in that it strengthens the sternness and judgment.
As known, this matter is comparable to [the verse],<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 25:21-22</i> “If your enemy is hungry, give him bread to eat; [and if he is thirsty, give him water to drink, for [in doing so] you are heaping hot coals [upon his head etc.]”
This is to say that with this kindness and goodness, he perpetrates complete malevolence and judgment upon his [enemy], by destroying his soul.
Similarly, [it states],<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 7:10</i> “He pays His enemies up front, in order to destroy them.” This is likewise the case in any aspect of judgment and retribution that is done through the aspect of kindness.
This [kindness] gives much greater strength and force to the judgment, and is called <i>Chessed</i> of <i>Gevurah</i> (Kindness of Judgment).
This is like [the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 30:31,32</i>] “And <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה shall cause His glorious voice to be heard” in the camp of Sancheriv.
Similarly, the opposite is true of the aspect of <i>Gevurah</i> of <i>Chessed</i> (Sternness of Kindness). [That is,] there will be a much greater strength and force in an act of kindness which is done through the quality of judgment.
An example of this is the <i>Gevurot G’shamim -</i> “The strength of the rains,”<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah Ta’anit 1:1</i> which come in a constricted fashion so that they should come forth with abundance.
This is similar to the <i>Tzimtzum-</i>constriction of any light of influence, so that it may be received [by the recipient].
This [principle] also applies to the divisions of the “72 bridges”<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">See Pardes Rimonim, Shaar 21 (Shaar Pratey HaShemot), Chapter 5. Rabbi Nechunia Ben HaKanah (<i>Sefer HaBahir</i>) calls <i>HaShem</i>’s-יהו״ה name of 72 by the term “the 72 Bridges.” This refers to the name that arises from the three verses that begin with the words, “<i>VaYisa, VaYavo, VaYeit</i>” (Exodus 14:19-21). Each of these verses possess 72 letters, and they into 72 three letter combinations, made up of the letters of these three verses. This name is a name of Kindness, as indicated by the fact that the numerical value of 72 is Kindness-<i>Chessed-</i>חסד. However, it is expressed through the vehicle and vessels of <i>Gevurah-</i>Sternness, as indicated by the fact that the numerical value of 3 verses x 72 letters = 216, which is the numerical value of Judgment-Gevurah-גבורה-216. (Also see Ginat Egoz of Rabbi Yosef Gikatilla, translated as HaShem Is One, Vol. 3, The Gate explaining that the Explicit Name (<i>Shem HaMeforash</i>) is ע״ב-72 and יר״ו-216.)</i> and likewise to the “afflictions of love,” [as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 3:12</i> “For <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה admonishes the one He loves,] and like a father, he desires His child.”
That is, the kindness is specifically actualized through a garment of the quality of judgment.
It is specifically this [kind of expression of kindness] that [brings out] the [strength and] force of the kindness, even more than the [expression of] the essential kindness.
This is similar to [the statement],<sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Megillah 13b</i> “He precedes the cure to the infliction,” and as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote">Hosea 6:1</i> “For He has torn, and He will heal us; [He has smitten, and He will bind us up].”
Now, at first glance, why is the infliction necessary altogether? However, through the healing, one becomes healthier and stronger [than at first].
This is because sickness is the aspect of harsh judgment. It is remedied by means of the quality of Judgment within Kindness, that is, medicine, which is [made] of harsh substances.
This [principle] applies to the sweetening of every judgment. [It takes place] specifically in its [essential] source. That is, it is specifically [by means] of the Judgment in the Kindness (<i>Din SheBeChessed</i>).
This is because it is the strength of the Kindness, [which is required] to overpower the Judgment and sweeten it. This will suffice for those of understanding.
Through all the above, the inter-inclusions of <i>Chessed</i> and <i>Gevurah</i>, and the particular ways of how [they inter-include] may be understood, in that even <i>Gevurah</i> of <i>Chessed</i> [may be inter-included] with <i>Chessed</i> of <i>Gevurah</i>.
[This holds true] even though they may be two extreme opposites, [such as in a case] in which one is potent Kindness (<i>Chessed</i>) and one is potent Judgment (<i>Gevurah</i>).
Moreover, they are certainly [opposites] in that they are expressed within exchanged [and opposing] garments, [in which] one actualizes a judgment and one actualizes a kindness.
Nonetheless, since each one is specifically an actualization for something that is its opposite, that is, <i>Gevurah</i> of <i>Chessed</i> actualizes judgment but its inner [motivation] is kindness, and <i>Chessed</i> of <i>Gevurah</i> actualizes kindness but its inner [motivation] is judgment, therefore, specifically [because of this] they can come together as one, since each one [includes and], at the very least, indicates these two opposites.
This may be illustrated [by the fact that it was the angel] “Gavriel who [offered to] save Avraham,”<sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Pesachim 118a – When he was thrown into the fiery furnace by Nimrod.</i> and similarly, [by the fact that it was Gavriel] who<sup class="footnote-marker">12</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Yoma 77a – It states (Ezekiel 8:16), “He brought me to the inner court of the house of HaShem, and behold, at the door of the temple of HaShem, between the <i>Ulam</i> (porch) and the Altar there were about twenty five men. Their backs were towards the temple of HaShem, and they faced east, and they bowed down eastward, to the sun.” The Talmud continues, “From the fact that it states that they faced east don’t we know that their backs were towards the temple of HaShem? Rather, what do we learn from the fact that their backs were turned towards the temple of HaShem? This teaches us that they were revealing themselves, and defecating (towards the <i>Shechinah</i>). The Holy One blessed be He said to (the angel) Michael, “Michael, your people have sinned.” Michael answered, “Master of the Universe, isn’t it enough that there are good people amongst them?” The Holy One blessed be He answered him, “I will burn them, including the good ones that are amongst them (because they did not rebuke the sinners).” Then (Ezekiel 10:2) “G-d spoke to the man who was clothed in linen (referring to Gavriel) and said, “Go in between the wheels (referring to the <i>Ophanim</i> angels), under the cherub (referring to the <i>Chayot HaKodesh</i> angels), and fill your hand with coals of fire from between the cherubim, and throw them upon the city.” And he went in, in my (Ezekiel’s) sight.” It then continues and says (Ezekiel 10:7) “And the cherub stretched forth his hand from between the cherubim to the fire that was between the cherubim, and he took thereof and gave it into the hands of him that was clothed with linen (Gavriel), who took it and went out.” Rav Channa Bar Bizna said in the name of Rabbi Shimon Chasidah, “Had the coals not cooled from the hands of the cherub to the hands of Gavriel, there would not remain even a remnant or a refugee from the enemies of Israel.” (Note: The term “The enemies of Israel” is a euphemism for Israel themselves. The Talmud did not wish to express a curse in regard to the Jewish people so it turned it around against their enemies.) We see from this story that the coals cooled in the hands of Gavriel, the angel of <b>fire</b>. Now, seemingly, they should have gotten hotter in his hands. However, because he possesses the quality of <i>Chessed</i> as well, he is actually capable of cooling the coals.</i> “cooled the coals.”
This [comes] from the aspect of the <i>Gevurah</i> in the <i>Chessed</i>.
Similarly, a good [heavy] sweat eliminates the illness of [high] fever, like [the above-mentioned fact that harsh] medications heal afflictions.
[Furthermore], it was he [Gavriel] who smote the camp of Sancheriv, in an aspect of <i>Chessed</i> which is in <i>Gevurah</i>, as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">13</sup><i class="footnote">Kings II 19:35; Isaiah 37: 36; Talmud Bavli, Sanhedrin 95b</i> “The angel of the <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה went out [and smote in the camp of Ashur] etc.,” as known. This will suffice for those of understanding.
This then, is [the meaning of the teaching],<sup class="footnote-marker">14</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar beginning of Parshat Korach<i>.</i></i> “To include the left in the right and the right in the left.”
This is similar to light of <i>Chessed</i> in a vessel of <i>Gevurah</i>, wherein the vessel actualizes the opposite of its light.
That is, the vessel of <i>Gevurah</i> actualizes judgment, which is the opposite of the light of kindness within it.
The reverse is also true. A vessel of <i>Chessed</i> may actualize kindness, which is the opposite of the light of <i>Gevurah</i> within it.
However, this is not at all a contradiction, since this [phenomenon] is the aspect of lights and vessels, which is related to the matter of “form” and “substance” (as will later be explained).
This is in accordance to that which is explained elsewhere regarding the matter of the inter-inclusions of the name of seventy-two and the name of forty-two, which are the [first] two paragraphs of the <i>Shema</i> recital.<sup class="footnote-marker">15</sup><i class="footnote">The first paragraph of the <i>Shema</i> recital has 42 words, beginning with the word “<i>V’Ahavta</i> – And you shall love” until the end of the paragraph. This paragraph corresponds to the name of 42 letters. It is explained in the writings of the <i>Arizal</i> that the name of 42 letters (of <i>Ana B’Koach</i>) is a name of Sternness-<i>Gevurah</i>. In contrast, the second paragraph of the <i>Shema</i> recital has 72 words, beginning with “<i>V’Hayah</i> – And it shall come to pass” until the word “<i>V’Samtem</i> – And you shall place them.” The name of 72 is a name of kindness (as is indicated by its numerical value, which is equal to the word <i>Chessed</i>, as mentioned previously). Now, the first paragraph speaks of love of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה (<i>Chessed</i>), while the second paragraph speaks of the retribution which will ensue when one strays from <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה (<i>Gevurah</i>). So although the first paragraph represents <i>Gevurah</i>, it is expressed through vessels (i.e. letters) of <i>Chessed</i>. In contrast, the second paragraph represents <i>Chessed</i>, but is expressed through vessels of <i>Gevurah</i>. (Also see the <i>Kavanot</i> of the Arizal to the <i>Shema</i> recital<i>.</i>)</i>
Another example [of this principle] is [the fact that] the binding of Yitzchak was [done] by Avraham, the [epitomal] man of kindness.
[This is] likewise the case in regard to the “waving”<sup class="footnote-marker">16</sup><i class="footnote">See Numbers 8:5 through 8:21</i> of the Levites, who became included within the Kindnesses of the <i>Kohanim</i>-Priests.<sup class="footnote-marker">17</sup><i class="footnote">The Levites are rooted on the side of <i>Gevurah,</i> while the Priests (<i>Kohanim</i>) are rooted on the side of <i>Chessed</i>.</i>
This is as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">18</sup><i class="footnote">Numbers 18:3</i> “[Bring your brethren also of the tribe of Levi, the tribe of your father,] bring them near to you, [so that <b>they may join to you</b>, and minister to you].”
Why is it possible for them to serve their opposites? There are many other such examples.
Now, all of this is only possible because of the aspect of sub-divisions that exist in each [<i>sefirah</i>].
Therefore, “a kind finds its kind and become awakened,”<sup class="footnote-marker">19</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Eruvin 9a</i> even when the two are literally opposites.
This is similar to the matter of the differences between Michael and Gavriel, the angels of fire and water.
[Nonetheless] they do not extinguish each other, as it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">20</sup><i class="footnote">Job 25:2</i> “He makes peace in His high places.”
This is specifically because each one [latently] possesses something of his opposite.
However, in [regard to] the completely simple [essential] lights, such as the aspect of <i>Nekudot</i> – Points, which are called <i>Ketarim</i> – Crowns, it is impossible for them to become inter-included whatsoever.
This is because each one is completely different from the other, and nothing of its opposite can be found in it altogether.
An example [of this] is the essential aspect of goodness which is in the essence of the soul of a good person, and is called “The depth of goodness.” [In no way can it compromise] with the essential evil, which is called “the depth of evil.”
Only in true penitents – <i>Ba’alei T’shoova,</i> do we find that even the essence of evil has been transformed into goodness, so much so that,<sup class="footnote-marker">21</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Yoma 86b</i> “their transgressions themselves become counted as merits.”
This is because they give themselves over with [complete] self-sacrifice to the Essential Self of the light of the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, who is even beyond the essential differences between <i>Chessed</i> (Kindness) and <i>Gevurah</i> (Judgment).
Therefore, it is specifically through giving ourselves over to <i>HaShem-</i>יהו״ה, blessed is He, with complete self-sacrifice, that we are capable of praying and saying, “May it be desirable before You,” meaning, in the Essential Self of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He etc.
Similarly, [regarding the thirteen qualities of mercy, it states],<sup class="footnote-marker">22</sup><i class="footnote">Exodus 34:6</i> “And <i>HaShem-</i>יהו״ה passed before him and proclaimed, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, Benevolent and Gracious God etc.,” [thus] transforming even <b>essential</b> judgment into kindness, as will be explained concerning the matter of the “Thirteen Fixtures of the Beard.”<sup class="footnote-marker">23</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Yod-Gimel Tikkunei Dikna</i></i> This will suffice for those of understanding.
(This [sub-division and inter-inclusion] comes about by means of the aspect of the <i>Kav V’Chut</i> – Line and Thread, which possesses [something] of the power of the Essential Self of the light of the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה Himself, literally.
This is in accordance to the statement of our Sages,<sup class="footnote-marker">24</sup><i class="footnote">Pardes Rimonim, Shaar 32 (<i>Shaar HaKavanah</i>), Chapter 2, citing Sifrei.</i> “[One must pray] to Him [alone], and not to His qualities,” not even to His essential qualities. All this will be further explained, with the help of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He. This will suffice for those of understanding.)

Chapter 23

[We] now [must understand] the aspect of <i>Keter</i> [more] particularly, [to understand] how it is the aspect of an intermediary.
In its inner aspect it possesses something of the last level of the Emanator, while in its external aspect it is the root and head of the Emanated, as stated in <i>Etz Chayim.</i><sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">See Etz Chayim, Shaar 42 (<i>Shaar Drushei ABY”A</i>), Chapter 1.</i>
Moreover, as known, the first three <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Atik Yomin</i> are separate and exalted and do not become invested within the emanated.
This is [the meaning of the words,]<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">See the liturgy of the morning blessings of the <i>Shema</i>.</i> “[The King who alone is exalted…] who transcends the days of the world.”
Because of this it is called “<i>Atik Yomin</i> – The Ancient of Days.” [<i>Atik</i>] shares the same three letter root as “<i>HaMa’atik Hareem</i> – Who <b>removes</b> Mountains.”<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">Job 9:5</i> [In other words, <i>Atik Yomin</i>] is <b>removed</b> from the days of the world. Now, all this is well known.
Now, we must understand this in a manner of particulars, since <i>Atik Yomin</i> and <i>Arich Anpin</i> are considered to be one, except that in general, the aspect of <i>Atik Yomin</i> is considered to be the end of the World of the Unlimited One, whereas the aspect of <i>Arich Anpin</i> is the root and beginning of the Emanated [worlds], as stated in <i>Etz Chayim</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">See Etz Chayim, Shaar 42 (<i>Shaar Drushei ABY”A</i>), Chapter 1.</i>
As known, the explanation of these matters is that these [two levels of <i>Keter</i>] are the aspects of pleasure (<i>Ta’anug</i>) and desire (<i>Ratzon</i>).
Now, we observe that within every desire there is a pleasure, and if not for the pleasure there would be no desire for the thing at all.
This is like the desire for wealth or honor. If not for the pleasure of [wealth or honor], he would have no desire for them at all.
Therefore, seemingly, pleasure is the inner aspect of desire.
However, we also observe the opposite, that if there is no desire there is no pleasure.
That is, he will have no pleasure whatsoever from something he does not desire. If so, desire is inner to pleasure.
What we see is that the one cannot exist without the other, because desire cannot exist without pleasure, and pleasure cannot exist without desire.
According to this, we must say that the two are one, because it is only when they bound together as one, that [<i>Keter</i>] exists.
All this [holds true] whether it is the simple essential pleasure and desire, or whether it is a composite pleasure and desire that the soul spreads forth and is drawn after, even though it is not of [the soul’s] essence, but is [rather] a separate thing from it.
Generally, we see that the nature of the soul is to be drawn after something that is pleasurable, to the point that its entire essence could be drawn after [it] and included in it.
[This is] like a composite pleasure for a specific [thing], which is separate [from the essence], such as honor, wealth, insight, or the emotional [traits] of kindness, judgment, conquest and self-aggrandizement, or the like.
[This is true of] anything that the soul craves, such as lusting for all worldly pleasures, and the like.
Although none of these [desires] are in an aspect of an essential <i>Heyulie</i> pleasure, and it is only that the soul is drawn after them and lusts for them, nonetheless, from this we see that the essence of the soul is in an aspect of a <i>Heyulie</i> of pleasure.
It is for this reason that it is drawn to composite pleasures and flees from pain, which is the opposite of pleasure.
These [two, pleasure and pain,] are two lines that are equally counterbalanced, literally.
Commensurate to the spreading forth of the soul to become filled with light from pleasurable things, so will its light become completely diminished and withdrawn by pain and anguish.
From this we see that the essence of its being is pleasure.
However, the principal [proof for this] is from the fact that it will flee and become withdrawn due to pain.
This is a greater proof [of this phenomenon].
It is for this reason that the early Kabbalists decreed and stated that pleasure is considered to be of the essence of the soul, and they stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">Sefer Yetzirah 2:2</i> “There is nothing higher than pleasure.”
However, this is not [entirely] true. Rather, the essence of the soul becomes <b>filled</b> with great pleasure, and its entire essence is drawn after it, to the point that it may expire when it is almost entirely drawn into it. This is like [the verse],<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 84:3</i> “my soul expires etc.”
The reverse is likewise true, that it will expire and its light will become completely and absolutely diminished by the intensity of extreme pain [or anguish], as known.
Now, an even clearer proof [of this] is from what we observe regarding even the particular powers of the soul; that it is mainly the pleasure in a particular power that establishes its existence at all times.
For example, [regarding] the power of the quality of kindness; although it is essential and natural in the nature of [of a person who is] good to bestow goodness, [nonetheless,] its principal existence [comes about from] the pleasure, in that he takes pleasure in influencing goodness.
The true existence of his good nature is that by nature he takes great pleasure in [bestowing] goodness, to the point that the main vitality of his soul comes about through the pleasure [that he gets from doing acts of] goodness and kindness.
The reverse is true of someone who is cruel by nature. This only means that his entire vitality is the pleasure [that he gets] from doing evil and cruelty, as known.
Likewise, the primary existence of the quality of Victory (<i>Netzach</i>) is the immense pleasure [that he gets], to the point that the entire vitality of his soul is drawn into being victorious over his fellow.
Should he not be victorious, he may [actually] become ill.
Similarly, this is the case with each and every particular quality, including Insight (<i>Chochmah</i>) and Desire (<i>Ratzon</i>).
Their principal existence and source is the pleasure [in them], as is clearly observable that without the pleasure in conceptualization, a person will not have the power to innovate any insight.
This is in accordance with the statement,<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar I 138a - Rabbi Yitzchak the son of Rabbi Yossi was traveling from Kaputkia to Lud. He encountered Rabbi Yehuda. Rabbi Yitzchak said to him, “Say that our associates, the Sages of the Mishnah, should be awakened to this matter; that the <i>Yetzer Hara</i> (lust) should be banished from the world, except during the time of marital relations.” [Rabbi Yehuda] answered him, “By your life! The <i>Yetzer Hara</i> (lust) is necessary for the world, just as rain [is necessary] for the world. If not for the <i>Yetzer Hara</i> (lust), there would be no pleasure in learning [Torah].”</i> “Were it not… for the pleasure in [Torah] study etc.”
[Moreover], as known regarding the matter of,<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote">Ecclesiastes 8:1</i> “A man’s wisdom illuminates his face,” that the “<i>Lachloochit</i> – Moisture” within which is the <i>Heyulie</i> for pleasure, is the source for the conceptualization of any concept.
However, it is only in regard to desire that we observe that without desire there cannot be pleasure. ]We find this phenomenon] even in all the particular qualities.
For example, if [a person] does not desire kindness or judgment, he will have no pleasure in them at all.
Similarly, if he does not desire to become intelligent, he will find no pleasure in [intellectual pursuits] at all.
Likewise, if he does not at all desire victory, he will have no pleasure in victory. [The same is true of] self-aggrandizement or all other worldly pleasures, such as wealth or honor and the like.
Without desire, there is no pleasure in them, whatsoever.
In other words, because this entire matter is that since the whole essence of the soul is drawn after the pleasure and desire, (for, [just as with pleasure,] the desire also draws forth the entire soul, to the point where it can expire because of its desire for something, as is known,) therefore, all its particular powers also [derive] their principal existence from the pleasure and the desire.
The absence of [pleasure and desire in any particular matter] is the pain of the matter, this being the opposite of pleasure.
If something [stands in] opposition to [his] desire, although, [in and of itself], it is not [necessarily] a painful thing, he will automatically be agonized by it.
For example, if he desires to love his enemy, he will delight in him.
On the other hand, if he no [longer] desires someone who he loves, he will be agonized by him.
Similarly, if he enjoys something that is hateful and damaging to him, he will desire it, or if he is pained by something that he loves, he will no [longer] desire it.
This is because desire and pleasure are one essence, and it is impossible to know which precedes [the other].
At times the one is internal and the other is external, while at [other] times the opposite [is true].
[However,] the one cannot be found without the other, for if there is no pleasure there is no desire, and if there is no desire there is no pleasure.
[This is the case] whether it is a simple [desire or pleasure] or whether it is a composite [desire or pleasure], as mentioned above. This will suffice for those of understanding.

Chapter 24

Now, to one who contemplates [how things are] above, the analogue for all that has been previously stated will be understood.
[That is, he will understand] how the aspect of the essence of the simple pleasure of the Essential Self of the light of the Unlimited One, as it is before <i>Tzimtzum,</i> which is called,<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">See Emek HaMelech, Shaar Sha’ashuey HaMelech B’Atzmooto.</i> “the Delight of the King in Himself,” is literally an infinite aspect.
Moreover, [he will understand that] even the ten essential <i>Sefirot</i>, from <i>Keter</i> to <i>Malchut</i> of The Unlimited One (<i>Ein Sof</i>), all [derive their existence] from the simple pleasure in His Essential Self.
By way of analogy, even the essential kindness of the [human] soul, [derives] its existence primarily from the pleasure [of it].
Nonetheless, in truth, the Essential Self of the limitless light of the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, is even beyond the aspect of simple pleasure.
However, it is drawn after and radiates within the aspect of pleasure, just as the essence of the [human] soul is drawn after pleasure.
It is for this reason that it was stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">Sefer Yetzirah 2:4</i> “There is nothing higher than pleasure.”
For example, [vested] within the aspect of the desire for kindness of <i>HaShem</i>’s-יהו״ה Essential Self, is the simple [essential] pleasure.
It is drawn forth and radiates greatly, until it descends and even comes into a separate matter.
This [separate matter] is the aforementioned aspect of the Primal Pleasure and Desire (<i>Ta’anoog V’Raton HaKadoom</i>) that follows the <i>Tzimtzum</i>, to become the source for the [entire] chaining down of the worlds of <i>ABY”A</i>.
It descends [further], to the point that it is drawn down to the very end of everything, such as even the most final particular of the ten <i>sefirot</i> of [the world of] <i>Atzilut</i> – Emanation.
This is [understood] by way of the aforementioned analogy of the pleasure that exists to give being to the [emotional] quality of Victory (<i>Netzach</i>), and the like.
This then, is the [meaning] of the statement in <i>Etz Chayim</i>, that <i>Atik Yomin</i> and <i>Arich Anpin,</i> which are the pleasure and the desire, are one entity, (and they are called the “three heads which are engraved, one within the other.<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar III (<i>Idra Zuta</i>) 288a. Also see Etz Chayim (<i>Shaar Arich Anpin</i>) Shaar 13, Chapter 2.]</i> Sometimes one [pleasure] is internal [and sometimes desire is internal] etc., as mentioned previously.) and that the one cannot be without the other.
[<i>Keter,</i> which is the pleasure and desire, is] invested within each and every <i>sefirah,</i> [even] in the most particular of particulars, for without it, it can have no existence at all, as previously explained at length.
Moreover, it [also] encompasses them all.<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">See Ma’amirei Admor HaZaken, HaKtzarim, page 492. See also, Zohar II (<i>Ra’ayah Mehemnah</i>) 42b, and introduction to Tikkunei Zohar 17a.</i>
(This is in accordance with what is explained elsewhere with the analogy of the ten pits which are dug in succession. The [water in the] first is drawn into each [subsequent] pit etc. Likewise, it states in the Zohar, “He made a big vessel, [like a person who makes a big excavation, which becomes filled with the water that comes out of a spring… He then made a small vessel, which is the letter <i>Yod,</i> which became filled with it from the source (<i>Keter</i>), and He called it a spring flowing with <i>Chochmah</i> - Insight.] Through it, He called Himself, ‘<i>Chacham</i> – Wise’, [and the vessel He called <i>Chochmah</i> - Insight.]” Similarly, it states, “You brought out ten ‘<i>Tikkunim</i> – Vessels’ and called them ten <i>sefirot</i> etc.”)
This is because the aspect of <i>Atik Yomin</i> is considered to still be a part of the World of The Unlimited One (<i>Ein Sof</i>).<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">See Etz Chayim<i>,</i> (<i>Shaar Drushei ABY”A</i>) Shaar 42, Chapter 1. See also Shaarei Teshuvah of the Mittler Rebbe, pg. 104.</i>
This is because the World of The Unlimited One (<i>Ein Sof</i>) is considered to continue until the aspect of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>, which is the aspect of the “letters” of the end action that arose in the aforementioned Primal Thought and Desire (<i>Machshava V’Ratzon HaKadoom</i>).
It is [these “letters,” which are] the last level of the Essential Self of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, that become the <i>Keter</i> of <i>Atik Yomin</i>, which is the aspect of the revelation of the light of the pleasure from the aforementioned concealed pleasure and Primal Desire (<i>He’elem Ha’Oneg V’Ratzon HaKadoom</i>).
Therefore, even <i>Keter</i> of <i>Atik Yomin</i>, and the [<i>sefirot</i>] of <i>Chochmah, Binah</i> and the emotions that are within it, are all considered to be of the end of the World of The Unlimited One (<i>Ein Sof</i>).
However, [this is not the case] with <i>Arich Anpin</i>, which is the aspect of the revelation of the desire that comes because of the pleasure.
Because [the desire] is drawn to spread forth below, it is called the beginning and root of the Emanations, which refers to the ten <i>sefirot</i> of [the world of] <i>Atzilut</i>, both generally and particularly.
It is for this reason that the aspect of <i>Keter</i> is generally called an intermediary aspect, which possesses something of the last level of the Essential Self of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, but is the beginning of the Emanated.
Because the lights of the Emanated are in an aspect of “the revelation of the concealed,” they therefore are in an aspect of separateness from the Essential Self of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, as previously explained (in chapter nineteen<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">In the Hebrew text it says (chapter 12), but it is a typo which should say (chapter 19), as corrected above.</i>).
By way of analogy, this is like the emotions of <i>Chessed</i> or <i>Gevurah</i> for a separate thing, which come from the power of the qualities of <i>Chessed</i> and <i>Gevurah</i> of the Essential Self.
Nevertheless, it is the aspect of the pleasure and desire which comes from the Essential Self of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, that vests within everything in order to constantly give them existence, as mentioned previously.
This is because, the source of this pleasure and desire is in the Essential Self of the light of The Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, and is called “the Delight of the King in Himself” (<i>Sha’ashoo’ei HaMelech B’Atzmo</i>).
This is similar to the [aforementioned] analogy of the soul, which is drawn after every pleasure, which is proof that the pleasure fills its light.
If so, then this itself is the reason that it is from the particular pleasure within each of the particular [emanations of] lights, that they primarily [derive] their existence.
[This is true] even until the aspect of <i>Malchut,</i> which is the [quality of] Dominion.
Were it not for the pleasure in it, it would have no existence.
The absence of the light of the pleasure [for something] equals the absence of the light of its existence. This will suffice for those of understanding.
Now, all the above is only in a general manner.
In a manner of particulars, however, it is only the aspect of the first three [<i>sefirot</i>] of <i>Atik Yomin</i> that are considered to be [part] of the Essential Self of the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He.
On the other hand, the seven lower <i>sefirot</i> of [<i>Atik Yomin</i>] become invested within the “<i>Gulgulta</i> – Skull” of <i>Arich Anpin</i>.
<i>Chessed</i> (Kindness) of <i>Atik Yomin</i> [vests] within the “<i>Gulgulta</i> – Skull” [of <i>Arich Anpin</i>], <i>Gevurah</i> [of <i>Atik Yomin</i> vests] within “<i>Mocha Stima’ah</i> – the Hidden Brain” [of <i>Arich Anpin</i>] etc.<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">See Etz Chayim<i>,</i> (<i>Shaar Arich Anpin</i>), Shaar 13, Ch. 6-7.</i>
This then, is the meaning of [the statement,<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote">See the liturgy of the <i>Yotzer</i> blessing of the morning <i>Shema</i> recital.</i> “The King who alone is exalted], who transcends the days of the world.”
This is because the coming into being of the desire from the pleasure is primarily from the aspect of the emotions of the pleasure, as known.
For example, <i>Chessed</i> (kindness) of the pleasure [vests within <i>Keter</i> of the desire].
By way of analogy, when a person is in a state of pleasure during the joy of his son’s wedding, or the like, he will then bestow goodness and abundant kindness upon everyone.
[This is] because of the pleasure that uplifts his soul (for the aforementioned reason).
During such a time, he may be aroused to grant every desire.
In other words, even a desire for judgment may be overturned to kindness.
This [overturning of the desire from <i>Chessed</i> to <i>Gevurah</i>] is dependent upon the aspect of the [essential] point of desire, which is higher than the “hidden reason for the desire” (<i>Ta’am Kamoos LaRatzon</i>) that divides into <i>Chessed</i> and <i>Gevurah</i> – kindness and judgment.
This then, is an analogy through which one may understand how the aspect of <i>Chessed</i> of <i>Atik Yomin</i> vests within the “<i>Gulgulta</i> – Skull” [of <i>Arich Anpin</i>].
Now, the aspect of <i>Gevurah,</i> which is judgment, and is the opposite of pleasure, is what vests within “<i>Chochmah Stima’ah</i> – the Hidden Wisdom” of <i>Arich Anpin</i>, which is the “hidden reason for the desire” (<i>Ta’am Kamoos LaRatzon</i>).
This is the <b>precision</b> of the desire, that it should be a particular way, and not in any other way.
This is in accordance with what is written in books of Kabbalah,<sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote">See Etz Chayim<i>,</i> (<i>Shaar Arich Anpin</i>) Shaar 13, Chapter 6.</i> that the early [Kabbalists] decreed and stated that <i>Chochmah</i> is an aspect of judgment.
This is because, when desire comes according to the dictates of <i>Chochmah</i>, it comes with precision and restriction that it should be like this and not like that.
For this reason, there are many judgments in the laws of the Torah, since the Torah comes out of <i>HaShem</i>’s-יהו״ה upper wisdom-<i>Chochmah</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar II 62a; 85a; (<i>Ra’aya Mehemna</i>) 121a; Zohar III 81a; 182a, 261a.</i>
In contrast, the radiance of the thirteen qualities of mercy is from [a level] higher than the <i>Chochmah</i> of the desire, and can [therefore] “pardon iniquity.”
Certainly [this is the case in regard to] the aspect of the first three <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Atik Yomin</i>, which are not invested in the Emanated.
This is the aspect of the pleasure as it is within Himself.
As of yet, no desire whatsoever has been born of it, except that all desires are destined to come from it.
It is considered to be part of the general essence of the simple pleasure (<i>HaTa’anoog HaPashoot</i>).
That is, it is from the aspect of the source of all pleasures in the Essential Self of the limitless light of the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He.
This is as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 36:10</i> “With you is the source of life,” that is, the source of all the pleasures [within] the Primal Desire [for Creation] (<i>Ratzon HaKadoom</i>).
In the general totality [of the chaining down] it this called<sup class="footnote-marker">12</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar III (<i>Idra Rabba</i>) 128a</i> “<i>Atika D’Atikin</i> – The Ancient of the Ancients.”
[However, more particularly] it is called “<i>Atik Yomin</i> – The Ancient of Days,” as stated in Daniel,<sup class="footnote-marker">13</sup><i class="footnote">Daniel 7:9</i> “And <i>Atik Yomin</i> sat etc.” [<i>Atik –</i> Ancient] is a term of antiquity, which [indicates] the aspect of the eternity of the Essential Self of the limitless light of the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, as He comes to radiate within the chaining down of the line and thread.
However, in regard to His actual Essential Being [it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">14</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Yevamot 16b</i>] “Is there old age before the Holy One blessed be He!?”
This is in accordance with what is stated elsewhere<sup class="footnote-marker">15</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar II 134a; See also Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Devarim, Vol. 1, pg. 224; Na”Ch<i>,</i> pg. 226; Also see the Opening Gateway (<i>Petach HaShaar</i>) to Imrei Binah of the Mittler Rebbe, translated as The Gateway to Understanding.</i> regarding the matter of the word “<i>Va’ed</i> – Forever” (ועד), which through a permutation of letters equals “<i>Echad</i> – One” (אחד), referring to the simple [Oneness] Himself.
For, when the Essential Self of the limitless light of the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, who [even] transcends the time of “<i>Yemei Kedem</i> – the Preceding Days,” radiates within time, then time too becomes eternal and is then called “<i>Atik Yomin</i> – the Ancient of Days.” This will suffice for those of understanding.

Chapter 25

We must now understand the details of the matter of the ten <i>Sefirot</i> of [the world of] <i>Atzilut</i> – Emanation.
In other words, [we must understand] the descent of the light from the externality of <i>NeHi”Y</i><sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Netzach, Hod</i> and <i>Yesod</i>.</i> of <i>Arich Anpin</i> into <i>Abba</i><sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">As mentioned previously, when referring to the <i>Partzuf</i> – The complete Stature of <i>Chochmah</i> or <i>Binah</i>, they are referred to as <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i> – Father and Mother. The reason they are called “Father” and “Mother” is because it is <i>Chochmah</i>, the “Father,” which provides the seminal flash of insight, which is subsequently developed in <i>Binah</i>, the “Mother.” (This unification gives birth to offspring, i.e., the emotions and actions, as will be explained later.)</i> and <i>Imma</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">Also see Likkutei Biurim (R’ Hillel Paritcher), chapter 25.</i>
[Now,] sometimes it states<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">See Etz Chayim<i>,</i> (<i>Shaar Abba V’Imma</i>) Shaar 14, Chapter 1. See also Imrei Binah (of Rabbi DovBer of Lubavitch) Shaar HaTefilin pg.116c.</i> that the “Arms”<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Chessed</i> and <i>Gevurah</i> of the <i>Arich Anpin</i>.</i> of <i>Arich Anpin</i> vest within <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i>.
(However, the statement<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar I (<i>Idra Rabba</i>) 249. See also, Zohar II (<i>Idra D’Mishkena</i>) 122b.</i> that “The head of the King is fixed within <i>Chessed</i> and <i>Gevurah</i>” refers to the “head” of <i>Arich Anpin</i> [within] which <i>Chessed</i> and <i>Gevurah</i> of <i>Atik Yomin</i> are affixed. [That is to say,] <i>Chessed</i> of <i>Atik Yomin</i> [is vested] within the “<i>Gulgulta</i> – Skull,” [i.e., <i>Keter</i> of <i>Arich Anpin</i>] etc., as previously explained.)
[However,] sometimes it states<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar III 289b; See also Etz Chayim, Shaar HaKlallim, Ch. 5.</i> that <i>Abba</i> suckles from the eighth “<i>Mazal</i>” [which is] “<i>Notzer</i>,” and <i>Imma</i> [suckles] from the thirteenth “<i>Mazal</i>” [which is] “<i>VeNakeh</i>.”<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote">"8 There are thirteen qualities of Mercy which <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה revealed to Moshe.
