(Exodus 34:6-7) They are:<br>1. <i>E-L</i> - Benevolent God<br>2. <i>Rachum</i> - Compassionate<br>3. <i>V'Chanun</i> - and Gracious<br>4. <i>Erech</i> - Long (slow)<br>5. <i>Apayim</i> - Suffering (to anger)<br>6. <i>V'Rav Chesed</i> - and Abounding in Kindness<br>7. <i>V'Emet</i> - and Truth<br>8. <i>Notzer Chesed</i> - He Preserves Kindness<br>9. <i>L'Alaphim</i> - for two thousand generations<br>10. <i>Noseh Avon</i> - Pardoning Iniquity<br>11. <i>VaPeshah</i> - and Transgression<br>12. <i>V'Chata'a</i> - and Sin<br>13. <i>V'Nakeh</i> - and He Cleanses.<br>These “thirteen qualities of mercy” are often referred to as “the thirteen fixtures of the beard of <i>Arich Anpin</i>.” The eighth and thirteenth qualities, “<i>Notzer</i>” and “<i>V’Nakeh</i>,” are referred to as “<i>Mazalot</i>.” The root of the word “<i>Mazal-</i>מזל” is “<i>Nozel-</i>נוזל” which means “to flow down.” These two are called “the upper <i>Mazal</i> and the lower <i>Mazal</i>,” because influence flows down from them to the intellectual <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Chochmah</i> and <i>Binah</i>, as will be explained."</i>
Now, as known regarding the matter of the “<i>Ko’ach Mah</i> – the Power of What”<sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar III (<i>Ra’aya Mehemnah</i>) 28a, 34a.</i> (כח מה) that <i>Chochmah</i> – Insight (חכמה), is<sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote">Job 28:12</i> “found from nothing,” and is in an aspect of “Nothing – <i>Ein</i>.”
[In contrast,] <i>Binah</i> - Comprehension is called “Something – <i>Yesh</i>.”
The light and influence of the “Nothingness” (<i>Ein</i>) of <i>Chochmah</i> – Insight, radiates and is drawn into the aspect of the comprehension of <i>Binah</i>.
That is, [there is a transition] from the intangible “nothing” (<i>Ein</i>) to the tangible “something.”
Moreover, [<i>Chochmah</i> and <i>Binah</i> – Insight and Comprehension] are called,<sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar II 56a; Zohar III 4a</i> “The two lovers who never separate” [about which it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">12</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar III (<i>Idra Zuta</i>) 290b</i>] “They dwell as one.”
This is the aspect of the “point” of <i>Chochmah</i> – Insight, that flashes like a lightning bolt from that which is above the intellect. (In common language [this is called] “understanding.”)
In other words, [it flashes] from the potential power to conceptualize (<i>Koach HaMaskeel</i>), which is called “The Hidden Insight” – <i>Chochmah Steema’a</i> of <i>Arich Anpin</i>. [This potential to conceptualize] is called “the Concealed Insight – <i>Chochmah HaNe’elama</i>.” It is the source that brings forth all intellect from “nothingness,” and is called “<i>Maskeel</i>,” as known.
This then, is the explanation of the statement that the light of <i>Abba</i> suckles from the eighth “<i>Mazal</i>” [which is] “<i>Notzer</i>.”
The letters [of the word “<i>Notzer</i>-נוצר” may are the same as the letters of the word] “pipe-<i>Tzinor</i>-צנור.” [That is,] it is like a thin pipe.
Similarly, the aspect of the “<i>Sa’arot</i> – Hairs” of the eighth “<i>Mazal</i>” is the growth aspect of the aforementioned potential power to conceptualize (<i>Koach HaMaskeel</i>).
That is, it sprouts forth all kinds of concepts from “nothingness.”
Now, the development (suckling) [of this seminal flash], that is, the growth of the brain of <i>Abba</i> (Insight) and the growth of the brain of <i>Imma</i> (Comprehension), comes from the thirteenth “<i>Mazal</i>,” which is “<i>VeNakeh</i>.”
These two “<i>Mazalot</i>,”<sup class="footnote-marker">13</sup><i class="footnote">This is the plural of the word “<i>Mazal</i>.”</i> the upper “<i>Mazal</i>” and the lower “<i>Mazal</i>,” are the roots of the [intellectual] brains of <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i>.
This is to say that in the potential power to conceptualize itself, there is a root for the development of the brain of understanding (<i>Chochmah</i>) and a root for the development of the brain of grasp and comprehension (<i>Binah</i>).
These [two, <i>Chochmah</i> and <i>Binah</i>] are called “the brain of <i>Abba</i>” and “the brain of <i>Imma</i>,” as known.
Now, just as the aspect of the brain of <i>Binah,</i> which is the brain of grasp and comprehension, receives from the aspect of the “nothingness” of the brain of <i>Chochmah,</i> so too, in their source, there is a unification of the two “<i>Mazalot</i>” of “<i>VeNotzer</i>” and “<i>VeNakeh</i>.”
It is known that although the “<i>Mazalot</i>” are called “<i>Sa’arot</i> – Hairs,” that only break forth and come out from the aspect of the excess of the “Hidden Brain” of <i>Arich Anpin</i>, nonetheless, their [true] source is from the essence of the “<i>Gulgulta</i> – Skull.”
[This is to say that their source] is higher than the innerness of the “Hidden Brain” itself.
It is for this reason that they burst forth in an aspect of excess.
This is analogous to the bursting forth of steam from the [pressure] of a tightly sealed [pot].
For example, when the potential power for intellect greatly overwhelms the [power of] <i>Chochmah,</i> there is a fallout of excess [insight] from <i>Chochmah</i> [into <i>Binah</i>, that is, from insight into comprehension]. The source of this excess is higher than the actual light of the intellect itself.
It is for this reason that it states, “The excess of the Upper <i>Chochmah</i> is Torah,” specifically in praise [of the Torah], as explained elsewhere.<sup class="footnote-marker">14</sup><i class="footnote">See Imrei Binah (of Rabbi Dov Ber of Lubavitch), Shaar HaKri’at Shma<i>,</i> page 57a and elsewhere.</i>
Likewise, this is the reason for the greatness of the thirteen qualities of mercy, which are called “the thirteen fixtures of the beard [of <i>Arich Anpin</i>]” that come out of the excess of the “Hidden Brain-<i>Mocha Steema’a</i>.”
This is as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">15</sup><i class="footnote">Exodus 34:6</i> “And <i>HaShem-</i>יהו״ה passed before him and proclaimed, ‘<i>HaShem-</i>יהו״ה <i>HaShem-</i>יהו״ה.’”
This is higher than the “Hidden Brain-<i>Mocha Steema’a</i>,” which is called the “hidden reasoning and wisdom for the concealed desire” and is also called “The intellect that is hidden from all contemplation” or “the wonders of <i>Chochmah</i>.”
According to this, when it states that the light of <i>Abba</i> suckles from the [eighth] “<i>Mazal</i>,” this is actually [from] higher than the “Hidden <i>Chochmah</i>” itself.
It is for this reason that it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">16</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar III (<i>Idra Rabba</i>) 134a</i> “Everything is dependent upon <i>Mazal</i>, even the <i>Sefer Torah</i> (Torah Scroll) in the <i>Heichal-</i>sanctuary,” which refers to the unification of <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i> below.
[This is] the [flash of the] “point” of <i>Chochmah</i> in the chamber of <i>Binah</i>, from “nothing to something,” as mentioned above.<sup class="footnote-marker">17</sup><i class="footnote">See Introduction to Zohar 6a. Also see Zohar II 180a</i>
The [flash of insight from <i>Chochmah</i> to <i>Binah</i>] is what is meant by,<sup class="footnote-marker">18</sup><i class="footnote">See Sefer Yetzirah, 1:1</i> “Book-<i>Sefer</i>-ספר” and “Story-<i>Seepoor</i>-ספור,” which is called “the <i>Sefer Torah</i> (Torah Scroll) in the <i>Heichal</i>-sanctuary,” as known.
Now, this is much higher than the statement that <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i> enclothe the “Arms” of <i>Arich Anpin</i>.
Moreover, this is certainly [higher] than the aspect of <i>NeHi”Y</i> of <i>Arich Anpin</i> as they are vested within <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i>.
[This is so] because, as known, the aspect of the seven lower [<i>sefirot</i>] of <i>Arich Anpin,</i> are only the aspects of the emotional [<i>Sefirot</i> of] <i>ChaGa”T</i><sup class="footnote-marker">19</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Chessed, Gevurah</i> and <i>Tiferet</i>.</i> etc.
These are called,<sup class="footnote-marker">20</sup><i class="footnote">Exodus 14:31, 13:9. (<i>“HaYad HaGedolah</i> – The Great Hand” is <i>Chessed</i> and “<i>HaYad HaChazakah</i> – The Mighty Hand” is <i>Gevurah</i>.)</i> “the Great Hand and the Mighty Hand,” and in the Zohar they also are called by the term,<sup class="footnote-marker">21</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar III 249b – “<i>Toorey D’Chashoocha –</i> Mountains of Darkness” and “<i>Toorey D’Nehorah</i> – Mountains of Light.”</i> “The Mountains of Darkness.”
(This is in accordance with what is known, regarding the teaching, “This gazelle goes to the mountains of darkness and gathers her food from there.” This refers to how <i>Malchut</i> goes up to <i>ChaGa”T</i> of <i>Arich Anpin</i>, as it states, “The ark was uplifted… in the seventh month” which refers to <i>Rosh HaShanah</i>, during which <i>Malchut</i> goes up to “<i>Harei Ararat</i>” which is [translated by the Targum as] ‘the mountains of darkness.’”)
These are like mountains that are [so] high that the light of the sun does not shine upon them.
In other words, this is the aspect of the emotions of the desire, which are higher than revealed intellect and reasoning.
In contrast, the emotions that are according to intellect and reasoning are called, “the Mountains of Light,” since <i>Chochmah</i> is called “Light.”
However, the emotions of the desire are called “the Mountains of Darkness,” [for they are] emotions that are hidden in the desire.
[Now,] their source is from the aforementioned aspect of the “Hidden Wisdom – <i>Chochmah Stima’ah</i>,” which is called “The Concealed Insight<i>-Ta’aloomot Chochmah</i>.”
This is the matter of the “Hidden Reasoning for the Desire,” from which the two lines of <i>Chessed</i> and <i>Gevurah</i> (Kindness and Judgment) of the desire divide.
This then is [the meaning of] the statement that the “Arms” of <i>Arich Anpin</i> vest within <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i>.
This is as we clearly observe that the root for intellectual reasoning [leaning] towards kindness and merit, exists because of the quality of <i>Chessed</i> (Kindness) and the great love within one’s desire.
This is similar to “a bribe, which blinds [the eyes of the wise] etc.”<sup class="footnote-marker">22</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 16:19, also see Exodus 23:8</i>
Because of the bribe, he has a love in [his] desire [towards this person].
He will therefore find justification, and his intellectual powers will be caused to lean from [a judgment of] guilt to merit.
This is similar to [the Talmudic<sup class="footnote-marker">23</sup><i class="footnote">See Talmud Bavli Ketubot 105b</i> account of] Rabbi Yishmael, who “took a basket of fruits… and said [to himself], ‘If he wishes he could justify [himself] like this etc.’”
[From the above] we find that the emotions [of <i>Arich Anpin</i>] vest within the innerness of <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i>, and that <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i> are “worn” on the outside [like a garment].
This is as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">24</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 8:14.</i> “I am <i>Binah</i>, <i>Gevurah</i>” of <i>Arich Anpin</i>, “is mine,” as explained in <i>Etz Chayim</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">25</sup><i class="footnote">See Etz Chayim, (<i>Shaar Abba V’Imma</i>) Shaar 14, Ch. 2.</i> This will suffice for those of understanding.
Now, as the levels descend further, the intellectual [<i>Sefirot</i>] of <i>Chochmah</i> and <i>Binah</i> of <i>Atzilut</i>, only receive from the aspects of <i>Netzach</i> and <i>Hod</i> of <i>Arich Anpin</i>.
That is, [these <i>Sefirot</i>] bring the influence of <i>Chessed</i> and <i>Gevurah</i> down.
Similarly, in various places [the <i>Sefirot</i> of] <i>Netzach</i> and <i>Hod</i> are called<sup class="footnote-marker">26</sup><i class="footnote">See Introduction of Tikkunei Zohar 17a; Also see Shaarei Orah of Rabbi Yosef Gikatilla, translated as Gates of Light, Shaar 3 &amp; 4.</i> “the Righteous Scales,” even in reference to the lower emotions that go according to the light of the intellect.
However, the emotions of the desire, which is called “<i>Arich Anpin</i> – the <b>Long</b> Countenance,” are unlimited, like the desire itself, which is unlimited.
Therefore, even the aspects of <i>Netzach</i> and <i>Hod</i> are in an unlimited aspect.
This is as known regarding the explanation of the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">27</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 145:7</i> “The remembrance of Your abounding goodness,” that it refers to the aspect of <i>Yesod</i> of <i>Arich Anpin</i>.
This is likewise the case in the verses, “In Your great goodness”<sup class="footnote-marker">28</sup><i class="footnote">See the liturgy of the Morning prayers.</i> and “If he will redeem you, good”<sup class="footnote-marker">29</sup><i class="footnote">Ruth 3:13</i> and “Great goodness for the house of Israel,”<sup class="footnote-marker">30</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 63:16</i> and the like.
In contrast, the aspect of <i>Yesod</i> of “<i>Zeir Anpin</i> – the Small Countenance” is the aspect of the emotions that are born of <i>Binah</i> – Comprehension.
They are in an aspect of great immaturity.
This is in accordance with what is explained elsewhere regarding the matter of,<sup class="footnote-marker">31</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 92:13</i> “The righteous [shall flourish] like the palm tree,” [that this] refers to the aspect of <i>Yesod</i> of <i>Zeir Anpin</i>.
[In contrast, the continuation of the verse is,] “He shall grow like a cedar in Lebanon,” which refers to the aspect of <i>Yesod</i> of <i>Atik Yomin</i> and <i>Arich Anpin</i>, [which is in an infinite aspect.]
Similarly, it states regarding King Solomon,<sup class="footnote-marker">32</sup><i class="footnote">Kings I 5:13</i> “He spoke [of trees,] from the cedar that is in Lebanon even unto the hyssop [that springs out of the wall].” [The hyssop] refers to the aspect of the smallness of <i>Yesod</i> of <i>Zeir Anpin</i>, as it is in <i>Malchut</i>, which is called<sup class="footnote-marker">33</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar I 228b and Zohar II 133a.</i> “a wall.”
(As is known in the [Kabbalistic] intentions of [the prayer], “Amen, May His Great Name be blessed,” that “His Name” (<i>Shmo-</i>שמו-346) has the same numerical value as “Desire” (<i>Ratzon</i>-רצון-346). [Moreover,] “His Great Name” refers to the aspect of <i>Yesod</i> and <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Arich Anpin</i>, in that they should be “drawn down” into <i>Abba, Imma</i>, <i>Zeir Anpin,</i> and <i>Nukvah,</i> so that the “right” overpowers the “left.” This is like [the statement,] “In Your great goodness, let your fierce anger turn away from Your people etc.” This will suffice for those of understanding.)

Chapter 26

We must now understand the further descent of the light [as it is] within the ten <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i> (Insight and Comprehension) themselves.
[That is, we must understand] how the inner aspect of the brains of <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i> (Insight and Comprehension) receive [influence] from <i>Chessed</i> and <i>Gevurah</i> of <i>Arich Anpin</i> (Kindness and Sternness of Desire).
Moreover, [we must] certainly [understand] as they ascend to receive from the <i>Mazalot</i> of <i>Arich Anpin</i>, as mentioned previously.
[Finally, we must understand] the external aspect of <i>NeHi”Y</i><sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Netzach, Hod</i> and <i>Yesod</i>.</i> of <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i> (the gut emotions of Insight and Comprehension) which vest within the “brains” of <i>Zeir Anpin</i> (Intellect of the Emotions), as stated in <i>Etz Chayim</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">See Etz Chayim (<i>Shaar Drushei HaNekudot</i>) Shaar 8 Ch. 2; Shaar 16 (<i>Holadat Av”A V’Zu”N</i>) Ch. 7.</i>
Now, the [explanation of this] matter is known, that the inner aspects of the brains of <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i> are likened to <i>Shabbat</i> and <i>Yom Tov</i>.
This is because <i>Shabbat,</i> which is referred to as,<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">See Exodus 31:14, 15. See Zohar III 95a; Also see Pri Etz Chayim (<i>Shaar Mikra Kodesh</i>) Shaar 20, Ch. 1.</i> “<i>Kodesh</i> – Holy,” is [observed] through the pleasure of “<i>Chochmah</i> which is a thing unto itself.”
This is the aspect of the inner light of <i>Abba-</i>Insight (which is the innerness of <i>Atik Yomin</i> (Pleasure). This is the reason for the statement,<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 58:13</i> “And you shall <b>call</b> the <i>Shabbat</i> pleasure,” as explained elsewhere<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">See Siddur Im Divrei Elokim Chayim<i>,</i> Seder Seudah Shelishit, pg. 204c.</i> at length, regarding the matter of the three meals of <i>Shabbat</i>.)
<i>Yom Tov,</i> however, is refered to as,<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">Exodus 12:16; Leviticus 23:4</i> “<i>Mikra Kodesh</i> – It is called Holy,” [which is] an aspect of joy, as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 113:9</i> “The mother of the children rejoices.”
[The “mother”] refers to the aspect of the brains of <i>Imma</i> [Comprehension] which receives from <i>Abba</i> [Insight], because the cessation [from work] of <i>Shabbat</i> is also within <i>Chochmah</i>.
That is to say, it is the inner aspect of <i>Abba</i>, which is the aspect of the “<i>Koach Mah –</i> The Potential Power of What (כח מה).”
[This is] the “[intangible] nothingness” of <i>Chochmah</i>, before it spreads forth to become a “[tangible] something” within the comprehension of <i>Binah</i>.
Similarly, <i>Binah,</i> in its inner aspect, is the depth of the comprehension (<i>Omek HaMoosag</i>), for, as known, there is the “nothingness” (<i>Ayin</i>) of <i>Chochmah</i> in <i>Binah</i>, and there is [the somethingness (<i>Yesh</i>) of] <i>Binah</i> in <i>Chochmah</i>.
This is the meaning of [the statement],<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote">Sefer Yetzirah 1:4</i> “Be understanding in wisdom and wise in understanding,” which [refers to] the aspect of the inner unification of <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i>.
This is not the case, however, with the external flow of the influence of <i>Chochmah</i> and <i>Binah</i>, that is, their <i>ChaGa”T</i> and <i>NeHi”Y</i> etc., such as the emotional [<i>sefirot</i>] of <i>Chochmah</i>, which are called the aspect of the six directions of <i>Abba</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote">The six directions of Abba (<i>Vav Kitzvin D’Abba</i>) refer to the three emotions, <i>Chesed, Gevurah</i> and <i>Tiferet</i> and the three gut emotions, <i>Netzach</i>, <i>Hod</i> and <i>Yesod</i>, of Insight<i>-Chochmah.</i></i>
For example [this is] the [quality of] <i>Chessed</i> of <i>Chochmah</i> (Kindness of Insight)<i>,</i> which is the intellectual power that leans towards kindness, or the different intellectual power [of <i>Gevurah</i> of <i>Chochmah</i>] that leans towards judgment.
These [in turn] radiate within <i>Chessed</i> and <i>Gevurah</i> of <i>Binah</i> (Kindness and Sternness of Comprehension).
That is, it comes into comprehension, with sound reasoning and explanation, either for merit or liability.
These are called the emotions of the comprehended intellect, before they are born as actual [heartfelt emotions] in and of themselves (as will be explained).
Now, when a person cannot find a reason in a [way of] comprehendible explanation [for his position], but is, nonetheless, incapable of conceding to the opposite [position] because of his intellectual leanings, this is an aspect of <i>Chessed</i> and <i>Gevurah</i> of <i>Abba</i> (Kindness and Sternness of Insight), [as it is] before it radiates from the “nothingness” [of <i>Chochmah-</i>Insight] into the “somethingness” of <i>Binah</i>–Comprehension. (An example of this is the matter of [the Talmudic<sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Beitza 6a</i> incident in which] “Rav kept silent etc.”)
([However, the statements,<sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote">Mishnah Avot 3:13</i>] “Silence is a protective fence for wisdom” or<sup class="footnote-marker">12</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Megillah 18a</i> “[If speech is worth one <i>Selah</i><sup class="footnote-marker">13</sup><i class="footnote">A <i>Selah</i> was an ancient monetary currency used during Talmudic times.</i>, then] silence is worth two,” refer to the sublimation of the “<i>Koach Mah</i> – The Potential Power of What” of <i>Chochmah</i>, which ascends to the source from which all wisdom comes, and brings out new insights from there. This [source] is called “<i>Chochmah Stima’ah</i> – The Hidden Wisdom,” as previously explained.)
Now, the aspect of <i>NeHi”Y</i> of <i>Chochmah</i> (The gut emotions of Insight) is the aspect of the “scales” of intellect and insight, as to how this intellectual matter should come to be expressed. This is the aspect of “the kidneys that give counsel.”
(This is the matter of the strength of the intellect, which is called, “Strong Mindedness.”
Just as the legs have the strength to uphold the entire body, so too, the aspects of <i>Netzach</i> and <i>Hod</i> of <i>Abba</i> uphold the “body” of the mind.
The reverse is true if he is not strong minded. He will easily fall [and retreat] from his logical reasoning, [and change his stance] from [judging something as being] liable to [being] meritorious, or from being impure to being pure etc.
The same principle applies to <i>Netzach</i> and <i>Hod</i> of <i>Imma</i>.)
In general, the brains of <i>Zeir Anpin,</i> which are [heartfelt] emotions that are below intellect (as will be explained), come about from the enclothement of the aspect of the <i>NeHi”Y</i> of <i>Abba</i> into the <i>NeHi”Y</i> of <i>Imma</i>.
Now, the particular matters of the unifications of <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i> are well known.
[This refers to] whether [their unification] is in their inner aspect, for their own purpose, which is the [unification] of their first three [<i>Sefirot</i>] before they spread forth into the emotional [<i>Sefirot</i>], or whether they unify to bring about new “brains” for <i>Zeir Anpin</i> and <i>Nukvah</i>, which is only [the external unification of] <i>NeHi”Y</i>.
The [difference between these two unifications] is the [same as the] difference between <i>Shabbat</i> and the weekdays.
(In the <i>Shema</i> recital, the [inner] intention of [the words] “<i>HaShem</i> our God-<i>Hashem Elohei”nu-</i>יהו״ה אלהינ״ו” is the inner [unification] of <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i> (Insight and Comprehension), from which [it follows that] “<i>Hashem</i> is One-<i>HaShem Echad</i>-יהו״ה אחד,” [which refers to] the unification of <i>Zeir Anpin</i> and <i>Nukvah</i> (Emotions and Speech [or actions]) as they receive an aspect of additional influence of new intellect, so that they may be able to give birth etc.
This is [brought about] by giving ourselves over to <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, with complete self-sacrifice during the <i>Shema</i> recital. In contrast, when [one studies] Torah and [performs] the commandments without self-sacrifice, then <i>Zeir Anpin</i> and <i>Nukvah</i> (Emotions and Speech [or Action]) only [receive] from an external unification of <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i> (Insight and Comprehension), as explained elsewhere.
An example [of the inner unification] is the matter of the ten martyrs who brought about an ascent of the “Feminine Waters-<i>Mayim Nukvin</i>” to the inner aspect of <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma,</i> specifically through giving their [actual] lives over to <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, with complete self-sacrifice.)
(This [also] is the matter of the unification of the “upper <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i>,” and the unification of the “lower <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i>,” which are <i>Yisroel Saba</i> and <i>Tvunah</i>, as was explained at length in regard to the matter of <i>Binah</i> and <i>Tvunah</i>.
The aspect of <i>Yisroel Saba</i> is the six directions of <i>Abba</i>,<sup class="footnote-marker">14</sup><i class="footnote">This refers to the three emotions (<i>Chessed, Gevurah, Tiferet</i>) and the three gut emotions (<i>Netzach, Hod, Yesod</i>) of the insight-<i>Chochmah.</i></i> and <i>Tvunah</i> is the six directions of <i>Imma</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">15</sup><i class="footnote">This refers to the three emotions (<i>Chessed, Gevurah, Tiferet</i>) and the three gut emotions (<i>Netzach, Hod, Yesod</i>) of the comprehension-<i>Binah.</i></i>
These [two] are called “The lower <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i>.”
[However], there is another <i>Yisroel Saba</i> that is even higher than the “upper <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i>.”
This is the six directions of the “Hidden <i>Chochmah</i>” of <i>Arich Anpin</i> and [the higher] <i>Tvunah</i> is the six directions of <i>Binah</i> of <i>Arich Anpin</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">16</sup><i class="footnote">See HaGahot Tzemach to Etz Chayim, (<i>Drush Igullim V’Yosher</i>) Shaar 1, Anaf 5.</i>
The source for the inner unification of the “upper <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i>,” involving their first three [<i>Sefirot,</i> as explained above], is drawn from the [unification of the higher <i>Yisroel Saba</i> and <i>Tvunah</i> of <i>Arich Anpin</i>].)
Now, when intellect is drawn down from <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i> to <i>Zeir Anpin</i> and <i>Nukvah</i> in order to give birth to souls, it then is necessary for the unification of <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i> to be in the inner intellect, in their root within the two <i>Mazalot</i> of <i>Arich Anpin</i>.
(This then, is the meaning of [the statement],<sup class="footnote-marker">17</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Mo’ed Katan 28a</i> “Children, [health, and livelihood] are dependent upon <i>Mazal</i>”).
This is as explained elsewhere, that this is the [inner] meaning of [the prayer,<sup class="footnote-marker">18</sup><i class="footnote">See beginning of <i>Amidah</i> prayer. Also see Pri Etz Chayim (<i>Shaar Ha’Amidah</i>), Shaar 9, Ch. 3.</i> “The Supernal God, who bestows good kindnesses, the Possessor of all, who remembers the kindnesses of the forefathers and brings a redeemer to their children’s children etc.”] The “Supernal God-<i>El Elyon</i>-א״ל עליון” refers to the ascent of the inner light of <i>Abba</i> (Insight) as it receives from the <i>Mazal</i> of “<i>Notzer</i>.”<sup class="footnote-marker">19</sup><i class="footnote"><i>HaShem</i>’s-יהו״ה title God-<i>E”l-</i>א״ל is a title that relates to <i>Chochmah.</i> Therefore “The Supernal God-<i>E”l Elyon-</i>א״ל עליון” refers to the inner light of <i>Chochmah</i>-Insight as it ascends to receive from the <i>Mazal</i> of <i>Notzer</i> of <i>Arich</i>-Desire.</i>
Then, [the result of this is that] “He bestows good kindnesses” through the aspect of <i>Yesod</i>, which is called “The Possessor of all,”<sup class="footnote-marker">20</sup><i class="footnote">As will be explained later (in chapter thirty-six), <i>Yesod</i> is also called “<i>Kol</i>-All-כל,” since everything (i.e. all the preceding lights) gather in <i>Yesod</i> in order to spread forth as influence to the recipient.</i> to give birth to offspring through [the resulting unification of] <i>Zeir Anpin</i> and <i>Nukvah</i>.
This then, is the meaning of [the continuation of the words of the prayer], “He remembers the kindnesses of the forefathers and brings a redeemer to their children’s children.”
The analogy for this is well known. It is similar a person who is particularly outstanding in his [deep] insight [and wisdom]. Since he knows the concept to its depth, specifically to the very source of its inception, he is therefore capable of [bringing out] influence from it to someone who is of a much lesser [intellectual capacity than himself], even to a small child.
[This is to say that] he can make new combinations [to explain] how to conceptualize this concept, specifically not merely [explaining it] as it [already] is [in his own mind].
Furthermore, he is capable of formulating and giving rise to entirely new and different concepts, through this concept.
However, such is not the case in regard to a person who is not so exceptionally wise and who grasps the concept and wisdom merely as it is.
It is [difficult] enough for him to make the “breakthrough” and grasp it himself.
However, he will be incapable of “giving birth” to new insights from it altogether.
Certainly, he will be incapable of lowering it and “bringing down” the explanation of the concept, so that [even] a child could understand it.
[From all the above] we find that the aspect of <i>NeHi”Y</i> of <i>Chochmah</i> (the gut emotions of Insight), which is the aspect of <i>Yesod</i>, that is, the power to influence a recipient, is specifically dependent on the potential power to conceptualize (<i>Ko’ach HaMaskeel</i>), which is the source from which all concepts are “hewn” from “nothing” to “something.”
This is likewise so in regard to the birth of souls from the aspect of <i>NeHi”Y</i>.
[The aspect of <i>NeHi”Y</i>] cannot give birth [to new souls] unless there is additional [influence of] strength in the source of its intellect, from a much higher level than intellect.
This is the reason that for there to be a birth of souls through the unification of <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i>, there must be [influence] from higher than the source of the intellect of <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i>.
This is the aspect of the <i>Mazalot</i> of the “Hidden Wisdom” (<i>Chochmah Steema’a</i>) which is even higher than <i>Chochmah</i> and <i>Binah</i> of <i>Arich Anpin</i> itself, as previously explained.
This is also the reason for the inner unification of <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i> during the night of the “Holy <i>Shabbat</i> (<i>Shabbat Kodesh</i>).”
This is because [this unification] is to give birth to souls.
This is, therefore, specifically the time for the “marital relations of the Sages.”<sup class="footnote-marker">21</sup><i class="footnote">See Introduction to Zohar 14a; Also see Zohar II 136a &amp; 204b, and elsewhere.</i>
This is because they are Torah Scholars who are called “<i>Kodesh</i> – Holy” and the source of <i>Shabbat</i> is in the “upper <i>Kodesh</i> –Holiness,” which is the inner aspect of the light of <i>Abba</i>, as previously explained. This will suffice for those of understanding.

Chapter 27

Now, after having explained somewhat in a manner of particulars, about the matter of the lights of <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i> and their internal and external unifications, as previously explained, we must now explain the specifics of the matter of the lights of <i>Zeir Anpin</i>, which are called <i>Yisroel</i> and <i>Yaakov</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">See Etz Chayim, (<i>Shaar HaKelipot</i>) Shaar 48, Ch. 2 &amp; 3.</i>
[Moreover, we must explain] all the particulars of the unifications of <i>Zeir Anpin</i>, which are [either] called a union of <i>Yisroel</i> and <i>Leah</i> or a union of <i>Yaakov</i> and <i>Rachel</i> etc., as known.
However, we must first have an introductory understanding regarding the matter of Lights and Vessels (<i>Orot V’Keilim</i>), both generally and particularly.
Now, the explanation of the statement,<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">See Introduction to Tikkunei Zohar 3b</i> [“He and His life force are one, He and His organs are one”], is known. [That is,] “He and His life force are one” refers to the lights (<i>Orot</i>), while “He and His organs are one” refers to the aspect of the vessels (<i>Keilim</i>).
Now, both generally and particularly speaking, the aspect of the lights of the ten <i>sefirot</i> is called,<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">Sefer Yetzirah 1:2 – “<i>Eser Sefirot Blimah</i>”</i> “Ten <i>sefirot</i> without what (<i>Bli Mah</i>),” that is, without “whatness.”
This is as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">See Introduction to <i>Tikkunei Zohar</i> 17b.</i> “He is not of any of these qualities at all.”
It is solely because of the aspect of the vessels that they are in an aspect of a tangible existence.
This is the [meaning of the] statement,<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">See Introduction to Tikkunei Zohar 17a and 17b.</i> “He brought forth ten vessels which we call ten <i>Sefirot</i>… to show… and to conduct the worlds with them etc.”
Likewise, the fact that, in general, the ten <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Atzilut</i> are called by four names,<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">The Divine names may be expanded by spelling out their individual letters as follows; <i>Alef</i>-אל"ף, <i>Beit</i>-בי"ת, <i>Gimmel</i>-גימ"ל etc. The letters <i>Hey</i>-ה and <i>Vav</i>-ו each have three possible spellings: ה"י, ה"א, ה"ה, and וי"ו, וא"ו, ו"ו. The Name <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה may therefore be expanded into several possible spellings depending on the variant spellings of the letters <i>Hey</i>-ה and <i>Vav</i>-ו.</i> <i>A”V-</i>ע״ב-72<i>, Sa”G</i>-ס״ג-63<i>, Ma”H-</i>מ״ה-45 and <i>Ba”N</i>-ב״ן-52, [is only in regard to the aspect of the vessels].
[The name] <i>A”V-</i>ע״ב-72<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">See <i>Etz Chayim</i> (<i>Shaar RaPa”Ch Nitzotzin</i>) <i>Shaar</i> 18, Chapter 2.</i> is an expansion [of the Name <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה] with <i>Yod’s</i>, and refers to <i>Chochmah</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote">That is, יו"ד ה"י וי"ו ה"י, expanded with <i>Yod’s</i>-י. This is the name of 72-A"V-ע"ב which is its numerical value. This name refers to <i>Chochmah</i>.</i>
[The name] <i>Sa”G-</i>ס״ג-63<sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar III (<i>Ra’ayah Mehemnah</i>) 246b; See also Etz Chayim (<i>Shaar Ozen Chotem Peh</i>) Shaar 4, Ch. 3; Shaar HaKlallim, Ch. 8.</i> is [an expansion] with <i>Yod’s</i> and an <i>Aleph</i>, and refers to <i>Binah</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote">That is, יו"ד ה"י וא"ו ה"י, expanded with <i>Yods-</i>י and an <i>Aleph-</i>א in the <i>Vav</i>-וא״ו. This is the name of 63-<i>SA"G</i>-ס"ג which is its numerical value. This name refers to <i>Binah</i>.</i>
[The name] <i>Ma”H-</i>מ״ה-45<sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote">See Etz Chayim (<i>Shaar Leah V’Rachel</i>) Shaar 38, Ch. 1 and 2.</i> is [an expansion] with <i>Aleph’s-</i>א and refers to <i>Zeir Anpin</i>,<sup class="footnote-marker">12</sup><i class="footnote">That is, יו"ד ה"א וא"ו ה"א, expanded with <i>Aleph’s</i>-א. This is the name of 45-<i>M"AH</i>-מ"ה which is its numerical value. This name corresponds to the emotive <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Zeir Anpin</i>.</i> [and the name] <i>Ba”N-</i>ב״ן-52<sup class="footnote-marker">13</sup><i class="footnote">See Etz Chayim (<i>Shaar RaPa”Ch Nitzotzin</i>) Shaar 18, Ch. 3.</i> is [an expansion] with <i>Heh’s-</i>ה, and refers to <i>Malchut</i>, as known.<sup class="footnote-marker">14</sup><i class="footnote">That is, יו"ד ה"ה ו"ו ה"ה, expanded with <i>Heh’s-</i>ה. This is the name of 52-<i>B"AN</i>-ב"ן which is its numerical value. This name corresponds to <i>Malchut</i> (i.e., <i>Nukvah</i>).</i>
As known, in the terminology of the <i>Zohar,</i> the ten general <i>Sefirot</i> are only called,<sup class="footnote-marker">15</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar II 67b, and the commentaries there.</i> “The secret of the Holy Name.”
All this is specifically only in regard to the aspect of the vessels (<i>Keilim</i>), as known.
Now, the explanation of the matter is known, that in regard to the statement,<sup class="footnote-marker">16</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar II 153a, and Zohar I 138a; Also see Zohar Chadash<i>, Ruth</i> 80a.</i> “There are three rulers above, the brain, the heart and the liver,” these are the three vessels for the <i>Nefesh, Ruach,</i> and <i>Neshamah</i>.
The <i>Neshamah</i> [vests] within the brain, the <i>Ruach</i> [vests] within the heart, and the <i>Nefesh</i> [vests] within the liver.
However, the aspects of the <i>Chayah</i> and <i>Yechidah</i> [of the soul] transcend the limitations of vessels.
Now, the aspect of the vessels (<i>Keilim</i>) is composed of a beginning, middle and end. [This is to say that] there is the inner [part] of the vessels, the middle [part] of the vessels, and the external [part] of the vessels.
[This is in accordance to] what is known regarding the matter of the “248 limbs of the King” which are the nine <i>Sefirot</i> of <i>Zeir Anpin</i>.
[That is,] nine times nine equals eighty-one.
Then, three times eighty-one, corresponding to the three levels in the vessels – the beginning, middle, and end – equals two-hundred and forty-three.
[Now, with the addition of] the five Kindnesses (<i>Chassadim</i>) which spawn growth, it equals two-hundred and forty-eight.
This is the general matter of the vessels of <i>Zeir Anpin</i>, which are called “The body of the King.”
In addition [to the “organs”], “He prepared garments for them, from which souls for human beings’ issue forth.”<sup class="footnote-marker">17</sup><i class="footnote">See Introduction to Tikkunei Zohar 17a</i>
[These “garments”] are the garments of thought, [speech and action], as will all be explained.
However, [regarding] the general explanation of the matter of lights and vessels, although there are many very different ways [to explain it], it may, nonetheless, generally [be understood as follows]: It is like the spiritual light and vitality (<i>Ohr V’Chayoot</i>) of the spiritual [power of] sight, as it vests and integrates in [a way of] physicality, in the physical substance of the eye, [thus creating] the aspect of physical sight.
Now, two aspects are [involved] in this: The first is a change of existence, from spiritual to physical.
[This is to say that] physical sight grasps physicality, which is not the case with the spiritual light of [the power of] sight.
This is similarly the case with the light of the spiritual potential power of intelligence, which integrates with the physicality of the vessel of the brain, to the point that it is called, <i>Hitchachmoot –</i> “Active Intellect.”
Likewise, [there is a change of existence] from the [spiritual] potential power to move, as it [vests] within actual physical movement.
So too, [there is a change of existence] from the spiritual potential power of growth, as it becomes integrated and vested in the actual physical growth of physical vegetation.
The second [aspect] is the matter of the limitation and measure of the substance of the vessel. [This is to say that] it is limited and quantified with [specific] measure.
An example [of this is that] physical sight [is only clear] up to sixty miles.
Similarly, [both] the matter of active [physical] intellect or physical movements, spread forth specifically with constraints and limitations, until their limited strength expires.
For example, the strength of the physical comprehension of the vessel of the brain diminishes and expires due to the limited capacity of the vessel.
Similarly, the physical power of movement of the strength of the arm will diminish and expire due to [strenuous] activity, or when lifting a heavy load and the like.
This is because of the limitation of the [physical] power to move.
(This is not the case with the essential spiritual potential power of movement, which has no limitation or cessation.
This is evidenced by [the fact that] in a sudden panic, a person may lift something which [under normal circumstances] is much heavier than his ability [to lift]. This comes from the aspect of the encompassing [lights of the soul], as known.)
Now, this is [the general principle] in every matter of “Substance and Form” (<i>Chomer</i> V’<i>Tzurah</i>).<sup class="footnote-marker">18</sup><i class="footnote">Substance (<i>Chomer</i>) and Form (<i>Tzurah</i>) is another way of saying Vessel (<i>Keli</i>) and Light (<i>Ohr</i>).</i>
]This is to say[ that aside from the fact that the “substance” (<i>Chomer</i>) comes in [a way of] a change of existence, it also limits the “form” (<i>Tzurah</i>).
Nonetheless, the “substance” has a similarity and likeness to the “form,” such as the “substance” of the vessel of the eye [which is specifically suited] for sight, or the “substance” of the vessel of the brain [which is specifically suited] for thought, and the like.
However, the “substance” is made from the thickening and condensation<sup class="footnote-marker">19</sup><i class="footnote">The three-letter root of the word <i>Hagshamah-</i>הגשמה is <i>Geshem-</i>גשם which means condensation or materialization. Because of this the Hebrew word for rain is <i>Geshem-</i>גשם<i>.</i></i> of the spiritual “form,” from its lowest level.
For example, the power of physical growth comes about from the last level of the spiritual [power] of growth.
Similarly, the last level of the spiritual life force of the soul becomes vested within the [physical] blood, as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">20</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 12:23</i> “For, the blood is the soul.”
Likewise, the last level of the light of the spiritual intellect, integrates with the “substance” of the vessel of the brain and the last level of the condensation of the spiritual [power] of sight, integrates with the “substance” of the vessel of the eye.
Because of this [phenomenon] we observe that the growth of the [physical] “substance,” always comes simultaneous to the growth of the [spiritual] “form,” literally as one.
For example, the developmental growth of the “substance” of the [physical] body is simultaneous to the developmental growth of the spiritual light and vitality of the “form,” such as [the fact that] the developmental growth and ability of the “substance” of the [physical] brain comes in proportion to the development of the light and form of the [spiritual] intellect, so that when a child matures and the light of his intellect develops spiritually, automatically, the ability of the vessel of his brain develops [as well].
This is as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">21</sup><i class="footnote">Job 32:7</i> “Days speak and many years teach wisdom.”
That is to say, the vessel becomes developed in proportion to the light, each and every day until the age of seventy, at which point a person reaches intellectual maturity, as known. This will suffice for those of understanding.

Chapter 28

Now, the analogue from all of the above analogies regarding the aspects of the three vessels of the brain, the heart and the liver, can be understood generally, as follows:
The light of <i>Chochmah</i> of [the world of] <i>Atzilut</i>, as it is emanated from the Essential Light of the Emanator, is comparable to the light of the spiritual intellect itself, as it is drawn from the essential potential <i>Chochmah</i> power of the aspect of the essence of the soul.
It still is literally one with the source from whence it was hewn.
[This is] is similar to<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">Sefer Yetzirah 1:7</i> “The flame [that is bound to the coal],” or like the aforementioned revelation of the desire from the essential [hidden] desire of the aspect of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>.
Now, although this is merely like an indicator or a color, (as explained before at the end of chapter nineteen regarding the matter of “He calls out the generations from the beginning,” that this refers to the ten <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Atzilut</i> which came out of the concealment of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>, which is the revelation of the [general] desire in a separate thing,) nonetheless, they are called the “Ten <i>Sefirot</i> without whatness,”<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">Sefer Yetzirah 1:2 – “<i>Eser Sefirot Blimah</i>”</i> because they still are intangible.
This is because a color is also essential, since it is impossible to have an opposite color to the essence of a thing.
[An example of this is when] the color of [the inside of] an apple is white, which indicates its essential sweetness.
Likewise, although it is [coming forth] into a separate matter, nonetheless, the light of an intellect or desire that leans towards kindness, indicates the essence.
Therefore, [it is understood that] the existence of the lights of the ten <i>sefirot</i> [of <i>Atzilut</i>] comes from the aspect of the essential letters of the Emanator, [that is, <i>Adam Kadmon</i>].
An example of this is the name <i>A”V-</i>ע״ב-72 [יו״ד ה״י וי״ו ה״י] from which the aspect of the Light of <i>Chochmah</i> of <i>Atzilut</i> comes into revelation.
This name indicates the essential <i>Chochmah</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>.
Likewise, the name <i>Sa”G-</i>ס״ג-63 [יו״ד ה״י וא״ו ה״י] indicates the essential light of <i>Binah</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>.
This is [true of all the names] <i>A”v-</i>ע״ב-72<i>, Sa”G-</i>ס״ג-63<i>,</i> [<i>Ma”H-</i>מ״ה-45 and <i>Ba”N-</i>ב״ן-52] that <b>precede</b> the ten <i>Sefirot</i> of [the world of] Emanation-<i>Atzilut</i>. They are [therefore] called, “The names of the Emanator.”
This is similar to how the last aspect of the spiritual Form (<i>Tzurah</i>) becomes bound to the beginning of the existence of the light and form within the substance of the vessel (<i>Keli</i>).
This is in accordance to what was previously explained regarding the,<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">Leviticus 17:14</i> “blood which is the soul,” and [regarding] the spiritual power of growth, and [regarding] the eye and the brain etc.
However, the aspect of the Vessel (<i>Keli</i>) that limits the light of <i>Chochmah</i> of <i>Atzilut</i> is like the light of the intellect as it already is merged within the substance of the brain.
[In this case] the substance of the brain only receives from the “thickening” of the end of the light of the intellect.
Therefore, aside from the fact that there is a [profound] change of existence, it also limits [the light].
This is similar to the light of <i>Chochmah</i> as it vests within the brain, which is [then] called “<i>Chochmah Mocha</i> – Insight is the Brain.”<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar III (<i>Ra’ayah Mehemnah</i>) 235b; Introduction to Tikkunei Zohar 17a</i>
It is then that because of the aspect of the vessel of <i>Chochmah,</i> it comes into the aspect of a tangible existence of intellect, which is called, “The conceptualization of a certain specific concept.”
The same [principle applies] to the spiritual emotions in the “Heart” and the spiritual <i>Nefesh</i> in the “Liver.”
This then, is the matter of the “Three rulers above.” These are the three general vessels for the <i>Nefesh, Ruach</i> and <i>Neshamah</i> of <i>Zeir Anpin</i> of [the world of] Emanation-<i>Atzilut</i>.
The <i>Neshamah</i>, which is the aspect of the intellectual <i>Sefirot</i> of <i>Chochmah</i> and <i>Binah</i> of <i>Zeir Anpin</i>, [vests] within the “Brain,” the <i>Ruach</i> [vests] within the “Heart,” [and the <i>Nefesh</i> vests within the “Liver”].
These [vessels] are the “letters” of the Lights of <i>Atzilut</i>, which [refers to] the matter of the four names, <i>A”v-</i>ע״ב-72<i>, Sa”G-</i>ס״ג-63<i>,</i> [<i>Ma”H-</i>מ״ה-45 and <i>Ba”N-</i>ב״ן-52] of <i>Atzilut</i>.
These [four names] are called the vessels for the [light of the] ten <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Atzilut</i>, which limit the light and restrain it, because the vessels are made from the “thickening” of the lights, as stated in <i>Etz Chayim</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">See Etz Chayim<i>,</i> (<i>Shaar Ha’Akoodim</i>) Shaar 6, Ch. 3.</i>
As known, this is called, “The somethingness of the Light,” as it appears in an aspect of a “something,” with tangible existence. This will suffice for those of understanding.
(We find that there are two types of names of <i>A”v-</i>ע״ב-72<i>, Sa”G-</i>ס״ג-63<i>,</i> [<i>Ma”H-</i>מ״ה-45 and <i>Ba”N-</i>ב״ן-52] etc.
The first [set of names] is before [the world of] <i>Atzilut</i> [within <i>Adam Kadmon</i>]. The second [set of names], which are the vessels that limit, is after [the world of] <i>Atzilut</i>.
According to this, when a person directs his attention to the [external] names, his [actual] intention is [<b>really</b>] to the source of the lights.
For example, a person who directs his attention to the aspect of the name <i>A”V-</i>ע״ב-72 [יו״ד ה״י וי״ו ה״י]<i>,</i> the source of the light of <i>Chochmah</i> etc., automatically is [also] directing his attention to the vessel of <i>Chochmah</i>, causing it to be drawn down. This will suffice for those of understanding.
These are the [Kabbalistic] <i>Kavanot</i> (devotions or intentions) of the Names [of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה] during the eighteen blessings of the <i>Amidah</i> prayer.
This is because, the source of the [external] limiting vessels [which are the names of <i>Atzilut</i>] is from the names of <i>Atzmoot HaMa’atzeel</i>-The Essential Self of the Emanator, and the two [levels] are interdependent, as will be explained. This will suffice for those of understanding.)
This, then, is the meaning of the statement,<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">Introduction to Tikkunei Zohar 17a</i> “[He made ten <i>Tikkunim</i> (fixings)] which we call ten <i>Sefirot</i>… to show… to conduct [the worlds] etc.,” because <i>Tikkunim</i> (Fixings) is the aspect of vessels (<i>Keilim</i>) for the Lights (<i>Orot</i>) of [the world of] <i>Atzilut</i>.
By way of analogy: a “fixing” for the eye, so that its physical sight may spread further, [may be accomplished] through the means of eyeglasses.
Likewise, the physical organ of the eye is the “fixing” through which the spiritual [power of] sight spreads forth, as explained elsewhere.
[It is] therefore [understood] that all aspects of the spreading forth of influence down, can only come about specifically through the vessels which limit.
For example, it is through the vessel of the brain, which grasps the intellectual concept, that [the concept may be] drawn down to arouse emotions in the heart or to be expressed to another person.
Similarly, it is through the means of the heart, which is the vessel for the spiritual light of love and kindness, that [this light] can come into the category of being influenced to a recipient.
It is [specifically] because of this that the [vessels] are called <i>Tikkunim</i> – Fixings, [because they “fix” the light] so that it can be drawn down from [the world of] <i>Atzilut</i> to [the world of] <i>Briyah</i>.
In other words, it’s [sole purpose is] only “to show” etc.
On the other hand, from the aspect of the Essential Light of the Emanator, [the sefirot] are called “Ten <i>sefirot</i> without whatness,”<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">Sefer Yetzirah 1:2 – “<i>Eser Sefirot Blimah</i>”</i> as explained before and as explained elsewhere at length.

Chapter 29

Now, [it must be understood], even in the <i>Hitbonenut</i> – contemplation of the Lights and Vessels (<i>Orot V’Keilim</i>) of [the world of] <i>Atzilut,</i> in a more particular manner, that the primary intent is only [to understand] the matter of “He and His life force are one, [and He] and His organs are one,” that in truth, there is no difference between “He and His life force are one” and “He and His organs are one.”
This is because even though the Lights are “<i>Bli Mah</i> – without whatness,” [that is, they are intangible], while the Vessels are in an aspect of “<i>Yesh -</i> somethingness” [and are therefore tangible], nevertheless, from the angle of the Essential Self of the Emanator, He actually made the root for the existence of the Vessels before making the root for the existence of the Lights.
The fact that the Vessel comes about from the “thickening” of the Light [poses no contradiction to this], since the root and source [of the vessels] preceded this.
This [source] is called the “Simple [Primal] Matter – <i>Chomer Pashoot</i>” or “The <i>Heyulie</i> Matter” which precedes the “Form – <i>Tzoorah</i>” [of the Lights].
The explanation of this matter is known, and may be understood through the well know preface regarding the matter of vessels which actually limit. That is, there are two kinds of limitations (<i>G’vool</i>):
The first is the essential potential power to limit.
Examples of this are the vessels of the brain which limits or the eye which limits, and the like.
However, this is still only in potential rather than in actuality.
For example, in the hand there is the potential power to limit every physical movement, [even] before it actually limits any [specific] movement.
Now, although the actual revealed limitation is, literally, exactly like the spiritual potential power to limit of the hand, which is the root and source for the actual limitation, nevertheless, there is no comparison between the potential power to limit and the actual limitation [itself].
Firstly, one is spiritual and essential, whereas the other is physical and separate from the essence.
Secondly, the potential power to limit is not actual limitation.
Rather, [the person] limits his strength according to his will and choice, and it is [therefore] not a limitation of necessity, that is to say, [it is not] that he does not have the power to spread forth further.
Rather, he does not desire to spread forth further.
[Therefore], this is only [that which] <b>makes</b> limitations, while [it itself] is not truly limited. [In other words, it is not] like an actualized limitation, which is truly limited.
(This is in accordance with what is explained elsewhere regarding the matter of the innerness of the vessels and the externality of the vessels, as will be explained with the help of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He.)
[Through this] it may likewise be understood [regarding how it is] in the upper realms, in the root and source of the vessels which limit the light.
That is, [we may understand] the source and root of their power to limit, which is drawn from the same Singular Preexistent Intrinsic and Essential Self of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, from which the lights themselves are drawn.
For example, the source of the existence of the light of a desire is from the concealed essential source of all desires.
Now, the potential power to limit is also drawn from there, which limits the power to spread the light of the desire forth, so as not to spread forth further [than desired].
This is so that the “reasoning for the desire” could come about.
This is because if the power and light of the desire would not cease, the “reasoning for the desire” could never come about.
This is controlled by the <i>Kav HaMidah</i>-The Measuring Line, which makes all the actual limitations of the lights.
In the same manner, it makes all the actual limitations of the vessels of the ten <i>Sefirot</i> which limit, and dictates how they will actually limit.
However, their root and source, is not the aspect of true limitation, but rather, it determines the type of limitation.
(This comes from the <i>Kav HaMidah</i> – The Measuring Line, from the aspect of <i>Gevurah</i> of <i>Ohr Ein Sof-</i> Sternness of the Light of the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He.
This is the power to gather in, which is similar to the power to spread out, since they are two lines of equal balance.
This is because [being that <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, is] “All Capable” (<i>Kol Yachol</i>) [He therefore] also has the power to limit (as explained elsewhere).<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">See Avodat HaKodesh<i>,</i> Section 1, Ch. 8. Also see Derech Emunah (by the same author, Rabbi Meir Ibn Gabai), Ch. 2.</i>
It was explained above<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">See Chapter 13.</i> that this is the aspect of the <i>Reshimu</i> – Impression, which is the source of the limitations of the vessels of the ten <i>Sefirot</i> of [the world] of <i>Atzilut</i>.
The aspect of the <i>Kav</i> – Line, which is drawn from the <i>Reshimu</i> – Impression, is the source of all the Lights, as explained elsewhere at length.)
Therefore, although the aspect of the Vessels of [the world of] <i>Atzilut</i> actually limit through the aspect of the [four] names <i>A”v-</i>ע״ב-72<i>, Sa”G-</i>ס״ג-63<i>,</i> [<i>Ma”H-</i>מ״ה-45 and <i>Ba”N-</i>ב״ן-52], which are called “Letters,” however, this is only due to the potential power to make limitations within the Essential Self of the Emanator [Himself].
This then, is the meaning of “He and His organs are one.” That is, [the Vessels] come about from the power of the <i>Ein Sof -</i> The Singular Preexistent Essential and Unlimited Being of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה Himself, blessed is He, in the same way that, “He and His life force are one,” in regard to the aspect of the Lights.
(However, in truth, even the aspect of the vessels of the ten <i>Sefirot</i> of [the world of] <i>Atzilut</i> are potential limitation (<i>Koach HaGvool</i>), rather than actual limitation (<i>Gvool B’Po’el</i>).
It is only when the light and influence is limited to [create] “something” from “nothing” in [the worlds of] <i>Briyah, Yetzirah</i> and <i>Asiyah</i>, that they can be considered to be actual limitation (<i>Gvool B’Po’el Mamash</i>), as will be explained with the help of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He.)
According to the above, when a person focuses his intention on the names of <i>A”V-</i>ע״ב-72<i>, Sa”G-</i>ס״ג-63 etc., which are in an aspect of vessels that actually limit, this itself [constitutes] focusing his intention upon the source of the names of <i>A”V-</i>ע״ב-72<i>, Sa”G-</i>ס״ג-63 etc., which are the source of the Light of [the world of] <i>Atzilut</i>.
(This is the Essential Name of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה – <i>Shem Ha’Etzem</i>, which indicates the Essential Self of the Source, as previously explained.)<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">See at length in Ginat Egoz of Rabbi Yosef Gikatilla, translated as HaShem Is One, Vol. 1, The Gate of Intrinsic Being (<i>Shaar HaHavayah</i>) and on.</i>
In other words, [his intention] is [focused] on the source of the existence of the Vessels, [about which it states] “He and His organs are one,” as explained above.
From this it is self-understood that the statement, “He and His organs are one,” also applies to the above mentioned “Fixings-<i>Tikkunim.</i>”
This is because the actual limitation (<i>Gvool B’Po’el</i>) is unified with the potential power to limit (<i>Koach HaGvool</i>), which brings about this actual limitation.
[This may be understood] by way of analogy, from the potential power to limit of the hand, which is unified and bound to the actual limitation of the movement, as mentioned above.
(This is most certainly true of the Vessels of the Brain, Heart [and Liver], which cannot yet be considered to be actual limitation (<i>Gvool B’Po’el</i>), as explained above.
Rather, they limit and describe the Lights, only so that they may become recognizable as a tangible existence.
Nonetheless, the [Vessels] are rooted in the Essential Self of the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, just as the Lights are rooted in His Essential Self.
These [two powers] are equally balanced, and literally have a single source, this [source being] the aspect of <i>Ein Sof -</i> The Singular Preexistent Essential and Unlimited Being of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה Himself, literally.
This is because just as the Limitless Light of the Unlimited One spreads down [without limit], so too it [exists above] without end.
These [two powers, that is, the limitless ability to reveal and the limitless ability to restrain revelation] are <i>Chessed</i> and <i>Gevurah</i> of <i>Atzmoot –</i> Kindness and Sternness of the Essential Self of the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He.
However, regarding the Lights and Vessels [as they are] in their source, it is the reverse of [how they are] in their revealed aspect.
This is because as they are revealed, the aspect of restraint - <i>Tzimtzum</i> is in the Lights, and the kindnesses of spreading forth, is in the Vessels.
This is because even though the [Vessels] limit [the Lights, nonetheless,] all spreading down [of influence] comes about specifically through them.
However, in their source, the opposite is true.
The restraint-<i>Tzimtzum</i> is in the <i>Reshimu-</i>Impression, which makes potential limitation, while the spreading forth of kindnesses-<i>Chassadim</i> is in the lights, which comes about from the aspect of the <i>Kav-</i>Line. This is explained elsewhere, and will suffice for those of understanding.

Chapter 30

From the above we may understand the statement,<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">Introduction to Tikkunei Zohar 17b</i> “If You would withdraw from them, all [the names] would remain as a body without a soul.”
This refers to the aspect of the vessels of the Brain, the Heart and [the Liver], which [by themselves] are called “A body without the soul.”
[The soul] refers to the aspect of the Lights of the <i>Nefesh, Ruach</i> and <i>Neshamah</i> etc.
However, after having previously stated that the Vessels (<i>Keilim</i>) come from the thickening of the Lights (<i>Orot</i>), how then is it possible for there to be a Vessel (<i>Keli</i>) without Light (<i>Ohr</i>)?
Rather, according to what was stated above, that the source of the Vessels (<i>Keilim</i>) preceded the source of the Lights (<i>Orot</i>), therefore the Vessels have their own existence, independent [of the lights]. Regarding this it states, “He and His organs are one.”
(Accordingly, a person who directs his intentions to the name <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה<i>,</i> such as during the eighteen benedictions of the <i>Amidah</i> prayer, should direct his intention to the source of the vessel, which is the main aspect of The Name, since “He and His organs are one.”
This automatically brings about that the Light (<i>Ohr</i>) is drawn to the Vessel (<i>Keli</i>), since,<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Kiddushin 2b</i> “It is the nature of a man to [pursue the woman].” This will suffice for those of understanding.)
Now, there are three levels in the vessels; the inner, the intermediate and the outer.
The [explanation of this] matter is known, that corresponding to the nine <i>Sefirot</i>, <i>ChaBa”D, ChaGa”T</i> and <i>NeHi”Y</i>, there are three kinds of vessels.
The innerness of the Vessels is the aspect of the restriction of the light of <i>ChaBa”D</i> of the Light (<i>Ohr</i>).
The intermediary aspect of the Vessels is the restriction of the <i>ChaGa”T</i> of the Light, and the externality of the vessels is the limitation of the <i>NeHi”Y</i> of the Light.
This is the meaning of [the verse],<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 32:7</i> “You conceal – <i>Atah Seter</i> (אתה סתר).” [The word <i>Seter</i> – Conceal (סתר)] is a backwards spelling of [the acronym] <i>Rosh –</i> Beginning (<b>ר</b>אש), <i>Toch</i> – Middle (<b>ת</b>וך), and <i>Sof –</i> End (<b>ס</b>וף),<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">See Emek HaMelech<i>,</i> Shaar 12<i>,</i> Ch. 4.</i> because the main restriction and concealment [of the Light] is in the externality of the vessels.
Furthermore, in regard to the matter that the aspect of influence and the lowering of [that] influence to the recipients [comes about] specifically through Vessels (<i>Keilim</i>), there also are three levels.
The innerness of the vessels is the aspect of the bringing [down] the Light of the influence of <i>ChaBa”D</i>.
The Middle [aspect] is the bringing [down] and drawing forth of the Light of <i>ChaGa”T</i>, and the Externality is the bringing [down] of the influence of <i>NeHi”Y</i>.
By way of analogy, [this is like] the nine <i>Sefirot</i> of the Light of the quality of <i>Chessed</i> – Kindness, as it is limited within three kinds of “letters.”
The letters of Thought (<i>Machshavah</i>) are the aspect of the inner vessel for the <i>ChaBa”D</i> of <i>Chessed</i> – Kindness.
The letters of Speech (<i>Deeboor</i>) are the intermediary vessel for <i>ChaGa”T</i> of <i>Chessed</i> – Kindness, and the letters of the Action (<i>Ma’aseh</i>) are [the outer vessel for] the aspect of <i>NeHi”Y</i> of the Light of <i>Chessed</i> – Kindness.
[In other words, this outer vessel] is the power to actualize the kindness, to do it in actual deed.
This [actualization of the kindness] has a vessel specific to it. Likewise, the love of the kindness has a vessel specific to it, and the intellect and reasoning of the kindness has a vessel specific to it.
In most cases, the intellect and reasoning of the kindness are entertained in one’s Thought (<i>Machshavah</i>), the love [of the kindness] is said in Speech (<i>Deeboor</i>) and the power to actualize [the kindness] is actualized in Deed (<i>Ma’aseh</i>).
(However, when [the Light of <i>Chessed</i> – Kindness] comes [to <b>actually</b> be expressed] in the three types of Letters (<i>Otiot</i>) of Thought, Speech and Action, they are [only] called “Garments – <i>Levooshin</i>.”
This is lower than the aspect of the vessels about which it states “He and His <b>organs</b> are one,” which is not the case with the Garments - <i>Levooshin</i>.
Rather, [this statement] refers to the Vessels (<i>Keilim</i>) for the <i>Nefesh, Ruach</i> and <i>Neshamah</i>, which are the Brain, the Heart [and the Liver].
Now, in the [vessel of the] Heart there are [also] three levels; inner, middle and outer, corresponding to the nine <i>Sefirot</i>.
There is the aspect of <i>ChaBa”D</i> of the emotional qualities of love or fear, which is called the “Intellect of the Emotions” (<i>Mooskal Shel HaMeedot</i>).
This is in the right ventricle of the heart, within which light radiates from the brain of <i>Chochmah</i>, which rules over the heart.
The <i>ChaGa”T</i> of the love and fear is called the “Feeling” (<i>Moorgash</i>).
This is the aspect of the intermediary vessel of the heart, which is the Spirit of Life (<i>Ruach HaChayim</i>) that beats in the left ventricle.
This is drawn from the brain of <i>Binah</i>, which is called “<i>Ruach</i>.”
This is the aspect of the vessel of the felt vitality of the emotions, when they become aroused.
The externality of the heart is the “Breath of the Chest” (<i>Havel HaChazeh</i>), which is the vessel for the natural [reactions] of the emotions.
This corresponds to the aspect of <i>Nefesh</i>, that is, the aspect of <i>NeHi”Y</i> of the [heartfelt] emotions.
It is this [level] which radiates into the <i>Nefesh</i> that is “in the blood,” which, generally, is a vehicle for the <i>Ruach</i> of the heart.
Likewise, the aspect of the <i>Nefesh</i> in the Liver includes three levels; inner, middle and outer etc.
The <i>Zohar</i> calls the inner [level], “The Impression of Life – <i>Keesta D’Chayoota</i>.”
This refers to the aspect of the impression (<i>Reshimoo</i>) that remains of the aspect of the <i>Ruach</i> during sleep.
This is the aspect of the intellect of <i>ChaBa”D</i> in their immature state (<i>Katnoot</i>), [as they are] in the <i>Nefesh</i>.
The middle [aspect of the <i>Nefesh</i> in the Liver] is the arousal of the physical life force of the power of movement and feeling, which is in the blood, “which is the <i>Nefesh</i>,” such as the pulse of the hand.
The outer [aspect of the <i>Nefesh</i>] is the aspect of <i>NeHi”Y</i> of the Liver, which sends the external life force to all the limbs.
Now, the inner [aspects may become] separated, as explained elsewhere at length.
[This is to say] that during the time of exile, which is called “sleep,” the radiance of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Atzilut</i> [which is] the aspect of the soul of the worlds of <i>BY”A,</i> is only in an aspect of an “Impression of Life – <i>Keesta D’Chayoota</i>.”
[It is only] an <b>impression</b>-<i>Reshimoo</i> of the aspect of <i>Ruach</i> of the Heart of the “Upper Man-<i>Adam HaElyon</i>.”
[This is because] during the exile the Assembly of Israel<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">The “Assembly of Israel” (<i>Knesset Yisroel</i>) refers to the aspect of the General Godly Soul of the Jewish People, where all the Jewish souls converge as one, and is another name for the aspect of the Divine Presence (<i>Shechinah</i>). (See Shaarei Orah of Rabbi Yosef Gikatilla, Gate 1 – <i>Malchut.</i>)</i> is compared to a fetus.
In other words, they are similar a fetus, whose head is folded between its knees, “three inside of three.”
[This is to say] that the Brains of <i>ChaBa”D</i> are concealed within <i>ChaGa”T,</i> and <i>ChaGat</i> is [concealed] within <i>NeHi”Y</i>, as stated elsewhere.)
Now, regarding the matter of the Commandments (<i>Mitzvot</i>), which are called the two-hundred and forty-eight organs of the King, as known, three times nine times nine – corresponding to the three levels of beginning, middle and end of the vessels – equals two-hundred and forty-three, as previously mentioned.
[Now], with the inclusion of the five kindnesses which bring about growth, they are two-hundred and forty-eight.
The aspect of <i>ChaBa”D</i> is the light of the devotional intent in the [performance of the] commandment (<i>Mitzvah</i>).
There is a specific inner vessel for this, [with a specific restriction and] limitation.
The aspect of <i>ChaGa”T</i>, is the love, awe and nullification, for which there is an intermediary vessel etc.
The aspect of <i>NeHi”Y</i> is the aspect of the power to actualize, [that is] only to do the will of the King, for which there is an external vessel.
(Generally, these are called Intent – <i>Kavanah</i>, Blessing – <i>Brachah</i>, and Action – <i>Ma’aseh</i> or Unification – <i>Yichud</i>, Blessing – <i>Brachah</i>, and Holiness – <i>Kedushah,</i> which are called [by the acronym] <i>YaBo”K-</i>יב״ק.<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">Which has a numerical value of <i>HaShem Elohi”m</i>-יהו״ה אלהי״ם-112. (See at greater length in Ginat Egoz of Rabbi Yosef Gikatilla, translated as HaShem Is One, Vol. 1, The Gate of Intrinsic Being (<i>Shaar HaHavayah</i>).</i>
As is explained elsewhere at length, these are [also represented by] the matter of the Flesh (<i>Basar</i>), Veins (<i>Geedin</i>) and Bones (<i>Atzamot</i>) of every limb.)
Now, the Five Kindnesses that bring about growth (<i>Heh Chassadim HaMagdeelim</i>) are the aspect of the general drawing down and revelation of the Godly Light through [the fulfillment of] each [particular] commandment.<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">In Etz Chayim (<i>Shaar Pirke HaTzelem</i>, Ch. 6) it states that the five kindnesses (<i>Heh Chassadim</i>) is the aspect of the influence of the last <i>Heh-</i>ה of the name <i>Sa”G-</i>ס״ג-63 of <i>Binah,</i> which is the aspect of <i>Tvunah</i>, which was previously explained.</i>
This is by way of the drawing down of the <i>Kav</i> – Line, which draws from the Source of all kindnesses, for “He waters the tree,” similar to the statement, “You fill all the names” etc.
(Now, according to this, the statement, “They would remain as a body [without a soul” becomes understood]. This is because even the aspect of the “Body-<i>Goofa</i>,” with the aforementioned three vessels, requires the radiance of the Limitless Light of the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, within the <i>Kav</i>, which “fills all the names.”
This is because there is an independent source for the existence of the Vessels (<i>Keilim</i>), as previously explained.
However, if this is the case, then why is this statement made dependent upon something which [at first glance] is not the essence of the matter, which is the statement “they will remain like a body without a soul.”
However, since the essential matter of the vessels is that they correspond to the nine <i>Sefirot</i> of the <i>Nefesh, Ruach</i> and <i>Neshamah</i>, and it is because of the increase of the light that there is growth in the vessels, in order for the light of the influence to be brought down, [therefore,] “If You would withdraw [from them, they would remain as a body without a soul”].
[In other words], the vessel would remain like a body without a soul; that is, it could not spread forth, whatsoever. This will suffice for those of understanding.)

Chapter 31

Now, there is a great advantage of the aspect of the Vessels (<i>Keilim</i>), over and above the aspect of the Lights (<i>Orot</i>). This is because there is a greater aspect of inter-inclusion in the vessels than in the lights. This is the main aspect of <i>Tikkun</i> – Rectification.
For, as known, the main aspect of <i>Tikkun</i> – Rectification comes about because of the abundance of vessels.<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">See Etz Chayim (<i>Shaar HaTikkun</i>) Shaar 10, Ch. 5, and Shaar 12, Ch. 4.</i>
[Moreover,] it is specifically by means of the external aspect of the vessel, which is the aspect of <i>NeHi”Y</i>.
This is evidenced by the fact that we find that in some circumstances, the light of <i>Chessed</i> – Kindness may radiate within a vessel of <i>Gevurah</i> – Judgment, or that a light of <i>Gevurah</i> – Judgment [may radiate] within a vessel of <i>Chessed</i> – Kindness.
If this is so, that the light may be exchanged to radiate within its opposite vessel, if it is because of [the light] itself, then why can it not become inter-included and bound with a light that is its opposite and opposes it?
For example, the light of the quality of <i>Chessed</i> – Kindness will not tolerate the light of the quality of Judgment (<i>Din</i>), whatsoever.
Rather, we must say, that this [inter-inclusion] is because of the aspect of the vessel (<i>Keli</i>), which has the ability to tolerate an opposite light that opposes it.
This is because it is specifically in the vessels that the aspect and matter of the inter-inclusion of a thing with its opposite [is possible]. This is not the case [in regard to] the Lights (<i>Orot</i>).
[Similarly,] in man, the main aspect of rectification is from the angle of his body.
As we clearly observe with our senses in regard to the nature of man’s organs, that each organ contains an inter-inclusion of its fellow [organs],<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">See Siddur Im Divrei Elokim Chayim, Shaar Nefilat Apayim 91c; Also see Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Kuntreisim<i>,</i> pg. 407.</i> to the point that it is possible to rectify a lacking [in one organ] through healing a different organ.
For example, for a problem in the sight of the eye, healing may be applied to the power of the nerves in the foot, since they include within themselves [something of] the nerves of the eye.
However, in the case of old age and the like, [in which] the light and vitality of the brain becomes weakened to the point that [one’s] sight becomes weakened, one cannot heal [this] through strengthening the power and light of the vitality of the <b>emotions</b> of the heart, even though the heart and brain are inter-included with one another.
It is only through strengthening the <b>vessel</b> of the heart that the vessel of the brain may become strengthened, so that the power of the intellect will radiate to a greater degree, and he will [thereby] have better vision.
This is because there is not as much of a connection and inter-inclusion between the light of the intellect and the light of the emotions, as there is between the vessel of the heart and the vessel of the brain.
This is likewise the case in regard to the vessel of the eye, with the vessel of the nose and the vessel of the ear, and the like.
It is for this reason that it is specifically from the angle of the aspect of the Vessel (<i>Keli</i>) that it is possible for its opposite light to radiate within it. This will suffice for those of understanding.
This may be further understood from our observation that the emotions of <i>Chessed</i> – Kindness and <i>Gevurah</i> – Judgment are opposites which literally oppose each other.
Nonetheless, when these emotions come into a vessel, such as actual thought, speech and action, it is possible for the light of <i>Chessed</i> – Kindness to radiate in a thought, speech and action, that is its opposite.
[This is so] since it is possible to think, speak and do the opposite of what is in his heart.
Similarly, [a person] can become angry in his heart against someone who he loves in his heart, or he may have mercy in his heart towards someone who he despises etc.
This is because the heart is prepared to become a receptacle for that which is its opposite, since there is a greater inter-inclusion of one thing and its opposite in the vessels, [rather] than the lights.
(The fact that in jubilation there is trembling and in wrath there is mercy, or the opposite, that in trembling there is jubilation and in mercy there is wrath, is all specifically due to the vessels.)
We similarly find this [matter] in the six days of creation. The first day is the aspect of the <i>Chessed</i> – Kindness of “Let there be light,”<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 1:3</i> while the second day is the aspect of the <i>Gevurah</i> – Judgment of “Let there be a firmament,”<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 1:6</i> as it states in the <i>Zohar,</i><sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar I 205a, and Zohar III 94b.</i> “Each day has its function.”
Nevertheless, in each day there is specifically an inter-inclusion of the other days, as known.
This is because it is specifically when the light comes into the vessel that is called “day-<i>Yom</i>-יום,” that an inter-inclusion of one thing with its opposite [occurs].
This is because, when the matter comes to be influenced in actuality, it is impossible that kindness will not have the aspect of judgment inter-included in it, or that judgment [will not have] the aspect of kindness [inter-included in it].
This is not the case, however, when the light and influence [remains] without a vessel, as of yet.
An example of this is a <i>Halachic</i> legal ruling that is specifically for [the purpose of] practical application.
Of necessity, there will be an inter-inclusion of kindness within the judgment or of judgment within the kindness.
However, this is not the case if the ruling is not [necessarily] for practical application.
[From all the above] we find that the primary aspect of inter-inclusion is in the aspect of the externality of the vessels, which relate to action. This will suffice for those of understanding.
However, at first glance, there seems to be a contradiction to all this.
This is because, in reality, the fact that the light is capable of radiating within its opposite vessel is because of the nullification of the vessel to the light.
This comes about by means of the aspect of the inner name of <i>Ma”H-</i>מ״ה-45 [יו״ד ה״א וא״ו ה״א],<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">See introduction to Tikkunei Zohar 17a</i> which is the source of the aspect of the inter-inclusions in the lights, specifically from the radiance of the <i>Kav</i> – Line.
It is specifically for this reason that the inter-inclusion is in the innerness of the vessels, (An example of this is the devotional intent in the performance of the <i>Mitzvot-</i>commandments, which includes two opposites. This is similar to the [matter of the] <i>Atzamot V,Geedin</i> –Bones and Tendons etc. This is not the case, [however], in the actual action.) rather than in the externality.
This is because, [as known,<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">See Midrash Bereshit Rabba 50:2 and elsewhere.</i>] one angel cannot perform two opposite missions.
This is because all sending forth of influence comes about specifically from the externality of the vessels, which brings out the influence.
This is similar to the external vessels of the “letters,” and the like.
