It is for this reason that “The face of the Lion is to the right etc.,”<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote">Ezekiel 1:10</i> and they [are incapable of] changing their function, nor can they join together to exchange missions with each other.
Because of this [the <i>Zohar</i> states,] “Each day specifically has <b>its own</b> function.”
However, the [explanation of the] matter is that because the inner aspect of the vessels receives from the aspect of the inner lights which become limited within the vessel, [therefore,] when there is an inter-inclusion in the lights, there is an automatic inter-inclusion in the innerness of the vessels. This is similar to the arousal and comprehension of [the angels] Michael and Gabriel etc.
[However,] the externality of the vessels [receive] from the aspect of, “The Potential Power to Limit-<i>Koach HaGvool</i>,” which is in an aspect of an encompassing [light].
There can therefore be two opposites as one within them, which is the aspect of the inter-inclusion of one thing with its opposite, specifically.
This is similar to all miracles, which specifically take place in the aspect of the externality of the vessels, which is the [performance of the miracle] in actuality.
For example, every place in which a miracle happens is a place that [simultaneously] withstands a thing and its opposite. [This is to say that, at once, it includes] that which is above nature within nature.
An example of this is the transformation of the sea to dry land, and similarly, [the fact that] the place of the Holy Ark was not according to [natural] measurable dimensions, as explained elsewhere.<sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Yoma 21b</i>
Likewise, it is [specifically] from there that the source of divisions comes, to separate each [thing] unto itself.
This comes about due to of the aspect of the <i>Kav HaMidah –</i> The Measuring Line in the Encompassing [Light], since it is the source of the vessels that limit.
For this reason, the primary aspect of rectification-<i>Tikkun</i> is specifically the aspect of the abundance of subdivisions.
It is specifically because of the [subdivisions] that there can be an abundance of inter-inclusions of one thing with its opposite as one.
This is likewise the primary aspect of the “Man of Rectification” (<i>Adam D’Tikkun</i>), about whom it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 139:5</i> “<i>Achor V’Kedem Tzartanee</i> – You have formed me back and front,” [which refers] specifically to formation (<i>Yetzirah</i>) in a body of substance (<i>Goof Chomer</i>).
<i>Kedem</i> – Front, refers to the aspect of the simple substance (<i>Chomer Pashoot</i>) that preceded the form (<i>Tzoorah</i>), which is the light.
This is in the source of the vessels that preceded the light.
<i>Achor</i> – Back, refers to the aspect of the vessel of substance that follows [the investment of] the Light and Form etc. This will suffice for those of understanding. This is in accordance with the explanation of this matter elsewhere at length, (and should suffice for those of understanding.)

Chapter 32

We now must understand the aspect of “the Upper Man” of [the world of] <i>Atzilut,</i> who is “upon the throne etc.”<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">Ezekiel 1:26</i>
This is the aspect of <i>Zeir Anpin</i><sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">See Etz Chayim (<i>Shaar RaPa”Ch Nitzotzin</i>) Shaar 18, Ch. 5; Also see Etz Chayim<i>,</i> Shaar 42, Ch. 1.</i> of <i>Atzilut</i> which receives from the aspect of <i>NeHi”Y</i> of <i>Chochmah</i> and <i>Binah</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">See Etz Chayim (<i>Shaar Drooshey HaNekudot</i>) Shaar 8, Ch. 2.</i>
As known, this is the matter and aspect of the Emotions (<i>Midot</i>) of [the world of] <i>Atzilut</i>, which is the primary [source] and root of the influence for the “source of the source” of the vitality of the worlds.
[Nonetheless,] it [itself] is still the end of the world of the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, since “He and His life force and organs are one,”<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">See introduction to Tikkunei Zohar 3b</i> as previously explained.
Therefore, even up to the aspect of the vessels of <i>Zeir Anpin</i>, in the aspect of the externality of the <i>NeHi”Y</i> of [<i>Zeir Anpin</i>], is still considered to be of the end of the world of the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He.
Now, the explanation of these matters [may be understood in a manner] of “From my flesh I shall behold God,”<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">Job 19:26</i> because “Man was made in the image of God,”<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 9:6</i> as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 1:26</i> “[Let us make man] in our form and in our likeness.”
Now, we observe in the human soul, that its aspects of <i>Chayah</i> and <i>Yechidah</i> are the aspects of the encompassing [lights, relative] to the <i>Nefesh, Ruach</i> and <i>Neshamah</i>, and transcend the limitation of lights within vessels.
This is the aspect of the simple essential desire and pleasure, which is in the aspect of the <i>Yechidah</i> [level of the soul], plus the aspect of the innerness and source of the intellect, which is called <i>Maskil</i>, and is the aspect of the encompassing [light] of the <i>Chayah</i> [level of the soul].
They do not become limited within the vessels at all.
It is only from <i>Chochmah</i> down [that the light] is drawn into a vessel.
This is the aspect of the <i>Neshamah</i> which is within the brain, the <i>Ruach</i> within the heart etc.<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote">…and the <i>Nefesh</i> in the Liver, as previously explained.</i>
However, the light of the encompassing desire and pleasure nevertheless radiates from its concealment, from the inner aspect of the light of <i>Chochmah</i>, within the <i>Nefesh, Ruach</i> and <i>Neshamah</i>, which are within the three vessels of the Brain, the Heart [and the Liver].
This is the revelation of the desire that comes into the revealed intellect and reasoning in the aspect of the brain of <i>Chochmah</i>, which is called the Light of <i>Abba</i> [<i>Chochmah</i>].
From there it is drawn down and spreads forth into <i>Binah</i>, which is comprehension.
From the comprehension (<i>Binah</i>) of the brain, the emotional arousal in the heart is drawn down.
This is to say that the thirty-two chambers of the brain, which are called the “thirty-two pathways of <i>Binah</i>,” open up to become the intellect of <i>Zeir Anpin</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar III (<i>Idra Rabba</i>) 128b, 129a &amp; 136a</i>
This is because the Intellect (<i>Mochin</i>) divides into four, that is, <i>Chochmah, Binah, Chessed</i> and <i>Gevurah</i>.
Each one of these [four] has eight chambers within it, thus totaling thirty-two.
It is for this reason that [the heart] is called <i>Lev –</i> Heart (לב), because its source is in the thirty-two pathways (ל"ב שבילין), which are the thirty-two chambers.<sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote">See Etz Chayim, Shaar 31, Ch. 4.</i>
It is through them that <i>Da’at,</i> which includes <i>Chessed</i> and <i>Gevurah</i>, causes the light of the intellect of <i>Chochmah</i> and <i>Binah</i> to lean [and] be aroused [either] towards <i>Chessed</i> or <i>Gevurah</i>, that is, towards merit or judgment.
These are also called the emotions of the intellect, which are the seven lower [<i>sefirot</i>] of <i>Binah</i>, each of which includes seven. These are the fifty gates of <i>Binah</i>.
[However,] all this is one [related] matter, except that the fifty gates of <i>Binah</i> still are within the comprehension of <i>Binah</i>, such as the “Kindnesses that are concealed within <i>Yesod</i> of <i>Imma</i>.”<sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote">See Likkutei Torah, Bamidbar 6d.</i>
In other words, this is the aspect of the arousal of love, as it still is within intellect and comprehension. It thus is considered to be “concealed” and “hidden” within comprehension.
Afterwards, it comes out into revelation as an actual arousal of the quality of love within the heart, which is called <i>Zeir Anpin</i>.
In this fashion, the aforementioned thirty-two pathways come out in a revealed way to the heart from the concealed arousal of the brain, and it is for this reason that it is called “Heart-<i>Lev</i>-לב-32.”
This is in accordance with what is stated in <i>Etz Chayim</i>,<sup class="footnote-marker">12</sup><i class="footnote">See Etz Chayim, Shaar 31 (<i>Shaar Partzufei Zu”N</i>), Ch. 4; Also see Ma’amarei Admor Ha’Emtza’ee, Devarim, Vol. 3, pg. 994.</i> that the reason it is called “<i>Lev-</i>לב-32” is because the thirty-two lights of <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i> gather there. These are the thirty-two pathways.
(These are the thirty-two [times that it states in the Act of Creation] “And God said-<i>VaYomer Elohi”m</i>-ויאמר אלהי״ם,” which [refers to] <i>Binah</i>, as it receives from <i>Abba</i><sup class="footnote-marker">13</sup><i class="footnote">See Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee<i>,</i> Vayikra, Vol.2, pg. 625; Devarim<i>,</i> Vol. 2, pg. 651.</i>) as explained elsewhere at length.
Now, certainly, in order for there to be an arousal of an emotion in the heart from the concealed arousal of that emotion as it exists in the intellect and comprehension of <i>Binah</i>, there must first be an aspect of a <i>Tzimtzum,</i> concealment and gathering, which is called a withdrawal.
(This is analogous to a seed decaying so that there can be a transformation from one [state of] being to a different [state of] being, as known.<sup class="footnote-marker">14</sup><i class="footnote">See Tanya 113a; Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Vayikra Vol. 2, pg. 598.</i>)
This [<i>Tzimtzum –</i> lessening] is the aspect of the “Narrowness of the neck – <i>Meitzar HaGaron</i>” of <i>Binah</i>, in which the arousal of the intellect becomes concealed, and is drawn down as an arousal in the heart through a transformation of [its state of] being.
(This is similar to the aspect of the “Airy Membrane – <i>Krooma D’Avirah</i>” that conceals and separates between the upper power which transcends intellect, [and the intellect], so that it may be revealed as the light of the intellect through a transformation of [its state of] being.
It is also similar to the “Diaphragm – <i>Chatzer HaKaved</i>” which divides and separates between the respiratory system and the digestive system in order to bring about a transformation of [state of] being, as explained elsewhere at length.)
Nevertheless, the emotions of the heart are patterned after the emotions of the intellect, literally. They are literally according to how they were aroused in the brain, without any deviation whatsoever, even as much as the “thorn of the letter <i>Yod</i>,”<sup class="footnote-marker">15</sup><i class="footnote">This expression means “even the tiniest amount.” An equivalent English idiom would be, “Even to a hair’s breadth.”</i> as known.
The only exception is that in the heart they come about through a transformation of their [state of] being, according to the limitation and restraint of <i>Netzach</i> and <i>Hod</i> of <i>Binah</i>, which constitute the sending forth of the influence of the light of the essential comprehension, for the sole purpose of arousing the emotions, as known.
Now, included in the emotions of the heart are the three levels of <i>ChaBa”D, ChaGa”T</i> and <i>NeHi”Y</i>.
These are the “<i>Mooskal</i> – The Intellect [of the Emotions],” the “<i>Moorgash</i> – The Felt [arousal of the emotions]” and the “<i>Mootba</i> – The Natural [Response of the Emotions],” which were mentioned previously.
Each of these consists of three vessels; inner, middle, and external, as explained previously at length.
However, even the aspect of the externality of the vessels of <i>NeHi”Y</i> of the heart, which is the aspect of the arousal of the kindness and love of the heart, as it comes to be [expressed] as influence to the outside, which is called <i>NeHi”Y</i> of the chest [as it is expressed] within the Thought, Speech and Action, which comes [about] through the externality of the vessel of the heart, which is the aspect of the “<i>Mootba</i> – The Natural [response of the emotions]” of the breath of the chest of <i>Zeir Anpin</i> of [the world of] <i>Atzilut</i>, about which it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">16</sup><i class="footnote">See Introduction to <i>Tikkunei Zohar</i> 3b.</i> “He and His organs are one,” is [nonetheless] all still in an aspect of the limitless state of the Unlimited One (<i>Ein Sof</i>), <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He.
By way of analogy, this is similar to man below.
When the essential desire, which is in an aspect of the encompassing [light] of the aforementioned <i>Yechidah</i> [level of the soul], radiates and comes into revelation in the brains of <i>Chochmah</i> and <i>Binah</i>, to the point that it descends and constricts within the “smallness” of the brains of <i>Netzach</i> and <i>Hod</i> of <i>Chessed,</i> as it is felt in the heart, which is the breath of the chest, we find that even there, the [essential] desire radiates.
This is because, as we observe, the desire is even felt in the breath of the heart.
This is called, “<i>Re’oota D’Leeba</i> – The Desire of the Heart,”<sup class="footnote-marker">17</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar I 100a and elsewhere.</i> which is the fact that his heart lusts in a <b>felt</b> way for something good, and loathes that which is bad and despised, through the absence of desire [for it] in the heart.
This being the case, [we find that] there is an instantaneous unification and bond between the [original] source of the essential desire and the [external] breath of the heart, as if they are literally one entity.
Through this analogy we may understand the Upper Man, which is the aspect of <i>Zeir Anpin</i>.
Regarding the heart of <i>Zeir Anpin</i> it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">18</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 8:21</i> “And He said unto His heart,” causing it to lean toward Kindness.
Likewise, [a different verse states,]<sup class="footnote-marker">19</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 6:6</i> “And He saddened His heart,” [causing it to lean] toward Judgment, and the like.
We find that within the aspect of the externality of the vessels of <i>Netzach</i> and <i>Hod</i> of this heart, there is a radiance of the aspect of the simple essential desire of the Essential Self of the limitless Light of the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, Who precedes the first <i>Tzimtzum</i>.
([This aspect] was mentioned previously in chapter ten, in regard to the aspects of <i>Yachid</i> and <i>Echad</i> etc., through the analogy of the essential desire for kindness [as it exists] within the essence of the [human] soul etc.)
This being the case, even up to the aspect of the externality of the heart of <i>Zeir Anpin,</i> it still is completely considered to be the end of the World of the Unlimited One (<i>Olam HaEin Sof</i>), <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He.
This is because, “He and His organs are one” just as it is in a human being, whose heart is one with his essential desire. This will suffice for those of understanding.

Chapter 33

From all the above we understand the matter of a single <i>Hitbonenut</i>-contemplation of the many particulars that come together as one general [overarching principle] which includes them all.
This is similar to [the matter of] “Whatever <i>HaShem-</i>יהו״ה desires He has done in the heavens and the earth etc.”<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 135:6</i> The root of this “desire of <i>HaShem-</i>יהו״ה” is rooted in the first source (which is called <i>Yachid</i> – Singular etc).
This is the aspect of the essential <i>Heyulie</i> desire for kindness in the Essential Self of the limitless light of the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה Himself, blessed is He, who is [an] absolutely simple [singularity]. This [desire for kindness] is similar to the essentially good and kind nature embedded in the essence of the human soul (as explained above in chapter ten).
Once it arose in <i>HaShem</i>’s-יהו״ה will and desire to bestow goodness in a particular way from this general <i>heyulie</i> light, [this desire] descended with a great chaining down. [Nonetheless], all [this was] still within Himself [and was still] in the aspect of Limitlessness (<i>Ein Sof</i>), until this desire reached the aspects of <i>Netzach</i> and <i>Hod</i> of the externality of the vessel of the “Heart.”
In other words, [it reached] the external emotions (<i>Midot</i>) of <i>Malchut</i> of the Unlimited One (<i>Ein Sof</i>), even though, as it is there, [in <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Ein Sof</i>] it completely transcends the aspect of limitations of lights within vessels.
Rather, it all is literally in the aspect of the Unlimited One (<i>Ein Sof</i>), as “He estimated it within <b>Himself</b>.”<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">See Mikdash Melech to <i>Zohar</i> 16a</i>
Afterwards, there was a <i>Tzimtzum</i> [withdrawal] and it descended by means of the aspect of the Line (<i>Kav</i>) into the ten <i>sefirot</i> of Circles (<i>Igullim</i>) etc., until the aspect of <i>Keter</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>. [Now, <i>Keter</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>] is the source of the concealed desire (<i>Ratzon HaNe’elam)</i> which becomes revealed as the “desire for the desire” within <i>Keter</i> of <i>Atik Yomin</i> etc.
[This desire then continued to descend] until the aspects of the desire and pleasure within <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i>, and became limited within the [revealed] desire, intellect, and comprehension, which are the three upper <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Chochmah</i> and <i>Binah</i> etc.
[It then continued to descend] until the aspect of the seven lower <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Binah</i>.
[Then it continued] until the aspect of the “immature brains – <i>Katnoot HaMochin</i>” of <i>NeHi”Y</i> of <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i> [as they vest] within <i>Zeir Anpin</i>, as explained before.
From there it underwent further restraint (<i>Tzimtzum</i>) on the three levels of <i>ChaBa”D</i> and <i>ChaGa”T</i> of <i>Zeir Anpin</i> etc., until the aspect of the externality of the vessels of <i>Netzach</i> and <i>Hod</i> [of <i>Zeir Anpin</i>], which is the aspect of the “Breath of the Chest.”
There, [the descent of] the light of the simple desire, which was included in the concealed Essence of the <i>Heyulie</i> desire for kindness, concludes.
Moreover, this entire chaining down (<i>Hishtalshelut</i>), from the [essential] desire that arose hidden in the Essential Self of the Singular Preexistent Intrinsic and Unlimited Being of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, until it came to be felt in the breath of the heart, happened and was drawn down instantaneously, since “He and His life force and organs are one.”
This means that, “He” literally refers to the aspect of the Essential Self of the limitless light of the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה Himself, blessed is He, whereas “His life force” refers to [both] the concealed and revealed aspects of the ten <i>Sefirot</i>, [which are] “like a flame [that is bound to the coal] etc.”<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">Sefer Yetzirah 1:7</i>
[This continued] until the aspect of the ten <i>sefirot</i> of <i>Zeir Anpin</i>.
“And His organs” refers to the aspect of the vessels of <i>Zeir Anpin</i>.
“Are one” means that all this is still in the aspect of His Unlimited Being (<i>Ein Sof</i>).
This is because although the aspect of the vessels, which limit the external emotions of the heart of <i>Zeir Anpin</i>, are [in the aspect of] ultimate “smallness” compared to the exaltedness of the essential emotions of the aspect of <i>Malchut</i> of the Unlimited One – <i>Ein Sof</i>, they nevertheless are considered to be the aspect of the end of the beginning, as scripture states, “He calls out the generations from the beginning etc.”<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 41:4</i>
Their final conclusion is the aspect of the “immature” [or “tiny”] emotions of <i>Zeir Anpin</i>.
Because of this, <i>Zeir Anpin</i> is called “The Small Face,”<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">The literal translation of “<i>Zeir Anpin</i>” is “The Small Face.”</i> [since] it is similar to the small face of a little child compared to the “Large Face”<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">See Talmud Bavli, Chagigah 13b</i> of “an elder who has acquired wisdom.”<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">See Talmud Bavli, Kiddushin 32b</i>
The one is completely intellectually immature, whereas the other is completely mature.
Nonetheless, they are equally within the category of man, except that one is considered to be an “immature person,” while the other is considered to be a “mature person.” However, the form of how they are is the same.
This is because the emotions of a child are also according to intellect and concealed desire etc., except that it comes [revealed] with total immaturity.
[However] in a mature adult, his emotions are mature, according to the breadth of his intellect and his very lofty and exalted desire.
This is likewise the comparison between the immature emotions of <i>Zeir Anpin,</i> which are emotions that are limited according to the immature intellect of <i>Netzach</i> and <i>Hod</i>, compared to the aspect of <i>Arich Anpin</i>, which is called the “Large Face.”
[This is to say that <i>Arich Anpin</i> represents] the mature countenance and brains of “an elder who has acquired wisdom” from the source of the concealed wisdom [itself], which is higher than the “[Airy] Membrane (<i>Krooma D’Avira</i>).”
This is the aspect of the hidden intellect (<i>Sechel HaNe’elam</i>) which is in the concealed desire (<i>Ratzon HaNe’elam</i>) that is the root of the Emanated etc.
In the same way, even the aspect of the emotions of the concealed desire and intellect of <i>Arich Anpin</i> are in the aspect of immaturity compared to the aspect of the even greater “man,” That is, the aspect of <i>Adam Kadmon,</i> who is called “The Man of Creation.”
(As known, <i>Zeir Anpin</i> is called “The Man of Action,” <i>Arich Anpin</i> is called “The Man of Formation” and <i>Adam Kadmon</i> is called “The Man of Creation.”
In each of these there are ten <i>Sefirot</i> in a concealed and revealed [manner], as scripture states,<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 43:7</i> [“For My glory, I have created, formed, and even actualized”]. “For My glory” refers to <i>Malchut</i> of the Unlimited One (<i>Ein Sof</i>), “I have created” refers to <i>Adam Kadmon</i>, “formed” refers to <i>Atik Yomin</i> and <i>Arich Anpin</i>, and “actualized” refers to the aspect of <i>Zeir Anpin,</i> about whom it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 1:26</i> “Let us make man in our image [and in our likeness].”)
This is analogous to the formation of lines that are made small [representing] something [much] bigger, such as how a map is patterned after planet earth.
Nonetheless, this image contains everything in it.
Nothing is missing, not even the amount of “the thorn of the letter <i>Yod</i>,” except that it is a very tiny [scale model] in which the form of a tiny line may be a five hundred <i>Parsa</i> long river on planet earth, and the like.
Likewise, by way of analogy, are the immature emotions of an infant, compared to the emotions of an elder of seventy years.
This is similar to the ability [of an adult] to give birth to [offspring] who are like him etc.
(This is in accordance with what is explained elsewhere regarding the matter of “<i>Bootzin Bootzin</i> [<i>Mikeetphay Yediya</i>] – “Small pumpkins [are discernable when they burst forth from their sap] etc.”<sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote">See Talmud Bavli, Brachot 48a; Also see Siddur Im Divrei Elokim Chayim, Erev Shabbat, 164d; Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Kuntreisim pg. 207.</i>)
This is similarly the case in regard to the aspect of the emotions of the “Man” of [the world of] <i>Atzilut</i>. Even though they become [revealed] in a most diminished fashion (<i>Tzimtzum</i>) in comparison to the aspect of the emotions of <i>Adam Kadmon</i> and <i>Arich Anpin</i>, nonetheless, it all is one, except that it comes from the aspect of a most incredible length to a most incredible brevity.
(This is the meaning of [the verse],<sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 30:4</i> “What is his name, what is his son’s name-<i>Mah Shmo, Mah Shem Bno-</i>מה שמו מה שם בנו.” “What is his name-<i>Mah Shmo-</i>מה שמו” [refers to the aspect of] <i>Ma”H-</i>מ״ה-45 [יו״ד ה״א וא״ו ה״א] of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>, and “What is his son’s name-<i>Mah Shem Bno-</i>מ״ה שם בנו” is the aspect of <i>Zeir Anpin</i>, as explained in several places.)
This then, is the general <i>Hitbonenut</i>-contemplation [of the verse, “Whatever <i>HaShem-</i>יהו״ה desires He has done in the heavens and the earth etc.”] “Whatever <i>HaShem-</i>יהו״ה desires” in the Essential Self of the limitless light of the Unlimited One, blessed is He, literally, “He has done in the heavens-<i>Shamayim-</i>שמים,” which is the aspect of <i>Zeir Anpin</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">12</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar II 62b, and Zohar III (<i>Idra Zuta</i>) 288a.</i>
[The word “Heavens-<i>Shamayim</i>-שמים” is a composite of the two words] “Fire-<i>Aish-</i>אש” and “Water-<i>Mayim</i>-מים,”<sup class="footnote-marker">13</sup><i class="footnote">See Talmud Bavli, Chagigah 12a; Sefer Yetzirah 1:11-12, and the commentaries there; Also see Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Vayikra, Vol. 2, pg. 498; Devarim Vol. 4, pg. 1,392.</i> [that is,] <i>Chessed</i>-Kindness and <i>Gevurah</i>-Judgment of the immaturity of [the world of] <i>Atzilut</i>.
([This matter is true even down] to the aspect of the “Heavens-<i>Shamayim</i>-שמים” of [the world of] <i>Asiyah-</i>Action.)
This is because, “Their beginning is imbedded with their end,”<sup class="footnote-marker">14</sup><i class="footnote">Sefer Yetzirah 1:6 – “Their end is bound with their beginning and their beginning with their end.”</i> from the <i>Chochmah</i> at the “top” of <i>Adam Kadmon</i> [all the way] to the <i>Chochmah</i> at the end, in the emotions of <i>Zeir Anpin</i>.
(This [also is the meaning of] the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">15</sup><i class="footnote">Samuel I 25:32; Kings I 1:48, 8:15</i> “Blessed is <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, the God of Israel.” [This refers to <i>Yisroel</i>] <i>Sabba</i> which is the aspect of <i>Adam Kadmon,</i> about which it states, “I have created etc.”
Similarly, [the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">16</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 6:4</i>] “<i>Shema Yisroel-</i>Listen Israel etc.,” refers to the worlds of <i>Briyah, Yetzirah</i> and <i>Asiyah</i> in a general manner (<i>Klallut</i>).)
(More particularly, “Whatever <i>HaShem-</i>יהו״ה desires” in the emotions of [the world of] <i>Atzilut</i>, “He has done in the heavens and the earth” of [the worlds] <i>Briyah, Yetzirah</i> and <i>Asiyah</i>, [all the way] to the aspect of the physical constellations and planets, which are the root of influence for the [four categories of] inanimate (<i>Domem</i>), vegetative (<i>Tzome’ach</i>), animal (<i>Chai</i>), and speaker (<i>Medaber</i>) within the physical [world], [all of] which will be explained with the help of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה.)

Chapter 34

Now, in the aspect of <i>Zeir Anpin</i> of [the world of] <i>Atzilut</i> (Emanation) there are two levels, which are called <i>Yisroel</i> (Israel) and <i>Yaakov</i> (Jacob),<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">See Etz Chayim (<i>Shaar HaKelipot</i>) Shaar 48, Ch. 2 &amp; 3.</i> as known.
[We will now] explain the [various] particulars of levels in this.
[However,] we must first understand that the reason it is called by the name <i>Yisroel-</i>ישראל is “because you have ruled over (שרית) <i>Elohi”m-</i>אלהי״ם [and prevailed] etc.”<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 32:29; Also see Etz Chayim (<i>Shaar Leah V’Rachel</i>) Shaar 38, Ch. 2.</i>
This is the [matter of the] name of <i>Ma”H</i>-מ״ה-45 (יו״ד ה״א וא״ו ה״א) which clarifies and rules over the name of <i>Ba”N</i>-ב״ן-52 (יו״ד ה״ה ו״ו ה״ה),<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">See Etz Chayim (<i>Shaar TaNT”A</i>) Shaar 5, Ch 1. Also see Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Devarim, Vol. 1, pg. 5; Vol. 2, pg. 573; Vol. 4, pg. 1213.</i> for [it states],<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar II (<i>Hechalot</i>) 254b; Also see Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Devarim, Vol. 1, pg. 295, and Shemot, Vol. 2, pg. 321.</i> “They are clarified with <i>Chochmah</i>,” and,<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">See Pri Etz Chayim (<i>Shaar Tefilah</i>) Shaar 1, Chapter 7; Also see Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Kuntreisim, pg. 543.</i> “It is in the power of the man to clarify,” and,<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">See Talmud Bavli, Yevamot 65b</i> “It is the nature of man to conquer etc.”
In order to explain these things, we must first understand the difference between the aspect of <i>Yisroel Saba</i> (The Elder Israel) and <i>Yisroel Zoota</i> (The Little Israel).<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar II 216a</i>
The aspect of the emotional [<i>Sefirot</i>] of <i>Chochmah</i> itself are called “<i>Yisroel Saba</i> – The Elder Israel.”
Now, there are two levels in this: The first [level] is the emotions that are in the Light of <i>Abba</i> (<i>Ohr Abba</i>), and the second [level is] the emotions that are in the Hidden <i>Chochmah</i> (<i>Chochmah Stima’ah</i>).
This is called “The First Man – <i>Adam Kadma’a</i>” in the terminology of the <i>Zohar</i>.
Regarding this it states, “What (<i>Ma”H-</i>מ״ה) is his name, and what (<i>Ma”H-</i>מ״ה) is his son’s name.”
Now, the emotions that are lower than <i>Chochmah</i> [intellect] are called “<i>Yisroel Zoota</i> – The Little Israel,” for they are in an aspect of immaturity.
[This is] because they come [to be revealed] through the diminishment and concealment of the main essence of the intellect.
[All that is revealed] is what the external vessels of <i>Netzach</i> and <i>Hod</i> of <i>Abba</i> draw forth to give rise and bring out an intellect for kindness (<i>Chessed</i>) and love, which is called “<i>Chessed Zoota</i> – The Little Kindness.”
(This may be compared to the seminal drop which is in the brain of the father etc. Similarly, it states “What (<i>Ma”H-</i>מ״ה) is his son’s name” in reference to “<i>Yisroel Zoota</i> – The Little Israel,” which is drawn from the seminal drop of <i>Abba</i> (The Father) [<i>Chochmah</i>] etc., as known.)
Now from the aspect of <i>NeHi”Y</i> of <i>Abba,</i> [influence] is drawn into <i>NeHi”Y</i> of <i>Imma</i>.
[<i>NeHi”Y</i> of <i>Imma</i>] is the aspect of the influencing and lowering of the comprehension and reasoning of this emotion of kindness.
However, the aspect of <i>NeHi”Y</i> of <i>Imma</i> is withdrawn during the birthing and revelation of the arousal of the quality of love and the like, [of the heartfelt emotions].
For, as is clearly observable, the reasoning and the intellect becomes abbreviated and withdrawn during the arousal of the [heartfelt] emotions.
(This [explains] the matter of,<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote">Exodus 1:16</i> “You shall see on the birthing stones,” that is, the thighs become cold at the time of birthing.<sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote">See Talmud Bavli, Sotah 11b; Etz Chayim (<i>Shaar HaMochin</i>) Shaar 20, Ch. 3; Also see Biurei Zohar (of the Mittler Rebbe) Balak 105b; Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Devarim, Vol. 2, pg. 378.</i>
[This is] because, the first <i>NeHi”Y</i> is withdrawn and a new <i>NeHi”Y</i> is drawn forth, as explained elsewhere.)
This is called the aspect of, “Breaking through the <i>Yesod</i> of <i>Imma</i>,” to give birth to the [heartfelt] emotion.
At first, the [emotion of] love is hidden and concealed, included in the intellect, like a fetus in the womb of its mother.
However, after the [heartfelt] emotions are born they include the kindnesses (<i>Chassadim</i>) of <i>Abba</i> and the judgments (<i>Gevurot</i>) of <i>Imma</i> with [all] their general and particular aspects.
Now, there are three levels in this: There is the aspect of “<i>Mochin D’Yenika</i> – The Intellect of Suckling,” the aspect of “<i>Mochin D’Gadlut Rishon D’Imma</i> – The Intellect of the First Maturation from <i>Imma</i>,” and “<i>Gadlut Sheni D’Abba</i> – The Second Maturation from <i>Abba</i>,” as known.
As known, the explanation of these things is that the emotions are in an aspect of a fetus, three within three.
That is, only the externality of <i>NeHi”Y</i> [is revealed]. Included within them, in a concealed manner, are <i>ChaBa”D</i> and <i>ChaGa”T</i>.
[This is to say that] these are only the [instinctual] nature of the emotions.
Through suckling (<i>Yenikah</i>), they become developed and prepared to receive intellect. This is similar to an infant whose limbs grow from suckling his mother’s milk, as known.
[This continues] until when he is six years of age his emotions have intellect, but in a very limited fashion.
However, [now] his actions and ways have an aspect [and degree] of reasoning and intellect, and are not just the natural instinctive emotions [that are] only like those of an animal.
This continues until he is nine years of age, at which point he is capable of procreation.<sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote">See Talmud Bavli, Yevamot 68a</i>
At this point he has an aspect of additional growth of his intellect, more than what is necessary for the emotions alone.
Moreover, it now is possible for the beginning of an emotion that comes into being only according to intellect and reasoning, and if the intellect dictates the opposite, then an opposite emotion will be born, until his emotions are entirely according to [the dictates of] the intellect.
In contrast, prior to the age of nine he only had intellect according to the emotions that were already [instinctively] embedded in him, which he can have insight into.
This [type of intellect] is also found in wild animals and domesticated animals, that they have insight within their [natural] emotions to find food and sustenance, except that in mankind [this aspect] is called “the animal of the speaker – <i>Chai SheB’Medaber</i>.” This will suffice those of understanding.
From nine years of age and up, he is prepared for the second maturation, [which is] from <i>Abba</i>.
This is to say that [now] it is possible for the intellect to overpower the emotions, (as explained elsewhere at length regarding the matter of,<sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote">Numbers 23:9; See Biurei Zohar (of the Mittler Rebbe), Balak 103d.</i> “From the pinnacles of the boulders etc.”).
Because of this he is capable of procreation, since now each <i>sefirah</i> [of the emotions] includes the nine <i>sefirot</i> of <i>ChaBa”D, ChaGa”T</i> and <i>NeHi”Y</i>.
This is because when the aspect of the intellect of <i>ChaBa”D</i> of each emotion is developed, then automatically the aspect of <i>NeHi”Y</i> has the power to give birth to offspring, for the two are interdependent (as explained at length in chapter twenty six).
When he was six years of age each emotion included only <i>ChaGa”T</i> and <i>NeHi”Y</i> and the intellect was very constricted, according to the limitations of the natural instincts of the emotions alone.
The second maturation is from the age of thirteen until twenty,<sup class="footnote-marker">12</sup><i class="footnote">See Shaarei Teshuvah (of the Mittler Rebbe), Vol. 1, pg. 7a.</i> during which [time] he is capable of selling the [movable] properties of his father.<sup class="footnote-marker">13</sup><i class="footnote">See Talmud Bavli, Bava Batra 155a; 156a; Likkutei Torah BaMidbar 2a; Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Na”Ch pg. 519; Kuntres HaHitpaalut (sections on “intellectual love and fear”); Biurei Zohar (of the Mittler Rebbe) Balak ibid.; Etz Chayim, Shaar 25, Drush 6.</i>
This is the aspect of <i>Keter</i> and <i>ChaBa”D</i> of each emotion. [In other words,] this is the aspect of the [active] persuasion of the desire of each emotion, from higher than the intellect of that emotion etc.
[This stage of development continues] until the age of twenty, which is the maturity of the intellect of the emotions in their complete state.
[This is because now] he knows how to sell the [immovable] properties of his father, that is, with the brains of <i>Abba</i> (Father) which is the source of the emotions, to transfer it from one domain to another etc.
For example, this is like the changes [he can make] in the combinations of the letters of the intellect, which comes because of the root and source of the depth of the intellect in its essential source, specifically.
(This is as previously explained with the analogy of an outstandingly wise individual etc.)
This then, is the aspect of “<i>Yisroel</i> – ישראל,” [the letters of which spell] “<i>Li Rosh</i> – לי ראש,”<sup class="footnote-marker">14</sup><i class="footnote">See Pri Etz Chayim (<i>Shaar HaLulav</i>) Shaar 29, Ch. 1. Also see Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Vayikra, Vol. 1, pg. 75; Shaarei Teshuvah (of the Mittler Rebbe) 94d.</i> meaning “A head” and intellect “for me,” which are the aspects of <i>Keter</i>, <i>Chochmah, Binah</i> and <i>Da’at</i>.
This is because, then [the intellect] is in an aspect of a much more mature state and is capable of refining the aspect of <i>Ba”N-</i>ב״ן-52 [יו״ד ה״ה ו״ו ה״ה], which is the aspect of <i>Elohi”m-</i>אלהי״ם, as known, because, “from <i>Chochmah</i> (חכמה),” that is, from the inner aspect of the <i>Koach Ma”H</i> (כח מ״ה) specifically,<sup class="footnote-marker">15</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar III (<i>Raayah Mehemna</i>) 28a; 34a.</i> which is from the aspect of <i>Keter</i> of <i>Chochmah</i> [as it radiates] within the emotions, “they are clarified.”
This is analogous to a very wise person. The more he knows the [subject] to the depth of the matter, at its first source, the more he knows how to clarify and refine it, to remove the errors etc.
Likewise, his wisdom will stand by him, so that he can support himself with his profession and profit from his work. This is called,<sup class="footnote-marker">16</sup><i class="footnote">See Talmud Bavli, Shabbat 11a; Also see Torat Chayim, Bereshit 2c; Etz Chayim, Shaar HaKlallim, Ch. 8.</i> “His Torah learning is his profession.”
This then, is the [explanation of] the matter of “It is the nature of man to conquer etc.,” which is the aspect of the name of <i>Ma”H</i>-מ"ה-45 [יו״ד ה״א וא״ו ה״א] of <i>Chochmah</i> (חכ<b>מה)</b> which refines [the name of] <i>Ba”N</i>-ב"ן-52 [יו״ד ה״ה ו״ו ה״ה] etc., and this is the meaning of “You have ruled over <i>Elohi”m-</i>אלהי״ם.” This will suffice those of understanding.

Chapter 35

This then, is the aspect of <i>Yisroel</i> (ישראל), that is, “The Ruler of <i>E-l – Sar E-l</i> – שר א״ל.<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">See Pri Etz Chayim (<i>Shaar HaKriyat Shma</i>) Shaar 8, Ch. 9; Also see Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtzaee, Hanachot 5577, pg. 271.</i> In other words, [he is thus called] because of the radiance of <i>Keter</i> within <i>Chochmah</i>, which is called “<i>E-l</i>-א״ל<i>,</i> the light of <i>Chochmah</i>.”<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar I 94a; Zohar III 30b, 31a, 65a; Also see chapter twenty-six above, regarding the words “The Supernal God – <i>E”l Elyon –</i> א״ל עליון.”</i>
For, <i>Keter</i> is what overrules, as explained elsewhere regarding the meaning of [the verse,] “Because you have ruled etc.”
We must now understand the matter of the unification of <i>Yisroel</i> and <i>Leah</i>, which is the unification of the emotions with thought, which is called <i>Leah</i>. In addition, [we must also understand] the unification of <i>Yaakov</i> and <i>Rachel</i> which is the unification of the emotions with speech.
[However,] we must first understand the difference between <i>Yisroel</i> and <i>Yaakov</i>.
This is because the aspect of <i>Yaakov</i> is the aspect of <i>Tiferet</i> of <i>Zeir Anpin</i> of <i>Atzilut</i>, which is the quality of Mercy.<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar I 87b, 157b; Zohar III 302a; Also see Pardes Rimonim (<i>Shaar Erchei HaKinuyim</i>) Shaar 23, Section on “<i>Rachamim</i>” and “<i>Tiferet</i>.”</i>
As known, the forefathers are “the chariot” [of the supernal qualities].
<i>Avraham</i> is in the aspect of <i>Chessed</i> – Kindness<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar I 47b; Also see Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtzaee, Kuntreisim, pg. 4.</i> of <i>Zeir Anpin</i>, <i>Yitzchak</i> is in the aspect of <i>Gevurah</i> - Judgment,<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">See Pardes Rimonim (<i>Shaar Erchei HaKinuyim</i>) Shaar 24, Ch. 3 (Section on <i>Gevurah</i>).</i> and <i>Yaakov</i> is the aspect of <i>Tiferet</i> – Mercy.
[Likewise,] it is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">Micah 7:20</i> “Give truth to <i>Yaakov</i>; Kindness to <i>Avraham</i> etc.”
[Moreover,] regarding the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">Joshua 2:12</i> “And you shall give me a sign (<i>Ot-</i>אות) of truth,” it states in the <i>Zohar</i>,<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar III 2a; Also see Sefer HaMaamarim 5565, Vol. 1, pg. 368.</i> “This is the letter (<i>Ot-</i>אות) <i>Vav</i>-ו.” This is the aspect of <i>Yaakov</i> who is the middle line, “The middle beam… [that passes through from one end to the other”].<sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote">Exodus 26:28; Also see Zohar II 175b. Similarly, it states (Genesis 25:27), “And the boys grew: and Esav was a cunning hunter, a man of the field; while <i>Yaakov</i> was a pure man (<i>Ish Tam</i>), dwelling in tents.” It is explained (Zohar I 146a) that the word “tents - <i>Ohalim</i>” is plural and teaches us that the aspect of <i>Yaakov</i> (<i>Tiferet</i>) dwells between the tent of <i>Avraham</i> (<i>Chessed</i>) and the tent of <i>Yitzchak</i> (<i>Gevurah</i>).</i>
As known, [the explanation of] the matter is that the right line [which consists] of <i>Chochmah, Chessed</i> and <i>Netzach,</i> is negated by the left line [which consists] of <i>Binah, Gevurah</i> and <i>Hod</i>.
For example, this is similar to how the quality of judgment negates the quality of kindness and limits its light.
]Likewise,[ the opposite [is true], that kindness limits the light of judgment.
We therefore find that both may cease. This cannot be called “Truth-<i>Emet-</i>אמת,” since the principal [definition] of Truth-<i>Emet</i>-אמת is that it endures [forever], as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote">Proverbs 12:19</i> “The lip of truth will be established forever; but a lying tongue is but for a moment.”
[In contrast,] falsehood is deceit (<i>Kazav</i> – כזב), as in the terminology,<sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote">Using the terminology of Isaiah 58:11</i> “[A spring of water] whose waters fail” (<i>Yekazvoo Meimav</i> –י<b>כזב</b>ו מימיו). As known, [under such conditions] the river [which is drawn from the waters of the spring] will cease.
However, the quality of Truth-<i>Emet</i>-אמת, is that it endures [forever]. This is because it includes the two opposites of <i>Chessed</i> and <i>Gevurah</i> [within itself]<i>.</i> [Therefore,] nothing at all obstructs it or opposes it. Because of this, “its waters do not fail.”
This then, is [the meaning of the statement in the <i>Zohar</i> that] “the letter of Truth is the letter <i>Vav</i>-ו,” which is the middle line that includes both <i>Chessed</i>-Kindness and <i>Gevurah</i>-Judgment. This [middle line] is <i>Da’at, Tiferet</i> and <i>Yesod</i> (as stated previously in chapter twenty-one).
Now, there is another benefit in the middle line of <i>DaTi”Y</i><sup class="footnote-marker">12</sup><i class="footnote">This is an acronym for the three <i>sefirot</i> of the middle line, <i>Da’at, Tiferet,</i> and <i>Yesod</i>.</i> in that it does not [undergo] change from beginning to end. Just as it is in the beginning, so is it in the end.
It does not undergo change as a result of the length of being drawn down.
This is because of the connection [and unity] that there is in its entirety, [so that] from beginning to end it is unified as a single entity. [In this way] it is like “the inner beam…that passes through” from the highest end to the lowest end.
This is not the case, however, with the other two lines. [That is,] in the right and left [lines] there is no aspect of a connection and bond of each [of the <i>Sefirot</i> with the other <i>Sefirot</i> of that line].
As a result, we do not find that their end is similar to their beginning.
An example of this is [the right line of] <i>ChaCha”N</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">13</sup><i class="footnote">This is an acronym for the three <i>sefirot</i> of the right line, <i>Chochmah</i>, <i>Chessed</i>, and <i>Netzach</i>.</i> We find that in <i>Netzach</i> (Conquest) there is a [qualitative] diminishment of the light of the influence [of <i>Chessed</i> – Kindness]. This is likewise the case in [regard to the <i>sefirah</i> of] <i>Hod</i> (Splendor).
As known in [regard to] the [explanation of] the matter of <i>Netzach</i> and <i>Hod.</i> They are called, “The two branches of the Willow (<i>Aravot</i>)<i>,</i> which lack flavor and scent.”<sup class="footnote-marker">14</sup><i class="footnote">Midrash Vayikra Rabba 30; See Zohar I 220b, (and the Mikdash Melech there); <i>Zohar</i> III 193b; Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtzaee, Bamidbar, Vol. 5, pg. 1,868; See also Shaar HaEmunah 101b.</i>
This is because the radiance of the intellect ceases in them, since <i>Chessed</i> (Kindness) is merely a branch of <i>Chochmah</i> (Wisdom)<sup class="footnote-marker">15</sup><i class="footnote">See Chapter 21.</i> and the principal intellect and reasoning of the kindness has already withdrawn and passed.
[The intellect] only remains in [the kindness] in a way of <i>Tzimtzum</i> - lessening and concealment.
Although it still possesses [the intellect] within itself in a concealed manner,<sup class="footnote-marker">16</sup><i class="footnote">See Shaarei Teshuvah (of the Mittler Rebbe) 114b and on; Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtzaee, Bamidbar, Vol. 5, pg. 1,867 and on; Na”Ch pg. 179.</i> there is nonetheless a separation from [the intellect], and there is not such a great connection and bond between them.
For example, [it states],<sup class="footnote-marker">17</sup><i class="footnote">Introduction to Tikkunei Zohar 17a</i> “<i>Chessed</i> is the right arm,” that is, [this refers to] the strength of the right arm which is separate from the brain etc.
[Likewise,] the aspect of <i>Netzach</i>, which is merely the victory of the commitment, is already more separate from the brains of <i>Chochmah,</i> since all that remains within it, is a faint impression of the love and kindness [of the heartfelt emotions].
This is similar to the “right thigh,” which is separate from the kindness of the “right arm,” for there is no [direct] bond between the thigh and the hand.
The same is true of the “left hand” and the “left thigh” which are the aspects of the left line of <i>BoGa”H</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">18</sup><i class="footnote">This is an acronym for the three <i>sefirot</i> of the left line, <i>Binah, Gevurah</i> and <i>Hod</i>.</i> The [<i>sefirot</i> of the left line] are separated one from the other.
Therefore, we do not find their beginning in their end. This is because of the cessation of the intellectual radiance, so that there can be a complete [qualitative] lessening [and diminishment], as in the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">19</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 32:26 (and Rashi there)</i> “And the hollow of Yaakov’s thigh was strained.”
This is to say that [the angel] hit him in the aspect of <i>Netzach</i>, “in the sinew of the thigh-vein,”<sup class="footnote-marker">20</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 32:33</i> to the point that the external [forces of impurity] receive [their sustenance] from there.
This is in accordance with the statement in <i>Zohar</i> regarding the thigh of a <i>Sota</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">21</sup><i class="footnote">Regarding the verses, (Genesis 32:26) “And Yaakov was left alone, and there wrestled a man with him etc.” and, “He saw that he did not prevail against him, he touched the hollow of his thigh,” the Zohar (Mishpatim 111b) explains that the <i>Sitra Achara</i> (the side of evil) persevered over the thigh, i.e. <i>Netzach</i>, of <i>Yaakov</i>, and “won” it from him. The Zohar then continues to explain that the aspect of the “thigh” (i.e., <i>Netzach</i>) of the aspect of Yaakov was weakened until the Prophet Shmuel came and rectified it. (It explains there that its weakness was that it did not draw down the light of prophecy. As is explained elsewhere, prophecy is primarily revealed through the aspects of <i>Netzach</i> and <i>Hod</i>.) From the time of Shmuel onward the <i>Sitra Achara</i> does not have dominion over the aspect of the thigh of <i>Yaakov</i>. Rather, the forces of evil and concealment now receive their sustenance from another “thigh,” the thigh of the adulteress (<i>Sota</i>). As scripture states regarding the adulteress - <i>Sotah</i> (Numbers 5:22), “These waters that cause curse shall enter your innards to distend the stomach and cause the thigh to fall.” The reason for this is because the <i>Sitra Achara</i> itself is compared to an adulteress, as stated (Proverbs 2:17), “Who forsakes the friend of her youth, and forgets the covenant of her God.” (See Zohar II 111b; Numbers 5:21, 27.)</i>
This also is the reason why regarding <i>Chessed</i> and <i>Gevurah</i> themselves it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">22</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Pesachim 56a</i> “<i>Yishmael</i> came out of <i>Avraham</i>,” for he is the excess and dregs of the Kindnesses (<i>Chassadim</i>). [It likewise states,] “<i>Esav</i> came out of <i>Yitzchak</i>” [referring to] the excess and dregs of the Judgments (<i>Gevurot</i>).<sup class="footnote-marker">23</sup><i class="footnote">See Etz Chayim, Shaar 31, Ch. 2</i>
However, <i>Yaakov</i> is the aspect of the middle line of <i>DaTi”Y,</i><sup class="footnote-marker">24</sup><i class="footnote">The middle line, <i>Da’at, Tiferet,</i> and <i>Yesod</i>.</i> In this line there is a connection and bond from its beginning to its end, so much so, that its end is found to be the same as its beginning, literally.
(For example, as known, it is impossible for an erection to occur without <i>Da’at</i> (concentration and interest) which [takes place] in the head.<sup class="footnote-marker">25</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Yevamot 53b</i> We, therefore, find that the aspect of <i>Yesod</i> and the aspect of <i>Da’at</i> in the brain of the head, are bound together as if they are one entity.)
This is because <i>Da’at</i>, [which] is an inner [light], radiates and is bound up to the compassion of the heart. They are one at all times, literally.
This is similar to the statement in <i>Zohar</i>,<sup class="footnote-marker">26</sup><i class="footnote">Tikkunei Zohar<i>,</i> Tikkun 13 (28a); Etz Chayim, Shaar HaKlallim, Ch. 8</i> “<i>Moshe</i> is inside and <i>Yaakov</i> is outside.”
This is the aspect of <i>Da’at,</i> which is the innerness of the emotions of compassion.<sup class="footnote-marker">27</sup><i class="footnote">Etz Chayim, Shaar HaKlallim<i>,</i> Ch. 11</i>
This is because the measure of mercy will literally be commensurate to the measure of <i>Da’at</i>.
Moreover, whoever does not have <i>Da’at</i> is cruel, such as children, or the like. [However], the more one increases his <i>Da’at</i>,<sup class="footnote-marker">28</sup><i class="footnote">Ecclesiastes 1:18</i> the more will he feel merciful.
This is because, as explained elsewhere at length, there is no interruption whatsoever between <i>Da’at</i> and <i>Rachamim</i> (Mercy), as there is between the aforementioned aspects of <i>Chochmah</i> (Wisdom) and <i>Chessed</i> (Kindness).
[Furthermore,] there most certainly is a bond [of the <i>Daat</i>] with the influence of <i>Yesod</i>, which is the aspect of the connection of the influencer to the recipient.
This [connection] comes about instantaneously from <i>Da’at</i>, as in [the verse],<sup class="footnote-marker">29</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 4:1</i> “And Adam <b>knew</b> Eve [his wife; and she conceived and bore etc.]”
(There is an internal aspect of <i>NeHi”Y</i> which are the “Kidneys that give council,” and the innerness of <i>Yesod</i> is the “End of the body; [the sign of the holy covenant].” The externality of <i>Netzach</i> and <i>Hod</i>, [however,] are “the two thighs.”)<sup class="footnote-marker">30</sup><i class="footnote">See Talmud Bavli, Brachot 61a; Introduction to Tikkunei Zohar 17a; Tikkunei Zohar, Tikkun 13 (29a).</i>
This is in accordance with the statement in <i>Zohar Bereishit</i> regarding [the verse],<sup class="footnote-marker">31</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 1:9</i> “Let the waters [under the heaven] be gathered into one place.” This is the aspect of <i>Yesod</i>,<sup class="footnote-marker">32</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar I 18a &amp; 33a.</i> within which all the influence gathers. It is thus called, “The ingathering of all the lights.”
This then, is the aspect of the middle line, [which is, “The inner beam] that passes through… from one end to the other.”
It is for this reason that [the middle line] is called “Truth-<i>Emet</i>-אמת,” which is made of the letters <i>Aleph</i>-א, <i>Mem</i>-מ, and <i>Tav</i>-ת. [These letters are] the first, middle, and last letters of the [Hebrew] <i>Aleph-Bet</i>,<sup class="footnote-marker">33</sup><i class="footnote">Midrash Bereshit Rabba 81:2 – <b>א</b>'ב'ג'ד'ה'ו'ז'ח'ט'י'כ'ך'ל'<b>מ</b>'ם'נ'ן'ס'ע'פ'ף'צ'ץ'ק'ר'ש'<b>ת</b>'</i> for, as [Truth] is in its beginning, so is it in its end, this being the principal aspect of Truth.
Because of this [the sages] stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">34</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Taanit 5b</i> “Yaakov did not die,” since, because of this very reason, death (<i>Mavet</i>), which is the root of the external shells (<i>Kelipot</i>), has no foothold whatsoever in the middle line.
It is for this reason that it states, “You have ruled over <i>Elohi”m</i>-אלהי״ם,” [which is] the aspect of <i>Ba”N</i>-ב״ן-52.<sup class="footnote-marker">35</sup><i class="footnote">יו״ד ה״ה ו״ו ה״ה</i>
Now, this specifically [refers to] the aspect of <i>Da’at</i> and <i>Chochmah</i> which are in the head of <i>Yisroel</i>-ישראל [which spells] “a head for me-<i>Li Rosh</i>-לי ראש,” as explained previously. Because of this [the angel] told him,<sup class="footnote-marker">36</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 35:10</i> “<i>Yisroel-</i>ישראל shall be your name.”
However, this is not the case in regard to [the aspect of] <i>Yaakov</i>. [This is because] the aspects of <i>Netzach</i> and <i>Hod,</i> which are the “two thighs,” come from the powers of <i>Chessed</i> and <i>Gevurah</i> of <i>Avraham</i> and <i>Yitzchak.</i>
Thus, for the reason stated above, [the angel was able to] hit him in the hollow of his thigh, which is the aspect of <i>Netzach</i> of the right line.
In contrast, regarding <i>Yisroel-</i>ישראל it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">37</sup><i class="footnote">Samuel I 15:29</i> “And also the <i>Netzach</i> of <i>Yisroel-</i>ישראל does not lie etc.”
This is because <i>Yisroel-</i>ישראל is the inner aspect of the emotions of <i>Chessed</i> and <i>Gevurah</i>, which is the aspect of <i>Da’at</i> of the middle line, about which it states, “For you have ruled etc.”
Likewise, [the reason for the statement] “<i>Yaakov</i> did not die,” is because it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">38</sup><i class="footnote">Job 4:21</i> “They die, but not in wisdom.”
(Similarly, the Sages stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">39</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar I 133a</i> “<i>Yaakov</i> serves in the heights,” which refers to <i>Chochmah</i> and <i>Binah</i>, for, “Great is <i>De’ah</i> [since it was placed between two Divine Names].”<sup class="footnote-marker">40</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Brachot 33a – The verse (Samuel I 2:3) states, “For <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה is a God-<i>E”l</i>-א״ל of knowledge<i>-Ki E-l De’ot HaShem</i>-כי א״ל דעות יהו״ה,” thus placing the aspect of <i>Da’at</i> (<i>De’ot-</i>דעות) between the two Holy Names of God-<i>El</i>-א״ל and the Name <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה. The sages thus stated, “Great is <i>Da’eh</i> since it was placed between two Divine Names.” The <i>Maharsha</i> (to Brachot ibid.) explains this statement of the Talmud to mean that the aspect of <i>Da’at</i> exists between the aspects of <i>Chochmah</i> and <i>Binah</i>.</i> This is higher than the “chest,”<sup class="footnote-marker">41</sup><i class="footnote">The “Chest” refers to the emotional <i>sefirot</i> of <i>ChaGa”T</i>, as previously explained.</i> as explained elsewhere.)
However, this is all in regard to the <b>source</b> of <i>Yaakov</i>, which is much higher, in the aspect of the middle line of <i>DaTi”Y</i>, for the above mentioned reason.
However, in regard to the externality of the emotions of <i>Yaakov</i> it states, “He hit him in the hollow of his thigh,” as explained elsewhere. This will suffice those of understanding.

Chapter 36

Now, it is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 37:2</i> “These are the offspring of <i>Yaakov</i>; <i>Yosef</i>.”
[<i>Yosef</i>] is the aspect of <i>Yesod</i>,<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar III (<i>Ra’ayah Mehemnah</i>) 236a; Zohar at the beginning of Parashat Noach; Pardes Rimonim, Shaar Erchey HaKinuyim (<i>Shaar</i> 23) section on <i>Yosef</i>.</i> which is the aspect of the “Upper Righteous One” (<i>Tzadik Elyon</i>).<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">See Shaarei Orah (of the Mittler Rebbe) 27a; Also see Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Parashat Mekeitz pg. 297-299.</i>
He is also called “the small <i>Vav</i>” (<i>Vav Ze’ira</i>) etc.<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar III 74b – That is, <i>Yaakov</i> (<i>Tiferet</i>) is called the “Big <i>Vav</i>-ו,” as explained at length in the previous chapter. In contrast, <i>Yosef</i> (<i>Yesod</i>) is called the “Small <i>Vav</i>” and is a lesser extension of the “Big <i>Vav</i>-ו<i>.</i>”</i>
Now, the explanation of these things is known regarding the matter of [the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">Chronicles I 29:11</i> “Yours, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, is the greatness (<i>Gedulah</i>) and the might (<i>Gevurah</i>) and the glory (<i>Tiferet</i>), the victory (<i>Netzach</i>), and the majesty (<i>Hod</i>):] for all (<i>Ki Kol-</i>כי כל)<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">See Shaarei Orah of Rabbi Yosef Gikatilla, translated as Gates of Light, Shaar 2 (<i>Yesod</i>) – <i>Yesod</i> is called by the title “All-<i>Kol-</i>כל,” because it draws influence from all the upper <i>Sefirot</i> which are above it and brings it down to <i>Malchut.</i> Since all existence is dependent on this, it is thus called by the title All-<i>Kol-</i>כל. Furthermore, the words “כי כל-<i>Ki Kol-</i>80” share the same numerical value as the word <i>Yesod</i>-יסוד-80<i>.</i></i> that is in the heavens and on earth is yours.”
The [Aramaic] translation of this [latter part of the verse] is, “He unites the heavens and [the earth].” This is the aspect of the light of the influence of <i>Yesod</i>, the Upper Righteous One, who is called “the life of the worlds.”<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar II 193b; See the liturgy of the <i>Baruch She’Amar</i> in the morning prayers; Shaarei Orah of Rabbi Yosef Gikatilla, Shaar 2 (<i>Yesod</i>); Also see Siddur Im Divrei Elokim Chayim, pg. 86d; Pirush HaMilot pg. 77c.</i>
By way of analogy, one who understands the light of an [intellectual] concept, in and of himself, but does not have the power to bring the light of this concept forth, to influence it outside [of himself] to a recipient,
behold, this is still only the aspect of the essence of this influence, as it is in himself.
However, one who is capable of bringing it out as an influence and revelation to recipients, is called the aspect of <i>Yesod</i>.
He is called, “He who unites [the heavens and the earth],” drawing forth [influence] from the influencer to the recipient.
This is as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 97:11.</i> “Light (<i>Ohr</i>-אור) is sown for the righteous,” and it states about light,<sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 1:3</i> “[And God saw the light,] that it was good (<i>Tov</i>-<i>טוב</i>),” just as the aspect of <i>Yesod</i> is called “Good-<i>Tov</i>-טוב,”<sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar I 60a; Shaarei Orah of Rabbi Yosef Gikatilla, Shaar 2 (<i>Yesod</i>); Also see Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Kuntreisim p. 224.</i> as in [the statement],<sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote">See Tanya, Shaar HaYichud VeHa’Emunah, Ch. 4; Also see Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Kuntreisim p. 5; Also see Torat Chayim, Bereishit, p. 30b and footnote 4 there.</i> “It is the nature of the good to bestow goodness” specifically to another.
Thus, the aspect of <i>Yesod</i> is called “Righteous – <i>Tzadik</i>” and “Good – <i>Tov</i>,” as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">12</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 3:10</i> “Say of the righteous (<i>Tzaddik</i>-צדיק), that he is good (<i>Tov</i>-טוב),” and it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">13</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 11:7</i> “For <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה is righteous, He loves righteousness,” that is,<sup class="footnote-marker">14</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 57:15</i> “to revive the spirit of the humble,” and as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">15</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 145:9</i> “<i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה is good (<i>Tov</i>-טוב) to all (<i>Kol</i>-כל).”
(Moreover, the word “<i>Tov</i>-Good-טוב” has a numerical value of seventeen,<sup class="footnote-marker">16</sup><i class="footnote">See Likkutei Torah (of the Arizal), Vayeshev; Also see Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Bereishit<i>,</i> pg. 294 and pg. 328; Shaarei Orah (of the Mittler Rebbe), pg. 170.</i> that is, א"ה ו"ה-17, which are the first letters of the words [of the verse],<sup class="footnote-marker">17</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 1:1; Jeremiah 23:24; See Zohar Hashmatot, 251a; Also see Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Kuntreisim p. 225.</i> “<b>א</b>ת <b>ה</b>שמים <b>ו</b>את <b>ה</b>ארץ – The Heavens and The Earth,” that is, “He unites the heavens and the earth.”<sup class="footnote-marker">18</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar Hashmatot, pg. 251a – The first two letters of this name (א''ה) are the first two letters of the name אהי״ה which is <i>Keter,</i> whereas the last two letters of this name (ו''ה) are the last two letters of the Name <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, which represent the lower levels of <i>Zeir Anpin</i> and <i>Nukva</i> (<i>Malchut</i>)<i>.</i> As the <i>Zohar</i> states on the words, <b>א</b>ת <b>ה</b>שמים <b>ו</b>את <b>ה</b>ארץ – The heavens and the earth, “These words form the acrostic אהו''ה, for with this name the heaven and the earth were created. The heavens were created with the א''ה and the earth and everything therein were created with the ו''ה.” We thus see that this name אהו״ה represents the union of the higher levels (the heavens) with the lower levels (the earth).</i>
This is the aspect of the connection of the influencer to the recipient, as known, and as explained elsewhere.
[The aspect of <i>Yesod</i>] is also called “Peace-<i>Shalom</i>-שלום”<sup class="footnote-marker">19</sup><i class="footnote">That is, it is the aspect of the bond between two things, the upper and lower, the Giver and recipient. (See Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Kuntreisim<i>,</i> p. 226.)</i> and “Covenant-<i>Breet</i>-ברית,” as [the verse states] regarding Pinchas,<sup class="footnote-marker">20</sup><i class="footnote">Numbers 25:12; Also see Yalkut Reuveni, Parashat Korach; Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Parashat Mikeitz<i>,</i> pg. 293; <i>Hemshech</i> 5672, pg. 1.</i> “Behold, I give to him my covenant of peace (<i>Breetee Shalom</i>-בריתי שלום).”
This is in accordance with what is explained elsewhere regarding the difference between the innerness of <i>Yesod</i> of <i>Zeir Anpin</i>, which is <i>Yosef</i>, and the externality of <i>Yesod</i>, which is the aspect of <i>Noach</i><sup class="footnote-marker">21</sup><i class="footnote">See Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Parashat Mikeitz, pg. 292.</i> who is [also] called “righteous” and “perfect,”<sup class="footnote-marker">22</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 5:9</i> as stated in <i>Zohar</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">23</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar, beginning of <i>Parshat Noach</i>; Also see Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Kuntreisim p. 225.</i>)
This then, is [the aspect of] the “small <i>Vav</i>,”<sup class="footnote-marker">24</sup><i class="footnote">See Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Kuntresim, L’Habin Shoresh Inyan Chevley Moshiach<i>.</i></i> which is the aspect of the collecting and gathering of the light and influence of the emotional qualities of <i>Yaakov</i>,<sup class="footnote-marker">25</sup><i class="footnote">i.e <i>Zeir Anpin.</i></i> that were explained above.
This then, is [the meaning of,] “These are the offspring of <i>Yaakov</i>; <i>Yosef</i>.” That is, the aspect of the offspring [that is, the influence] of the emotions is specifically through <i>Yosef</i>,<sup class="footnote-marker">26</sup><i class="footnote">i.e. <i>Yesod.</i></i> this being the “Light” that is “sown for the Righteous” [who receives from and is thus called] the “Eighteen Worlds” (<i>Chay Almin</i>).<sup class="footnote-marker">27</sup><i class="footnote">Tikkunei Zohar (Tikkun 18) 31b, 33a; Pardes Rimonim, Shaar 3, Ch. 5, Shaar 15, Ch. 2; See Torat Chayim, Parshat Noach, pg. 53a; Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Shemot Vol. 2, Parshat Zachor, pg. 499a; Siddur HaAri’zal, Kavanat HaLulav – The Eighteen worlds relate to the eighteen vertebrae of the spinal cord which is shaped like a <i>Vav</i> (ו)<i>.</i> It is specifically the spine which a) holds up the entire body and is thus the foundation of the body, and b) brings the influence down and thereby connects the <i>Daat</i> of the brain, all the way down to the lowest extremity of the body, which is <i>Yesod</i>. This being the case, <i>Yesod</i>, which is likened to the male reproductive organ, is considered to be the final extension from the spinal cord. This is because the influence of life force begins in conception as it exists in the brain, until it makes its way through the spinal cord and finally comes out of the male organ to impregnate the female. Because of this <i>Yesod</i> is likewise called, <i>Chay Almin-חי עלמין,</i> which means “The Life of the Worlds” and also means, “The Eighteen Worlds.” Since <i>Yesod</i> receives the final life force and influence through the spinal cord, it is also called <i>Chay Chooliot HaShedra-</i>The Eighteen Vertebrae of the Spine.</i>
Furthermore, it is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">28</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 92:13</i> “The righteous shall flourish like the palm tree and grow great like a cedar in the Lebanon.” For, the source of <i>Yesod</i> of <i>Zeir Anpin</i> is in <i>Yesod</i> of <i>Arich Anpin</i> and <i>Atik Yomin</i>, which transcend the intellect.<sup class="footnote-marker">29</sup><i class="footnote">See Pirush HaMilot of the Mittler Rebbe<i>,</i> Ch. 133</i>
For, “their beginning is bound with their end”<sup class="footnote-marker">30</sup><i class="footnote">See Pirush HaMilot<i>,</i> Ch. 76.</i> in that <i>Yesod</i> is called,<sup class="footnote-marker">31</sup><i class="footnote">Introduction to Tikkunei Zohar 17a</i> “the extremity of the body.”<sup class="footnote-marker">32</sup><i class="footnote">See Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Kuntreisim<i>,</i> pg. 225-226.</i>
It is for this reason that the principal pleasure [is felt] specifically at the end of the influencing, as known regarding the matter of,<sup class="footnote-marker">33</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 2:2; Also see Siddur Im Divrei Elokim Chayim, Shaar HaMilah 139b; Likkutei Torah (of the Alter Rebbe)<i>,</i> Tazria 20d.</i> “[And by the seventh day] God had ended [His work which He had done] etc.”<sup class="footnote-marker">34</sup><i class="footnote">See Ma’amarei Admur HaEmtza’ee, Kuntreisim pg. 227-232.</i>
(This is also the meaning of the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">35</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 39:6</i> “And <i>Yosef</i> was well built [and good looking].” That is,<sup class="footnote-marker">36</sup><i class="footnote">Midrash Bereshit Rabba 84</i> “His appearance resembled the beauty of <i>Yaakov</i>” – which is the aspect of <i>Tiferet</i> of <i>Zeir Anpin</i> – “And the appearance of <i>Yaakov</i> resembled the beauty of <i>Adam Kadma’a</i> (The Primal Man),”<sup class="footnote-marker">37</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Bava Batra 48a</i> – which is the aspect of <i>Arich Anpin</i> and <i>Adam Kadmon</i> etc.)<sup class="footnote-marker">38</sup><i class="footnote">See Pirush HaMilot<i>,</i> Ch. 75-76.</i>
Now, regarding the words [of the aforementioned verse,] “These are the offspring-<i>Eileh Toldot</i>-אלה תולדות;” This refers to the aspect of the “six directions” of <i>Zeir Anpin</i>, each of which also includes six,<sup class="footnote-marker">39</sup><i class="footnote">The six “directions” of <i>Zeir Anpin</i> are the three heartfelt emotions, <i>Chessed, Gevurah, Tiferet,</i> and the three gut emotions, <i>Netzach, Hod</i> and <i>Yesod,</i> each of which is also made up of six. <i>Chessed</i> is made up of <i>Chessed</i> of <i>Chessed, Gevurah</i> of <i>Chessed, Tiferet</i> of <i>Chessed</i> etc. <i>Gevurah</i> is made up of <i>Chessed</i> of <i>Gevurah, Gevurah</i> of <i>Gevurah, Tiferet</i> of <i>Gevurah</i> etc. The same principle applies to all six qualities, totaling a sum of thirty-six qualities.</i> thus totaling 36 which is the numerical value of the word “these are-<i>Eileh</i>-אלה.”<sup class="footnote-marker">40</sup><i class="footnote">See Likkutei Torah (of the Alter Rebbe), Pikudei 4c; Also see Torat Chayim<i>,</i> Noach 56b, and note 15 there.</i>
However, there can be no “offspring” without an additional influence of new intellect from <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i>, which is brought about by means of the maturation of <i>Keter, Chochmah, Binah</i> and <i>Da’at</i> of <i>Zeir Anpin</i>, as previously explained.<sup class="footnote-marker">41</sup><i class="footnote">See Likkutei Torah, Pekudei<i>,</i> Sections 4-6.</i>
(In the above, we again [observe] the aspect of a single <i>Hitbonenut</i> contemplation that includes many particulars in one general point, that is, from <i>Yesod</i> of <i>Malchut</i> of the Unlimited One (<i>Ein Sof</i>) until the aspect of <i>Yesod</i> of <i>Zeir Anpin</i>.
(This is in the same manner previously described regarding <i>Zeir Anpin</i> in general,<sup class="footnote-marker">42</sup><i class="footnote">See chapter 33.</i> which is the end of the world of the Unlimited One (<i>Ein Sof</i>).)
This is in accordance with what is written regarding King Solomon,<sup class="footnote-marker">43</sup><i class="footnote">Kings I 5:13</i> “[He spoke of trees, from the cedar tree that is in the Lebanon to the hyssop that is in the wall.]”<sup class="footnote-marker">44</sup><i class="footnote">The configuration of the ten <i>Sefirot</i> is called by the term, The Tree of Life-<i>Eitz Chayim-</i>עץ חיים. As explained above in chapter 22, the ten <i>Sefirot</i> not only exist as ten general qualities, but rather every single level and aspect is also subdivided into ten and those, in turn, are further subdivided into ten etc. This means that the “Tree of Life” exists on all levels, from the highest to the lowest levels. This is the meaning of, “He spoke of trees (i.e. the ten <i>Sefirot</i> as they exist throughout <i>Seder Hishtalshelut-</i>The Chaining Down) from the cedar tree that is in the Lebanon (i.e. from the highest level) to the hyssop that is in the wall (i.e. all the way down to the level of the “hyssop in the wall” which is <i>Yesod</i> of <i>Zeir Anpin</i> as it unifies with and influences <i>Malchut.</i>)</i> The words “from the cedar tree that is in the Lebanon” refers to the simple essential pleasure that is in the Essential Self of the light of the Unlimited One, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, when the desire of “I will rule” arose in His simple will.
The words “to the hyssop that is in the wall” refers to the aspect of the “small <i>Vav</i>,” that is, the immaturity of <i>Yesod</i> of <i>Zeir Anpin</i>, in its influencing and union with <i>Malchut</i> which is called “the wall.”<sup class="footnote-marker">45</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar I 228b; Zohar II 133a</i>
This is as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">46</sup><i class="footnote">Kings II 20:2</i> “Then he turned his face to the wall and prayed etc.,” and likewise it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">47</sup><i class="footnote">Kings II 4:10</i> “Pray, let us make a loft with a wall etc.,”<sup class="footnote-marker">48</sup><i class="footnote">The word used for “wall” here is “<i>Keer-</i>קיר.” The <i>Zohar</i> states that in the Greek language <i>Keer-</i>קיר means Lord-<i>Adon</i>-אדון and is thus a euphemism for the <i>Sefirah</i> of <i>Malchut-</i>Kingdom. This is because the Divine name associated with <i>Malchut</i> is <i>HaShem</i>’s-יהו״ה title my Lord-<i>Adona”y</i>-אדנ״י. (See Zohar I 228; Also see Sefer HaMaamarim 5643-5644, pg. 310.)</i> which refers to <i>Malchut</i>, as stated in the <i>Zohar</i>.
This, then, is the meaning of, “The righteous man shall flourish like the palm tree,” that is, he ascends to the “seventy years”<sup class="footnote-marker">49</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar III 16a, 24a; Also see Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Shemot Vol. 1, pg. 225.</i> of <i>Adam Kadmon</i> and there “he will grow like a cedar in the Lebanon” in an aspect of the limitlessness of the Unlimited One (<i>Ein Sof</i>), literally. This will suffice those of understanding.)
(It is also explained elsewhere that <i>Yosef</i> is called,<sup class="footnote-marker">50</sup><i class="footnote">See Etz Chayim (<i>Shaar HaTzelem</i>), Shaar 23, Ch. 3; Also see Biurei Zohar<i>,</i> Tisa 54c; Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Bereshit pg. 294, and Na”Ch pg. 118.</i> “an orphan from his mother,” but not from his father.
The [letters of the] word “orphan – <i>Yatom</i>” (יתום) form an acronym for [the words of the verse,] “[And <i>Yosef</i> was] well-built and good looking – <b>י</b>פה <b>ת</b>אר <b>ו</b>יפה <b>מ</b>ראה.”<sup class="footnote-marker">51</sup><i class="footnote">Etz Chayim, Shaar HaKlallim, Ch. 4; Also see Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Mikeitz pg. 293-294.</i>
Now, the reason that “he is an orphan from his mother” is because the aspect of <i>Yesod</i> of <i>Imma</i> is short<sup class="footnote-marker">52</sup><i class="footnote">See Etz Chayim, Shaar HaKlallim, Ch. 10; See also Siddur Im Divrei Elokim Chayim, Shacharit L’Shabbat 187d; Pirush HaMilot 43b and 43c; Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Na”Ch pg. 118.</i> and withdraws and becomes concealed during the birth of the emotions. For, as is clearly observable, when emotions are aroused the intellect withdraws.
It is for this reason that it states that <i>Binah</i> only spreads forth until <i>Hod</i> of <i>Zeir Anpin</i>, but not until <i>Yesod</i> of <i>Zeir Anpin</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">53</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar III (<i>Raaya Mehemna</i>) 244b; Also see Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Bereishit pg. 222.</i>
That is, it only [spreads forth] until [it causes] the aspect of the acknowledgment (<i>Hoda’ah</i>) which comes about because of the intellect.
However, it does not spread forth until <i>Yesod</i> of <i>Zeir Anpin</i>, which is the aspect of the essential connection of the heart, within which there is a glimmer from the aspect of <i>Yesod</i> of <i>Abba</i>.
[That is, the aspect of <i>Yesod</i> of <i>Abba</i>] is the aspect of the connection to the essential light of the concept, prior to its [investment] within the comprehension. Regarding this it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">54</sup><i class="footnote">Ecclesiastes 1:16</i> “My heart has seen much wisdom etc.,” [that is, this is] the sight of the intellect within the heart of flesh, specifically in <i>Yesod</i> of <i>Zeir Anpin</i>.
It is the aspect of the nullification that is drawn forth in the breath of the chest and heart, and as stated in <i>Ra’aya Mehemna</i>,<sup class="footnote-marker">55</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar II (<i>Ra’aya Mehemna</i>) 116b.</i> “With the eye of the intellect, which is in the heart, one can see everything.”
This is because the <i>Yesod</i> of <i>Abba</i> is longer than that of <i>Imma</i>,<sup class="footnote-marker">56</sup><i class="footnote">Etz Chayim, Shaar HaKlallim, Ch. 10; Siddur Im Divrei Elokim Chayim, Shacharit L’Shabbat 187d; Pirush HaMilot 43b and 43c; Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Na”Ch 118.</i> and is drawn forth until <i>Yesod</i> of <i>Zeir Anpin</i> even after the light of <i>Binah</i> has withdrawn.
Thus, [<i>Yesod</i> of <i>Zeir Anpin</i>] is called “an orphan from his mother” but not from his father etc., as is explained elsewhere at length.<sup class="footnote-marker">57</sup><i class="footnote">See Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Na”ch, pg. 118-119.</i>
This is also the matter of, “These are the offspring of <i>Yaakov</i>;” that is, the seminal drop of <i>Yesod</i> of <i>Abba</i> [<i>Yaakov</i>] is the [source of the] aspect of “<i>Yosef</i>,” that is, <i>Yesod</i> of <i>Zeir Anpin</i>. This will suffice those of understanding.)

Chapter 37

We now must understand the matter of the unifications of <i>Yisroel</i> and <i>Yaakov</i> with <i>Leah</i> and <i>Rachel</i>.
As known, the explanation of the matter of <i>Leah</i> and <i>Rachel</i> is that they are the matter of thought and speech.<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">Etz Chayim (<i>Shaar Ozen Chotem Peh</i>) Shaar 4, Ch. 1; Siddur Im Divrei Elokim Chayim, Shacharit 60c and 69a; Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Na”Ch, pg. 103; Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Vayikra, Vol. 1, pg. 227; Shaar HaEmunah pg. 95b.</i>
This is the matter of the two <i>Heh</i>’s (ה) of the Name <i>HaShem</i>-י<b>ה</b>ו״<b>ה</b>.<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar III (<i>Ra’aya Mehemna</i>) 244b; Also see Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Bereishit, pg. 222.</i> This is in accordance with what Zohar states<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar III (<i>Idra Zuta</i>) 290b; Also see Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Kuntreisim, pg. 428.</i> that [in the Song of Songs], “Solomon explains [regarding] two females,” as in the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">Song of Songs 4:8</i> “Come with me from Lebanon [my] bride etc.”
