In other words, the first <i>Heh</i>-ה of the Name <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה corresponds to,<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 29:16</i> “The name of the big one was <i>Leah</i>,” whereas the second <i>Heh</i>-ה [corresponds to,] “the name of the little one was <i>Rachel</i>.”<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">Also see Torat Chayim<i>,</i> VaYeitze<i>,</i> pg. 168c.</i>
However, we must first explain the matter of,<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 27:22</i> “The voice is the voice of <i>Yaakov</i>,” for there is an inner unheard voice [and an outer heard voice].<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar I 50b; Also See Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Kuntreisim, pg. 308 (citing Zohar); See Siddur Im Divrei Elokim Chayim, Shaar HaLulav 264d; Biurei Zohar, Balak 107c; Sefer HaMaamarim 5668, Vol. 1, pg. 253; Pirush HaMilot, Ch. 30; Sidur Im Divrei Elokim Chayim, Shacharit L’Shabbat 181b; Torah Ohr, Bereishit 6d; Likkutei Torah, Netzavim 47b, and Shir HaShirim 12b and elsewhere.</i>
Since, as known regarding the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 19:3; Also see Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Vayikra<i>,</i> Vol. 2, pg. 472.</i> “Day to day speech streams forth – יום ליום יביע אמר”; that the [word for “speech-<i>Omer</i>-אמר”] is [an acrostic for] “Fire-<i>Aish</i>-<b>א</b>ש,” “Water-<i>Mayim</i>-<b>מ</b>ים,” and “Air-<i>Ruach</i>-<b>ר</b>וח,” that is, <i>Chessed, Gevurah</i> and <i>Tiferet</i> (Kindness, Sternness and Compassion).
[This is to say,] that just as the [physical] voice is composed of the physical qualities of fire, water, and air, so too, the breath of the heart itself includes the spiritual qualities of fire, water and air.<sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar II (<i>Ra’aya Mehemna</i>) 43b; 184b; Also see Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Vayikra, Vol. 2, pg. 651; Also see Torat Chayim, Bereishit 39d, and footnote 26 there.</i>
These are the aspects of <i>Chessed</i>, <i>Gevurah</i>, and the intermediate quality [of <i>Tiferet</i>] which is the air (or vapor).
In other words, [this corresponds to] the aspects of the constriction or spreading forth of the spiritual breath of the heart.
For example, when a person is happy, there then is an aspect of the spreading forth of light [and vitality] in his heart. This is the breath of the Kindnesses (<i>Chassadim</i>).
In contrast, when he is depressed, there is an aspect of constriction and withdrawal. This is the aspect of the breath of Judgments (<i>Gevurot</i>).
The intermediary between <i>Chessed</i> and <i>Gevurah</i>, is the spiritual breath that is an intermediary composed of both <i>Chessed</i> and <i>Gevurah</i>.
This is like the air [or vapor] (<i>Ruach</i>) of the physical breath, which is an intermediary composed of both fire and water.
As known, thirst results from the element of fire (<i>Aish</i>).<sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote">See Tanya Ch. 3</i>
Similarly, regarding the physical voice it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">12</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 69:4</i> “My throat was raspy,” which comes about from an intensity of the element of fire in the breath of the heart.
The opposite is a clear [resonating] voice from the element of water (<i>Mayim</i>) of the breath of the heart.
The intermediary, which is the vapor (<i>Ruach</i>), is an admixture [of the two].
This is likewise true of [the emotions conveyed in] the intermediate voice, which contains an admixture of both joy and bitterness or sadness. It is called, “A delightful voice to the soul”; which specifically depends on the proportions of the spiritual admixture in the breath of the heart.<sup class="footnote-marker">13</sup><i class="footnote">See Torat Chayim Bereishit<i>,</i> 39d.</i>
Similarly, the spirit of life [and vitality] in the right and left ventricles [of the heart] is in a constant state of “running and returning” (<i>Ratzo V’Shoov</i>) with the heartbeat, as known that this too is in an aspect of constriction and spreading forth.
(However, here the opposite of the above takes place. For, when the spirit of life enters the heart from [the nervous system that extends from] the brain, the heart contracts to receive it. On the other hand, when it withdraws, the heart spreads forth.
This is because the vitality is specifically in a manner of “running and returning etc.,”<sup class="footnote-marker">14</sup><i class="footnote">This is also in accordance with the verse (Ezekiel 1:14), “The <i>Chayot</i> [angels] were running and returning.” Although in this verse the word “<i>Chayot</i>-חיות” refers to the Angels who are called “<i>Chayot HaKodesh</i>,” nonetheless, the word “<i>Chayot</i>-חיות” can also be translated as “life force” or “vitality” (<i>Chayoot-</i>חיות).</i> as explained in medical books.)
Now, all the above is called “The voice that is heard” in speech, this being the aspect of the vapor and breath of the speech.
This is the aspect of the “voice – <i>Kol</i>” and “speech – <i>Diboor</i>” which is mentioned in many places in <i>Zohar</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">15</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar I 36a, 50b; 74a; 98a; 142a, and elsewhere.</i>
This is the aspect of the unification of <i>Yaakov</i> and <i>Rachel</i>.
In other words, it is the aspect of the drawing forth of the emotions of the heart that come into an aspect of the vapor and breath of the heart, which is composed of the spiritual qualities of fire, water and air, until it reaches the aspect of the voice of speech.
Now, the aspect of the power of speech is drawn from the cavity of the lungs in the cardiovascular system, and is called<sup class="footnote-marker">16</sup><i class="footnote">See Targum Onkelos to Genesis 2:7.</i> “the speaking spirit” (<i>Ruach Memalela</i>).
(This then, is the meaning of the statement in Etz Chayim that <i>Keter</i> of <i>Nukvah</i> of <i>Zeir Anpin</i><sup class="footnote-marker">17</sup><i class="footnote">In other words, <i>Keter</i> of <i>Malchut</i> of the world of <i>Atzilut.</i></i> adheres to the chest of <i>Zeir Anpin</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">18</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Keter</i> of <i>Malchut,</i> which represents the desire to speak, is rooted in the emotions, in other words “the chest of <i>Zeir Anpin.”</i> See Etz Chayim (<i>Shaar Mochin D’Tzelem</i>) Shaar 26, Ch. 3.</i>
This is also the meaning of the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">19</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 119:89</i> “Forever, <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, your word stands in the heavens.”<sup class="footnote-marker">20</sup><i class="footnote">The words, “your word-<i>Dvarcha</i>-דברך” in this verse refers to <i>Malchut</i>, which represents the faculty of speech, and the words, “the heavens” refers to <i>Zeir Anpin,</i> which represents the emotions of the heart, which is in the chest. As explained before, the word <i>Shamayim-</i>שמים (The Heavens) is a composite of two words, fire-<i>Aish</i>-אש and water-<i>Mayim-</i>מים, which refer to the two primary emotions of <i>Zeir Anpin,</i> sternness- <i>Gevurah</i> and kindness-<i>Chesed</i>, as they are composed in <i>Tiferet</i>.</i>
It is also in accordance with what is explained elsewhere regarding the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">21</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 58:13</i> “<i>Mimtzo Chaftzecha V’Daber Davar</i>,” that the source of the power of speech is drawn from the breath of the heart of <i>Zeir Anpin</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">22</sup><i class="footnote">The whole of the verse is, “<i>V’Cheebadto MeAsot drachecha, Mimtzo Chaftzecha V’Daber Davar</i> - Honor <i>Shabbat</i> by desisting from doing your mundane activities, from seeking your mundane needs and speaking mundane words.” However, the word “<i>Chaftzecha</i> – Your mundane needs” shares the same root as the word “<i>Chafetz</i>” which means desire. Thus, the second half of the verse, “<i>Mimtzo Chaftzecha V’Daber Davar</i>” can be understood to refer to the “desire to speak.” As evidenced from the continuation above (in the chapter), the desire to express oneself in speech is dependent upon the emotions of the heart. When one is depressed, his speech is minimal, and the opposite is true when one is in a state of joy. This, then, is the meaning of the aforementioned statement of <i>Etz Chayim</i> that <i>Keter</i> (the desire) of <i>Nukvah</i> (<i>Malchut</i> or speech) adheres to the chest of <i>Zeir Anpin</i>.</i>
It is clearly observable that if [a person’s] heart is depressed and withdrawn [into itself], his speech will be minimal, whereas when [his heart] spreads forth [with joy], his speech will be expansive.
This is because the power of speech is dependent on the breath of the voice in the heart itself.<sup class="footnote-marker">23</sup><i class="footnote">See Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Vayikrah, Vol. 2 pg. 652.</i>)
Now, as long as it has not been drawn forth from the breath of the heart into speech, as in,<sup class="footnote-marker">24</sup><i class="footnote">See Midrash Tehillim 89:1; Kohelet Rabba 12:10</i> “The heart did not reveal to the mouth,” then the word of the King has not yet been actualized and brought out from “nothing” to “something,” whatsoever.<sup class="footnote-marker">25</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar Hashmatot 253a</i>
This is similar to [the statement],<sup class="footnote-marker">26</sup><i class="footnote">See Talmud Bavli, Niddah 16b</i> “However, <i>HaShem</i> did not declare who will be righteous and who will be wicked.”
This is because speech is already an actualization, as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">27</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 33:9</i> “For He spoke, and it was; [He commanded, and it stood fast.]” Similarly, it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">28</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 55:11</i> “The word that issued from My mouth shall not return unfulfilled, [but it shall accomplish that which I please] etc.”
However, while [it is still] in the “heart” of <i>Zeir Anpin</i> it can still be overturned from Judgment (<i>Din</i>) to Kindness (<i>Chessed</i>), as in the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">29</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 6:6</i> “And <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה repented [that he had made man on the earth, and it grieved him in his heart] etc.” It then states,<sup class="footnote-marker">30</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 8:21</i> “And <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה said in his heart, I will not again [curse the ground because of man] etc.”
This is the aspect of <i>ChaGa”T</i><sup class="footnote-marker">31</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Chessed, Gevurah</i> and <i>Tiferet</i>.</i> of the breath of the heart of <i>Zeir Anpin</i> that comes forth and unites with speech, which is called the revealed world, as known. This will suffice those of understanding.
Now, there is an aspect of an inner voice that is altogether not heard in speech. This is the aspect of the intellect within the emotions of <i>Chessed</i> and <i>Gevurah</i>.
For example, this is like the Love (<i>Ahavah</i>) and Fear (<i>Yirah</i>) that transcends the aspect of the spirit of life (<i>Ruach HaChayim</i>) that is in the heart, like the <b>essential</b> joy and love of kindness or the <b>essential</b> anger and judgment of fear and trepidation.
These are much more spiritual, even more than the spiritual compositions of fire, water and vapor mentioned above, which come to be composed in the physical heart.
Now, although this itself has a composition of [the aspects of] fire, water and air – which are the aspects of <i>Chessed, Gevurah</i> and <i>Tiferet</i>, nevertheless it is within the <b>inner</b> aspect of the heart.
That is, [it refers to] the aspects of <i>ChaGa”T</i>, within which there is a radiance of the <b>intellect</b>. [This radiance of the intellect] is called the inner voice of <i>Binah</i> within <i>Zeir Anpin</i>, which comes and is drawn from the brain to the heart.
Thus, when [this intellect] is drawn forth by way of the aspect of <i>Da’at</i> - which is the aspect of <i>Yisroel,</i> as previously explained – [and causes a spiritual arousal of the emotions] that is drawn immediately into the letters of thought, which is called <i>Leah</i>, this is called the unification of <i>Yisroel</i> and <i>Leah</i>.
This is to say that the inner emotions of the heart are immediately thought in his mind.
[For example,] should he become aroused by an intellect and reasoning for love and kindness, this emotion and the intellect within it, will immediately come into [the letters of] his thoughts.
[This is so] since, as known, the thoughts enclothe the emotions of <i>Yisroel</i> with their particulars.
[These thoughts] are called <i>Leah</i> (לאה), as in,<sup class="footnote-marker">32</sup><i class="footnote">See Likkutei Torah of the Arizal, End of Parshat Toldot; Also see Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Na”Ch, pg. 105.</i> being weary (<i>Nil’ah</i>-נלאה) of containing the emotions.<sup class="footnote-marker">33</sup><i class="footnote">The reason why the level of “thought” is called <i>Leah,</i> which is a term that denotes weariness, in that thoughts constantly go through a person’s mind without cessation. (See Torat Chayim, Parashat MiKeitz<i>,</i> pg. 169a-170a.)</i> The source of <i>Leah</i> is above in <i>Binah</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">34</sup><i class="footnote">See Torat Chayim, VaYeitze, pg. 170a; Also see Likkutei Torah of the Arizal, Parshat Vayeitze, section entitled “The mystery of Yaakov and his two wives.”</i>
The verse therefore states about <i>Leah</i>,<sup class="footnote-marker">35</sup><i class="footnote">Genesis 30:20; Also see Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee<i>,</i> Na”Ch<i>,</i> pg. 188.</i> “I have born him six sons,” referring to the aspect of the six directions of the emotions of <i>Zeir Anpin</i>.
However, the unification of <i>Yisroel</i> and <i>Leah</i> refers to the intellect of <i>Abba</i> and <i>Imma</i> as it is within <i>Zeir Anpin</i>, which unites with the lower <i>Leah</i>, that is, with the [letters of] thought that receives from the aspect of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Tvunah,</i> which is the source of thought etc.<sup class="footnote-marker">36</sup><i class="footnote">See Torat Chayim, Parashat YaYeitze<i>,</i> pg. 170a -171a. The aspect of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Tevunah</i> will be discussed later.</i> This will suffice for the understanding.
Now, there is also a unification of <i>Yisroel</i> and <i>Rachel</i>, which is when the radiance of the innerness of the intellect, as it is in the emotions, comes into speech.
Likewise, there is a unification of <i>Yaakov</i> and <i>Leah,</i> which is called “the fleeting thoughts of the heart” (<i>Hirhurei Liba</i>). In other words, this is when the aspect of the externality of the emotions rise up as fleeting thoughts in the brain.
So also, there is a unification of <i>Yaakov</i> and <i>Rachel,</i> which is the drawing forth of the externality of the emotions of the heart into speech, as mentioned above.
Now, the order of the drawing forth is sometimes as follows; The aspect of the emotions of the heart rise and unify with thought, and from thought they come [down] to the externality of the heart – which is the breath of the heart – and from the breath of the heart it enters into the breath of speech, which is called the voice and speech.
At other times, thought enters speech, like a person who says what he is thinking (in his intellect).
This is referred to as,<sup class="footnote-marker">37</sup><i class="footnote">See Etz Chayim (<i>Shaar Leah V’Rachel</i>) Shaar 38, Ch. 3; Also see Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Hanachot 5577, pg. 35.</i> “The heels of <i>Leah</i> entering into the head of <i>Rachel</i>.”
At the time that he speaks what he is thinking, it comes out from the voice of the breath of the heart into speech, through the five sources [of the letters in mouth].<sup class="footnote-marker">38</sup><i class="footnote">The five sources of the letters in the mouth are the throat, palate, tongue, teeth and lips. These divide the voice into specific letters of speech, as will be explained in later chapters.</i>
Now, certainly, what is in his heart arises in his thoughts, for there can be no thought without the emotions of the heart.
We therefore find that the aspect of <i>Yaakov</i> – which is the vapor and breath of the voice of the heart – functions both in thought and speech, which are called the two sisters, <i>Leah</i> and <i>Rachel</i>.
As known, [these two aspects are sometimes referred to as],<sup class="footnote-marker">39</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar I (<i>Sitrei Torah</i>) 152a; Zohar II 29b; Etz Chayim (<i>Shaar HaMochin D’Tzelem</i>) Shaar 23, Ch. 4.</i> “The concealed world – <i>Alma D’Itkasia,</i>” and “The revealed world – <i>Alma D’Itgalia</i>,”<sup class="footnote-marker">40</sup><i class="footnote">See Torat Chayim, Bereishit, pg. 168b.</i> [and are also referred to as,<sup class="footnote-marker">41</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Shabbat 104a; Also see Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Shemot Vol. 1, pg. 213; Shaarei Teshuvah 91b.</i>] “The closed utterance – <i>Maamar Satoom</i>” and “The open utterance – <i>Maamar Patuach</i>.” This will suffice for the understanding.
(In this manner there is a unification of <i>Yisroel</i> and <i>Leah</i> and a unification of <i>Yisroel</i> and <i>Rachel</i>, in the innerness of the emotions, in the aspect of the aforementioned “inner voice.”
This is the meaning of the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">42</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 19:3; Also see Siddur Im Divrei Elokim Chayim, Shacharit L’Shabbat 181a and on; Ma’amarei Admor HaZaken, Hanachot HaRav Pinchas, pg. 3.</i> “Day to day speech streams forth,” and then afterwards [in the following verse, which refers to thought,] “There is no speech,” that is, in thought “there are no words; [their voice is unheard.]”
This [latter unification refers to the unification] during <i>Shabbat</i>, [at which time] the unification is in the <b>innerness</b> of <i>Zeir Anpin</i> and <i>Nukvah</i>, as known, and as explained elsewhere.<sup class="footnote-marker">43</sup><i class="footnote">See Pirush HaMeelot pp. 37b-40a.</i> This will suffice for the understanding.)

Chapter 38

We must now understand the matter of the garments of thought, speech and action, in a manner of more particulars, as it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">Introduction to Tikkunei Zohar 17a</i> “You have fashioned garments for them etc.”
However, in order to understand this, we must preface with the explanations of the source and root of the aspect of the letters, and why at times they are called “Vessels – <i>Keilim</i>”<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">Etz Chayim, Shaar 6 (<i>Shaar HaAkudim</i>), Ch. 1; Also see Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah, end of Ch. 4; Shaarei Teshuvah, Vol. 1, pg. 38b.</i> and at times they are called “Garments – <i>Levooshin</i>.”<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">See Sefer HaMa’amarim 5562, Vol. 2, pg. 391; Sefer HaMa’amarim 5563, Vol. 1, pg. 249, and 261.</i>
We will afterwards explain, in a manner of particulars, the aspects of <i>Rachel</i> and <i>Leah,</i> and <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Tevunah</i> and <i>Binah</i>, all the way to the highest of levels etc.
Now, as known, the source of the letters is literally in the essence of the [human] soul,<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">Etz Chayim (<i>Shaar TaNT”A</i>) Shaar 5, Ch. 3; Also see Ma’amarei Admor HaZaken, Parshiyot HaTorah, Vol. 2, pg. 639 and pg. 730; Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Bamidbar, Vol. 1, pg. 309.</i> for “the soul is full of letters,” that is, from the very beginning and essence of its coming into being.<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">See Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Vayikra<i>,</i> Vol. 2<i>,</i> pg. 922-924; Sefer HaMaamarim 5665, pg. 194; Sefer HaMaamarim 5665, Hosafot pg. 309-310.</i>
They [the letters] are [there] in two ways; as letters of thought, and as letters of speech.<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">See Sefer HaMa’amarim 5666, p. 483; Sefer HaMaamarim 5665 pg. 195.; Maamarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Vayikra, Vol. 2, pg. 922-924.</i>
In other words, immediately upon the existence of the essence of the [human] soul, the letters of thought are unified in it.
They are essentially included in it, just as the power of movement is included in an animal etc.
Now, they come out and burst forth into revealed thought on three levels.
There is imagination and imagery without letters at all. There are simple, disjointed letters without combining or being connected to any particular matter, and there are letters that combine according to analytical thought.
Likewise, in the essence of the soul there [also] is the aspect of letters of speech.
In that the [human soul] is called,<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">See Genesis 2:7 and Targum Onkelos there.</i> “The Articulate Soul – <i>Nefesh HaMedaberet</i>” or “The Speaking Spirit – <i>Ruach Memalela</i>.”
They [too] are included there in an essential manner, and come out into revelation like the movement of an animal, or the like.
This is like the speech of the angels, about which it says,<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 6:3</i> “They call one to another [and say] etc.”
In this there are likewise three levels. There is the simple substance of each particular letter. This is called the breath of the spirit of speech.
Then there are the individual letters <i>Aleph</i>-א<i>, Beit</i>-ב<i>, Gimel</i>-ג<i>, Dalet</i>-ד etc., without combination [into words].
Then there is the combination of the letters [into words] which is called the form of speech in the “speaking spirit.”<sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote">See Tanya, Igeret HaKodesh, Epistle Five.</i>
This is similar to,<sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote">See Talmud Bavli, Brachot 18b – It happened that a certain Chassid (pious man) gave a dinar of charity to a poor man on the eve of Rosh Hashanah during a year of famine. His wife was angered over this, so he went and spent the night in the cemetery. While he was there, he heard two spirits of two deceased children conversing with each other. One said to the other, “My friend let us roam the world and hear from behind the curtain what misfortune is to come upon the world this year.” Her friend replied, “I cannot come with you, as I am buried in a reed mat. You go, however, and come back and tell me whatever you hear.” So, she went and roamed and returned. Her friend said to her, “What have you heard from behind the curtain?” She replied, “I heard that the crops of anyone who plants this year at the time of the first rains will be destroyed by hail.” Hearing this, the Chassid went and planted at the time of the second rain. Everyone’s crops were destroyed except for his. The next year he again went and spent the night in the cemetery, and he heard the same two spirits talking with each other. One said to the other, “Let us roam the world and hear from behind the curtain what misfortune is to come to the world this year.” She replied, “My friend, did I not already tell you that I cannot come with you because I am buried in a reed mat? You go and come back and tell me whatever you hear.” So she went and roamed and returned, and her friend said to her, “My friend, what have you heard from behind the curtain?” She replied, “I have heard that the crops of anyone who plants this winter at the time of the second rain will be blasted by a dry wind.” Hearing this, the Chassid went and planted at the time of the first rains. Everyone else’s crops were blasted except for his. His wife said to him, “Why is it that last year everyone else’s crops were destroyed by hail except for yours? And why is it that this year everyone’s crops were blasted except for yours?” So he told her the whole story. It was not more than a few days later when a quarrel broke out between the wife of the Chassid and the mother of the child whose spirit was overheard in the cemetery. In the course of that quarrel his wife said to the mother, “Come I will show you your daughter buried in a reed mat etc.” The next year he again went to spend the night in the cemetery, and heard the same two spirits conversing. The one said to the other, “My friend let us roam the world and hear from behind the curtain what misfortune is to come to the world this year.” She replied, “My friend, leave me be. The words that we spoke between ourselves in the past few years have already been heard amongst the living.”</i> “Two spirits conversing,” and to the speech of the Angels etc.<sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote">See Maamarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Vayikra, Vol. 2, pg. 923.</i>
Now, even before the coming into being of the source of the simple desire and the simple pleasure, there already are letters included in the essence of the soul.
However, only after the coming into being of the desire, do [these letters] come out to be the aspect of the revelation of the desire. They are then called “the letters of desire.”
This is the aspect of the revelation of the desire as a “something” with a tangible existence as a desire, this being the principal matter of the letters of the essence of the soul.
That is, they only are the aspect of the revelation [and expression] of the light of the essence of the soul in every aspect and manner of “somethingness” and tangible existence.
[In other words,] it is through the letters that it comes forth into revelation from the aspect of the concealed <i>Heyulie</i> etc.
(This is in accordance with what is written in <i>Likkutei Amarim</i>,<sup class="footnote-marker">12</sup><i class="footnote">See Tanya, Shaar HaYichud V’HaEmunah, Ch. 11-12; Iggeret HaKodesh, Epistle 5.</i> regarding the twenty-two letters that are embedded in the soul, that they are twenty-two powers or twenty-two movements of the soul etc.)
It is through this [matter of the letters] that it is possible for the desire to come into revelation in the light of the intellect.
If not for the revelation of the desire in an aspect of letters, that [by means of the letters] it appears as a tangible existence of desire, then the essential concealed desire would not come into any other garment, from one state of being to another state of being.
[This is to say, there would be no descent into the] aspect of a desire that is felt and revealed in the “intellect and reasoning for the desire,” as known. This will suffice for the understanding.
This also is the case with the intellect and reasoning for the desire, which is called the <i>Chochmah</i> of the desire (<i>Ratzon</i>).
The fact that it appears as a tangible existence of “reasoning for the desire” is from the aspect of the letters that are in it.
It is through this [the matter of the letters] that it descends from [its] state, to the state of the emotions of the desire.
An example of this is [the aspect of] love (<i>Ahavah</i>) that is in the desire. It too is only the existence of desire, except that it is vested within the existence of love, that because of his desire he loves etc.
(“Love-<i>Ahavah</i>-אהבה” is of the root “desire-<i>Avah</i>-אבה,”<sup class="footnote-marker">13</sup><i class="footnote">See Shoresh Yesha<i>,</i> section on “<i>Avah</i>-אבה,” cited in Sefer HaChakirah, 92a; Sefer HaShorashim of the RaDa”K, section on “Avah-אבה”; Also see Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Hanachot 5577, pg. 264.</i> and the <i>Heh</i>-ה [which is additional to the root, represents] the “Five Kindnesses-<i>Heh Chassadim</i>” that spread forth from <i>Chochmah</i> and <i>Binah</i> etc.)
Now, this desire itself, even as it is in the intellect and reasoning for the desire, still refers [only] to the essence of the desire as it transcends [actual] intellect and reasoning.
Nevertheless, it is through the letters that it transforms and is seen as transcending the intellect, to [being] within the intellect, to [being] within the emotions.
Similarly, there are letters for the emotions as well. This refers to the fact that the love that is within the desire has an apparent tangible existence etc.
This continues until the aspects of the desire of thought, speech and action. Each of these has the aspect of letters, all the way to the aspect of the desire for action, that is, when the action arises in his desire. There are specific letters for this.
This is likewise the case with [actual] intellect that follows the desire.
For if the intellect did not have a [tangible] existence in letters of intellect, which is the aspect of the revelation of the intellect as a [tangible] existence, then how would it be possible for the intellect to come forth with a transformation of being to an [emotional] arousal of love which is born of intellect?
For, even there [in the emotional arousal] it is the [very] same intellectual [point] that there was before the birth [of the emotion] of love.
It is only that [now this intellect] vests within the [emotional] existence of love.
This is only possible by means of the letters that are within it.
Likewise, it is in this manner that the letters of the emotions [come] into thought.
If the emotion did not have a tangible existence of letters, how could it possibly vest within the existence of thought etc.? The same is true of the letters of thought within speech etc.
We thus find that it is through the letters that there is an aspect of a chaining down from cause to effect, from the essence of the soul until the end action, and that the source of the letters is literally in the essence of the soul.
It is also understood from all the above that in the source from which the letters are hewn, that is, in the essence of the soul, the letters come into being as one with the essential light of the soul.
This is similar to how the power of movement [of an animal] comes into existence with it [that is, with the existence of the self of the animal] etc., and the like. This will suffice for the understanding.
Now, the analogue to all this is automatically understood: That is, the letters of the Upper Purity (<i>Tehiru Ila’a</i>), about which it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">14</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar I 15a</i> “He engraved an engraving,” refer to the aspect of the essential letters of thought and speech in the Essential Self of the limitless light of the Unlimited One (<i>Ein Sof</i>), <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He.
This is analogous to the letters that are embedded in the essence of the [human] soul, in the <i>Yechidah</i>, on the three above mentioned levels.
These letters chain down from one state of being to another state of being, such as from the simple desire of “I will rule” which arose in His thought before the <i>Tzimtzum</i>, until even the desire, intellect and emotions of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>, <i>Atik Yomin, Arich Anpin, Abba</i> and <i>Imma, Zeir Anpin</i> and <i>Nukvah</i> of <i>Atzilut</i>.
All this is drawn forth and descends from one to the other in a manner of cause and effect with a transformation from one state of being to another state of being, by means of the aspect of the letters of each of these states of being.
For, this [matter of the letters] is the aspect of the revelation of the “somethingness” [of that state of being,] giving it tangible existence, as explained above.
[This continues] until the aspect of the “end action” of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Atzilut</i>, which is the aspect of the letters of action of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Atzilut</i>, and continues [all the way] to <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Asiyah</i>, [which is] the root of the existence of our lowly world (as will be explained at the end of this treatise).
This is all included in the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">15</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 135:6</i> “[Everything that <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה desired, He has done.” That is,] “Everything that <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה desired” within His Essential Self, “He has done” in actuality. This will suffice for those of understanding.

Chapter 39

It now may be understood, in a general way, why the letters are called “Vessels – <i>Keilim</i>”<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">Etz Chayim, Shaar 6 (<i>Shaar HaAkudim</i>), Ch. 1; Also see Shaar HaYichud VeHaEmunah, end of Ch. 4; Shaarei Teshuvah, Vol. 1, pg. 38b.</i> and are also called “Garments – <i>Levushim</i>.”<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">See Sefer HaMa’amarim 5562, Vol. 2, pg. 391 and Sefer HaMa’amarim 5563, Vol. 1, pg. 249 and 261.</i>
This is because, at first glance, even though it limits the [spreading forth of] the essence, the aspect of the vessel is [nonetheless] considered to be of the essence.
For example, the letters that at all times are embedded in the essence of the soul, are unified with the essence.
This is analogous to how the letters that are engraved into an image or that protrude, like the letters of a seal [are one with it].
This is likewise so of the spiritual letters of the soul.
[Furthermore] this is similar to the revelation of the essence of an animal through its power of movement, or like the revelation of the life-force that spreads from the essence of the animal, as this power still [exists] embedded [and] concealed within the essential self [of the animal].
We likewise observe this with the letters of an intellectual concept; that they are included [in their source] in the essential power to conceptualize.
That is, immediately when [a person] brings [his] reasoning to light from his potential power to conceptualize (<i>Koach HaMaskeel</i>), its letters come out together with it.<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">See Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Vayikra Vol. 2, pg. 924; Also see the discourse entitled “<i>Samach T’Samach</i>” 5657 of Rabbi Shalom Dovber of Lubavitch.</i>
It is by and through these [letters] that its existence is [limited to] a certain manner of being a [tangible] “thing.” These are the letters of any concept to whosoever discovers it.
Proof for this, [that the letters, which are called vessels, are of the essence] is from two individuals who conceive the same concept or reasoning.
One will bring it out with certain letters and combinations, while the other will bring it out into revelation with a different manner of letters and combinations. [However, the concept remains the same.]<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">See Sefer HaMa’amarim 5715, page 244-247</i>
(This is like the various commentaries on the Talmud; such as the commentaries of <i>Rashi</i> and of <i>Tosefot</i>, the <i>R”osh,</i> or the <i>Ra”N</i>, and the like. [Sometimes] they may all be explaining the very same concept or reasoning, each one in his own unique language, nonetheless, all [their explanations] amount to the same matter and intent, except that each one explains it according to the letters of his intellect etc., as explained elsewhere.<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">See Shaarei Teshuvah 108d.</i>)
This is because when the concept itself is born, its letters are born along with it, through which it takes on [tangible] appearance as an aspect of a “something,” and even though [the letters] depict and define it, they nonetheless are considered to be essential to it.
This is likewise the case with the letters of desire and the letters of the emotions, such as the love of the heart etc.
It becomes revealed by the aspect of its letters, which are what [define the light of Kindness] giving it the aspect of a type of revelation, as a [tangible] existence in various different manners, such as a single concept that becomes revealed through different combinations [of letters] etc.
This then, is what is called the aspect of vessels (<i>Keilim</i>). This is the aspect of the “something” that depicts and defines, but is [nonetheless] considered to be essential.
For example, the aspect of all the vessels of the ten <i>sefirot</i>, [such as] the vessel for the light of <i>Chochmah</i>, the vessel for the light of <i>Chessed</i> and of <i>Netzach</i> etc., which is the aspect of the “something” that depicts them, as known.
(This is in accordance with what was explained in chapter twenty-eight; that from the “thickening” of the lights the vessels are made.
[Furthermore, it was] also [explained] that the root of the vessels preceded that of the lights, and is called “the simple substance” (<i>Chomer Pashut</i>) etc.
This is understood from what was said above regarding the letters that are in the essence of the [human] soul, that they [even] preceded the root for the existence of the light of the essential desire and pleasure etc.)
However, notwithstanding all the above, it is also true that the letters are also called “Garments – <i>Levushim</i>.”
This is because the aspect of a Garment (<i>Levush</i>) is that it is something completely separate from the essence.
It is only that the essence becomes vested in it. This is similar to how the body becomes vested in garments that are foreign and separate from it, which cover and conceal it.
This is similarly the case with the letters of the intellect. Once they come into being as existing [in a tangible way], the essence of the intellect becomes vested and concealed within them, so that all that is revealed is only the aspect of the letters of the concept, which is a manner that it becomes a [tangible] “something,” as if there were nothing besides this manner.
In truth, however, the essential light of the concept is not confined to this specific manner [of combinations of letters].
Rather, [this combination of letters] may be exchanged like a garment, and [the concept] may be invested into a completely different manner of [letter] combinations.
[However] none of these [letter formations] actually reach the essence of what [the concept] is, at all. Rather, it only vests and is revealed in them.<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">See Sha’ar HaGilgulim, Hakdamah 18; Also see Shaarei Teshuvah, Chinuch pg. 108b-108c.</i>
(This is similar to what was mentioned above, regarding the revelation of the same concept and reasoning [through the various unique manners of expression] in the language of the [Talmudic] commentators etc.)
The same [principle] applies to the letters of the desire (<i>Ratzon</i>), for we find that one simple desire may be invested in many different forms of revelation.
Nonetheless, it is all one single desire. Just as the body vests in its garments, so likewise, the desire becomes revealed in a manner that constantly undergoes change.
Similarly, we observe this with the letters of thought (<i>Machshavah</i>) that enrobe the emotions.
For, the love [felt] in the heart which has already come in its [distinct] manner of letters of [description and] revelation in the heart; when it [subsequently] enters thought, it then vests within the thought, literally like a body that becomes enrobed in a separate garment.
Regarding this it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 102:27; See Shaar HaEmunah pg. 97.</i> “Like a garment they are changed and exchanged,” literally.
This is because the garment of thought does not stand still for even a moment. Rather, it is [in a] constant [state of] “disrobing” and “enrobing,” “disrobing” and “enrobing” etc., from thought to thought etc.
This is likewise the case when the light of the intellect comes into the garment of the letters of thought. It literally “disrobes” and “enrobes” from thought to thought, [constantly].
(This is not the case, however, with the aforementioned aspect of the revelation of the letters of the essence of the intellectual [concept] itself, which are considered to be of the essence.
They only appear to be exactly like the garment of the letters of thought after they come into being as a [tangible] existence, separate [and apart] from the essence of the intellect, as explained above.)
[From all the above] we find that it is understood that both [matters] are true in the root of the aspect of the letters.
Sometimes they are in an aspect of “Vessels – <i>Keilim</i>.” This is when they are [still] in the root from which they are hewn, completely unified with the essence, as explained above.
However, they also come into an aspect of “Garments – <i>Levooshim</i>,” which are totally separate from the essence, as explained above.
(This is because the root of the letters is from the aspect of the Encompassing Lights<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote">See Sefer HaMa’amarim 5567, pg. 392.</i> (<i>Makifim</i>), which are the root of the Garments (<i>Levooshim</i>), and [furthermore] the root of the Vessels (<i>Keilim</i>) which define and depict etc. is also from there, as stated above and as explained elsewhere.)
From all of the above it may be generally understood how it is above in Godliness by a person who contemplates all the aspects of the garments of thought, speech and action, and the three types of letters [that there are] throughout all the particulars of the ten <i>Sefirot</i>, and throughout the [entire] chaining down [of the worlds] (<i>Hishtalshelut</i>), all the way to the highest heights in the Essential Self of the limitless light of the Unlimited One (<i>Ein Sof</i>), in the letters that, “He engraved an engraving in the Upper Purity,” and the like. This will suffice for the understanding.

Chapter 40

We now must understand the aspect of the source of the letters of the thought of <i>Binah</i>, <i>Tevunah</i> and <i>Leah</i> in a manner of particulars.
As explained in various places in the <i>Zohar</i>,<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">Tikkunei Zohar, Tikkun 69, 109a.</i> “There is one kind of thought and there is another kind of thought.”
For example, there is the aspect of the concealed thought (<i>Machshavah Stima’ah</i>) of <i>Arich Anpin</i>, and the aspect of the primal thought (<i>Machshavah HaKedoomah</i>) of <i>Adam Kadmon</i>, and the like.
Now the explanation of the matter is that in the Holy Tongue,<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">Biblical Hebrew</i> desire (<i>Ratzon</i>) is also called by the term “thought” (<i>Machshavah</i>).
For example, [the verse],<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">Jeremiah 18:8. See Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Devarim, Vol. 1, pg. 208 and Vol. 2, pg. 641.</i> “I repent of the evil that I <b>thought</b> to do to them,” means, “that I <b>desired</b> to do to them,” as known.
This is because desire immediately vests within thought in the brain. Thus, the desire and the thought of the desire are as one. Therefore “thought” is called by the term “desire,” and “desire” is called by the term “thought.”
For example, the statement,<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">See Etz Chayim, Shaar HaKlallim, Ch. 1.</i> “When it arose in His desire” means “When it arose in His thought” etc.
Now, this is called, “Concealed Thought” (<i>Machshavah Stima’ah</i>) in accordance to the aspect of the hiddenness of the desire. Thus, the thought within which the desire is invested, is likewise hidden and concealed. It therefore is called, “Concealed Thought.” (This is the aspect of the letters of the desire, as mentioned above.)<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">See Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Hanachot p. 263.</i>
However, the aspect of the Primal Thought (<i>Machshavah HaK’dooma</i>) of <i>Adam Kadmon</i> precedes even the Concealed Desire (<i>Ratzon HaNe’elam)</i>. On the contrary, it is the source of the Concealed Desire, which is called, “the Desire for the Desire,” (<i>Ratzon LaRatzon</i>) etc. This too is an aspect of thought, within which there vests the aspect of the Primal Desire that preceded all “Desires for Desires,” (as explained in chapter seventeen). Nevertheless, it is called by the term, the Primal <b>Thought</b>.
In this manner we may understand this concept all the way to the highest levels, even on the level of the thought of the Simple Desire, literally, as it is in the Essential Self of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, Himself, (as mentioned previously in chapter ten).
Now, in regard to desire that spontaneously enters the brain, we observe that it enters the nerves of the brain in a way of simple thought not made up of letters at all.
This is because, in truth, desire does not have an aspect of an organ (vessel), such as the other letters, for example, like how the light of the intellect vests within the organ of the brain etc.
However, the power and light of the desire spreads forth in the nerves of the brain, so that all the limbs obey the desire of the brain. (These are called the “nerves,” which are very fine and from which the power of movement and the power of feeling in the limbs come forth [through the nervous system] as known).
For example, when one stretches out his hand or foot, or gathers them in, it only is in accordance to the desire that rises spontaneously in his brain.<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">See Maamarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Drushei Chatunah Vol. 1, p. 42 and on.</i>
Now, there is also a different kind of thought, which is in an aspect of actual letters of thought.
These letters come about through the aspect of understanding and comprehension, that is, <i>Binah</i> that precedes them [and] which is called “Analytical Thought” (<i>Machshavah Iyunit</i>).<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">See Maamarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Vayikra Vol. 1, p. 255.</i>
As we clearly observe with every intellectual concept and reasoning, that it is grasped in the mind of <i>Binah</i> (which is called “understanding”), and immediately comes into analytical thought, which is called, “The thought of the Intellect,” (<i>Machshevet Sechel</i>).
This is the power of Analytical Thought (<i>Machshavah Iyunit</i>), which specifically includes all intellectual analysis, but has no relationship to desire (<i>Ratzon</i>) altogether.
This kind of thought is therefore not at all called by the term, “desire” (<i>Ratzon</i>), since it is not within the nerves of the brain [that is, in the nervous system] at all. Rather, it actually is only in the brain of <i>Binah</i> itself.
In other words, in the organ (vessel) for the comprehension and understanding of the intellectual concept itself, there is an organ (vessel) for the analytical thought of any intellectual comprehension.
This is the aspect of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Tevunah,</i> which is the last level of the light of the essential comprehension that brings about comprehension in a separate matter (as mentioned previously in chapter two).
It is from here that the aforementioned power of “the Thought of the Intellect” (<i>Machshevet Sechel</i>) is made, since the light of the comprehension of the concept initially comes into his mind even before any analytical thought. (This is called, “to grasp and understand alone.”)
That is, it is grasped in his mind even before he thinks of the concept through the garment of thought and analysis. Nevertheless, the comprehension and concept immediately spread into analytical thought.
This then, is the aspect of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Tevunah.</i> It is higher than the aspect of the <b>letters</b> of thought (<i>Otiyot HaMachshavah</i>) that are called <i>Leah</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote">See Siddur Im Divrei Elokim Chayim<i>,</i> Shacharit 60c, 69a; Also see Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Na”Ch, p. 103; Shaar HaEmunah 90b and 95b, and elsewhere.</i>
(This is also in accordance with what is known regarding the matter of the large <i>Dalet</i> of the word “One-<i>Echad</i>-אח<b>ד</b>,”<sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote">Deuteronomy 6:4; Also see Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Devarim Vol. 1, pg. 283 (and the notes there).</i> which is the aspect of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Tevunah</i> that comes from the aspect of the “back” (<i>Achorayim</i>) of <i>Imma</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote">See Maamarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Bereishit Vol. 1, p. 380.</i> It is the source for the coming into existence of the thought that comes forth in actual letters, as explained elsewhere.)
Now, the aspect of the conceptualization itself – which is grasped within comprehension and understanding – is also called by the term “thought.”
However, this is the aspect of the “somethingness” (<i>Yesh</i>) of the light of <i>Chochmah</i> which is called the <i>Chashav Ma”h</i><sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote">That is, the term “thought-<i>Machshavah</i>-מחשבה” divides into “The thought of <i>MaH-Chashav MaH</i>-חשב מ״ה.” See Zohar I 24a; Tikkunei Zohar, Tikkun 69, 112b.</i> (חשב מ”ה) of <i>Chochmah</i> (חכ<b>מה</b>).
There is also an inner aspect of the thought of <i>Binah,</i> that is, “not heard,” even in the aspect of the Thought of the Intellect (<i>Machshevet Sechel</i>) and it does not come into letters of thought altogether.
This is like the aspect of the depth of comprehension (<i>Omek HaMoosag</i>) which is ungraspable, even in the comprehension and thought of <i>Binah</i>, and the like.
(It is called,<sup class="footnote-marker">12</sup><i class="footnote">See Introduction to Zohar 1b; Biurei Zohar (of the Mittler Rebbe), Terumah 49c; Imrei Binah, Shaar HaTefillin, 121b and on; Torat Chayim, Noach, 57c. – It is explained that the word “Who-<i>Mi</i>-מי” always refers to <i>Binah</i>-understanding. This is because the word “<i>Mi-מי</i>” has a numerical value of 50, corresponding to the fifty gates of <i>Binah,</i> as mentioned in chapter thirty-two.</i> “<i>Mi D’lo Kayama L’She’ela</i> – He who is beyond inquiry.”) This will suffice those of understanding.
This then, is the meaning of the aforementioned statement, “There is thought,” that is, the concealed thought of the desire, as mentioned previously, and there is the analytical thought of <i>Binah,</i> which comes into the category of the aspect of actual letters of thought that are called <i>Leah</i> etc.
However, both these aspects exist even in the desire, which transcends intellect.
(In other words, this is the aspect of, “The Hidden <i>Binah</i>” (<i>Binah Stima’ah</i>) of <i>Arich Anpin,</i> which is the concealed thought in the hidden desire. That is, just as there is a hidden intellect and wisdom of <i>Arich Anpin</i>, which is, “hidden from all conceptualization,” and is the hidden <i>Chochmah</i> of <i>Arich Anpin;</i> which, as known, is called the hidden reasoning for the desire, so likewise, there is an aspect of, “The Concealed <i>Binah</i>” (<i>Binah Stima’ah</i>) etc.)
This is similar to the difference that we observed between the two types of thought, mentioned above about revealed thought.
This is to say that there is the desire that becomes revealed in the brain, which is the desire in the nerves of the brain. It is called, “the concealed thought” (<i>Machshava Stima’ah</i>), because of the concealment of this desire in the brain before it comes to <i>Chochmah</i> and <i>Binah</i>.
Furthermore, there is also the aspect of the analytical thought (<i>Machshava Iyunit</i>), which is the aspect of the “something” of the “nothing” of <i>Chochmah</i>, until it ultimately comes into the aspect of actual letters of thought.
(Now, according to what was stated previously (in chapter 38) regarding the first source of the letters of thought in the actual essential self of the soul, so likewise, there is a source for the letters of the thought of <i>Binah</i> in the essence of the soul.
This is similar to how there is a source for the lights of the letters of the desire that come into the nerves of the brain and the like.
The only difference, is that one comes as an aspect of revelation of desire and one comes as an aspect of revelation of letters of comprehension (<i>Binah</i>) that are grasped within intellectual comprehension.
Nevertheless, we observe that whatever it is that arises in his desires and thoughts, will come out until the aspect of the letters of thought of <i>Binah</i>. That is, the aspect of the concealed desire and thought is drawn into the revealed thought of <i>Binah</i>.)<sup class="footnote-marker">13</sup><i class="footnote">See Maamarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Bamidbar Vol. 5, pg. 1,753 and the notes there gleaned from the Lubavitcher Rebbe’s notes to the Maamarim of 5659 pg. 77, as well as Vayikra Vol. 2, pg. 568; Ohr HaTorah, Ki Tetze, pg. 968; Tanya Iggeret HaKodesh, epistle beginning with the words, “He garbs Himself with light;” Likkutei Torah, Shemini Atzeret 91b.</i>
(This is also the matter of the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">14</sup><i class="footnote">Exodus 3:14</i> “<i>Eheyeh Asher Eheyeh</i>-I shall be as I shall be,” which is the revelation of the general <i>Keter</i> of <i>Arich Anpin</i> within the particular <i>Keter,</i> which is in <i>Binah</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">15</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar III 11a, 65b; Shaar HaEmunah 60a. Zohar I 166b; Likkutei Torah Pinchas 80b, Re’eh 31d. – The Zohar explains: “The first name is <i>Eheyeh-אהי״ה</i> (which refers to <i>Keter</i>), which is concealed (and transcends grasp). This is like a person who says [to another] I am who I am, but [to the other] it is not known who He is. Subsequently [the verse states], “that I will be-<i>Asher Eheyeh</i>-<i>אשר אהיה</i>” [referring to <i>Chochmah</i> which is called “head-<i>Rosh-</i>ראש” and shares the same letters as “<i>Asher-אשר</i>,” and <i>Binah</i> which is likewise called “I will be-<i>Eheyeh-אהי״ה</i>.] That is, I am destined to become revealed within these other crowns. For at first, I was concealed [in <i>Keter</i>], but will subsequently be revealed, until there is a complete revelation of the Holy Name.”</i>
This is in accordance with what is known and explained elsewhere regarding the matter of,<sup class="footnote-marker">16</sup><i class="footnote">See Numbers 18:23. Also see <i>Torah Ohr, Lech Lecha</i>, 11b. Also see <i>Ma’amarei Admor HaZaken</i>, <i>Parshiyot HaTorah,</i> Vol. 1 pg. 84 and on. Also see <i>Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Vayikra</i>, Vol. 1, p. 375.</i> “The Levite, shall serve Him,”<sup class="footnote-marker">17</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar III 178b – Although the simple translation of this verse is, “The Levite, he shall do the service etc.” The Zohar explains that the verse may be understood more deeply to mean, “The Levite shall serve Him-<i>Hoo-הוא</i>.” For, the word <i>Hoo-</i>Him-הוא, in the third person, refers to the transcendent, concealed and innermost aspect of <i>Keter,</i> which is the inner pleasure of <i>Atik Yomin</i> that draws forth the Essential Self of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He.</i> that the revelation of <i>Atik Yomin</i> is specifically in <i>Binah</i>.<sup class="footnote-marker">18</sup><i class="footnote">See Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Hanachot 5577, p. 4; Torat Chayim, Lech Lecha, 81b, and elsewhere.</i>
This is also the matter of the three thorns of the letter <i>Yod</i>-י, as explained elsewhere at length.<sup class="footnote-marker">19</sup><i class="footnote">See Torat Chayim, Lech Lecha, 82b, and footnote 11 there, and elsewhere.</i> This will suffice for the understanding.)

Chapter 41

Now, as known regarding the matter of,<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">Introduction to Zohar 2b.</i> “The mother lends her clothing to the daughter,” this refers to the aspect of the five <i>Gevurot</i>-Judgments, <i>MeNaTzePa”Ch</i> (מנצפ”ך)<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">The five, “final letters,” of מנצפ״ך, or rather, םןץף״ך, are concluding letters that bring about separation and division between the words. See Sefer Yetzirah and citations in Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Vayikra<i>,</i> Vol. 1, p. 237; Also see Ginat Egoz of Rabbi Yosef Gikatilla, translated as HaShem Is One, The Letters of Creation, Vol. 2 &amp; 3.</i> of <i>Imma</i>,<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">See Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Devarim, Vol. 3, p. 1,023 and on; and Na”Ch, p. 17.</i> that are called,<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">Exodus 28:11</i> “The protrusions of the seal.”
This refers to the aspect of the combinations of letter-divisions of thought, as stated in <i>Zohar</i> on the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">Song of Songs 2:12; Zohar I 97b; Also see Sefer HaMa’amarim 5568, Vol. 1, p. 488.</i> “The voice of the <i>Tor-</i>dove is heard in our land,” (as explained elsewhere).<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">See Ohr HaTorah, Shlach p. 448 and elsewhere.</i>
However, it must first be understood that within thought itself there are three levels. These are the aspects of Thought of Thought, Speech of Thought, and Action of Thought.
As known, the explanation of these matters is according to the above explanation (in chapter 38<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">The text says chapter 37, but appears to be a typographical error (and was thus corrected).</i>) that there are three levels in thought:
For example, there is imagination without letters. This is like a toddler who does not yet have thought<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Chullin 12b</i> in a manner of combinations of letters, but rather only the imagery and form of thought. This type of thought is drawn from the power of imagination<sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Koach HaDimyon</i>-The Power of Imagination.</i> alone.
Now, although this imagery also has divisions and parts, in that its imagery is restricted to a specific matter, nevertheless, it is only by way of imagination. Thus, it is not yet regarded as being true thought, that is, that he thinks <b>into</b> the matter. Because of this the Sages stated that a small infant has no thought at all.<sup class="footnote-marker">10</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Chullin 12b; Maamarei Admor HaZaken 5568 Vol. 1, p. 488; 5570 p. 13; Maamarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Vayikra Vol. 2, p. 925..tions.                        is intellect is extremely contricted to the point of false imaginations.                         .tions.                        is intellect is extremely contricted to the point of false imaginations.</i>
Now, even when he matures somewhat and does indeed have combinations of letter-divisions in thought, nonetheless, they are not yet complete letters. Rather, it is only that he can restrict his thinking specifically to a particular matter.
For example, he can think with his brain regarding something that is given to him and distinguish between it and something else, until he desires one and rejects the other, as known.
This is the beginning of the matter of thought and is called, “Action of Thought” (<i>Maaseh SheB’Machshavah</i>).
In an adult this refers to when he thinks about how to do something or specifically how to form or write something in a particular manner or when whatever he actually needs to do, arises in his thoughts.
This is likewise the case when he forms the image of the written letters in his thoughts or when he forms an image of any separate physical thing, such as a fruit or a tree or the form of any image and the like; all this is called, Action of Thought (<i>Asiyah SheB’Machshavah</i>).
An infant, however, lacks even this aspect of thought, but only has the power of imagination (<i>Dimyon</i>).
(Nevertheless, this power of imagination is higher than the imaginations that occur in dreams etc.)
This is as explained elsewhere regarding the matter of the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">11</sup><i class="footnote">Hosea 12:11; Also see Imrei Binah, Shaar HaKriyat Shma, 71b.</i> “By means of the prophets I am depicted.”<sup class="footnote-marker">12</sup><i class="footnote">The Hebrew text of this verse (Hosea 12:11) is, “<i>B’Yad HaNevi’im Adameh</i> – ביד הנביאים אדמה.” The word “Depicted-<i>Adameh</i>-אדמה” shares the same root as “imagination-<i>Dimyon</i>-דמיון” indicating that the prophets (other than Moshe) only perceive Godliness through the power of imagination (<i>Koach HaDimyon</i>-כח הדמיון). See Imrei Binah, Sha’ar HaKriyat Shma, pg. 71b.</i> That is, the prophets perceive only by means of the power of imagination of the thought (<i>Koach HaMedameh SheBaMachshava</i>).
This is because, during the time of sleep, all that remains of the mind is the very last portion of the powers of thought, which is just the imagination of thought.<sup class="footnote-marker">13</sup><i class="footnote">It is for this reason that it states (Talmud Bavli, Brachot 57b) states that dreams are 1/60th of prophecy, and it is because of this that dreams may be interpreted.</i>
(This is the matter of <i>Galut-</i>Exile, which is compared to sleep,<sup class="footnote-marker">14</sup><i class="footnote">See Chapter 30.</i> as stated,<sup class="footnote-marker">15</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 126:1</i> “We were like dreamers.” Nevertheless, dreams are culled from the thoughts of the heart etc.,”<sup class="footnote-marker">16</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Brachot 55b</i> as explained elsewhere.)<sup class="footnote-marker">17</sup><i class="footnote">See introduction to Shaar HaEmunah and Shaar HaYichud, also translated as “Essential Faith;” Maamarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Hanachot 5577 pg. 244.</i>
Now, the aspect of Speech of Thought (<i>Dibur SheB’Machshavah</i>) is like when someone thinks the combinations of the letters of speech that another person speaks to him.
This is lower than the letters of thoughts that he thinks to himself, without hearing another person speak.
For example, this is when he thinks the combinations of the letters, “Master of the Universe<i>-Adon Olam</i>-אדון עולם.”<sup class="footnote-marker">18</sup><i class="footnote">See the beginning of the Liturgy of the morning prayers.</i> Within this particular combination of letters itself, when in his thoughts he hears another person speak the words, “<i>Adon Olam</i>,” all that takes place is that the letters of speech of the other fellow become engraved in his own thought. This is lower than the letters of “<i>Adon Olam</i>” as he thinks them himself.
Likewise, all thoughts that he thinks concerning how to speak before actually speaking (whereupon he immediately speaks) are called, “Speech of Thought” (<i>Dibur SheB’Machshavah</i>).
As known, this is because the aspect of “Speech of Thought,” brings about the aspect of “Thought of Speech.”
This is because his thinking how to speak, brings about the manner of thought he will have when he actually does begin to speak, what originally, he only thought to speak.
In contrast, the third level is the aspect of “Thought of Thought” (<i>Machshavah SheB’Machshavah</i>), which is when he thinks to himself.
For example, this is like when he thinks the combinations of the letters, “<i>Adon Olam</i> – Master of the Universe,” to himself, without speaking them out, or when he thinks any other matter in its various combinations that are called, “the letters of thought.”
However, here too, there are two levels: The first also falls into the general category of, “Speech of Thought” (<i>Dibur SheB’Machshavah</i>).
This is when he does not think into the concept or meaning of the letters of, “Master of the Universe<i>-Adon Olam</i>-אדון עולם,” or the like; this being the concept of sovereignty and lordship. He does not think about this altogether. Rather, he only thinks the combinations of the letters <i>Alef</i>-א and <i>Dalet</i>-ד of the word “<i>Adon</i>-אדון,” and the like.
Although this level is not brought out in speech, since it is higher than hearing the spoken words “<i>Adon Olam</i>,” nonetheless, this too is called by the term, “Speech of Thought” (<i>Dibur SheB’Machshavah</i>).
(Similarly, this is the matter of the speech of the angels, as the verse states,<sup class="footnote-marker">19</sup><i class="footnote">Isaiah 6:3; Also see Talmud Bavli, Brachot 18b; Ma’amarei Admor HaZaken 5570, p. 106; Ma’amarei Admor HaZaken, Inyanim, p. 82; Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Kuntreisim, p. 547; Torat Chayim, Noach, 67d.</i> “And they called out one to another etc.” This is similar to the letters of our human thoughts; as if a person is calling to his friend by name, simply by thinking it, in the same manner that he would call him through the faculty of speech. Such is the speech of the angels.
Similarly, in regard to the spirits of the departed, it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">20</sup><i class="footnote">Talmud Bavli, Brachot 18b</i> “Two spirits were conversing one with the other,” which, generally, cannot be heard by humans, as explained elsewhere.)
The second level of “Thought of Thought” is true thought.
This is that he thinks the intellectual concept of the matter contained in the letters of thought. It is because of this, that is, that he focuses on the concept, that he spontaneously thinks the combinations of letters specific to that concept.
(As we observe regarding the combinations of the letters of thought; that they come about solely according to the focus of the mind. If his mind is focused on a certain matter, accordingly the combinations will come about in a certain way, as known.)
For instance, if he focuses his mind on a specific matter regarding some business dealing, as opposed to the matter of lordship, he will think in different combinations of letters. It specifically goes according to what he is focused on.
This is called “Thought of Thought” (<i>Machshavah SheB’Machshavah</i>), which is also called, “The ability to Think” (<i>Koach HaMachshavah</i>). That is, it is the ability to think about any matter in a variety of different combinations.
(This is similar to “The ability to Speak” (<i>Koach HaDibur</i>), which is the ability to speak whatever one desires to speak, as will be explained.)
This is the aspect of the organ (vessel) for the Analytical Thought (<i>Machshavah Iyunit</i>) which is considered to be the Thought of the Intellect itself (<i>Machshevet Sechel</i>) (as mentioned above in chapter 40). This is the aspect of <i>Malchut</i> of <i>Tevunah</i> etc.
Now, specifically this type of thought is dependent upon <i>Da’at</i> (focus).
This is why it states that an infant has no thought; because since his ability to focus is small, therefore, so is his ability to think in combinations of letters small. Rather, he cannot think in letter combinations at all. However, great focus (<i>Gadlut HaDa’at</i>) brings about thoughts with many different combinations.
According to the manner of the depth of one’s concentration (<i>Ha’amakat HaDa’at</i>) into the depth of the concept (<i>Omek HaMoosag</i>) will be the depth of his thoughts in the aspect of a depth of the analytical thought (<i>Machshavah Iyunit</i>), as previously mentioned.
This is similar to the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">21</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 92:6; Also see Sefer HaMa’amarim 5566, p. 323; Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Bamidbar, Vol. 3, p. 1,081; Devarim, Vol. 2, p. 401; Torat Chayim, VaYeitze 170a.</i> “<i>HaShem-</i>יהו"ה, how great are Your works and how very deep are Your thoughts,” all of which depends on the depth of comprehension of <i>Binah</i> (<i>Omek HaMoosag</i>) etc. This is sufficient for the understanding.

Chapter 42

We may now understand the source of the power that divides the combinations of the letters of thought on the third level; when he thinks of a particular matter in various combinations. Where does this power of division come from?
However, as known, the aspect of the five severities <i>MeNaTZPaCH</i> (מנצפ״ך) of <i>Imma</i>, is the source of this power to divide.
As known, the explanation of the matter is that the aspect of <i>Imma</i> is the aspect of understanding and comprehending the concept to its length and breadth.
When he delves into the aspect of the depth of the comprehension, he still is only in the depth of the aforementioned aspect of analytical thought, that transcends the aspect of divisions into actual letters of thought in the intellectual reflection upon the concept. Rather, it is still only pure intellectual thought, as is clearly evident.
However, it is through the aspect of the five severities (<i>Gevurot</i>), which is the aspect of the restriction and withdrawal that is within the power of comprehension itself, that the light of the intellect of the aforementioned analytical thought descends into the aspect of divisions of different letters in particular combinations.
This is called the five severities (<i>Gevurot</i>) <i>MeNaTZPa”Ch</i> (מנצפ”ך) of <i>Imma,</i> that are also called, “The protrusions of the seal.”
Now, although, at first glance, this appears to be an aspect of descent and restriction, nevertheless, the source of this is from higher than the power of comprehending this particular concept.
Proof of this is from what we observe in a small child who does not yet think in combinations of letters when thinking of particular things.
For example, if we were to give him a particular object, although he can discern its value and would not exchange it for another object, which is division and discernment in thought, he is not yet able to formulate it in combinations of letters, as mentioned previously.
Nevertheless, when he is able to speak and make requests in speech for a particular thing, it is then certain that in his brain of thought, he now has these particular combinations for the particular thing that he requested in speech.
For, the letters are divided in thought prior to their expression in speech (as will be explained regarding the statement that,<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">Etz Chayim, (<i>Shaar Leah V’Rachel</i>) Shaar 38, Ch. 3; Also see Maamarei Admor HaEmtzaee, Hanachot 5577, p. 35.</i> “the heels of <i>Leah</i> enter into the head of <i>Rachel</i>,” that the aforementioned aspect of “speech of thought” becomes the “thought of speech”).
This also accords with what is written elsewhere regarding the teaching of the <i>Zohar</i> on the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">Song of Songs 2:12; Zohar I 97b; Also see Sefer HaMaamarim 5568, p. 488.</i> “The voice of the turtledove is heard in our land (<i>Artzeinu</i>-ארצינו).”<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">The term “Our land-<i>Artzeinu</i>-ארצינו” refers to <i>Malchut</i>, which is speech.</i> That is, it is specifically when there is the aspect of speech that the time of the division of the letters of thoughts begins.
(This is the meaning of the teaching that by way of request, “The mother (<i>Imma</i>) lends her garments, these being the five <i>Gevurot</i> of <i>MeNaTzPa”Ch</i> (מנצפ”ך), which are the divisions of the letters of speech, to the daughter.”)
If so, this proves that the source of the combinations is not in the comprehension itself.
For, a child can discern between that which is good [for him] and that which is bad [for him], even before being able to speak, but he nevertheless does not have combinations of letters in his thought until he is specifically able to speak, as stated above.
Rather, their source is higher than the comprehension of <i>Binah</i>, but is from the power and source of the depth of all comprehension etc.
(For example, this is like how the source of the combinations of the letters of speech are from <i>Abba</i>, that is, from the inner aspect of <i>Chochmah</i>, which is the power of conceptualization (<i>Koach HaMaskil</i>) of <i>Chochmah,</i> that is called <i>Kadmoot HaSechel</i> – that which precedes intellect.
(This accords with what is explained elsewhere regarding the matter of, “the two birds,”<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">See Biurei HaZohar, Pinchas, 113b and on.</i> as will be explained.)
Moreover, although it is the five <i>gevurot</i> of <i>MeNaTzPa”Ch</i> (מנצפ״ך) that are within the five sources of the mouth that divide and arrange the combinations of the letters of speech, nevertheless it is, “the father (<i>Abba</i>) who founded the daughter (that is, <i>Malchut</i> – speech).”<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">See Zohar III (<i>Ra’aya Mehemna</i>) 256b, 248a, 258a; Iggeret HaKodesh, Epistle 5; Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Devarim<i>,</i> Vol. 2, pg. 310; Maamarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Kuntreisim, p. 547 and on, and elsewhere.</i>
[This is to say that it is <i>Chochmah</i> that] is the aspect of the power to combine the combinations and they therefore come automatically, without intending how to combine them in the intellect or comprehension. This is as written,<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">See Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Na”Ch, pg. 120; Kuntreisim, p. 547.</i> “combinations to <i>Chochmah</i>,” as explained elsewhere, and as will be explained later.
So likewise, the power to combine the letters of thought is from the power and root of <i>Binah</i>.)
We therefore find that although the aspect of the combinations of thought come about through an aspect of <i>Tzimtzum</i>-restriction of the analytical thought, nevertheless, the power and root that makes these combinations and divisions is from higher than the power of comprehension of analytical thought itself.
It is for this reason that a small child cannot combine letters of thought until he is capable of combining letters of speech, even though he is indeed capable of grasping and discerning things, as explained above.
Hence, the statement that “a child does not have thought” refers specifically to the aspect of the combinations of the letters of thought, as their source comes from the power and root of the thought and comprehension of <i>Binah</i>. This will suffice for the understanding.
(The fact that thought precedes speech is one of the wondrous and hidden matters. For the root of speech is in the innerness and source of <i>Chochmah,</i> while the root of thought is in the innerness and source of <i>Binah</i>, and <i>Chochmah</i> precedes <i>Binah,</i> for <i>Chochmah</i> is called “<i>Ein -</i> nothing” while <i>Binah</i> is called “Yesh – something.”
(This accords with what is explained elsewhere regarding the difference between “<i>Daber</i> – speak” and “<i>Amarta</i> – say,”<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">See <i>Ma’amarei Admor HaZaken, Ethalech Liozhna,</i> p. 105. Also see <i>Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Drushei Chatunah</i>, Vol. 1, p. 39.</i> that the root of “<i>Dibur</i> – actual speech” is higher than “<i>Amirah</i> – saying” of thought etc.
This itself proves that, in a child, thought does not come in division of combinations until there are the divisions of speech.)
Nevertheless, it is specifically the five <i>gevurot</i> of <i>MeNaTzPa”Ch</i> (מנצפ״ך) of <i>Binah</i> that are the source for the five <i>gevurot</i> of the divisions of speech, for “The mother (<i>Imma</i>) lends her clothes to the daughter (<i>Malchut</i>),” as it states,<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote">Ezekiel 16:44</i> “Like mother, like daughter.”
In their roots, however, speech comes from <i>Chochmah</i>, and it is for this reason that it states that, “The father (<i>Abba</i>) founded the daughter (<i>Malchut</i>).”
Similarly, in regard to the aforementioned (in chapter 38) first source of thought and speech, as they are embedded in the essential self of the soul, where the three levels of thought etc., as they are in a revealed state were explained; there too in the essence, the letters of thought are included first, prior to the inclusion of the letters of speech, which is called “the speaking soul.”
For, just as with a soul that is manifest in a body, thought precedes speech by two years or so, so likewise the spiritual soul is not called the “speaking spirit” for a period of time, but it indeed already possesses thought.
Or we may say that everything that is higher and more essential in its root comes down later<sup class="footnote-marker">9</sup><i class="footnote">See Likkutei Biurim to Shaar HaYichud, pg. 169d; Shaarei Orah, Shaar HaPurim, p. 58, p. 65; Ma’amarei Admor HaEmtza’ee, Hanachot 5577, p. 121; Shaar HaEmunah 43b, and elsewhere.</i> and that it is for this reason that it is specifically the “speaking soul” that is called the “intellectual soul,” which refers to the essential aspect of <i>Chochmah</i> that precedes the essential aspect of thought that is within it.
Nevertheless, in its revelation it only comes later, for a reason that is explained elsewhere at length. This will suffice for the understanding.)

Chapter 43

From all the above, the analogue will be understood to one who contemplates how it is Above, when he contemplates the many particulars of the chaining down of the worlds from the highest level to the lowest level. They all are generally included in the first source that arose in His simple thought etc., within the essential Self of the Light of the Unlimited One (<i>Ein Sof</i>), <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, before the <i>Tzimtzum</i>.
This too includes the three levels of thought, speech and action of thought, mentioned above.
The aspect of action of the essential thought literally in the Essential Self of <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה, blessed is He, is similar to the matter of the last deed that arose first in thought.
(This is unlike what Maimonides explains that <i>HaShem-</i>יהו"ה knows everything through Self-knowledge.<sup class="footnote-marker">1</sup><i class="footnote">Mishneh Torah, Hilchot Yesodei HaTorah 2:10</i>
Rather, this is that He knows the entire chaining down of Atzilut, Briyah, Yetzirah and Asiyah as if it is outside of Himself. That is, through action of thought, like a person who pictures the form of something that is separate from him, even though there is nothing outside of <i>HaShem-</i>יהו"ה, blessed is He.)
The aspect of speech of the essential thought of <i>HaShem-</i>יהו"ה, is like the fact that He estimated in potential within Himself, that which is destined to be in the chaining down of the worlds etc.<sup class="footnote-marker">2</sup><i class="footnote">See Mikdash Melech to Zohar I 15a</i>
About this it is written,<sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup><i class="footnote">Zohar Bereshit 15a</i> “He engraved an engraving in the upper purity.” This is the engraving of the letters within His Essential Self etc.
This is also the meaning of,<sup class="footnote-marker">4</sup><i class="footnote">Psalms 33:9</i> “He said” – within the essential thought – “and the world was,” or the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">5</sup><i class="footnote">Balak 23:19</i> “Will He say and not do?” – through the first <i>Tzimtzum</i> etc., and the like.
As mentioned above, “saying” (<i>Amirah-אמירה</i>) is always the aspect of speech of thought. (This is higher than hearing the speech of one’s friend, as in the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">6</sup><i class="footnote">Kings II 19:16, Isaiah 37:17, Daniel 9:18</i> “Lend me your ear and listen etc.” or the verse,<sup class="footnote-marker">7</sup><i class="footnote">Malachi 3:16</i> “And <i>HaShem</i>-יהו״ה paid attention and listened” and the like.)
Now, “thought of thought” of His Essential Self is similar to what was explained above about thinking the intellectual understanding of a matter in various combinations etc.
This is when it arose in His desire and thought, “I shall rule” or the like. This is in accordance to His essential insight and desire etc.
Thus, it says,<sup class="footnote-marker">8</sup><i class="footnote">Baruch SheAmar prayer</i> “He spoke (<i>Amar</i>-אמר) and the world was” – in the aspect of the <i>Malchut</i> of the Unlimited One (<i>Ein Sof</i>), that is, “I shall rule (<i>Ana Emloch</i>-אנא אמלוך)” etc.
